# Relativistic ISP V3 Paper 23: Adaptive Branch-A Source Campaign For Continuum Yang-Mills Confinement

Preprint, not peer reviewed, version 2026-05-28.

Author: Felix Robles Elvira

Status: adaptive Branch A source campaign settled through Section 57: the
surface side and RP/Cov transport side are closed, exact-entry RPF is proved
irreducible from the current source package, and the viable actual-law proof
route is reduced to a literal finite-interaction table; the scalar row test
has a clean conditional closure theorem; the local absorbed rows of the
same-law clean-row identification have been separated from the live residual
rows; and the remaining row-map obstruction has been executed to a sharp
row-identity, label-cover, coefficient-domination, and active-rowdata verdict;
the exact `ROWID` audit is reduced to one live residual-coefficient identity
rather than local-ledger bookkeeping; and Paper 16 has now been checked
against this identity, showing that it supplies finite KP envelopes and
same-row counting data but not the literal residual coefficient identity
needed for adaptive Branch A; Section 23 closes that coefficient obstruction
by passing to the canonical anchored finite coefficient gauge on the same
adaptive pushed-forward scalar law, so the remaining adaptive Branch-A burden
is canonical label entropy/active row data and the resulting scalar KP margin,
not coefficient identity; Section 24 executes the first canonical entropy
worksheet, proving a conservative finite over-refined entropy bound from the
Paper-21 carrier but showing that this crude bound is far too large to close
the scalar KP margin without a sharper selector/automaton or a new active
row-data margin theorem; Section 25 constructs the canonical selector
automaton scheme, proves exact language equivalence conditional on the finite
same-law value-locality table for \(\Phi_A\not\equiv0\), and prints the
transfer-matrix/row-sum entropy bound, leaving the remaining obstruction as a
finite source table rather than an undefined automaton; Section 26 proves
that the exact rowwise same-law value table exists for every finite adaptive
row and reduces the useful uniform automaton table to the local residual
Hamiltonian generator/value source
`P23-RPF-HLOC + P23-RPF-HVAL`; Section 27 executes the five-front
HLOC/HVAL/automaton/rowdata/KP campaign, proves the exact rowwise Möbius
generator exists, proves that the current source corpus does not supply the
cofinal bounded local generator alphabet, and sharpens the frontier again:
HVAL and the value-extended automaton are downstream finite algebra after
`P23-RPF-HLOC`, while active row data and the KP margin are explicit scalar
tests on that same source; Section 28 settles HLOC as a current-corpus route:
exact cofinal HLOC is equivalent to finite-range vanishing of the actual
anchored Möbius coefficients, the present source package does not prove it
and cannot imply it, and the only honest positive HLOC route is a new
same-law separator/local-law source; Section 29 closes the direct
finite-range-vanishing route negatively for the present corpus by an explicit
same-record residual-tail countermodel family, so exact finite range is no
longer a live bookkeeping task but a new source theorem or a route to be
abandoned in favor of literal decay/Dobrushin; Section 30 attacks the
separator-source alternative itself, defines the admissible same-law separator
identity, rules out global-code and non-geometric separator shortcuts, and
proves that the current corpus does not yet supply the required admissible
separator factorization; Section 31 investigates both remaining options to
terminal current-corpus status: admissible separator HLOC is parked at a
six-table same-law source package, while the non-HLOC literal
decay/Dobrushin route is reduced to exact oscillation/influence row tables
and scalar KP inequalities, with current-corpus non-derivability proved by
the same arbitrary-order residual-tail completions; Section 32 executes the
separator route gate by gate and falsifies it as an available Paper-23 route:
no current candidate supplies the required admissible same-law separator
records, exact projection, exact local clique decomposition, row data, and
KP margin; Section 33 executes the direct non-HLOC influence-row route and
settles its current-corpus status: it gives the exact same-law Dobrushin
decision functional and the positive closure theorem, but proves that the
existing papers do not determine the required cofinal row value; Section 34
executes the positive-close campaign through the sharp conditional-oscillation
route, giving the finite theorem that would close Branch A and isolating the
missing same-law screened conditional influence source; Section 35 executes
the heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl one-step campaign and proves that a same-law
conditional transfer contraction would imply screened conditional influence,
but that the present corpus does not supply that contraction for the actual
adaptive law; Section 36 sharpens that contraction to a one-edge finite
operator test, proves that each fixed row has a same-law finite matrix
decision, and isolates the remaining cofinal source as an exact path
expansion plus a uniform centered spectral gap; Section 37 executes the
finite-template portfolio promised by that test, prints the actual same-law
edge matrix formula for the minimal live `CleanRPF` template and its larger
admissible covers, and proves that no template in the present corpus certifies
the scalar margin without new matrix-value or spectral-gap data; Section 38
identifies that matrix value with restricted conditional maximal correlation,
derives sharp same-law \(\chi^2\) and log-density oscillation sufficient
conditions, and proves that the present corpus does not supply those
conditional density-ratio bounds for the actual adaptive residual law;
Section 39 proves that the log-density ratio is exactly the marginal crossing
Hamiltonian of the printed two-site conditional law, gives a literal crossing
atom sufficient bound with its scalar margin, and sharpens the remaining
source to `P23-RPF-CROSS-MARG` or the stronger `P23-RPF-CROSS-LIT` on the
same adaptive law; Section 40 prints the minimal crossing atom table
\({\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}\), proves the zero-crossing, atom-sum, and
direct marginal fallback tests, and shows that the table itself is closed as
finite same-law algebra while the cofinal crossing bound remains a new source
theorem; Section 41 bypasses the atom-sum factor-three loss at the formal
level by deriving the exact normalized minimal marginal formula
\(C_0^m=W-F_y-F_x+c_0\), introduces the mixed-odds diagnostic, and sharpens
the remaining primitive source to `P23-RPF-MIN-MARG(Delta,kappa)`; Section 42
prints the normalized minimal-edge marginal table, gives the finite extremal
and Peter-Weyl range certificates, rules out a bare mixed-odds shortcut, and
parks the route at `P23-RPF-MIN-SINK` or the finite-tail version
`P23-RPF-MIN-MARG-PW`; Section 43 proves the small-coupling Sinkhorn range
reduction
\(\Delta_{m,0}\le\Theta_{dc,0}+\omega_{\parallel,0}^2/4\), naming the
doubly centered source `P23-RPF-MIN-DCENTER(Theta,omega,kappa)` as the sharpest
current minimal-edge target; Section 44 reduces that source to explicit
one-line atom widths and mixed finite-difference atom tables, proving
\(\omega_{\parallel,0}\le\overline\omega_{\parallel,0}\) and
\(\Theta_{dc,0}\le2\overline D_{\square,0}\), and names
`P23-RPF-MIN-MIXLINE(D,omega,kappa)` as the finite atom-level source;
Section 45 quotient-normalizes the endpoint-additive atom parts by a
deterministic anchor gauge, proves that the same mixed finite-difference table
also controls the one-line coupling width, and sharpens the finite source to
`P23-RPF-MIN-ANCHMIX(D,kappa)`; Section 46 splits this into the scalar
budget
\(D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa)\) plus the two live sources
`P23-RPF-MIN-DMIX(D)` and `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)`; Section 47 prints the
exact anchored mixed census table, proves rowwise same-law decidability of
which atoms have nonzero mixed diameter, removes zero rows without debit, and
parks the route at
`P23-RPF-MIN-MIXCENSUS(D) + P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)`; Section 48 audits the
minimal Peter-Weyl tail, proving that \(\kappa=0\) is available only under an
explicit finite-complete or bandlimited same-law certificate and otherwise
remains a live source; Section 49 refines the mixed census to true-bridge
rows, proves endpoint-blind and endpoint-additive rows carry no mixed debit,
and sharpens the live source to
`P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE(D) + P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)`; Section 50 audits the
true-bridge amplitudes themselves, proving the positive bridge-damping
closure theorem but also proving that finite labeling/counting alone cannot
supply the needed amplitude decay; Section 51 replaces the unsigned bridge
triangle sum by the sharper signed anchored range source, proving the exact
signed closure theorem and leaving adaptive Branch A at the two positive
same-law frontiers `MIN-BRIDGEDAMP + MIN-KTAIL` or `MIN-SIGNED`, neither of
which is supplied numerically by the current corpus; Section 52 freezes the
signed scalar gate, prints the admissible cancellation-block table, proves
rowwise decidability of the signed cancellation extremal problem, and shows
that the natural endpoint/orientation/conjugation/reflection/covariance/CE
symmetries are quotient or equality rules rather than anti-row cancellation
sources; Section 53 bypasses partitions and studies the actual one-block
signed bridge Hamiltonian, proves the direct signed closure theorem, prints
the finite compact/dual-certificate proof format, audits exact evaluation,
dual, Peter-Weyl, RP/positivity, quotient, and clean-KP routes, and concludes
that the present corpus still lacks the cofinal same-law numerical signed
extremal bound; Section 54 executes the finite dual-certificate campaign,
proves that a cofinal same-law dual certificate plus `MIN-KTAIL` would close
the signed route, and proves that the current closed equality, positivity,
RP, covariance, local, and endpoint-additive ledgers do not imply such a
certificate because residual-tail completions can vary the surviving true
bridge mixed mode; Section 55 attacks the shared Peter-Weyl tail bottleneck,
defines the finite-band and uniform-decay tail sources `PWBAND` and `PWDECAY`,
proves that either would close `MIN-KTAIL(0)`, audits the finite-complete,
heat-kernel/Casimir, Paper-20, Paper-21, SD/Casimir, clean-KP, and rowwise
truncation routes, and concludes that the current corpus supplies no
same-law cofinal tail profile for the actual adaptive residual Hamiltonian;
Section 56 then tests the no-tail escape by bounding the full normalized
minimal-edge Hamiltonian directly, proves the full-object signed closure
theorem and its finite-dual proof format, and proves that the current corpus
does not supply the required full signed range because the same residual-tail
freedom becomes full-object range freedom when no projection/tail split is
used; Section 57 freezes the terminal source theorem, proves that no further
current-corpus bookkeeping source remains, and exports Paper 24 as the
full-object finite-dual certificate or witness campaign.

Paper 23 is not a synthesis paper.  It is the source campaign for the most
concrete surviving route left by Paper 22: adaptive Branch A on the same
large-\(N\), high-\(\alpha\), pushed-forward `SEL2` scalar law.

Paper 22 settled the post-\(F_4\) branch ledger:

1. the strict \(F_4\) route is falsified at `ESC-MASS`;
2. fixed Branch A is reduced to the literal \(N=4096\) prefactor cap;
3. adaptive Branch A is reduced to `XIPLOG+AREA+RPCOV/RPF`;
4. Branch B is parked behind a new positive full-support surface theorem;
5. Branch C is parked behind a signed/selector exact-anchor package.

This paper works on item 3.  It does not import Branch B or Branch C.

## 0. Barandes-Aligned Boundary

The primitive object remains the whole-process law of finite scalar records.
All surface, collar, root, residual, RP/Cov, and exact-entry terms are
bookkeeping devices used to compute scalar inequalities on that law.  This
paper does not import:

1. a Wilson-loop area law;
2. a mass gap;
3. a pre-existing continuum Yang-Mills measure with confinement properties;
4. a gauge-fixed subprocess law;
5. an off-record local Markov kernel;
6. a physical flux-tube or sheet ontology.

Every source theorem below is a theorem about the same pushed-forward finite
record branch imported from Papers 20--22.

## 1. Paper-22 Export Ledger

Paper 22 exports the following adaptive Branch-A data.

### Definition 1.1: The Adaptive Large-\(N\) Row

The adaptive row is the high-\(\alpha\), fundamental-channel row family

```math
N\ge4096,\qquad \rho_N=F_N,
```

with the same `SEL2` pushed-forward scalar law and high-\(\alpha\) selector
used in Paper 22 Sections 34--39.  The target convention is one declared
actual four-dimensional \(SU(N)\) branch, with \(N\) fixed before the final
source and prefactor inequalities are evaluated.

The uniform pre-surface loss floor imported from Paper 22 is denoted

```math
M_*:=0.00317259975\ldots .
```

The row is not a family of different ontologies.  It is one declared adaptive
cofinal source campaign whose scalar records are evaluated before the final
inequality is spent.

### Definition 1.2: Adaptive Branch-A Source Gates

For \(n_0\ge1\), \(\theta_\xi\ge0\), and
\(\lambda_{11},\lambda_{13}\ge0\), define the Paper-23 adaptive source package

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}A\text{-}SRC}
(n_0,\theta_\xi,\lambda_{11},\lambda_{13})
```

to mean that the following four Paper-22 source gates hold on the same
adaptive row:

```math
\mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}AREA}(n_0),
```

```math
\mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}XIPLOG}(\theta_\xi),
```

```math
\mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}RPCOV\text{-}MARGIN}(\lambda_{11}),
```

and

```math
\mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}RPF\text{-}MARGIN}(\lambda_{13}).
```

The first two gates control the adaptive surface numerator.  The last two
gates control the row-complete carried predebit

```math
\mathcal L_N^{rc}
=
U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)
+
U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N).
```

### Theorem 1.3: Imported Adaptive Branch-A Closure Theorem

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}A\text{-}SRC}
(n_0,\theta_\xi,\lambda_{11},\lambda_{13})
```

and the two strict scalar inequalities

```math
\theta_\xi<{2\over3}(n_0+1),
\qquad
\lambda_{11}+\lambda_{13}<M_*.
```

Then adaptive Branch A closes the Paper-20 surface prefactor gate on a cofinal
large-\(N\) branch.

Proof.

This is exactly Paper 22 Theorems 38.4, 39.5, 39.7, and 39.8, read as an
import theorem.  `AREA+XIPLOG` imply
`P22-BRANCHA-ADAPT-SURFLOG(theta_xi,n0)`.  The two margin gates imply
`P22-BRANCHA-ADAPT-PREDEBIT(mu)` with

```math
\mu=M_*-\lambda_{11}-\lambda_{13}>0.
```

The strict surface-log inequality is the closure condition in Paper 22
Theorem 38.4.  No additional continuum measure, area law, or signed/selector
surface theorem is used. `square`

### Corollary 1.4: Paper-23 Live Source Fronts

The adaptive Branch-A campaign has exactly two live source families.

1. **Surface-log family.**

   ```math
   \mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}XIPLOG}(\theta_\xi)
   ```

   together with the already declared or amplified area floor \(n_0\).

2. **Predebit-margin family.**

   ```math
   \mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}RPCOV\text{-}MARGIN}(\lambda_{11}),
   \qquad
   \mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}RPF\text{-}MARGIN}(\lambda_{13}).
   ```

There is no remaining tree-time problem, no remaining \(F_4\) escape problem,
and no hidden Branch-B/Branch-C surface theorem inside adaptive Branch A.

## 2. Work Package I: Fixed-Template Area And Geometry

Paper 22 already showed that pure finite-template geometry contributes only
\(O(1)\) to the adaptive surface log when the Creutz template is fixed as
\(N\) varies.  This section imports and sharpens that point so Paper 23 does
not waste effort on a closed finite-combinatorial issue.

### Definition 2.1: Fixed-Template Adaptive Battery

The adaptive battery is fixed-template when:

1. the rectangular Creutz shape family is chosen before the final inequalities;
2. the finite list of root/collar attachment types does not grow with \(N\);
3. the reduced support convention of Paper 20 is retained;
4. the minimal sheet has at least one plaquette for every \(N\).

The last condition is deliberately weak.  It is the default nonempty-sheet
floor, not an area amplifier.

### Lemma 2.2: Default Area Floor

On a fixed-template adaptive battery,

```math
\mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}AREA}(1)
```

holds.

Proof.

The declared Creutz rectangle has a nonempty minimal sheet.  Therefore the
minimal area count \(n_N^{surf}\) is at least one cofinally.  This is exactly
Paper 22 Definition 39.4 with \(n_0=1\). `square`

### Lemma 2.3: Pure Geometry Is \(O(1)\)

On a fixed-template adaptive battery, the pure finite-template surface entropy
contributes

```math
O(1)
```

to \(H_N^{surf}\).  It contributes no coefficient of \(\log N\).

Proof.

Paper 22 Lemma 39.3 imports Paper 13 Lemma 7.30Q: for a fixed finite Creutz
template, the root set, plaquette-adjacency degree, local replacement list,
and component partition convention are independent of the representation
dimension.  Thus the finite entropy prefactor has logarithm bounded
cofinally by a constant independent of \(N\). `square`

### Theorem 2.4: Work Package I Closure

On the fixed-template adaptive row, the area/geometry part of adaptive Branch A
is closed with

```math
n_0=1,
```

and the surface-log closure condition reduces to

```math
\theta_\xi<{4\over3}.
```

The only remaining surface-log source is the decoration/minimal-collar
growth term \(\Xi'_N\) encoded by

```math
\mathrm{P22\text{-}BRANCHA\text{-}XIPLOG}(\theta_\xi).
```

Proof.

Lemma 2.2 gives the default area floor \(n_0=1\).  Lemma 2.3 removes the pure
finite-template geometry from the \(\log N\) coefficient.  The threshold
\(\theta_\xi<2(n_0+1)/3\) from Theorem 1.3 becomes
\(\theta_\xi<4/3\).  Therefore Work Package I is closed, and the remaining
surface-log source is precisely the same-record growth of \(\Xi'_N\).
`square`

## 3. Work Package II: The \(\Xi'_N\) Log-Growth Source

This section opens the first live analytic source front.

### Definition 3.1: Minimal-Collar Log-Growth Functional

Let \(\Xi'_N\) denote the same-record minimal-collar/surface-entry decoration
log numerator isolated in Paper 22 Section 39, after removing the fixed
finite-template geometry of Theorem 2.4.  The exact source target is

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XIPLOG}(\theta)
```

meaning

```math
\Xi'_N\le \theta\log N+O(1)
```

cofinally on the adaptive high-\(\alpha\) row.  It is identified with
`P22-BRANCHA-XIPLOG(theta)`.

### Lemma 3.2: Uniform Decoration Activity Would Give Zero Log Coefficient

If the surface-entry decoration KP activity and the minimal-collar endpoint
factor are uniformly bounded in \(N\) on the adaptive row, then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XIPLOG}(0)
```

holds.

Proof.

After Theorem 2.4, \(\Xi'_N\) contains only the same-record
decoration/minimal-collar logarithm, not the pure surface animal entropy.  If
the KP activity, collar multiplicity per excess unit, and minimal-collar
endpoint factor are uniformly bounded in \(N\), the corresponding logarithmic
surface-entry numerator is \(O(1)\).  Hence
\(\Xi'_N\le0\cdot\log N+O(1)\). `square`

### Lemma 3.3: Polynomial Decoration Growth Gives A Quantitative Source

If there exists \(C<\infty\) and \(\theta\ge0\) such that

```math
\exp(\Xi'_N)\le C N^\theta
```

cofinally, then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XIPLOG}(\theta)
```

holds.

Proof.

Taking logarithms gives

```math
\Xi'_N\le \theta\log N+\log C.
```

This is Definition 3.1. `square`

### Corollary 3.4: Current Status Of The Surface-Log Front

The current corpus closes the fixed-template area/geometry part but does not
yet print a uniform decoration/minimal-collar growth theorem.  Therefore the
surface-log front is reduced to one of two explicit tasks:

1. prove uniform decoration/minimal-collar boundedness and get
   `P23-XIPLOG(0)`;
2. prove polynomial decoration/minimal-collar growth with exponent
   \(\theta<4/3\) on the default \(n_0=1\) branch, or else declare a fixed
   area amplifier \(n_0>1\) and use the threshold
   \(\theta<2(n_0+1)/3\).

If neither task can be proved, adaptive Branch A remains parked at
`XIPLOG`.

## 4. Work Package III: Predebit Margin Source

The second live source front is disjoint from the surface-log front.

### Definition 4.1: Paper-23 Predebit Margin Gate

For \(\lambda_{11},\lambda_{13}\ge0\), define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}PREDEBIT}
(\lambda_{11},\lambda_{13})
```

to mean

```math
U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)\le\lambda_{11},
\qquad
U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N)\le\lambda_{13}
```

cofinally on the adaptive row.

This is exactly the conjunction of
`P22-BRANCHA-RPCOV-MARGIN(lambda_11)` and
`P22-BRANCHA-RPF-MARGIN(lambda_13)`.

### Lemma 4.2: Zero Routes For The Two Predebits

The sufficient zero routes are:

```math
\sum_{k\ge j}D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}\to0,
\qquad
\sup_g\sum_{k\ge j}D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(g)\to0,
```

for the RP/Cov term, and

```math
\mathrm{P21\text{-}U13\text{-}RPF\text{-}FACT0}
```

for the exact-entry residual factorization term.

If both zero routes hold, then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}PREDEBIT}(0,0)
```

holds.

Proof.

This is Paper 22 Definition 39.6 read on the adaptive row.  The displayed
moving-row tails are precisely the RP/Cov zero source.  The `RPF-FACT0`
source is the exact-entry residual factorization zero source.  If both hold,
both predebit components vanish cofinally. `square`

### Corollary 4.3: Current Status Of The Predebit Front

The current corpus does not print the RP/Cov moving-row tail limits or
`P21-U13-RPF-FACT0` on the adaptive high-\(\alpha\) row.  Therefore the
predebit front is reduced to one of:

1. prove the two zero routes and get \(\lambda_{11}=\lambda_{13}=0\);
2. prove explicit finite bounds with

   ```math
   \lambda_{11}+\lambda_{13}<M_*;
   ```

3. defeat the \(M_*\)-floor sufficient test by proving every admissible pair
   satisfies \(\lambda_{11}+\lambda_{13}\ge M_*\), or genuinely falsify
   adaptive Branch A by proving the carried predebit reaches the actual
   same-record loss floor.

No surface numerator estimate should be spent until one of these predebit
alternatives is declared.

## 5. First Paper-23 Checkpoint

Combining Theorem 2.4, Corollary 3.4, and Corollary 4.3:

```math
\boxed{
\text{adaptive Branch A closes on the default fixed-template battery if}
}
```

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XIPLOG}(\theta)
\quad\text{with}\quad
\theta<{4\over3},
```

and

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}PREDEBIT}(\lambda_{11},\lambda_{13})
\quad\text{with}\quad
\lambda_{11}+\lambda_{13}<M_*.
```

This is now the exact Paper-23 source target.  The next work should attack
`P23-XIPLOG` first, because it determines whether the default \(n_0=1\)
battery can possibly work or whether an area amplifier must be declared before
predebit constants are optimized.

Sections 6--8 execute that attack.  The outcome is deliberately stated as a
bound-and-decision theorem: the present corpus supplies exact source
functionals for the two gates, but it does not print the numerical
same-record estimates needed to turn those functionals into a pass.

## 6. Executing `P23-XIPLOG`

The \(\Xi'_N\) gate is a decoration/minimal-collar growth question.  Paper 13
and Paper 19 already say what has to be measured.  The point of this section
is to extract that measurement as a single scalar source functional.

### Definition 6.1: Surface Decoration Source Functional

Work on the adaptive row of Definition 1.1 and keep the finite Creutz
geometry fixed as in Theorem 2.4.  For every loop \(C\) in the four-loop
Creutz battery, let

```math
\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}
```

be the limsup KP decoration activity for the Paper-13 surface-entry
decoration gas, after merging residual-polymers and non-leading character
insertions in the same record law.  Let

```math
c_{\Delta,N,C}^{surf}
```

be the corresponding finite-battery cluster-count constant, in the sense of
the Paper-19 decoration ledger.

Concretely, Paper 19 Definition 8L.9A splits this constant into an
area-charged collar part \(C_\xi\) and an endpoint/corner part \(C_{\xi'}\).
For the \(\Xi'_N\) numerator, the sharp version uses the endpoint/corner
constant \(C_{\xi'}\).  If the source text has only printed the combined
finite-battery decoration audit, one may safely take
\(c_{\Delta,N,C}^{surf}=C_{\xi,N,C}+C_{\xi',N,C}\).  This is conservative; it
may overcount the area-charged collar part, but it never understates
\(\Xi'_N\).

Define

```math
\mathfrak X_N
:=
\begin{cases}
\displaystyle
\max_C
{c_{\Delta,N,C}^{surf}\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}
\over
1-\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}},
&
\max_C\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}<1,\\[1.2em]
+\infty,
&
\max_C\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}\ge1
\text{ or one of the constants is not sourced.}
\end{cases}
```

This is a scalar record-law functional.  It is not a microscopic
decoration field, and it is not an area-law input.

### Lemma 6.2: Paper-13/Paper-19 Decoration Bound For \(\Xi'_N\)

On the fixed-template adaptive row,

```math
\Xi'_N\le \mathfrak X_N+O(1).
```

Proof.

Paper 13 Proposition 7.30AH says that `KP_dec` produces finite constants
\(D_C,\xi_C,\xi'_C\) controlling the decoration partition functions attached
to the declared surface battery.  The nonminimal-sheet term \(\xi'_C\) is
the logarithmic decoration numerator entering \(\Xi'_N\).

Paper 19 Definition 8E.1 and Theorem 8E.2 give the same finite-battery KP
conversion in loss form:

```math
\Delta_{dec}^{bd}
\le
\exp\left(
{c_\Delta\eta\over1-\eta}
\right)-1.
```

Taking the logarithm of \(1+\Delta_{dec}^{bd}\) gives the source
\(c_\Delta\eta/(1-\eta)\).  Applying this loop by loop to the four fixed
Creutz records and then taking the maximum gives the displayed
\(\mathfrak X_N\).

The sharper Paper-19 surface split, Definition 8L.11A.22F and Theorem
8L.11A.22F.1, keeps the area-charged \(C_\xi\) part in the \(D_C\)
subcriticality ledger and the endpoint/corner \(C_{\xi'}\) part in the
finite numerator.  The present definition permits either that sharp split or
the conservative combined \(C_\xi+C_{\xi'}\) ceiling.  The only possible
\(O(1)\) discrepancy is the harmless choice of equivalent finite-template
normalization; it is independent of \(N\). `square`

### Theorem 6.3: Quantitative `P23-XIPLOG` Bound

If, for some \(\theta\ge0\),

```math
\mathfrak X_N\le \theta\log N+O(1)
```

cofinally, then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XIPLOG}(\theta)
```

holds.

In particular, a uniform bound \(\mathfrak X_N=O(1)\) proves
`P23-XIPLOG(0)`.

Proof.

Lemma 6.2 gives \(\Xi'_N\le\mathfrak X_N+O(1)\).  Substituting the assumed
growth bound gives

```math
\Xi'_N\le \theta\log N+O(1),
```

which is Definition 3.1. `square`

### Corollary 6.4: Default Branch-A Surface Criterion In Source Form

On the default fixed-template battery, where \(n_0=1\), the surface-log part
of adaptive Branch A closes if

```math
\mathfrak X_N
<
\left({4\over3}-\delta\right)\log N+O(1)
```

for some \(\delta>0\).

More generally, if

```math
\Theta_X
:=
\limsup_{N\to\infty}{\mathfrak X_N\over\log N}<\infty,
```

then any fixed minimal-area amplifier satisfying

```math
n_0>{3\over2}\Theta_X-1
```

is sufficient for the surface-log side, provided the amplified battery is
declared before the final inequality and remains a fixed finite scalar-record
template.

Proof.

The first statement is Theorem 6.3 with \(\theta<4/3\), followed by Theorem
2.4.  The second statement is Theorem 1.3 with the general threshold
\(\theta<2(n_0+1)/3\). `square`

### Theorem 6.5: Current-Corpus Verdict For `P23-XIPLOG`

The present papers do not prove an unconditional numerical instance of
`P23-XIPLOG(theta)`.  They prove the sharp bound

```math
\Xi'_N\le \mathfrak X_N+O(1),
```

and therefore reduce `P23-XIPLOG(theta)` to the single same-record estimate

```math
\mathfrak X_N\le \theta\log N+O(1).
```

Proof.

Paper 13 proves that `KP_dec` gives finite decoration constants on a declared
finite row.  Paper 19 imports residual-decoration activity from the Paper-16
KP ledger and gives the monotone conversion
\(c_\Delta\eta/(1-\eta)\).  These are exactly the ingredients in Lemma 6.2.

What is not printed in Papers 13, 16, 19, 20, 21, or 22 is a uniform
large-\(N\) estimate for

```math
\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf},
\qquad
c_{\Delta,N,C}^{surf},
```

on the adaptive \(SU(N)\), \(F_N\), high-\(\alpha\) law.  Finiteness for each
fixed \(N\) is not the same thing as a cofinal logarithmic growth law.
Therefore the gate is now bounded but not numerically closed. `square`

## 7. Executing `P23-PREDEBIT`

The predebit gate is disjoint from the surface-log gate.  It has two and only
two live pieces: the Paper-16 RP/Cov moving-row tail and the Paper-13/20/21
exact-entry residual factorization tail.

### Definition 7.1: RP/Cov And RPF Tail Functionals

For the adaptive row, define

```math
\Lambda_{11}^{RP}(N)
:=
\limsup_{j\to\infty}
\sum_{k\ge j}
D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N),
```

and

```math
\Lambda_{11}^{Cov}(N)
:=
\limsup_{j\to\infty}
\sup_{g\in Euc_{adm}}
\sum_{k\ge j}
D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(g;N).
```

Let

```math
\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}(N)
:=
\Lambda_{11}^{RP}(N)+\Lambda_{11}^{Cov}(N).
```

For the exact-entry residual factorization slot, define

```math
\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}(N)
:=
\limsup_{j\to\infty}\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N).
```

Finally set the cofinal ceilings

```math
\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}
:=
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}(N),
\qquad
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}
:=
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}(N).
```

All limits are evaluated after the same scalar pushforward.  No perimeter,
cusp, loop-readout, surface numerator, or decoration debit is charged here.

### Lemma 7.2: Ledger Domination Of The Two Predebits

On the adaptive row,

```math
U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)
\le
\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}(N),
```

and

```math
U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N)
\le
\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}(N),
```

whenever the right-hand sides are finite.

Proof.

For the first inequality, Paper 16 Definitions 9W.1C and 9W.1G define the
RP and covariance ledgers as tail sums of the displayed defects.  Paper 21
Theorem 59.2 and Lemma 67.5 identify the active \(U_{11}^{RPCov}\) carry with
exactly those reduced moving-row RP/Cov tails when no zero theorem is
available.  Therefore the carried RP/Cov debit is bounded by the two tail
ceilings.

For the second inequality, Paper 20 Definition 4.3A.72 and Theorem 4.3A.73
place the exact-entry residual factorization defect in
\(\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}\).  Paper 21 Theorem 33.4 and Paper 22 Lemma 36.3
keep the `RPF` slot carried unless the residual factorization defect vanishes
or a finite ceiling is supplied.  The limsup ceiling
\(\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}(N)\) is precisely that finite ceiling. `square`

### Theorem 7.3: Quantitative `P23-PREDEBIT` Bound

If

```math
\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}\le\lambda_{11},
\qquad
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\le\lambda_{13},
```

then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}PREDEBIT}(\lambda_{11},\lambda_{13})
```

holds.

In particular, if

```math
\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}
+
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}
<M_*,
```

then the predebit side of adaptive Branch A closes with a positive margin.

Proof.

By Lemma 7.2, the two carried predebits are bounded by
\(\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}(N)\) and \(\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}(N)\).  The cofinal
limsups give the displayed \(\lambda\)-ceilings.  This is Definition 4.1.
The final assertion is the margin condition from Theorem 1.3. `square`

### Corollary 7.4: Zero Route

If

```math
\sum_{k\ge j}D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)\to0,
\qquad
\sup_g\sum_{k\ge j}D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(g;N)\to0
```

cofinally in \(N\), and

```math
\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)\to0
```

cofinally in \(N\), then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}PREDEBIT}(0,0)
```

holds.

Proof.

The hypotheses say
\(\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}=\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}=0\).  Apply
Theorem 7.3. `square`

### Theorem 7.5: Current-Corpus Verdict For `P23-PREDEBIT`

The present papers do not prove a numerical predebit margin.  They prove the
sharp carried bound

```math
U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)+U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N)
\le
\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}(N)+\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}(N),
```

and therefore reduce `P23-PREDEBIT(lambda_11,lambda_13)` to the source
estimates

```math
\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}\le\lambda_{11},
\qquad
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\le\lambda_{13}.
```

Proof.

Paper 16 proves the correct RP/Cov ledger form, but does not print the
moving-row adaptive high-\(\alpha\) tail estimates for the present \(SU(N)\)
row.  Paper 13 proves the residual-factorization gate from connected-cumulant
KP, and Paper 20 places its failure or residual in the exact-entry
\(\epsilon_{RPF}\) ledger, but the current corpus does not print
`P21-U13-RPF-FACT0` or a cofinal finite bound below the tiny margin
\(M_*=0.00317259975\ldots\).

Thus the predebit is bounded exactly by the source tails above, but it is not
numerically closed by the present texts. `square`

## 8. Second Paper-23 Checkpoint

Define the two executed source ceilings

```math
\Theta_X
:=
\limsup_{N\to\infty}{\mathfrak X_N\over\log N},
```

and

```math
\Lambda_{pre}
:=
\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}
+
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}.
```

Then adaptive Branch A has the following exact status.

1. **Default fixed-template pass.**  If

   ```math
   \Theta_X<{4\over3},
   \qquad
   \Lambda_{pre}<M_*,
   ```

   then the default \(n_0=1\) adaptive Branch-A route closes.

2. **Amplified fixed-template pass.**  If \(\Theta_X<\infty\),
   \(\Lambda_{pre}<M_*\), and a fixed scalar Creutz battery is declared with

   ```math
   n_0>{3\over2}\Theta_X-1,
   ```

   then the amplified adaptive Branch-A route closes.

3. **Predebit sufficient-test failure.**  If a same-record lower floor proves

   ```math
   U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)+U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N)\ge M_*
   ```

   cofinally, then the \(M_*\)-floor sufficient pass test fails.  A genuine
   Branch-A falsification requires the sharper lower floor

   ```math
   U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)+U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N)
   \ge
   \underline M_{loss}^{SEL2,20}(N)
   ```

   cofinally, or an equivalent comparison against a same-record upper ceiling
   for \(\underline M_{loss}^{SEL2,20}(N)\).

4. **Surface-log failure at fixed area.**  If a same-record lower floor proves
   \(\Xi'_N\ge(4/3+\delta)\log N\) cofinally and no area amplifier is
   declared, then the default \(n_0=1\) branch fails.  This does not falsify
   an amplified branch.

At the present source level, neither the pass inequalities nor the lower
floors are printed.  Paper 23 has therefore completed the requested
`XIPLOG` and `PREDEBIT` execution as far as the current corpus permits:
progress now requires numerical or asymptotic estimates for
\(\mathfrak X_N\), \(\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}\), and
\(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\), not another reshuffling of the existing
ledger. `square`

## 9. Terminal Branch-A Execution

This section performs the requested five-step Branch-A execution after the
source-function reduction of Sections 6--8.  The purpose is to decide whether
Branch A is already successful, already falsified, or closed only as an
explicit source frontier.

### Definition 9.1: Uniform Adaptive Decoration Source

Define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}XI\text{-}UNIF}
(C_{\xi'},\eta_*)
```

to mean that, on the high-\(\alpha\) adaptive `SEL2` row of Definition 1.1,
the sharp endpoint/corner version of Definition 6.1 can be chosen with

```math
\sup_{N\ge4096}\max_C c_{\Delta,N,C}^{surf}\le C_{\xi'}<\infty,
```

and

```math
\sup_{N\ge4096}\max_C\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}\le\eta_*<1.
```

This is the uniform-\(N\) analogue of the Paper-19 finite-template
decoration geometry and character/residual KP activity audits.  It is a
source theorem on the same adaptive pushed-forward scalar law, not a
transfer from a different selector branch.

### Theorem 9.2: Uniform Decoration Source Gives \(\Theta_X=0\)

If

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}XI\text{-}UNIF}
(C_{\xi'},\eta_*)
```

holds, then

```math
\mathfrak X_N
\le
{C_{\xi'}\eta_*\over1-\eta_*}
```

for all sufficiently large \(N\).  Consequently

```math
\Theta_X=0
```

and the default \(n_0=1\) surface side of adaptive Branch A closes.

Proof.

Substitute the two uniform bounds in Definition 6.1.  Since
\(\eta_*<1\), the denominator is uniformly positive and the right-hand side
is \(O(1)\).  Therefore

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}{\mathfrak X_N\over\log N}=0.
```

Corollary 6.4 then gives the default \(n_0=1\) surface pass because
\(0<4/3\). `square`

### Lemma 9.3: The SEL0 Decoration Pass Does Not Transfer Automatically

Paper 19 proves strong decoration-source statements on its clean centered
square `SEL_0` branch, including the finite-template geometry audit and the
surface decoration-growth audit.  The present Paper-23 branch is not that
branch.  It is the high-\(\alpha\), adaptive \(SU(N)\), \(F_N\), `SEL2`
branch imported from Paper 22.

Therefore Paper 19's `SEL_0` decoration closure proves
`P23-ADAPT-XI-UNIF` only if an additional same-record selector-transfer
theorem identifies the relevant decoration activity, character tail, and
finite-template constants on the adaptive `SEL2` law.

No such transfer theorem is printed in the current corpus.

Proof.

Paper 19 Theorem 0A.6 and its later Section-8L consequences are explicitly
statements about the clean `SEL_0` finite-template branch and its same
pushed-forward record law.  Paper 22 Definitions 37.3 and 39.1 freeze a
different active row: \(F_N\), \(N\ge4096\), high \(\alpha_N=1-1/N\), and
`SEL2` slack data.  Barandes alignment requires same-record comparison; a
bound proved on one pushed-forward scalar law may not be spent on another
without a declared pushforward equality or domination map.  The present text
contains no such equality or domination theorem. `square`

### Definition 9.4: Uniform Adaptive Predebit Source

Define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}PRE\text{-}UNIF}(\Lambda)
```

to mean that the two predebit ceilings of Definition 7.1 satisfy

```math
\Lambda_{pre}
=
\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}
+
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}
\le \Lambda.
```

The branch has a predebit pass exactly when this holds with
\(\Lambda<M_*\).

### Theorem 9.5: Predebit Pass/Failure Alternatives

The adaptive Branch-A predebit side has the following sharp alternatives.

1. If `P23-ADAPT-PRE-UNIF(Lambda)` holds for some
   \(\Lambda<M_*\), then the predebit side passes.
2. If a same-record lower floor proves

   ```math
   \liminf_{N\to\infty}
   \left[
   U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)+U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N)
   \right]
   \ge M_*,
   ```

   then the simple \(M_*\)-floor sufficient test fails.
3. If a same-record lower floor proves

   ```math
   U_{11}^{RPCov,car,SEL2}(N)+U_{13}^{RPF,bd}(N)
   \ge
   \underline M_{loss}^{SEL2,20}(N)
   ```

   cofinally, or proves the same conclusion using a same-record upper ceiling
   for \(\underline M_{loss}^{SEL2,20}(N)\), then adaptive Branch A fails.
4. If none of these estimates is printed, the predebit side is not decided by
   the current corpus.

Proof.

Item 1 is Theorem 7.3 and the margin condition in Theorem 1.3.  Item 2
follows because Paper 22's \(M_*\) is only the imported lower bound used by
the sufficient pass test; reaching that number removes the certified
\(M_*\)-margin but does not by itself prove the actual denominator is
nonpositive.  Item 3 is the true falsifier: adaptive Branch A needs
\(M_{pre,N}^{rc}=\underline M_{loss}^{SEL2,20}(N)-\mathcal L_N^{rc}>0\)
cofinally.  If the carried predebit reaches the actual loss floor, the
pre-surface denominator is nonpositive and the branch cannot pass.  Item 4
is simply the law of excluded hidden assumptions: no upper margin and no
lower floor means no pass and no falsification. `square`

### Theorem 9.6: Terminal Branch-A Pass Theorem

Adaptive Branch A is successful if the following two same-record source
packages hold on the high-\(\alpha\) `SEL2` row:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}XI\text{-}UNIF}
(C_{\xi'},\eta_*),
```

and

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}PRE\text{-}UNIF}(\Lambda)
\quad\text{with}\quad
\Lambda<M_*.
```

Under these hypotheses the default fixed-template battery \(n_0=1\) closes
adaptive Branch A.

Proof.

Theorem 9.2 gives \(\Theta_X=0<4/3\).  Theorem 9.5 gives
\(\Lambda_{pre}\le\Lambda<M_*\).  Apply the default fixed-template pass in
Section 8. `square`

### Theorem 9.7: Terminal Current-Corpus Verdict For Branch A

From the current Papers 13, 16, 19, 20, 21, 22, and Sections 1--9 of this
paper, adaptive Branch A is not an unconditional success and is not
falsified.  It is closed to the following terminal source frontier:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}XI\text{-}UNIF}
(C_{\xi'},\eta_*)
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}PRE\text{-}UNIF}(\Lambda<M_*).
}
```

Equivalently, without the uniform endpoint/corner decoration source and the
uniform RP/Cov+RPF predebit margin, no remaining algebraic or bookkeeping
step inside Branch A can complete the confinement proof.

Proof.

Step 1, the \(\Xi'\)-log attack, is executed by Sections 6 and 9.  The sharp
source is the endpoint/corner decoration activity \(\mathfrak X_N\).  Paper
19 provides the right finite-template mechanism on `SEL_0`, but Lemma 9.3
blocks spending it on the adaptive `SEL2` row without a selector-transfer
theorem.

Step 2, the area window, is already closed on the default fixed-template
battery with \(n_0=1\); if \(\Theta_X\) is finite but not \(<4/3\), Section 8
gives the exact fixed-area amplifier.  No area amplifier can repair an
infinite or unsourced \(\Theta_X\).

Step 3, the predebit attack, is executed by Sections 7 and 9.  Paper 16
supplies the RP/Cov ledger form, Paper 20 supplies the exact-entry RPF
ledger, and Papers 21--22 show that both remain carried without the
moving-row tail and RPF factorization estimates.  The exact combined
quantity is \(\Lambda_{pre}\).

Step 4, the pass test, is Section 8:
\(\Theta_X<4/3\) and \(\Lambda_{pre}<M_*\) close the default branch; the
amplified branch replaces \(4/3\) by \(2(n_0+1)/3\).

Step 5, the failure test, also appears in Sections 8 and 9.  A same-record
lower floor \(\Lambda_{pre}\ge M_*\) defeats the \(M_*\)-floor sufficient
test, but falsifies adaptive Branch A only if it reaches the actual
\(\underline M_{loss}^{SEL2,20}(N)\) denominator floor, or a same-record upper
ceiling for that floor.  A same-record surface lower floor can falsify only
the declared fixed-area subbranch.  The current corpus prints neither lower
floor.

Thus Branch A is mathematically closed as a source frontier, but not closed
as a successful confinement proof and not falsified.  Continuing Branch A
without proving one of the boxed source packages would only rename the same
obstruction. `square`

## 10. First Attempt To Prove The Terminal Source Packages

Section 9 named the two terminal packages.  This section pushes them once
more.  The goal is to separate the pieces that are genuinely closed by the
existing papers from the pieces that still require new same-record source
theorems.

### Definition 10.1: Adaptive Endpoint/Corner Geometry Gate

Define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XI\text{-}GEOM}(C_{\xi'}^A)
```

to mean that the fixed-template adaptive row of Definition 2.1 has a
uniform endpoint/corner collar ceiling

```math
\sup_{N\ge4096}\max_C c_{\Delta,N,C}^{end}
\le C_{\xi'}^A<\infty,
```

where \(c_{\Delta,N,C}^{end}\) is only the endpoint/corner part of the
surface decoration constant.  It does not include the surface KP activity
\(\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}\).

### Lemma 10.2: Fixed Templates Close Endpoint/Corner Geometry

On the fixed-template adaptive row,

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XI\text{-}GEOM}(C_{\xi'}^A)
```

holds for some finite constant \(C_{\xi'}^A\).

Proof.

Paper 19 Definition 8L.9A identifies the endpoint/corner constant
\(C_{\xi'}\) as a finite-template collar-excess constant: it is obtained by
maximizing over a finite list of endpoint and corner collar types, not by
evaluating a continuum field or a Wilson-loop law.  Lemma 8L.9A.1 proves the
corresponding statement for the centered square `SEL_0` template.  The proof
uses only finiteness of the local rectangular Creutz template, fixed collar
width in block units, and a finite list of corner/endpoint slots.

Definition 2.1 gives exactly the same kind of finite geometric data for the
adaptive row: the rectangular Creutz shape family is fixed before the final
inequalities, the root/collar attachment list does not grow with \(N\), and
the reduced support convention is fixed.  Changing the representation label
from \(F_4\) or a fixed \(\rho\) to \(F_N\) changes scalar coefficients, but
it does not create new geometric endpoint/corner slot types.  Therefore the
maximum endpoint/corner collar excess over the adaptive row is the maximum
of one finite list.  Call that maximum \(C_{\xi'}^A\). `square`

### Definition 10.3: Adaptive Decoration Activity Transfer

Define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XI\text{-}ACT\text{-}TRANS}(\eta_*)
```

to mean that the high-\(\alpha\), large-\(N\), `SEL2` pushed-forward scalar
law admits a uniform surface decoration KP activity bound

```math
\sup_{N\ge4096}\max_C\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}\le\eta_*<1.
```

This can be proved either directly on the adaptive `SEL2` law or by a
same-record domination/equality theorem transferring the Paper-19 decoration
activity audits to this adaptive law.  A formal analogy with the clean
`SEL_0` branch is not sufficient.

### Theorem 10.4: Exact Remaining Surface Source

The two gates

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XI\text{-}GEOM}(C_{\xi'}^A)
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XI\text{-}ACT\text{-}TRANS}(\eta_*)
```

imply

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}XI\text{-}UNIF}
(C_{\xi'}^A,\eta_*).
```

Consequently the default surface side of adaptive Branch A closes.

Proof.

Definition 9.1 has exactly two requirements: a uniform endpoint/corner
ceiling and a uniform subcritical decoration activity ceiling.  Lemma 10.2
supplies the first requirement.  Definition 10.3 supplies the second.  Then
Theorem 9.2 gives \(\Theta_X=0\), so Theorem 2.4 closes the default
\(n_0=1\) surface side. `square`

### Lemma 10.5: Pre-Execution Corpus Does Not Prove `XI-ACT-TRANS`

Before the adaptive cutoff construction of Section 11, the current imported
corpus does not prove
`P23-XI-ACT-TRANS(eta_*)`.

Proof.

Paper 19 Theorem 8L.8A proves the heat-kernel character-tail audit on the
clean `SEL_0` analytic import.  Paper 19 Theorem 8L.11A.22F.2 then closes
the surface decoration-growth audit on the same record law, using the same
finite-template decoration geometry, residual activity, and character-tail
activity.  This is a strong result, but it is explicitly same-record.

The adaptive row in this paper is the high-\(\alpha_N=1-1/N\), \(F_N\),
large-\(N\), `SEL2` row inherited from Paper 22.  None of Papers 19--23 prints
a theorem saying that the Paper-19 `SEL_0` residual and character-tail KP
activities dominate, equal, or uniformly control the adaptive `SEL2`
surface decoration activity.  Barandes alignment forbids treating the
intermediate template gas as ontology and then moving it between laws by
interpretation.  The needed comparison must be a theorem about pushed-forward
scalar records.  Since that theorem is not printed in the imported papers,
`XI-ACT-TRANS` remains open at the end of Section 10. `square`

### Definition 10.6: Uniform Predebit Zero Sources

Define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPCOV\text{-}TRANS0}
```

to mean that the Paper-16 RP/Cov ledger tails vanish uniformly on the
adaptive row:

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}
\limsup_{j\to\infty}\sum_{k\ge j}D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)=0,
```

and

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}
\limsup_{j\to\infty}\sup_g
\sum_{k\ge j}D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(N;g)=0.
```

Define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
```

to mean that the exact-entry residual factorization defect vanishes uniformly
on the same adaptive row:

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}(N)=0.
```

### Theorem 10.7: Zero Sources Close The Predebit Package

If

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPCOV\text{-}TRANS0}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
```

hold, then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}ADAPT\text{-}PRE\text{-}UNIF}(0)
```

holds.  In particular the predebit side closes because \(0<M_*\).

Proof.

Definition 7.1 identifies the RP/Cov ceiling
\(\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}\) with the cofinal limsup of the RP and
covariance moving-row tail sums.  `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0` says this ceiling is
zero.  Definition 7.1 also identifies \(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\) with
the cofinal limsup of the RPF factorization defect.  `P23-RPF-TRANS0` says
this ceiling is zero.  Therefore

```math
\Lambda_{pre}
=\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}
+\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}
=0,
```

which is `P23-ADAPT-PRE-UNIF(0)`. `square`

### Lemma 10.8: Current Corpus Does Not Prove The Uniform Zero Sources

The current corpus does not prove `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0` or
`P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

Proof.

Paper 16 Definition 9W.1C and Definition 9W.1G print the RP and covariance
ledger forms.  Theorems 9W.1D, 9W.1H, and 9W.1I show that those ledgers
imply the RP/Cov closure clauses when their summable vanishing tails are
available.  They do not, by themselves, evaluate the high-\(\alpha\),
large-\(N\), adaptive `SEL2` moving-row tail sums appearing in Definition
10.6.

Paper 21 Definition 33.3 and Theorem 33.4 isolate the RPF slot as a pure
same-law residual factorization defect after record availability is closed.
They set \(U_{13}^{RPF,car}=0\) only under `P21-U13-RPF-FACT0`; otherwise
they carry a finite template bound.  Paper 22 keeps the same slot carried.
No theorem in the current corpus proves the uniform adaptive \(N\to\infty\)
version of that factorization-zero statement. `square`

### Theorem 10.9: Terminal Source Frontier After The First Proof Attempt

After closing the finite endpoint/corner geometry in Lemma 10.2, adaptive
Branch A has exactly the following same-record live source gates:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XI\text{-}ACT\text{-}TRANS}(\eta_*),
\qquad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPCOV\text{-}TRANS0},
\qquad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}.
}
```

If all three hold, adaptive Branch A closes on the default fixed-template
battery.  If any one of them is unavailable, Branch A remains open at that
source gate.  At the end of Section 10, the imported corpus proves none of
the three and falsifies none of the three.  Section 11 then executes this
frontier and closes the first gate.

Proof.

Theorem 10.4 reduces `P23-ADAPT-XI-UNIF` to the already closed geometry gate
plus `XI-ACT-TRANS`.  Theorem 10.7 reduces
`P23-ADAPT-PRE-UNIF(Lambda<M_*)` to `RPCOV-TRANS0` and `RPF-TRANS0`, with
\(\Lambda=0\).  Theorem 9.6 then closes adaptive Branch A.  Lemmas 10.5 and
10.8 give the Section-10 negative statement: the needed same-record adaptive
transfer/zero theorems have not yet been printed. `square`

## 11. Executing The Three Live Gates

Section 10 left three gates.  This section executes them in order.  The
answer is mixed: the surface activity gate closes after declaring the
adaptive character cutoff; the two predebit zero gates do not close from the
present corpus.

### Definition 11.1: Adaptive Surface Activity Split

On the high-\(\alpha\) row of Definition 1.1, write the surface decoration
activity as the same-record sum

```math
\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}
\le
\eta_{res,N}^{A}
+
\eta_{ch,N}^{A},
```

where:

1. \(\eta_{res,N}^{A}\) is the large-field/residual KP activity measured in
   the same `SEL2` pushed-forward scalar law used by Paper 22 Lemma 34.3;
2. \(\eta_{ch,N}^{A}\) is the non-leading character-tail conversion activity
   measured by the same finite surface-entry decoration battery.

This is a scalar split of the decoration ledger.  It is not a decomposition
of a hidden surface field.

### Lemma 11.2: Uniform Adaptive Residual Activity Ceiling

For the adaptive row,

```math
\sup_{N\ge4096}\eta_{res,N}^{A}
\le
\eta_{res}^{A,*}
:=
{\log2\over2(20+\log2)}
<1.
```

Proof.

Paper 22 Lemma 34.3 is already on the same high-\(\alpha\) `SEL2` scalar law.
It proves

```math
\bar\eta_{res,20}(N)\le {1\over2}\tau_{20}(N),
```

with

```math
\tau_{20}(N)
=
{\log(1+F_{F_N}(s))\over20+\log(1+F_{F_N}(s))}.
```

The signal \(F_{F_N}(s)\) is positive and strictly below one because it is a
product of two factors in \((0,1)\).  Hence
\(\log(1+F_{F_N}(s))<\log2\), and the displayed uniform ceiling follows.
The ceiling is crude but same-record and independent of \(N\). `square`

### Definition 11.3: Adaptive Weyl-Casimir Character Cutoff

Fix the character-tail budget

```math
\eta_{ch}^{A,*}
:=
{1-\eta_{res}^{A,*}\over2}.
```

For each \(N\ge4096\), let

```math
C_W(N),\quad \nu_W(N),\quad R_W(N),\quad t_W(N),\quad a_{ch}(N)>0
```

be the row-\(N\) Weyl-Casimir tail constants supplied by the Paper-16
heat-kernel character-tail estimate for `SU(N)` after the finite
character-to-record norm and local record-label overhead have been absorbed
into the weighted tail.  Choose the representation cutoff schedule

```math
R_{N,j}
\ge
\max\left\{
{R_W(N)\over t_{i(j)}},
{2\over a_{ch}(N)t_{i(j)}}
\left[
\nu_W(N)\log{1\over t_{i(j)}}
+\log{C_W(N)\over\eta_{ch}^{A,*}}
\right]
\right\}
```

for all sufficiently fine \(j\) in the row \(N\) subsequence.

The schedule is allowed to depend on \(N\), but it is declared before the
Branch-A inequalities are spent.  It uses only compact-group heat-kernel tail
data and finite record-label overhead; it does not use an area law, mass gap,
or confinement assumption.

### Lemma 11.4: The Adaptive Character Tail Is Uniformly Subcritical

With the cutoff schedule of Definition 11.3,

```math
\sup_{N\ge4096}\eta_{ch,N}^{A}
\le
\eta_{ch}^{A,*}.
```

Proof.

For each fixed \(N\), Paper 19 Theorem 8L.8A applies to the compact group
`SU(N)` once the finite character-to-record norm, finite Clebsch-Gordan
multiplicities, and local record-label overhead of the declared finite
surface-entry battery are absorbed into the weighted character tail.  The
constants may depend on \(N\), since the rank changes, but for every finite
\(N\) they are finite and \(a_{ch}(N)>0\).

The cutoff in Definition 11.3 is exactly the Paper-19/Weyl-Casimir cutoff
with \(\eta_{ch}^{A,*}\) substituted for the target tail.  Therefore, for
each \(N\),

```math
\limsup_j C_{ch,N,j}Tail_{CE,N,j}
\le
\eta_{ch}^{A,*}.
```

Taking the supremum over \(N\) after the rowwise limsup preserves the same
budget because the budget is independent of \(N\).  The proof does not
assert uniform rank-independent Weyl constants; it lets the declared cutoff
schedule absorb the \(N\)-dependence. `square`

### Theorem 11.5: `P23-XI-ACT-TRANS` Is Closed By The Adaptive Cutoff

The adaptive row satisfies

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}XI\text{-}ACT\text{-}TRANS}(\eta_*^A),
```

where

```math
\eta_*^A
:=
\eta_{res}^{A,*}+\eta_{ch}^{A,*}
=
{1+\eta_{res}^{A,*}\over2}
<1.
```

Consequently the surface side of adaptive Branch A closes on the default
fixed-template battery.

Proof.

Definition 11.1 gives
\(\eta_{dec,N,C}^{surf}\le\eta_{res,N}^A+\eta_{ch,N}^A\).  Lemma 11.2 gives
the uniform residual ceiling \(\eta_{res}^{A,*}\).  Lemma 11.4 gives the
uniform character-tail ceiling \(\eta_{ch}^{A,*}\).  Their sum is
\(\eta_*^A=(1+\eta_{res}^{A,*})/2<1\).  This is precisely Definition 10.3.
Theorem 10.4 and Lemma 10.2 then give `P23-ADAPT-XI-UNIF`, hence
\(\Theta_X=0\). `square`

### Lemma 11.6: The Adaptive Cutoff Does Not Smuggle A New Surface Theorem

The proof of Theorem 11.5 is admissible under the no-smuggling boundary.

Proof.

The residual ceiling is Paper 22 Lemma 34.3, a scalar estimate on the same
high-\(\alpha\) `SEL2` pushed-forward law.  The character cutoff is the
standard compact-group heat-kernel tail construction used in Paper 19
Theorem 8L.8A, applied row by row to `SU(N)` with all rank-dependent finite
label overhead absorbed by \(R_{N,j}\).  A larger cutoff changes the finite
readout battery, not the physical law, and it is chosen before the final
Branch-A inequalities are evaluated.  No Wilson-loop area law, mass gap,
continuum Yang-Mills measure, or off-record Markov factorization is used.
`square`

### Definition 11.7: Uniform Moving-Row RP/Cov Rate Gate

`P23-RPCOV-RATE-A` is the assertion that there are row-shell envelopes

```math
r_{RP;N,j,k}^{A},
\qquad
r_{Cov;N,j,k}^{A}(g),
```

such that

```math
D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)\le r_{RP;N,j,k}^{A},
```

```math
D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(N;g)
\le r_{Cov;N,j,k}^{A}(g),
```

and

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}
\sum_{k\ge j}r_{RP;N,j,k}^{A}=0,
```

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}
\sup_g\sum_{k\ge j}r_{Cov;N,j,k}^{A}(g)=0.
```

### Theorem 11.8: `RPCOV-TRANS0` Is Equivalent To Uniform Moving-Row Rates

The gate `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0` holds if `P23-RPCOV-RATE-A` holds.  Conversely,
if `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0` holds, then `P23-RPCOV-RATE-A` holds by taking the
envelopes equal to the defects themselves.

Proof.

The forward implication is immediate from Definition 10.6 and the displayed
majorants.  The converse uses the nonnegative defects
\(D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)\) and \(D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(N;g)\) as
their own envelopes. `square`

### Theorem 11.9: Present Answer For `RPCOV-TRANS0`

The present corpus does not prove `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0`.

Proof.

Paper 16 prints the correct RP and covariance ledger forms.  Paper 21
Definition 29.1 then identifies the stronger data actually needed by the
`SEL2` moving row: explicit row-shell envelopes whose diagonal tails vanish.
Paper 21 Lemma 29.2 proves that the Paper-16 fixed-battery ledgers do not, as
written, supply those moving-row rate data.  Paper 22 repeats the same
decision for the fixed \(N=4096\) and adaptive Branch-A worksheets.  Section
11 adds no new estimate for the projective, regulator, volume, readout,
approximant, or covariance-buffer defects.  Hence the equivalence in Theorem
11.8 leaves `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0` unproved. `square`

### Definition 11.10: Uniform RPF Connected-Cumulant Gate

`P23-RPF-CKP0-A` is the assertion that the exact-entry residual
factorization defect admits a same-record connected-cumulant KP envelope

```math
\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)
\le
A_N e^{-\mu_N m_j}
```

with a cofinal schedule \(m_j\to\infty\) such that

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}A_N e^{-\mu_N m_j}=0.
```

This is the uniform adaptive version of the Paper-21
`P21-U13-RPF-FACT0` route.

### Theorem 11.11: Present Answer For `RPF-TRANS0`

`P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds if `P23-RPF-CKP0-A` holds.  The present corpus does
not prove `P23-RPF-CKP0-A` and therefore does not prove `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

Proof.

The first statement follows by substituting the connected-cumulant envelope
in Definition 10.6.  For the present-corpus statement, Paper 21 Definition
33.3 isolates `RPF` as a pure same-law residual factorization defect, and
Theorem 33.4 states that it is zero only under `P21-U13-RPF-FACT0`; otherwise
one may carry a finite template bound.  The finite Bell-number/moment-cumulant
ceiling printed there proves finiteness, not decay to zero, and does not by
itself certify a bound below the tiny adaptive predebit margin
\(M_*=0.00317259975\ldots\).  Paper 22 Lemma 36.3 preserves the same
decision.  No theorem in Papers 13, 16, 19, 20, 21, 22, or the preceding
sections of this paper supplies the uniform adaptive connected-cumulant decay
gate above. `square`

### Theorem 11.12: Branch-A Execution Verdict After Steps 1--5

After executing the five-step attack, adaptive Branch A has the following
status.

1. `P23-XI-ACT-TRANS(eta_*^A)` is proved by the adaptive residual ceiling and
   the rowwise Weyl-Casimir character cutoff.
2. Therefore the whole surface side of adaptive Branch A closes with
   \(\Theta_X=0\) on the default fixed-template battery.
3. `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0` is not proved; it is equivalent to the missing uniform
   moving-row RP/Cov rate data of Theorem 11.8.
4. `P23-RPF-TRANS0` is not proved; it is reduced to the missing uniform
   connected-cumulant factorization decay gate of Definition 11.10.
5. Consequently adaptive Branch A is not an unconditional confinement proof
   from the current corpus.  It is also not falsified, because no same-record
   lower floor proves that the RP/Cov plus RPF predebit reaches the actual
   denominator floor \(\underline M_{loss}^{SEL2,20}(N)\).

The live frontier is therefore exactly

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPCOV\text{-}TRANS0}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}.
}
```

Proof.

Items 1 and 2 are Theorem 11.5.  Items 3 and 4 are Theorems 11.9 and 11.11.
Item 5 follows from Theorem 9.5: without a predebit ceiling below \(M_*\)
there is no pass, and without a same-record lower floor reaching the actual
loss denominator there is no falsification. `square`

## 12. Predebit Obstruction Settlement

Section 11 deliberately stopped before using a new selector move.  It asked
whether the imported fixed-battery Paper-16 RP/Cov ledgers already imply the
moving-row tails on the original labels.  They do not.  The remaining question
is sharper:

Can the adaptive high-\(\alpha\) row spend a cofinal diagonal shell selector
without changing the pushed-forward scalar law?

The answer is yes for RP/Cov and no, by the current corpus, for RPF.  This
section records that settlement.

### Definition 12.1: Reduced RP/Cov Live Slots

On the adaptive Branch-A row, import the Paper-21 reduced `T_11` convention
row by row in \(N\).  The reflection-positivity defect is

```math
D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)
=
\eta_{projRP;j,k}^{SEL2}(N)
+\eta_{regRP;j,k}^{SEL2}(N)
+\eta_{volRP;j,k}^{SEL2}(N).
```

The covariance defect is

```math
D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(g;N)
=
\eta_{exactCov;j,k}^{11}(g;N)
+\eta_{blockCov;j,k}^{11}(g;N)
+\eta_{projCov;j,k}^{SEL2}(g;N)
+\eta_{regCov;j,k}^{SEL2}(g;N)
+\eta_{volCov;j,k}^{SEL2}(g;N)
+\eta_{appCov;j,k}^{11}(g;N).
```

The following pieces are not live:

```math
\eta_{ctRP}^{11}=\eta_{binRP}^{11}=0,
\qquad
\eta_{ctCov}^{11}=\eta_{binCov}^{11}=0.
```

They are either already charged in the reduced Paper-12/Paper-21 transport
ledger or eliminated by exact scalar-record conventions.  No perimeter,
cusp, readout, decoration, or surface-entry term is allowed in this slot.

For exact hypercubic motions preserving the chosen finite template,

```math
\eta_{exactCov}^{11}
=
\eta_{appCov}^{11}
=
\eta_{blockCov}^{11}
=0,
```

so only the projective, regulator, and volume-buffer covariance pieces remain.
For larger admissible motion families those three exact-template zeroes are
not automatic; they must be included in the covariance row ledger.

### Definition 12.2: Rowwise Paper-16 Ledger Import

`P23-RPCOV-ROWLEDGER-A` is the assertion that, for each fixed \(N\) and each
fixed finite row battery \(j\), the reduced defects of Definition 12.1 satisfy
the Paper-16 fixed-battery tail limits

```math
\sum_{k\ge K}
D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)
\longrightarrow0,
\qquad K\to\infty,
```

and

```math
\sup_{g\in Euc_{adm}}
\sum_{k\ge K}
D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(g;N)
\longrightarrow0,
\qquad K\to\infty.
```

The second display is understood with \(Euc_{adm}\) replaced by the exact
hypercubic subgroup if the active branch declares only exact hypercubic
covariance at this finite-table stage.

Paper 16 supplies the ledger form.  Paper 21 Lemma 28.4 proves the diagonal
zero consequence once such fixed-row tails and a cofinal shell selector are
available.  Paper 21 Lemma 29.2 only blocks the stronger claim that the
original moving labels \(k\ge j\) already carry a uniform rate envelope.

### Definition 12.3: The RP/Cov Diagonal Shell Selector

For each \(N\) and \(j\), choose thresholds

```math
K_{N,j}^{RP}\ge j,
\qquad
K_{N,j}^{Cov}\ge j
```

such that

```math
\sum_{k\ge K_{N,j}^{RP}}
D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)
< {1\over 2j},
```

and

```math
\sup_{g\in Euc_{adm}}
\sum_{k\ge K_{N,j}^{Cov}}
D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(g;N)
< {1\over 2j}.
```

Set

```math
K_{N,j}^{RPCov}:=\max\{K_{N,j}^{RP},K_{N,j}^{Cov}\}.
```

The `P23-RPCOV-DIAGSEL-A` selector is the cofinal relabeling that pairs row
battery \(j\) with shell lower bound \(K_{N,j}^{RPCov}\) before evaluating the
adaptive Branch-A inequalities.

This selector is a scheduling of already-imported finite scalar records.  It
does not alter the pushed-forward law, add a continuum measure, change the
representation channel, or spend a result from a different selector branch.

### Lemma 12.4: Admissibility Of The Diagonal Selector

`P23-RPCOV-DIAGSEL-A` is Barandes-aligned and admissible for adaptive Branch A.

Proof.

The primitive object is still the whole-process finite scalar-record law.  The
selector changes only which cofinal refinement shell is paired with a fixed
finite row battery before the final scalar inequality is evaluated.  This is
the same kind of cofinal scheduling already used in Section 11 for the
adaptive Weyl-Casimir character cutoff: the cutoff is declared before the
final pass inequality and then kept on the same pushed-forward law.

No local subprocess law, off-record Markov kernel, Wilson-loop area law,
continuum Yang-Mills measure, or independent covariance model is introduced.
The row battery, scalar records, and admissible motion family are fixed before
the defect tails are summed.  Hence the selector is bookkeeping over the same
records, not a physical-law replacement. `square`

### Theorem 12.5: `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0`

Assume `P23-RPCOV-ROWLEDGER-A` and use the admissible selector
`P23-RPCOV-DIAGSEL-A`.  Then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPCOV\text{-}TRANS0}
```

holds, and the adaptive RP/Cov predebit is zero:

```math
\overline\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}=0.
```

Proof.

For fixed \(N,j\), Definition 12.2 gives tails tending to zero as the shell
lower bound \(K\) goes to infinity.  Therefore the thresholds in Definition
12.3 exist.  On the relabeled cofinal schedule,

```math
\sum_{k\ge K_{N,j}^{RPCov}}
D_{11;j,k}^{RP,red,SEL2}(N)
\le {1\over 2j},
```

and

```math
\sup_{g\in Euc_{adm}}
\sum_{k\ge K_{N,j}^{RPCov}}
D_{11;j,k}^{Cov,red,SEL2}(g;N)
\le {1\over 2j}.
```

After the cofinal relabeling, the symbol \(j\) in the moving-row tail
functional denotes the paired shell lower bound \(K_{N,j}^{RPCov}\).  Thus

```math
\Lambda_{11}^{RPCov}(N)
\le
\limsup_{j\to\infty}{1\over j}
=0
```

for every fixed \(N\).  Taking the outer cofinal limsup in \(N\) preserves
zero.  This is precisely `P23-RPCOV-TRANS0`. `square`

### Corollary 12.6: What Was Actually Settled

The RP/Cov obstruction was never a new physical positivity, mass-gap, or
surface theorem.  It was a scheduling question:

1. on the original moving labels, Paper 21 Lemma 29.2 correctly says the
   current papers do not print uniform rate envelopes;
2. on a declared cofinal diagonal shell schedule, Paper 21 Lemma 28.4 applies;
3. Section 12 makes that diagonal schedule explicit for adaptive Branch A.

Therefore the RP/Cov slot is closed on the adaptive branch once the
fixed-row Paper-16 ledger import of Definition 12.2 is accepted on the same
scalar law.

### Definition 12.7: Final RPF Source Gate

The remaining exact-entry factorization gate is

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}=0.
```

Equivalently, it is enough to prove the uniform connected-cumulant KP source
gate

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CKP0\text{-}A},
```

meaning that the same pushed-forward adaptive `SEL2` law admits constants or a
cofinal schedule with

```math
\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)
\le
A_N e^{-\mu_N m_j},
\qquad
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}
A_N e^{-\mu_N m_j}=0.
```

This is the adaptive version of Paper 21's `P21-U13-RPF-FACT0`/connected
cumulant route.

### Theorem 12.8: The RPF Obstruction Is Not A Diagonal-Shell Problem

The diagonal-shell selector that closes RP/Cov does not close RPF.  The
present corpus proves no same-record theorem implying
`P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

Proof.

RP/Cov defects are transport tails indexed by a fixed row battery and a later
refinement shell.  Once fixed-row summability is available, a cofinal shell
selector can push the tail below \(1/j\).

The RPF slot is different.  Paper 20 Definition 4.3A.72 and Paper 21
Definition 33.3 identify it as a residual factorization defect in the
exact-entry law.  Paper 21 Theorem 33.4 says it vanishes only under
`P21-U13-RPF-FACT0`, for example by the connected-cumulant KP criterion of
Paper 13 Theorem 7.30AS.  The finite Bell-number bound in Paper 21 gives
finiteness of a template cumulant sum; it does not give decay to zero along
the adaptive high-\(\alpha\), large-\(N\) row.

Thus a shell relabeling can close transport tails but cannot manufacture
connected-cumulant factorization decay.  No theorem in Papers 13, 16, 20, 21,
22, or Sections 1--12 of this paper proves `P23-RPF-CKP0-A` on the same
adaptive scalar law. `square`

### Theorem 12.9: Final Branch-A Obstruction After Settlement

After Sections 6--12, adaptive Branch A has the following rigorous status.

1. The surface side is closed with \(\Theta_X=0\).
2. The RP/Cov predebit is closed by `P23-RPCOV-DIAGSEL-A`, assuming the
   fixed-row Paper-16 ledger import of Definition 12.2.
3. The only live pass obstruction is the exact-entry residual factorization
   gate

   ```math
   \boxed{\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}.}
   ```

4. If `P23-RPF-TRANS0` is proved, then `P23-ADAPT-PRE-UNIF(0)` holds and
   adaptive Branch A closes the Paper-20 surface prefactor gate.
5. If a same-record lower floor proves

   ```math
   \overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*,
   ```

   then adaptive Branch A is falsified as a route to the Paper-20 gate.
6. The current corpus proves neither 4 nor 5.

Consequently Paper 23 settles all bookkeeping and transport obstructions for
adaptive Branch A.  The remaining issue is not a hidden constant: it is the
single named source theorem `P23-RPF-TRANS0`, i.e. same-law connected-cumulant
factorization decay for the exact-entry residual.

Proof.

Item 1 is Theorem 11.5.  Item 2 is Theorem 12.5.  Item 3 is Theorem 12.8.
Item 4 follows from Corollary 7.4 and Theorem 1.3.  Item 5 is the negative
alternative of Theorem 9.5 with the RP/Cov ceiling now zero.  Item 6 is the
current-corpus verdict of Theorem 12.8. `square`

## 13. Final RPF Settlement

This section settles the remaining obstruction in the only honest sense
available from the current source stack.  It proves the exact positive theorem
that would close RPF, then proves that the hypotheses already closed in this
paper do not imply that theorem.  Thus adaptive Branch A is not waiting on a
hidden bookkeeping constant.  It is waiting on a genuinely new same-record
connected-cumulant theorem.

### Definition 13.1: Adaptive RPF Weighted Cumulant Norm

For a fixed adaptive row \(N\) and exact-entry battery \(j\), let
\({\mathcal X}_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)\) be the finite connected block-template list
of Paper 21 Definition 33.1, transported to the adaptive \(SU(N)\) row.  Let
\(\kappa_X^{SEL2}(N,j)\) be the connected residual cumulant of the scalar
records in \(B_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)\).

For every connected set \(X\), define the template coefficient weight

```math
W_{N,j}(X)
:=
\sum_{\Gamma:\,X\subseteq\Gamma}
|c_{\Gamma,X}^{tpl}(N,j)|.
```

For \(\mu>0\), set

```math
{\mathcal K}_{RPF}(N,j;\mu)
:=
\sum_X
W_{N,j}(X)\,
|\kappa_X^{SEL2}(N,j)|\,
e^{\mu(|X|+\operatorname{diam}X)}.
```

The sum is over connected templates in the row-\(j\) RPF battery.  If a
template is absent, its weight is zero.  This is the total finite-template
norm needed for the exact-entry debit.  The stronger Paper-13 KP norm is the
corresponding local \(\sup_x\) version; either one may be used if it dominates
the displayed total template norm on the declared battery.

### Theorem 13.2: Positive Closure Criterion For RPF

Assume there exists a cofinal choice of \(\mu_N>0\) such that

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}
{\mathcal K}_{RPF}(N,j;\mu_N)=0.
```

Then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
```

holds.  Consequently adaptive Branch A closes the predebit side with
`P23-ADAPT-PRE-UNIF(0)`.

Proof.

Paper 21 Definition 33.3 bounds the pure RPF factorization defect by the
template cumulant sum

```math
\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)
\le
C_{RPF,j}^{tpl}(N)
=
\sum_{\Gamma}\sum_{X\subseteq\Gamma}
|c_{\Gamma,X}^{tpl}(N,j)|\,|\kappa_X^{SEL2}(N,j)|.
```

By Definition 13.1 this sum is bounded directly by
\({\mathcal K}_{RPF}(N,j;\mu_N)\), since
\(e^{-\mu_N(|X|+\operatorname{diam}X)}\le1\).  Hence the assumed cofinal
vanishing of \({\mathcal K}_{RPF}\) implies

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}
\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)=0.
```

This is Definition 12.7.  The predebit conclusion follows from Theorem 12.9.
`square`

### Lemma 13.3: What The Current Corpus Actually Bounds

The current source stack supplies only the finite Bell-type bound

```math
|\kappa_X^{SEL2}(N,j)|
\le
{\mathfrak B}_{|X|}
```

for normalized scalar records, together with whatever finite template
coefficient sum is declared in `P21-U13-RPF-BD`.  It does not imply

```math
{\mathcal K}_{RPF}(N,j;\mu)\to0
```

for any cofinal adaptive schedule.

Proof.

Paper 21 Definition 33.3 gives the Bell-number moment-cumulant ceiling and
explicitly states that it is a finite bound, not a locality or KP-smallness
theorem.  Paper 13 Definition 7.30AR states the missing positive hypothesis:
exponential connected-cumulant decay plus KP polymer smallness.  Paper 22
Lemma 36.3 then records that the RPF slot cannot be spent as zero from the
present papers.  No theorem in Papers 13, 20, 21, 22, or Sections 1--12 of
this paper upgrades Bell finiteness into decay of \({\mathcal K}_{RPF}\).
`square`

### Definition 13.4: Common-Mode RPF Completion

Fix any finite adaptive row battery whose already closed coordinates satisfy
the surface, RP/Cov, block-convergence, central-extraction, and
whole-process-compatibility clauses used in Sections 1--12.  A common-mode
RPF completion adjoins to the RPF residual battery a centered normalized
scalar record \(R_x\in\{-1,1\}\) at each block \(x\) by choosing one global
Bernoulli variable \(Z\) with

```math
\mathbb P(Z=1)=\mathbb P(Z=-1)={1\over2},
\qquad
R_x:=Z.
```

The already closed coordinates are taken independent of \(Z\), and their
joint law is left unchanged.

This is a finite scalar-record completion.  It is not asserted to be the
physical Yang-Mills law.  Its purpose is logical: it tests which conclusions
follow from the already stated source hypotheses alone.

### Lemma 13.5: Common Mode Preserves Closed Gates But Violates RPF Decay

The common-mode completion leaves all previously closed non-RPF source gates
unchanged, while producing non-decaying connected residual cumulants:

```math
\kappa_{\{x,y\}}^{SEL2}=1
```

for every pair of distinct block sites \(x,y\) in the common-mode residual
subbattery.

Proof.

All already closed coordinates are independent of \(Z\) and have the same
law as before.  Therefore any source gate depending only on those coordinates
is unchanged: the surface activity estimates, RP/Cov transport tails, block
record availability, central extraction, and whole-process compatibility
clauses see the same scalar records as before.

For the RPF residual records, \(\mathbb E[R_x]=0\) and
\(\mathbb E[R_xR_y]=\mathbb E[Z^2]=1\).  Hence the two-point connected
cumulant is

```math
\kappa_{\{x,y\}}
=
\mathbb E[R_xR_y]-\mathbb E[R_x]\mathbb E[R_y]
=1.
```

This value is independent of the separation of \(x\) and \(y\), so no
exponential connected-cumulant decay and no vanishing weighted RPF norm can be
deduced from the previously closed coordinates alone. `square`

### Theorem 13.6: Current-Source Independence Of `P23-RPF-TRANS0`

`P23-RPF-TRANS0` is independent of the source package closed in Sections
1--12.  More precisely, the closed package admits:

1. a product residual completion with all RPF connected cumulants zero; and
2. a common-mode residual completion with non-decaying RPF connected cumulants.

Therefore no proof of `P23-RPF-TRANS0` can be obtained from the current source
package without adding a new same-record connected-cumulant hypothesis such as
the criterion in Theorem 13.2.

Proof.

The product completion takes the RPF residual records independent across
blocks, centered, and independent of the already closed coordinates.  Then all
connected residual cumulants of order at least two vanish, so RPF factorizes.

The common-mode completion is Definition 13.4.  By Lemma 13.5 it preserves the
closed coordinates but has non-decaying connected cumulants.  The two
completions agree on the data used by the already closed source gates and
disagree on RPF.  Hence those gates do not logically imply
`P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

This is a same-record no-go statement.  It does not compose local Markov
subprocesses, does not import a continuum Yang-Mills measure, and does not
assert a physical hidden variable in the actual branch.  It says only that the
current hypotheses do not determine the exact-entry residual cumulants.
`square`

### Theorem 13.7: Final Verdict For Adaptive Branch A

Adaptive Branch A is settled as a source campaign.

1. It is not an unconditional continuum Yang-Mills confinement proof from the
   current corpus.
2. It is not falsified as an actual branch, because no theorem computes a
   same-record lower floor

   ```math
   \overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*.
   ```

3. It is parked at the irreducible source theorem

   ```math
   \boxed{\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}}
   ```

   or equivalently at a same-law connected-cumulant KP theorem of the form
   Theorem 13.2.
4. Any future continuation that keeps Branch A alive must prove
   either a sufficient weighted-cumulant vanishing theorem such as Theorem
   13.2 or a same-law KP factorization theorem such as the actual-law route of
   Section 14.  Otherwise it must leave Branch A and open a different branch.

Proof.

Sections 10--12 closed the surface and RP/Cov transport sides.  Theorem 13.2
states exactly what would close the remaining RPF side.  Lemma 13.3 shows the
current corpus does not supply that estimate.  Theorem 13.6 shows the estimate
is not a consequence of the already closed source package.  Therefore the
campaign has reached a genuine irreducible source theorem, not a removable
bookkeeping obstruction. `square`

## 14. A Viable Actual-Law Route To `RPF-TRANS0`

Section 13 used the strongest easy sufficient condition:
\({\mathcal K}_{RPF}\to0\).  That is not the only route, and it is probably
too strong.  Paper 13's `RPF` gate does not require every local residual
cumulant to vanish.  It requires that the exact residual density be rewritten
as a compatible polymer gas with KP-small activities on the same pushed-forward
law.  Local connected cumulants may remain nonzero; they are allowed to become
local polymer activities.

Thus the most credible way to prove `P23-RPF-TRANS0` on the actual adaptive
`SEL2` pushed-forward law is not "all cumulants go to zero."  It is:

```text
same-law residual cumulants
  -> exact cumulant-to-polymer representation
  -> uniform KP smallness
  -> RPF factorization defect equals zero.
```

### Definition 14.1: Actual-Law RPF Polymer Transform

For the adaptive row \(N\) and exact-entry battery \(j\), let
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\) be the actual pushed-forward scalar law and let
\(\{R_x^{N,j}\}_{x\in\Lambda_{N,j}}\) be the centered normalized residual
records in the RPF battery.

`P23-RPF-POLY-ACT` is the assertion that the finite residual density admits an
exact cumulant-to-polymer rewrite on this same law:

```math
\log
\mathbb E_{\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}}
\exp\left(\sum_{x\in\Lambda}h_xR_x^{N,j}\right)
```
