```math
=
\sum_{\Gamma\subseteq\Lambda\ {\rm conn}}
\Psi_{\Gamma}^{N,j}(h_\Gamma),
```

where every \(\Psi_{\Gamma}^{N,j}\) is a finite polynomial or absolutely
convergent finite cumulant series built only from cumulants of the records
\(R_x^{N,j}\) under \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).

This is not a new process law.  It is the finite moment-cumulant identity read
as a polymer transform on the already declared scalar records.

### Definition 14.2: Actual-Law RPF KP Smallness

`P23-RPF-ACTUAL-KP(q,a)` holds if `P23-RPF-POLY-ACT` holds and, cofinally in
\((N,j)\), the polymer activities at the source value used by the RPF residual
satisfy

```math
\sup_x
\sum_{\Gamma\ni x}
|\Psi_{\Gamma}^{N,j}|\,
e^{a|\Gamma|}
\le q<1.
```

The constants \(q<1\) and \(a>0\) must be certified on the same adaptive
`SEL2` pushed-forward law.  They may not be imported from a continuum
Yang-Mills measure, Wilson-loop area law, mass gap, or auxiliary Markov
subprocess.

### Theorem 14.3: Actual KP Smallness Proves `RPF-TRANS0`

If `P23-RPF-ACTUAL-KP(q,a)` holds for some \(q<1\), then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
```

holds.

Proof.

The exact cumulant-to-polymer rewrite gives the residual factorization required
by Paper 13 Definition 7.30AG.  The displayed \(q<1\) bound is precisely the
KP smallness condition used in Paper 13 Definition 7.30AR.  Paper 13 Theorem
7.30AS then proves `RPF` for the exact-entry residual.  Paper 21 Theorem 33.4
identifies that conclusion with the zero branch of the pure same-law RPF
factorization defect:

```math
\epsilon_{RPF,j}^{SEL2}(N)=0
```

cofinally after the declared battery is frozen.  Hence
\(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}=0\), which is `P23-RPF-TRANS0`. `square`

### Definition 14.4: Same-Record Dobrushin/KP Certificate

The most direct finite way to prove `P23-RPF-ACTUAL-KP(q,a)` is the following
same-record influence certificate.

For residual blocks \(x,y\), define \(I_{xy}^{N,j}\) to be the variation
influence of the outside residual coordinate \(y\) on the conditional law of
the residual coordinate \(x\), computed inside the finite pushed-forward law
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  Set

```math
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
:=
\sup_x
\sum_y e^{a\,d(x,y)}I_{xy}^{N,j}.
```

`P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT(q,a)` is the assertion that

```math
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
\le q<1.
```

Every conditional probability in this definition is a finite scalar record of
the actual pushed-forward law, possibly after the RPF battery is enlarged
before the selector is evaluated.

### Theorem 14.5: Dobrushin Certificate Sources Actual KP

`P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT(q,a)` implies `P23-RPF-ACTUAL-KP(q',a')` for some
\(q'<1\) and \(a'>0\), after possibly reducing \(a\) and increasing \(q\)
inside the strict margin.

Proof.

This is the finite Dobrushin-Shlosman cluster-expansion implication applied to
the declared scalar residual battery.  Since the state space is finite at each
\((N,j)\), the conditional probabilities and influences are ordinary finite
numbers.  A weighted influence norm strictly below one gives uniqueness of the
finite-volume Gibbs specification, exponential decay of connected residual
cumulants in the weighted graph metric, and an absolutely convergent
cluster/polymer expansion for the logarithmic moment-generating function.
Those activities obey a KP bound with slightly weakened constants
\((q',a')\).  No continuum measure or local Markov factorization is used; the
argument is a finite scalar-record theorem about \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).
`square`

### Definition 14.6: Paper-16 Transfer Route For The Actual Law

`P23-RPF-KP16-XFER(q,a)` is the source package asserting that the Paper-16
clean finite-template analytic worksheet transfers to the actual RPF residual
battery:

1. each RPF residual atom \(R_x^{N,j}\) is localized in a uniformly bounded
   block collar after `BC`, `CE`, `WP`, and the RP/Cov diagonal selector;
2. the Paper-16 clean residual activity and character-tail estimates dominate
   the RPF residual activities on the same pushed-forward `SEL2` law;
3. the norm-conversion surcharge from Paper-16 residual variables to the RPF
   residual records is finite and absorbed into \(q<1\);
4. the resulting finite influence matrix satisfies
   `P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT(q,a)`.

This is the realistic transfer theorem.  It does not assert new physics; it
identifies the RPF exact-entry residual records with the analytic finite-row
objects that Paper 16 already knows how to control, and it does so under the
actual adaptive law.

### Theorem 14.7: The Actual-Law Proof Path

The following implication is the viable route to proving the obstruction on
the actual adaptive `SEL2` pushed-forward law:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}KP16\text{-}XFER}(q,a)
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOBRUSHIN\text{-}ACT}(q,a)
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTUAL\text{-}KP}(q',a')
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}.
```

Thus the next proof-producing task is not to make the Bell cumulant ceiling
smaller.  It is to prove the transfer package `P23-RPF-KP16-XFER(q,a)` by a
finite same-record influence table for the actual RPF residual atoms.

Proof.

The first implication is the definition of the transfer package.  The second
is Theorem 14.5.  The third is Theorem 14.3.  All arrows are same-record
finite statements on \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\). `square`

### Corollary 14.8: Work Order For The Actual Proof

To prove `P23-RPF-TRANS0`, do the following, in this order.

1. Print the actual residual atoms \(R_x^{N,j}\) in the adaptive RPF battery.
2. Prove their bounded-collar localization after the already closed `BC`,
   `CE`, `WP`, and RP/Cov diagonal gates.
3. Compute the finite influence entries \(I_{xy}^{N,j}\) under the actual
   pushed-forward law, not under an auxiliary law.
4. Use Paper-16 analytic constants to bound the weighted row sum
   \(\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)\).
5. Prove a strict uniform margin \(q<1\).

If step 5 passes, adaptive Branch A closes.  If step 5 fails with a certified
lower floor large enough to force \(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\), then
adaptive Branch A is falsified.  If the influence table cannot be printed on
the actual law, Branch A remains parked at `P23-RPF-KP16-XFER`, not at an
unidentified obstruction.

## 15. Literal RPF Atoms And The Finite Influence Row

Section 14 left one possible ambiguity: what exactly are the "actual RPF
residual atoms" before a factorization theorem has been proved?  This section
removes that ambiguity.  On every finite adaptive row, the pushed-forward
scalar law itself prints a canonical finite interaction expansion by
Möbius/inclusion-exclusion on the declared residual battery.  The RPF
problem is therefore not whether atoms exist.  They do.  The problem is
whether their oscillations satisfy a same-law weighted row-sum bound below
one.

This is the Barandes-aligned form of the problem: the atoms are not hidden
subprocesses.  They are finite scalar functions extracted from the complete
pushed-forward record law.

### Definition 15.1: Actual RPF Residual Density

Fix an adaptive row \(N\) and exact-entry battery \(j\).  Let
\(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) be the over-refined finite vertex cover of all block,
collar, plaquette-character, and residual records used by the Paper-13 `RPF`
gate after `BC`, `CE`, `WP`, and the RP/Cov diagonal selector have been
applied.  Let

```math
\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}
```

be the actual pushed-forward scalar law on the finite compact record space
\(\Omega_{N,j}\), and let \(\lambda_{N,j}\) be the corresponding finite
reference Haar/readout measure on the same record coordinates.

On the essential support of \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\), write

```math
d\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}
=
p_{N,j}(\omega)\,d\lambda_{N,j}(\omega).
```

Let \(K_p^{CE,N,j}\) denote the central one-plaquette factor already selected
by the `CE` gate.  The exact RPF residual density is

```math
{\mathcal R}_{N,j}(\omega)
:=
Z_{N,j}\,
{p_{N,j}(\omega)
\over
\prod_{p\in P_{N,j}}K_p^{CE,N,j}(\omega_p)},
```

where \(Z_{N,j}\) normalizes the residual expectation.  Set

```math
H_{N,j}(\omega):=\log {\mathcal R}_{N,j}(\omega)
```

on the essential support.  If the density is zero on a null boundary, all
oscillations below are essential oscillations on that support.  No auxiliary
measure is introduced.

### Definition 15.2: Literal Conditional-Interaction Atoms

Choose a base configuration \(o\in\Omega_{N,j}\) in the essential support.
For every nonempty finite \(A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}\), define

```math
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A)
:=
\sum_{B\subseteq A}
(-1)^{|A|-|B|}
H_{N,j}(\omega_B,o_{A\setminus B},o_{V_{RPF}^{N,j}\setminus A}).
```

The literal RPF atom supported on \(A\) is the centered scalar record

```math
R_A^{N,j}
:=
\Phi_A^{N,j}
-
\mathbb E_{\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}}\Phi_A^{N,j}.
```

The printed atom list is

```math
{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}
:=
\{A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}: A\ne\emptyset,\ 
  \Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0\}.
```

Thus the \(R_x^{N,j}\) shorthand of Section 14 is replaced by the honest
hyperedge list \(R_A^{N,j}\).  A single rooted residual coordinate \(x\) sees
the atoms

```math
{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}(x)
:=
\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}:x\in A\}.
```

### Lemma 15.3: Exact Reconstruction From Literal Atoms

For every finite \((N,j)\),

```math
H_{N,j}(\omega)-H_{N,j}(o)
=
\sum_{\emptyset\ne A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}}
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A).
```

Consequently the literal atoms are an exact representation of the actual
adaptive `SEL2` pushed-forward residual law.

Proof.

This is the finite Möbius inversion formula on the Boolean lattice of subsets
of \(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\).  For a fixed \(\omega\), expand the right-hand side and
collect the coefficient of

```math
H_{N,j}(\omega_B,o_{V\setminus B})
```

for each \(B\subseteq V\).  The coefficient is

```math
\sum_{A\supseteq B}(-1)^{|A|-|B|}.
```

It is \(1\) when \(B=V\) and \(0\) for all proper \(B\).  The missing
constant is exactly \(H_{N,j}(o)\).  All terms are functions of the finite
pushed-forward record law, so the reconstruction is same-record. `square`

### Definition 15.4: Literal Localization And Literal Decay

Let \(d_{RPF}\) be the graph distance on the over-refined vertex cover.  Define
the atom diameter by

```math
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A):=
\max_{x,y\in A}d_{RPF}(x,y).
```

Let \(\ell_{RPF}(A)\) be the size of the minimal connected block-hull
containing \(A\).  If \(A\) is already connected, then
\(\ell_{RPF}(A)=|A|\).  Nonconnected Möbius atoms are charged to their
connected hull, because the RPF polymer expansion sees connected supports.

`P23-RPF-LITLOC(R_0,L_0)` holds if

```math
\Phi_A^{N,j}\equiv0
```

cofinally whenever

```math
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)>R_0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_{RPF}(A)>L_0.
```

Exact bounded-collar localization is useful but stronger than necessary.
The decay version is the real row test.  Let

```math
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}\Phi_A^{N,j}
-
\operatorname*{ess\,inf}\Phi_A^{N,j}.
```

`P23-RPF-LITDECAY(A_0,\mu_0)` holds if, cofinally in \((N,j)\),

```math
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
\le
A_0
\exp\{-\mu_0(\ell_{RPF}(A)+\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A))\}
```

for every literal RPF atom \(A\).  Exact bounded-collar localization is the
degenerate case in which the tail oscillations vanish beyond a finite range.

### Definition 15.5: Finite RPF Influence Matrix

For \(x\ne y\), set

```math
I_{xy}^{N,j}
:=
2
\sum_{A\supseteq\{x,y\}}
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j}),
\qquad
I_{xx}^{N,j}:=0.
```

The weighted row norm is

```math
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
:=
\sup_x
\sum_y e^{a d_{RPF}(x,y)}I_{xy}^{N,j}.
```

This is a computable upper bound for the Dobrushin variation influence of
Definition 14.4.  It is intentionally slightly wasteful: it uses only
oscillations of literal same-law interaction atoms.

### Lemma 15.6: Literal Row Norm Dominates Conditional Influence

The Dobrushin influence matrix of Definition 14.4 is bounded entrywise by
the matrix \(I_{xy}^{N,j}\) of Definition 15.5.

Proof.

Condition on all coordinates except \(x\).  Changing the outside coordinate
\(y\) can only change those terms in the conditional Hamiltonian for \(x\)
whose support contains both \(x\) and \(y\).  Each such interaction changes
by at most its oscillation, and total-variation comparison of two one-site
finite conditional laws costs at most twice the Hamiltonian oscillation.
Summing over the affected literal atoms gives the displayed entrywise bound.
All conditionals are conditionals of the finite pushed-forward law
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\). `square`

### Definition 15.7: RPF Finite Counting Ledger

`P23-RPF-FINCOUNT(C_{RPF},h_{RPF})` holds if, cofinally in \((N,j)\), the
literal atom labels satisfy

```math
\#\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}(x): \ell_{RPF}(A)=n\}
\le
C_{RPF}e^{h_{RPF}n}
```

for every root \(x\) and every \(n\ge1\).  When the atom labels are the same
finite residual labels counted in Paper 16 Definition 9M.1E, one may take

```math
C_{RPF}=C_{KP},
\qquad
h_{RPF}=h_{KP}.
```

On a fully explicit finite-template row with block-graph degree \(\Delta_B\)
and residual label count \(L_{KP}\), Paper 16 Corollary 9M.1F gives the clean
choice

```math
C_{RPF}=1,
\qquad
h_{RPF}=\log(e\Delta_B L_{KP}).
```

### Theorem 15.8: Literal Decay Gives The Actual-Law Dobrushin Gate

Assume `P23-RPF-FINCOUNT(C_RPF,h_RPF)` and
`P23-RPF-LITDECAY(A_0,mu_0)`.  If there is an \(a>0\) such that

```math
\delta_{RPF}:=\mu_0-h_{RPF}-a>0
```

and

```math
Q_{RPF}(a)
:=
2A_0C_{RPF}
{e^{-\delta_{RPF}}
\over
(1-e^{-\delta_{RPF}})^2}
<1,
```

then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOBRUSHIN\text{-}ACT}(Q_{RPF}(a),a)
```

holds.  Consequently `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

By Lemma 15.6,

```math
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
\le
2\sup_x
\sum_{A\ni x}
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
\sum_{y\in A\setminus\{x\}} e^{a d_{RPF}(x,y)}.
```

For an atom of connected-hull size \(n\), the inner sum is bounded by
\(n e^{a\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)}\).  Literal decay gives

```math
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
e^{a\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)}
\le
A_0e^{-\mu_0 n}e^{-(\mu_0-a)\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)}
\le
A_0e^{-(\mu_0-a)n},
```

using \(\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)\le n\) for the connected hull, after
increasing the graph metric normalization by a harmless finite-template
constant if necessary.  The finite counting ledger then gives

```math
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
\le
2A_0C_{RPF}
\sum_{n\ge1}
n e^{-(\mu_0-h_{RPF}-a)n}
=
Q_{RPF}(a).
```

The strict inequality \(Q_{RPF}(a)<1\) gives the Dobrushin gate of Definition
14.4.  Theorem 14.7 then proves `P23-RPF-TRANS0`. `square`

### Definition 15.9: Paper-16 Literal-Atom Transfer Test

`P23-RPF-LIT-KP16-XFER(A_0,\mu_0,C_{RPF},h_{RPF},a)` is the concrete finite
row version of `P23-RPF-KP16-XFER`.  It consists of:

1. the literal atoms \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) of Definition 15.2 are the same residual
   labels as the Paper-16 clean finite-template residual coefficients after
   `BC`, `CE`, `WP`, and RP/Cov diagonal selection;
2. Paper 16's clean analytic worksheet supplies the oscillation envelope
   `P23-RPF-LITDECAY(A_0,mu_0)` on these exact atoms;
3. Paper 16's finite counting ledger supplies
   `P23-RPF-FINCOUNT(C_RPF,h_RPF)` on these exact atoms;
4. the scalar row inequality \(Q_{RPF}(a)<1\) of Theorem 15.8 holds.

The transfer is allowed to include a finite norm-conversion surcharge
\(\lambda_{RPF}\) by replacing \(A_0\) with \(e^{\lambda_{RPF}}A_0\).  It is
not allowed to charge RP/Cov tails, surface decoration, character-tail
conversion, `KPdec`, or whole-process mismatch a second time.

### Corollary 15.10: What Is Now Closed And What Remains

The "print the actual atoms" part of the Section-14 work order is closed:
the literal atoms are the finite functions \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) in Definition
15.2, and Lemma 15.3 proves that they reconstruct the exact residual density
of the actual adaptive `SEL2` pushed-forward law.

The remaining nontrivial task is the scalar row test

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LIT\text{-}KP16\text{-}XFER}
(A_0,\mu_0,C_{RPF},h_{RPF},a)
}
```

with

```math
\mu_0>h_{RPF}+a,
\qquad
2A_0C_{RPF}
{e^{-(\mu_0-h_{RPF}-a)}
\over
(1-e^{-(\mu_0-h_{RPF}-a)})^2}
<1.
```

If this test passes, `P23-RPF-TRANS0` follows and adaptive Branch A closes.
If the literal atom table gives a certified lower floor preventing the
displayed inequality for every admissible \(a>0\), then Branch A fails at a
numerical RPF row-sum obstruction.  If the Paper-16 clean worksheet cannot be
identified with these literal atoms, the exact remaining obstruction is the
identification clause of Definition 15.9, not the pushed-forward law itself.

## 16. Sharp Scalar Row Test For Literal RPF Atoms

Section 15 reduced the actual-law route to a single scalar inequality.  This
section solves that inequality exactly, including the range-absorption
variant.  The point is to prevent a common mistake: importing a Paper-16 KP
pass is not enough unless it survives the extra RPF row costs.  The RPF
Dobrushin row carries a total-variation factor \(2\) and a root-row factor
\(n\).

### Definition 16.1: Compressed RPF Row Constants

For a proposed literal-atom transfer set

```math
(A_0,\mu_0,C_{RPF},h_{RPF},a)
```

define

```math
B_{RPF}:=2A_0C_{RPF},
\qquad
\Delta_{RPF}:=\mu_0-h_{RPF}.
```

For \(0<a<\Delta_{RPF}\), set

```math
\delta(a):=\Delta_{RPF}-a,
\qquad
Q(a):=
B_{RPF}
{e^{-\delta(a)}
\over
(1-e^{-\delta(a)})^2}.
```

Thus the Section-15 row test is exactly \(Q(a)<1\) for some
\(0<a<\Delta_{RPF}\).

### Theorem 16.2: Optimized No-Absorption Row Test

Assume the constants \(A_0,\mu_0,C_{RPF},h_{RPF}\) are fixed.  The following
are equivalent:

1. there exists \(a>0\) such that the Section-15 RPF row test passes;
2. \(\Delta_{RPF}>0\) and

   ```math
   Q_0:=
   B_{RPF}
   {e^{-\Delta_{RPF}}
   \over
   (1-e^{-\Delta_{RPF}})^2}
   <1;
   ```

3. \(\Delta_{RPF}\) exceeds the explicit threshold

   ```math
   \Delta_{RPF}
   >
   \Delta_{crit}(B_{RPF})
   :=
   \log\left(
   {2+B_{RPF}+\sqrt{B_{RPF}^2+4B_{RPF}}\over2}
   \right).
   ```

If these conditions hold, every sufficiently small positive \(a\) passes.  If
they fail, no positive \(a\) can pass with these constants.

Proof.

For \(0<a<\Delta_{RPF}\), the quantity
\(\delta(a)=\Delta_{RPF}-a\) decreases as \(a\) increases.  The function

```math
\delta\mapsto
B_{RPF}{e^{-\delta}\over(1-e^{-\delta})^2}
```

is strictly decreasing for \(\delta>0\).  Hence the infimum over admissible
positive \(a\) is obtained in the limit \(a\downarrow0\), giving \(Q_0\).
This proves the equivalence of items 1 and 2.

For item 3, put \(x=e^{-\Delta_{RPF}}\in(0,1)\).  The inequality \(Q_0<1\)
is

```math
B_{RPF}x<(1-x)^2,
```

or

```math
x^2-(2+B_{RPF})x+1>0.
```

On \(0<x<1\), this holds exactly when

```math
x<
{2+B_{RPF}-\sqrt{B_{RPF}^2+4B_{RPF}}\over2}.
```

Taking negative logarithms gives the displayed threshold. `square`

### Corollary 16.3: What Paper-16 Must Actually Supply

Suppose the Paper-16 clean worksheet is identified with the literal RPF atoms
with a norm-conversion surcharge \(\lambda_{RPF}\).  Then the safe import is

```math
A_0=e^{\lambda_{RPF}}A_{res},
\qquad
\mu_0=\mu_{res},
\qquad
C_{RPF}=C_{KP},
\qquad
h_{RPF}=h_{KP}.
```

The no-absorption literal RPF route passes only if

```math
\mu_{res}-h_{KP}
>
\Delta_{crit}(2e^{\lambda_{RPF}}A_{res}C_{KP}).
```

Equivalently,

```math
2e^{\lambda_{RPF}}A_{res}C_{KP}
{e^{-(\mu_{res}-h_{KP})}
\over
(1-e^{-(\mu_{res}-h_{KP})})^2}
<1.
```

This is stronger than Paper 16's basic `HK-KP-TEST` because the RPF influence
row differentiates the residual density with respect to a root coordinate.
It cannot be replaced by the one-denominator Paper-16 activity test unless
the extra factor is explicitly paid.

### Definition 16.4: Same-Law Local Absorption For Literal RPF Atoms

`P23-RPF-LIT-ABSORB(R)` holds if all literal RPF atoms whose connected hull
size satisfies

```math
\ell_{RPF}(A)<R
```

can be absorbed into the already declared local block law, central
one-plaquette factor, finite record normalization, or fixed exact-entry
battery on the same pushed-forward `SEL2` law, while the remaining atoms
\(\ell_{RPF}(A)\ge R\) keep the same constants
\(A_0,\mu_0,C_{RPF},h_{RPF}\).

This is not permission to discard local residuals.  They must be moved into a
declared local ledger that is not charged again to RP/Cov, surface
decoration, character tail, `KPdec`, or whole-process mismatch.

### Theorem 16.5: Sharp Range-Absorbed Row Test

Assume `P23-RPF-LIT-ABSORB(R)`,
`P23-RPF-FINCOUNT(C_RPF,h_RPF)`, and
`P23-RPF-LITDECAY(A_0,mu_0)`.  For \(0<a<\Delta_{RPF}\), define

```math
Q_R(a)
:=
B_{RPF}
{e^{-\delta(a)R}\bigl(R-(R-1)e^{-\delta(a)}\bigr)
\over
(1-e^{-\delta(a)})^2}.
```

Then the range-absorbed literal RPF row passes if and only if

```math
\Delta_{RPF}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
Q_R(0)<1.
```

Equivalently,

```math
B_{RPF}
{e^{-\Delta_{RPF}R}\bigl(R-(R-1)e^{-\Delta_{RPF}}\bigr)
\over
(1-e^{-\Delta_{RPF}})^2}
<1.
```

Proof.

After absorption, the proof of Theorem 15.8 starts its size sum at \(n=R\):

```math
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
\le
B_{RPF}\sum_{n\ge R}n e^{-\delta(a)n}.
```

The finite geometric identity

```math
\sum_{n\ge R}n x^n
=
{x^R(R-(R-1)x)\over(1-x)^2},
\qquad 0<x<1,
```

gives the displayed \(Q_R(a)\).  As in Theorem 16.2, \(Q_R(a)\) is minimized
as \(a\downarrow0\), so existence of an admissible positive \(a\) is
equivalent to \(Q_R(0)<1\). `square`

### Corollary 16.6: Exact Obstruction Trichotomy

For the literal adaptive RPF route, exactly one of the following must happen.

1. **Direct pass.**  The constants satisfy the no-absorption threshold of
   Theorem 16.2.  Then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` follows.
2. **Range-rescued pass.**  The no-absorption threshold fails, but a same-law
   local absorption certificate `P23-RPF-LIT-ABSORB(R)` exists and the
   range-absorbed inequality of Theorem 16.5 holds.  Then
   `P23-RPF-TRANS0` follows.
3. **Real obstruction.**  Neither direct pass nor range-rescued pass can be
   certified, or the literal atoms cannot be identified with the Paper-16
   clean residual worksheet.  Then adaptive Branch A remains open at the
   concrete source theorem

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LIT\text{-}KP16\text{-}XFER}.
   ```

If, in case 3, the same literal row table also proves a lower floor
\(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\), then adaptive Branch A is falsified.
Otherwise it is parked, not refuted.

### Corollary 16.7: Next Computation

The next computation is no longer conceptual.  It is the finite constant
table

```math
\lambda_{RPF},\quad
A_{res},\quad
\mu_{res},\quad
C_{KP},\quad
h_{KP},\quad
R_{\rm absorb}.
```

All six entries must be attached to the literal atoms
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) of Definition 15.2 on the actual adaptive pushed-forward
`SEL2` law.  Once this table is printed, the Section-16 formulas decide the
RPF route without further interpretation.

### Corollary 16.8: Clean Import Has A Nontrivial Decay-Surplus Floor

On the cleanest Paper-16 finite-template import with no norm-conversion
surcharge, \(C_{KP}=1\), and \(A_{res}\ge1\), the no-absorption RPF route
requires at least

```math
\mu_{res}-h_{KP}
>
\Delta_{crit}(2)
=
\log(2+\sqrt3)
\approx 1.31696.
```

Thus a merely positive Paper-16 residual margin
\(\mu_{res}-h_{KP}>0\) is far from enough for direct RPF closure.  If the
available surplus is small but positive, the only honest rescue inside this
route is a same-law local-absorption certificate raising the effective
starting hull size \(R\).

Proof.

In the stated clean case,

```math
B_{RPF}=2A_{res}C_{KP}\ge2.
```

The function \(B\mapsto\Delta_{crit}(B)\) in Theorem 16.2 is increasing, so
the best possible direct threshold is attained at \(B=2\).  Substitution gives

```math
\Delta_{crit}(2)
=
\log\left({4+\sqrt{12}\over2}\right)
=
\log(2+\sqrt3).
```

The conclusion follows from Corollary 16.3. `square`

### Definition 16.9: Minimal Absorption Range

When \(\Delta_{RPF}>0\), define the exact minimal absorption range

```math
R_{min}^{RPF}
:=
\min\left\{
R\ge1:
B_{RPF}
{e^{-\Delta_{RPF}R}
\bigl(R-(R-1)e^{-\Delta_{RPF}}\bigr)
\over
(1-e^{-\Delta_{RPF}})^2}
<1
\right\},
```

if the set is nonempty.  Since the displayed expression tends to \(0\) as
\(R\to\infty\), the set is nonempty whenever \(\Delta_{RPF}>0\).

The scalar obstruction after Section 16 is therefore not the existence of an
integer \(R\).  It is the existence of a same-law absorption theorem proving
`P23-RPF-LIT-ABSORB(R)` for some \(R\ge R_{min}^{RPF}\) without recharging a
previously closed ledger.

## 17. Finite Constant Table And Clean Conditional Closure

Section 16 asks for the table

```math
\lambda_{RPF},\quad
A_{res},\quad
\mu_{res},\quad
C_{KP},\quad
h_{KP},\quad
R_{\rm absorb}.
```

This section sources that table from Paper 16 as far as the present corpus
allows.  The result is sharp: the scalar RPF row test is no longer the main
mathematical difficulty if the clean finite-template row truly identifies
with the literal atoms of Definition 15.2.  The remaining difficulty is the
same-law identification/finite-row-data theorem.

### Definition 17.1: Clean Literal-Atom Identification Package

`P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID(lambda_RPF)` is the assertion that, on the actual
adaptive `SEL2` pushed-forward law:

1. every literal atom \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) of Definition 15.2 is represented by a
   Paper-16 clean finite-template residual coefficient on the same finite
   record row;
2. the support hull \(\ell_{RPF}(A)\) is the connected-polymer size counted
   by Paper 16's `HK-FIN-COUNT`;
3. the oscillation norm of each literal atom is bounded by the Paper-16
   residual coefficient norm with surcharge \(e^{\lambda_{RPF}}\);
4. strictly local terms already absorbed into the central plaquette factor,
   local block law, heat-time tangent, finite record normalization, or exact
   battery are not recharged to RP/Cov, surface decoration, character tail,
   `KPdec`, or whole-process mismatch.

The strict literal-equality branch has \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\).  If the
identification uses a finite norm conversion, that conversion is exactly
\(\lambda_{RPF}\).

### Definition 17.2: Paper-16 Active Clean Row Data

`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA` holds if the actual adaptive literal RPF row has the
Paper-16 clean finite-template data

```math
\Delta_B,\quad L_{ent},\quad L_{KP},\quad
C_0,\quad R_G,\quad C_v^{row},\quad r_{res}^{clean},
```

with:

1. `HK-FIN-COUNT(Delta_B,L_ent,L_KP)` on the same finite record row;
2. finite-range covariance import with \(C_G=C_0e^{2R_G H}\) at chosen rate
   \(2H\);
3. finite vertex source with constant \(C_v^{row}\);
4. clean counterterm row, so nonlocal counterterm and scheme amplitudes are
   zero after local absorption;
5. large-field margin can be run at any prescribed finite value;
6. the asymptotically-free tail can be restricted to any prescribed
   \(g_*^2>0\).

This is exactly the same kind of finite-row data used in Paper 16 Theorem
9N.1Q.3, but it must be verified for the literal adaptive RPF atoms, not
imported by analogy.

### Lemma 17.3: Constants Exported By The Clean Row

Assume `P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID(lambda_RPF)` and
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA`.  For any chosen surplus \(\delta>0\), the clean row
may be run with

```math
C_{KP}=1,\qquad
h_{KP}=\log(e\Delta_B L_{KP}),
```

and, after choosing the finite-range covariance and large-field margins as in
Paper 16 Corollary 9N.1Q.2,

```math
\mu_{res}=h_{KP}+\delta.
```

Moreover, for every \(\varepsilon>0\), the cofinal AF tail can be chosen so
that

```math
A_{res}\le1+\varepsilon.
```

With global finite KP prefactor \(P_{KP}\), replace \(C_{KP}=1\) by
\(C_{KP}=P_{KP}\) and leave \(h_{KP}\) unchanged.

Proof.

Paper 16 Corollary 9M.1F gives \(C_{KP}=1\) and
\(h_{KP}=\log(e\Delta_B L_{KP})\) from the finite counting data.  In Paper 16
Corollary 9N.1Q.2, choose the clean worksheet with \(m=0\) and
\(H=h_{KP}\).  Then choose

```math
\mu_G=2(h_{KP}+\delta),
\qquad
\sigma_{lf}^{sharp}\ge h_{KP}+\delta.
```

The exported residual decay is

```math
\mu_{res}
=
\min(\mu_G/2,\sigma_{lf}^{sharp})
=
h_{KP}+\delta.
```

On the clean row, Paper 16 Definition 9N.1K gives

```math
A_{res}^{clean}
=
{C_v^{row}C_GC_{ent}g_*^2\over1-\theta_{clean}}+1.
```

Since the AF tail can be restricted to arbitrarily small \(g_*^2\), first
make \(\theta_{clean}\le1/2\), then make
\(2C_v^{row}C_GC_{ent}g_*^2\le\varepsilon\).  This gives
\(A_{res}^{clean}\le1+\varepsilon\).  The surcharge
\(\lambda_{RPF}\) is not included in \(A_{res}\); it enters the RPF row test
through \(e^{\lambda_{RPF}}\), as in Corollary 16.3. `square`

### Theorem 17.4: Clean Conditional Direct RPF Closure

Assume `P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID(lambda_RPF)` and
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA`.  If \(P_{KP}\) is the finite global KP prefactor
\(P_{KP}=1\) on the strict clean count, then choose
\(\varepsilon>0\) and \(\delta>0\) such that

```math
\delta
>
\Delta_{crit}\!\left(2e^{\lambda_{RPF}}(1+\varepsilon)P_{KP}\right).
```

Then the direct no-absorption row test passes with

```math
A_{res}\le1+\varepsilon,
\qquad
\mu_{res}=h_{KP}+\delta,
\qquad
C_{KP}=P_{KP},
\qquad
R_{\rm absorb}=1.
```

Consequently

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
```

holds, and adaptive Branch A closes the predebit side with zero RPF debit.

Proof.

By Lemma 17.3, the clean row exports the displayed constants.  Therefore

```math
\mu_{res}-h_{KP}=\delta,
\qquad
B_{RPF}\le2e^{\lambda_{RPF}}(1+\varepsilon)P_{KP}.
```

The chosen \(\delta\) is strictly larger than the critical threshold for this
upper bound.  Theorem 16.2 and Corollary 16.3 then give the no-absorption
literal RPF row test.  Theorem 15.8 gives the actual-law Dobrushin gate, and
Theorem 14.7 gives `P23-RPF-TRANS0`. `square`

### Corollary 17.5: Literal Finite Table In The Clean Branch

Under the hypotheses of Theorem 17.4, the finite table can be printed as

| entry | clean value or bound | source |
| --- | --- | --- |
| \(\lambda_{RPF}\) | \(0\) in strict literal equality; otherwise finite surcharge | `P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID` |
| \(C_{KP}\) | \(P_{KP}\), equal to \(1\) in strict clean counting | Paper 16 `HK-FIN-COUNT` |
| \(h_{KP}\) | \(\log(e\Delta_B L_{KP})\) | Paper 16 Corollary 9M.1F |
| \(\mu_{res}\) | \(h_{KP}+\delta\) | Paper 16 Corollary 9N.1Q.2 with \(m=0\) |
| \(A_{res}\) | \(\le1+\varepsilon\) | cofinal AF tail in Lemma 17.3 |
| \(R_{\rm absorb}\) | \(1\) | no-absorption direct pass |

The direct pass condition is exactly

```math
\delta
>
\Delta_{crit}\!\left(2e^{\lambda_{RPF}}(1+\varepsilon)P_{KP}\right).
```

In the strictest clean case \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\), \(P_{KP}=1\), and
\(\varepsilon\downarrow0\), this requires

```math
\delta>\log(2+\sqrt3).
```

### Corollary 17.6: Current Status After Printing The Table

The scalar row test obstruction is conditionally solved.  If the literal RPF
atoms of the actual adaptive `SEL2` law satisfy
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID(lambda_RPF)` and `P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA`, then
Theorem 17.4 proves `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

The current corpus has not yet proved those two same-law identification/data
clauses for the adaptive high-\(\alpha\) `SEL2` row.  Therefore the remaining
Branch-A obstruction is now sharper:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}FINTPL\text{-}ID}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWDATA}.
}
```

It is no longer a vague residual-factorization issue and no longer a scalar
inequality mystery.  It is the same-law verification that the actual adaptive
literal atoms are governed by the clean finite-template Paper-16 analytic
row.  Without that verification, adaptive Branch A remains parked; with it,
adaptive Branch A closes.

## 18. Literal-To-Clean Dictionary For The RPF Obstruction

Section 17 reduces adaptive Branch A to a clean-row identification and row-data
problem.  This section attacks the identification half directly.  The point is
not to spend Paper-16 clean estimates by analogy.  The point is to classify the
literal atoms of Definition 15.2 into rows that are already absorbed by the
strict `SEL2` ledger and rows that still require an actual clean residual
dictionary.

The outcome is useful even though it is not yet the final RPF theorem: all
strictly local and previously closed scalar sources are removed from the live
RPF table.  What remains is a smaller, sharper obstruction, namely a literal
same-law dictionary for the genuine nonlocal residual atoms plus the Paper-16
finite row data for those atoms.

### Definition 18.1: Literal RPF Classifier

Let \(A\) be a finite literal interaction atom from Definition 15.2, with
centered coefficient \(R_A^{N,j}\) on the actual adaptive `SEL2` pushed-forward
law.  A literal classifier is a map

```math
\mathfrak c_{RPF}(A)\in
\{
\mathrm{CElead},
\mathrm{LocTime},
\mathrm{Nonbulk},
\mathrm{CollarBianchi},
\mathrm{IntYM2},
\mathrm{CtSch},
\mathrm{ProjRead},
\mathrm{CleanRPF}
\}.
```

The intended meanings are as follows.

| class | literal source | clean target | status on the strict adaptive row |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `CElead` | central plaquette heat-kernel coefficient | \(K_p^{CE}\) and \(T_j^{SEL2,conv}\) | divided out before RPF |
| `LocTime` | scalar normalization, heat-time tangent, finite record normalization | local time/normalization coordinate | absorbed, no residual atom |
| `Nonbulk` | finite counterterm, projective, readout, collar transition, or clean nonbulk scalar source | Paper-20 strict nonbulk ledger | zero only on the strict exact clean branch |
| `CollarBianchi` | boundary/collar Bianchi or off-sheet rooted source | Paper-20 clean good-collar ledger | zero on the strict clean-collar branch |
| `IntYM2` | interior Bianchi/off-sheet root, including the `{4,33,J2}` YM2 list | Paper-20 `HKSD-TPL` and `INTBULK-FOC` ledger | zero after finite root census and matching |
| `CtSch` | nonlocal counterterm or scheme polymer after local absorption | Paper-16 clean minimal counterterm row | zero only if the clean minimal row is used |
| `ProjRead` | projective, covariance, regulator, or readout mismatch | RP/Cov/readout ledgers, not RPF | forbidden inside RPF; restore carried debit if present |
| `CleanRPF` | genuine nonlocal residual interaction left after all declared local absorptions | Paper-16 clean residual polymer coefficient | live dictionary row |

The classifier is admissible only if every atom is assigned to exactly one
class.  A row assigned to `ProjRead` is not an RPF row; it invalidates a zero
RPF debit unless the corresponding external ledger is restored.

### Lemma 18.2: Local And Previously Closed Classes Do Not Enter RPF

On the strict exact-record, clean-minimal-counterterm, clean-collar adaptive
`SEL2` branch compatible with the Paper-16 clean row and the Paper-20 strict
scalar ledger, the classes

```math
\mathrm{CElead},\quad
\mathrm{LocTime},\quad
\mathrm{Nonbulk},\quad
\mathrm{CollarBianchi},\quad
\mathrm{IntYM2},\quad
\mathrm{CtSch}
```

do not contribute to the literal RPF residual sum.  More precisely, after
dividing out the declared central plaquette factor and using the same scalar
time/normalization coordinates, their total contribution is either exactly
zero in the RPF ledger or has already been spent in a distinct non-RPF ledger.

Proof.

The `CElead` and `LocTime` rows are part of the chosen central block law and
the time/normalization coordinate.  They are not residual interactions by the
definition of \(\mathcal R_{N,j}\).

For `Nonbulk`, Paper 20's strict clean branch sets the nonbulk scalar source
to zero after the exact covariance/readout convention, the clean minimal
counterterm convention, and the finite-template nonbulk census are imposed.
If any of those conventions is not imposed, Paper 20 does not give a zero row:
the term must be restored as a carried nonbulk debit, outside RPF.

For `CollarBianchi`, Paper 20 closes the boundary/collar Bianchi and off-sheet
roots on the clean good-collar branch.  Again, a nonclean collar row is not a
hidden RPF residual; it is a carried collar or boundary debit.

For `IntYM2`, Paper 20 verifies the actual `SEL2` heat-kernel scalar-derivative
template `P20-SEL2-HKSD-TPL`: after scalar normalization, heat-time tangent,
counterterm/scheme, collar, boundary, large-field, and projective/readout
labels are removed, the only nonabsorbed second-order interior labels are
`{4,33,J2}`.  The finite root census and generator matching prove
`INTBULK-FOC`, hence the interior Bianchi/off-sheet contribution is zero on
the strict reduced branch.

For `CtSch`, Paper 16's clean minimal row absorbs the relevant and marginal
local pure-gauge counterterms into the declared time coordinate and sets the
nonlocal counterterm/scheme polymer amplitudes to zero.  If a different
counterterm convention is used, the term is a counterterm/scheme debit, not an
RPF atom.

Thus none of these rows is allowed to appear in the live literal RPF table
without double charging. `square`

### Definition 18.3: Clean Residual Dictionary

`P23-RPF-CLEAN-DICT(lambda_RPF)` is the assertion that the remaining
`CleanRPF` atoms admit a same-law finite dictionary

```math
\mathcal D_{RPF}^{clean}:
A\longmapsto (Y_A,\sigma_A,J_A)
```

with the following properties.

1. \(Y_A\) is the connected Paper-16 clean residual polymer on the same
   adaptive finite record row.
2. \(\sigma_A\) is a finite local label belonging to the Paper-16 clean
   finite-template list counted by `HK-FIN-COUNT`.
3. The support hulls agree:

   ```math
   \ell_{RPF}(A)=|Y_A|.
   ```

4. The literal coefficient is dominated by the clean residual coefficient on
   the same pushed-forward law:

   ```math
   \|R_A^{N,j}\|
   \le
   e^{\lambda_{RPF}}\,
   \|K_{16}^{clean}(Y_A,\sigma_A;N,j)\|.
   ```

5. The dictionary has only the finite multiplicity already included in
   Paper-16's \(L_{KP}\).  No additional hidden label multiplicity is allowed.

The strict literal-equality branch has \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\) and \(J_A\) equal
to the literal coefficient of the clean residual polymer.  A finite norm or
coordinate conversion is allowed only through the displayed surcharge
\(\lambda_{RPF}\).

### Lemma 18.4: No-Double-Charge Reduction To `CleanRPF`

Assume the strict adaptive branch conventions used in Lemma 18.2.  If an
admissible classifier \(\mathfrak c_{RPF}\) exists and every non-`CleanRPF`
row is assigned to one of the closed/absorbed rows in Lemma 18.2, then the
literal RPF residual is exactly the sum of the `CleanRPF` atoms:

```math
H_{N,j}^{RPF}
=
\sum_{A:\mathfrak c_{RPF}(A)=\mathrm{CleanRPF}} R_A^{N,j}.
```

If a row is instead classified as `ProjRead`, or if a nonclean nonbulk,
counterterm, collar, or readout convention is used, the displayed identity is
false.  The missing term must be restored to its external carried ledger, and
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID` is not licensed.

Proof.

This is finite-template bookkeeping.  Definition 15.2 obtains \(H_{N,j}\) by
finite Möbius inversion of the actual residual density after declared central
and local factors are removed.  Lemma 18.2 removes every class whose
contribution is either part of those declared factors or already closed in a
different ledger.  Since the classifier is disjoint, the only rows left in
the RPF sum are the `CleanRPF` rows.  The second statement is exactly the
contrapositive of disjoint ledger bookkeeping. `square`

### Theorem 18.5: Dictionary Implies The Finite-Template Identification

Assume the strict adaptive branch conventions of Lemma 18.2, an admissible
literal classifier, and `P23-RPF-CLEAN-DICT(lambda_RPF)`.  Then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}FINTPL\text{-}ID}
(\lambda_{RPF})
```

holds.

Proof.

By Lemma 18.4 the live literal residual consists only of `CleanRPF` atoms.
Definition 18.3 maps each such atom to a Paper-16 clean residual polymer on
the same finite record row, preserves the connected hull size, and bounds the
literal norm by the clean coefficient norm with surcharge
\(\lambda_{RPF}\).  The finite label multiplicity is already included in
Paper-16's \(L_{KP}\), so no extra combinatorial factor is introduced.  These
are precisely the four clauses of Definition 17.1. `square`

### Corollary 18.6: Sharpened Remaining Obstruction

After the local ledger audit, adaptive Branch A no longer needs a vague
finite-template identification theorem.  It needs the following two explicit
same-law inputs:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}DICT}(\lambda_{RPF})
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWDATA}.
}
```

With those two inputs, Theorem 18.5 gives
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID(lambda_RPF)`, and Theorem 17.4 gives
`P23-RPF-TRANS0`.  Hence adaptive Branch A closes.

Without `P23-RPF-CLEAN-DICT`, the current corpus does not prove that the
actual high-\(\alpha\) adaptive `SEL2` literal atoms are the same residual
polymers controlled by Paper 16.  Without `P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA`, the
dictionary has no usable KP row constants.  These are now the two remaining
RPF tasks.

### Work Order After Section 18

The next finite tasks are therefore:

1. print the literal surviving `CleanRPF` atom list after the strict local
   cancellations of Lemma 18.2;
2. construct the row-by-row map
   \(A\mapsto(Y_A,\sigma_A,J_A)\);
3. check whether \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\) by literal equality, or print the finite
   conversion surcharge;
4. verify that all label multiplicities are already counted by
   \(\Delta_B,L_{ent},L_{KP}\);
5. print the active clean row data
   \(\Delta_B,L_{ent},L_{KP},C_0,R_G,C_v^{row},r_{res}^{clean}\).

This is the cleanest possible next attack on `P23-RPF-TRANS0`: first identify
the atoms, then spend the scalar table that Section 17 already proved is
strong enough.

## 19. Surviving `CleanRPF` Atom List And Row-Map Verdict

Section 18 left five finite tasks.  This section performs the first one and
part of the second.  The literal survivor list can be printed canonically from
the same pushed-forward scalar law.  What cannot yet be printed from the
current corpus is the coefficient-by-coefficient row map to Paper 16's clean
residual table.

This distinction matters.  The finite atoms exist by Möbius inversion.  The
clean residual polymer table exists in Paper 16.  The missing theorem is the
same-record equality or domination statement connecting the two tables on the
adaptive high-\(\alpha\) row.

### Definition 19.1: The Surviving Literal `CleanRPF` Table

For each finite adaptive row \((N,j)\), define the closed-row support families

```math
{\mathcal C}_{CE}^{N,j},\quad
{\mathcal C}_{loc}^{N,j},\quad
{\mathcal C}_{nb}^{N,j},\quad
{\mathcal C}_{colB}^{N,j},\quad
{\mathcal C}_{int}^{N,j},\quad
{\mathcal C}_{ct}^{N,j},\quad
{\mathcal C}_{pr}^{N,j}
```

to be the subsets of \({\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}\) classified in Definition
18.1 as `CElead`, `LocTime`, `Nonbulk`, `CollarBianchi`, `IntYM2`, `CtSch`,
and `ProjRead`, respectively.

The surviving literal clean-RPF table is

```math
{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}
:=
{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}
\setminus
\left(
{\mathcal C}_{CE}^{N,j}
\cup{\mathcal C}_{loc}^{N,j}
\cup{\mathcal C}_{nb}^{N,j}
\cup{\mathcal C}_{colB}^{N,j}
\cup{\mathcal C}_{int}^{N,j}
\cup{\mathcal C}_{ct}^{N,j}
\cup{\mathcal C}_{pr}^{N,j}
\right).
```

Equivalently,

```math
{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}
=
\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}:
\mathfrak c_{RPF}(A)=\mathrm{CleanRPF}\}.
```

Each survivor is printed with the row

| field | value |
| --- | --- |
| literal support | \(A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) |
| literal atom | \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) from Definition 15.2 |
| centered record | \(R_A^{N,j}=\Phi_A^{N,j}-\mathbb E\Phi_A^{N,j}\) |
| connected hull | \(Y(A):=\operatorname{Hull}_{RPF}(A)\) |
| hull size | \(\ell_{RPF}(A)=|Y(A)|\) |
| diameter | \(\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)\) |
| class | `CleanRPF` |
| live coefficient test | compare \(R_A^{N,j}\) to a Paper-16 clean residual coefficient |

This is a literal table schema, not an asymptotic existence assertion.  For
fixed \((N,j)\), \(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) is finite, hence the displayed set is a
finite list.

### Lemma 19.2: The Surviving Table Is The Whole Live RPF Hamiltonian

On the strict branch of Lemma 18.2,

```math
H_{N,j}^{RPF}
=
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}}R_A^{N,j}.
```

If \({\mathcal C}_{pr}^{N,j}\) is nonempty, or if any of the strict local
conventions fail, the displayed clean-RPF table is not a zero-debit RPF
table.  The corresponding term must be restored to its external carried
ledger.

Proof.

Definition 19.1 is exactly the `CleanRPF` sublist of the admissible classifier.
Lemma 18.4 then gives the displayed identity.  The failure statement is the
same no-double-charge alternative in Lemma 18.4. `square`

### Definition 19.3: Candidate Clean Row Map

A candidate clean row map is the finite assignment

```math
\mathfrak M_{RPF}^{N,j}:
A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}
\longmapsto
(Y_A,\sigma_A,K_A^{16})
```

where:

1. \(Y_A=Y(A)\) is the connected hull of the literal atom;
2. \(\sigma_A\) is a Paper-16 finite residual label counted by \(L_{KP}\);
3. \(K_A^{16}=K_{16}^{clean}(Y_A,\sigma_A;N,j)\) is the corresponding clean
   residual coefficient on the same pushed-forward row.

`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWMAP(lambda_RPF)` holds if, cofinally in \((N,j)\), such maps
exist and satisfy

```math
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
\le
e^{\lambda_{RPF}}\,
\|K_A^{16}\|
```

for every \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\), with all multiplicities of
the labels \(\sigma_A\) already included in Paper-16's \(L_{KP}\).

The strict literal-equality target is \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\) and
\(R_A^{N,j}=K_A^{16}\) after centering and the declared scalar
normalization.

### Theorem 19.4: Row Map Is Exactly The Missing Dictionary Input

If `P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWMAP(lambda_RPF)` holds, then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}DICT}(\lambda_{RPF})
```

holds.

Conversely, any proof of `P23-RPF-CLEAN-DICT(lambda_RPF)` restricts to a
candidate row map satisfying `P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWMAP(lambda_RPF)` on
\({\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\).

Proof.

Definition 18.3 asks for a same-law finite dictionary from the surviving
`CleanRPF` atoms to Paper-16 clean residual polymers, preserving hull size,
bounding coefficients with surcharge \(e^{\lambda_{RPF}}\), and introducing
no multiplicity beyond \(L_{KP}\).  Definition 19.3 is precisely that
dictionary written on the canonical surviving table of Definition 19.1.
The two formulations are therefore equivalent after Lemma 19.2 removes the
closed rows. `square`

### Corollary 19.5: What Is Closed Now

The first Section-18 task is closed:

```math
{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}
=
\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}:
\mathfrak c_{RPF}(A)=\mathrm{CleanRPF}\}
```

is the literal surviving atom list.  It is finite for every \((N,j)\), and
Lemma 19.2 proves that it is exactly the live RPF Hamiltonian on the strict
branch.

The second task is not closed by the current corpus.  Paper 16 prints the
clean residual finite row data and the counting constants

```math
C_{KP}=1,\qquad h_{KP}=\log(e\Delta_B L_{KP}),
```

once `HK-FIN-COUNT(Delta_B,L_ent,L_KP)` holds.  It does not print the adaptive
high-\(\alpha\) row map

```math
A\mapsto(Y_A,\sigma_A,K_A^{16})
```

for the literal atoms of Definition 15.2.  Paper 20 closes the local,
nonbulk, collar, counterterm, and interior scalar ledgers on the strict
branch; it also does not print this residual coefficient map.

Therefore the remaining obstruction is sharpened again:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWMAP}(\lambda_{RPF})
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWDATA}.
}
```

With these two inputs, Theorem 19.4 gives `P23-RPF-CLEAN-DICT`, Theorem 18.5
gives `P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID`, and Theorem 17.4 gives `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

### Work Order After Section 19

The next attack is no longer to ask "what are the atoms?"  They are printed by
Definition 19.1.  The next attack is:

1. enumerate the finite residual labels \(\sigma_A\) allowed in the adaptive
   row and compare them with Paper-16's \(L_{KP}\);
2. prove equality \(R_A^{N,j}=K_A^{16}\) on the strict row, or compute the
   smallest finite surcharge \(\lambda_{RPF}\);
3. print the active values or bounds for
   \(\Delta_B,L_{ent},L_{KP},C_0,R_G,C_v^{row},r_{res}^{clean}\);
4. insert those row data into Section 17's scalar table.

If step 2 fails because the literal atoms contain a row not present in
Paper-16's clean residual table, adaptive Branch A is not closed by the clean
route.  The remaining alternatives are a new actual-law KP theorem for that
extra row or a certified lower floor for the RPF predebit.

## 20. Executing The Row-Map Campaign

This section executes the six-step plan against the remaining mystery:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWMAP}
(\lambda_{RPF})
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWDATA}.
```

The conclusion is sharp.  The current corpus does not prove the clean route
unconditionally, but the obstruction is no longer vague.  The only possible
clean proof must pass an exact row identity, a finite label-cover test, a
coefficient-domination test, and the active clean row-data audit below.

### Definition 20.1: Exact Clean Row Identity

`P23-RPF-ROWID` is the assertion that, after `BC`, `CE`, `WP`, the RP/Cov
diagonal selector, and the strict local ledger removals of Lemma 18.2, the
adaptive residual Hamiltonian of Definition 15.1 is the same finite scalar
record Hamiltonian as the Paper-16 clean residual row.

Concretely, for every cofinal \((N,j)\), there must exist a finite record-row
identification

```math
\iota_{N,j}:
V_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\longrightarrow V_{16,KP}^{N,j}
```

such that:

1. \(\iota_{N,j}\) preserves the pushed-forward scalar law, not merely the
   gauge-coordinate proof variables;
2. \(\iota_{N,j}\) preserves the central heat-kernel factor removed by `CE`;
3. local heat-time, scalar normalization, relevant/marginal counterterms,
   collar Bianchi roots, interior `{4,33,J2}` roots, projective/readout
   effects, and RP/Cov tails are already assigned to the ledgers of Sections
   12 and 18;
4. the residual log-density \(H_{N,j}^{RPF}\) is the Paper-16 clean residual
   log-density on the identified row, up to an additive constant killed by
   centering.

This is stronger than saying both rows are finite.  It says they are the same
whole-process scalar row after the declared quotient by local ledgers.

### Definition 20.2: Adaptive Residual Label Alphabet

For \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\), define its adaptive residual label

```math
\sigma_A^{adapt}
=
\bigl(
\tau_{shape}(A),
\tau_{char}(A),
\tau_{source}(A),
\tau_{collar}(A),
\tau_{cent}(A)
\bigr),
```

where:

1. \(\tau_{shape}(A)\) is the connected block-hull shape of \(Y(A)\);
2. \(\tau_{char}(A)\) is the finite plaquette-character/readout label left
   after the central `CE` factor is removed;
3. \(\tau_{source}(A)\) is the residual source type after local
   counterterm/scheme, Bianchi, collar, projective/readout, and RP/Cov rows
   are excluded;
4. \(\tau_{collar}(A)\) is the finite clean-collar adjacency state, if the
   survivor touches the collar battery;
5. \(\tau_{cent}(A)\) records the centering/basepoint convention used in
   Definition 15.2.

Let

```math
\Sigma_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}
:=
\{\sigma_A^{adapt}:A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\}.
```

`P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(L_extra)` holds if the adaptive labels split as

```math
\Sigma_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}
\subseteq
\Sigma_{16,KP}^{N,j}
\sqcup
\Sigma_{extra}^{N,j},
\qquad
|\Sigma_{extra}^{N,j}|\le L_{extra},
```

cofinally, where \(\Sigma_{16,KP}^{N,j}\) is the Paper-16 residual KP label
alphabet counted by \(L_{KP}\).  The clean route requires

```math
L_{extra}=0.
```

If \(L_{extra}>0\), those extra labels are not clean Paper-16 residual
polymers.  They require a new actual-law KP theorem or a carried RPF debit.

### Lemma 20.3: Exact Equality Branch

Assume `P23-RPF-ROWID` and `P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(0)`.  If the centering and
scalar normalization conventions agree with Paper 16's clean residual
coefficient convention, then

```math
R_A^{N,j}
=
K_{16}^{clean}(Y(A),\sigma_A^{adapt};N,j)
```

for every survivor \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\).  Hence

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWMAP}(0)
```

holds.

Proof.

`P23-RPF-ROWID` identifies the two residual log-densities on the same
pushed-forward scalar row after all local ledgers have been removed.
Möbius inversion on a finite record cover is unique.  Since
`P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(0)` says every survivor label is a Paper-16 clean KP
label, the coefficient attached to the connected hull \(Y(A)\) and label
\(\sigma_A^{adapt}\) is exactly the clean coefficient.  Centering removes the
additive constant.  This is Definition 19.3 with \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\).
`square`

### Definition 20.4: Sharp Surcharge Functional

When a candidate label map exists but literal equality is not proved, define
the row surcharge

```math
\lambda_{map}(N,j)
:=
\sup_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}}
\log
{\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
\over
\|K_{16}^{clean}(Y_A,\sigma_A;N,j)\|}
```

with the conventions:

1. a zero denominator with nonzero numerator gives
   \(\lambda_{map}(N,j)=+\infty\);
2. a missing label gives \(\lambda_{map}(N,j)=+\infty\);
3. a zero numerator contributes nothing to the supremum.

The cofinal sharp surcharge is

```math
\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}
:=
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}\lambda_{map}(N,j).
```

### Lemma 20.5: Surcharge Branch

If `P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(0)` holds and
\(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}<\infty\), then for every
\(\lambda>\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}\),

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CLEAN\text{-}ROWMAP}(\lambda)
```

holds cofinally.

If \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}=+\infty\), the Paper-16 clean route does not prove
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWMAP(lambda)` for any finite \(\lambda\).

Proof.

The first claim is the definition of the limsup surcharge: after passing to a
cofinal tail, every survivor coefficient is bounded by the matched Paper-16
coefficient with surcharge \(e^\lambda\).  This is Definition 19.3.  The
second claim follows from the zero-denominator, missing-label, or unbounded
ratio alternatives in Definition 20.4. `square`

### Definition 20.6: Active Clean Row-Data Audit

`P23-RPF-ACTIVE-ROWDATA` is the concrete form of
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA` after the row map has landed.  It requires the finite
active values or certified bounds

```math
\Delta_B,\quad L_{ent},\quad L_{KP},\quad
C_0,\quad R_G,\quad C_v^{row},\quad r_{res}^{clean}
```

on the same adaptive pushed-forward row, with:

1. \(\Delta_B,L_{ent},L_{KP}\) counted after projection to the finite scalar
   record battery;
2. \(C_0,R_G\) imported only from the same finite-range covariance row;
3. \(C_v^{row}\) imported only from the same pushed-forward vertex ledger;
4. \(r_{res}^{clean}\) computed from the clean small-field/counterterm
   starting radii;
5. no local, RP/Cov, projective/readout, collar, or counterterm/scheme debit
   hidden inside \(L_{KP}\) or \(C_v^{row}\).

This is equivalent to `P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA` once
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWMAP(lambda_RPF)` has landed.

### Theorem 20.7: Final Clean-Route Decision Theorem

For adaptive Branch A's clean RPF route, exactly the following possibilities
remain.

1. **Zero-surcharge pass.**  If `P23-RPF-ROWID`,
   `P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(0)`, matching centering/normalization, and
   `P23-RPF-ACTIVE-ROWDATA` hold, then

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
   ```

   holds with \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\).

2. **Finite-surcharge pass.**  If `P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(0)`,
   \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}<\infty\), and
   `P23-RPF-ACTIVE-ROWDATA` hold, and Section 17's scalar inequality passes
   with any \(\lambda>\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}\), then
   `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

3. **Clean-route failure.**  If `P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(0)` fails, or
   \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}=+\infty\), then the Paper-16 clean route does not
   close RPF.  Adaptive Branch A then needs either a new actual-law KP theorem
   for the extra literal rows or a certified finite/lower RPF debit.

4. **Current-corpus park.**  The present corpus proves the literal atoms,
   the local ledger removals, the survivor table, and the scalar row test.  It
   does not print `P23-RPF-ROWID`, `P23-RPF-LABEL-COVER(0)`,
   \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}<\infty\), or `P23-RPF-ACTIVE-ROWDATA`.
   Therefore adaptive Branch A is not closed unconditionally by the current
   papers.

Proof.

Item 1 follows from Lemma 20.3, which gives
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWMAP(0)`, and Definition 20.6, which gives
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWDATA`.  Theorem 19.4 then gives
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-DICT`, Theorem 18.5 gives
`P23-RPF-CLEAN-FINTPL-ID`, and Theorem 17.4 gives `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

Item 2 uses Lemma 20.5 in place of Lemma 20.3 and then applies the same chain,
with the surcharge inserted into Section 17's scalar table.

Item 3 is immediate from Definitions 20.2 and 20.4: an extra label is not a
Paper-16 clean residual polymer, and an infinite surcharge cannot be absorbed
by the finite scalar table.

Item 4 is the inventory of the previous sections and source papers.  Paper 23
Section 15 prints the literal atoms.  Section 18 removes local and previously
closed rows without double charging.  Section 19 prints the survivor table.
Paper 16 prints the clean residual coefficient framework and finite row-data
worksheet on `T_HK^std`.  Paper 20 closes the strict local/nonbulk/collar/
interior scalar ledgers.  None of those results prints the adaptive
coefficient row identity or the survivor-to-clean label map. `square`

### Corollary 20.8: The Obstruction Is Settled To A Primitive Source Theorem

The mystery has the following final form:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LABEL\text{-}COVER}(0)
+
\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}<\infty
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTIVE\text{-}ROWDATA}.
}
```

If the equality branch is proved, the surcharge clause is replaced by
\(\lambda_{RPF}=0\).  If any clause fails, the clean Paper-16 route is not the
right route for RPF.  The alternatives are:

1. prove a new actual-law KP theorem directly for
   \({\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\);
2. carry a finite RPF debit and test it against \(M_*\);
3. prove a same-record lower floor that falsifies adaptive Branch A.

Thus the obstruction is settled as a primitive source theorem, not as a
scalar-row mystery and not as a local-ledger bookkeeping issue.

## 21. The `ROWID` Side-By-Side Audit

Section 20 shows that the clean route must begin with `P23-RPF-ROWID`.  This
section executes that audit.  The result is precise: the local and already
spent ledgers are compatible with the clean row on the strict branch, but the
actual residual coefficient identity is not printed by the current corpus.

The point is not semantic.  Paper 16's \(K_i(Y)\) is a clean residual
coefficient on the frozen standard heat-kernel row `T_HK^std`.  Paper 23's
\(R_A^{N,j}\) is a literal centered Möbius atom of the actual adaptive
`SEL2` residual density.  `ROWID` is the theorem that those are the same
finite scalar row after the declared local quotient.

### Definition 21.1: `ROWID` Component Gates

Split `P23-RPF-ROWID` into four component gates.

1. `P23-RPF-ROWID-LAW`: the finite pushed-forward law used in Definition 15.1
   is the same scalar record law as Paper-16 `T_HK^std`, after restricting to
   the adaptive high-\(\alpha\) row and the exact-entry battery.
2. `P23-RPF-ROWID-CE`: the central factor divided out in Definition 15.1 is
   exactly the local heat-kernel/plaquette factor treated as local in
   Paper-16 `T_HK^std`.
3. `P23-RPF-ROWID-LOCAL`: the differences coming from heat-time coordinate,
   scalar normalization, clean counterterm/scheme convention, collar/Bianchi
   roots, interior `{4,33,J2}` roots, projective/readout records, and RP/Cov
   transport have all been assigned to non-RPF ledgers and vanish or are
   carried there.
4. `P23-RPF-ROWID-RES`: after the first three identifications, the remaining
   residual log-density has the same finite connected residual coefficient
   table as Paper 16:

   ```math
   R_A^{N,j}
   =
   K_{16}^{clean}(Y(A),\sigma_A;N,j)
   ```

   for every survivor \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\), up to the
   centering convention of Definition 15.2.

Then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID}
```

is the conjunction of these four gates.

### Table 21.2: Side-By-Side Audit

| Paper-23 object | Paper-16/Paper-20 object | required bridge | current source status | verdict |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\) on \(\Omega_{N,j}\) | frozen pushed-forward row `T_HK^std` | same finite scalar law, not merely same gauge proof coordinates | Paper 23 freezes the adaptive law; Paper 16 freezes a clean heat-kernel row | live: needs `ROWID-LAW` |
| \(K_p^{CE,N,j}\) divided out of \(p_{N,j}\) | local heat-kernel plaquette/time factor in `T_HK^std` | exact central factor agreement after `BC/CE` | Paper 20/21 treat `CE` as a separate source gate; Section 15 assumes `CE` applied before RPF | conditional: closed only on the exact `CE` branch |
| local time, scalar normalization, relevant/marginal counterterms | Paper-16 clean minimal local row | local rows absorbed before residual polymers | Paper 16 clean minimal row and Paper 20 strict branch license this as a no-double-charge local audit | closed for debit purposes on strict branch |
| collar/Bianchi/interior `{4,33,J2}` roots | Paper-20 strict clean nonbulk/collar/interior ledgers | excluded from RPF and charged nowhere else | Paper 20 verifies `HKSD-TPL` and closes strict local scalar ledgers | closed for debit purposes on strict branch |
| projective/readout/RP-Cov transport | Paper-20/21 projective/readout and RP/Cov ledgers | not hidden in RPF | Paper 23 Section 12 closes RP/Cov by diagonal selector; projective/readout is strict only if exact branch is used | closed or carried outside RPF |
| survivor \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\) | Paper-16 clean residual polymer \(Y,\sigma\) | label cover \(\sigma_A\in\Sigma_{16,KP}\) | Paper 16 counts labels by \(L_{KP}\); Paper 23 prints survivor labels abstractly | live: needs `LABEL-COVER(0)` |
| literal coefficient \(R_A^{N,j}\) | clean coefficient \(K_{16}^{clean}(Y,\sigma;N,j)\) | coefficient equality or finite domination | Paper 16 gives clean coefficient framework; Paper 23 gives literal Möbius coefficient | live: needs `ROWID-RES` or \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}<\infty\) |

### Lemma 21.3: What The Current Corpus Actually Proves

On the strict exact branch, the current corpus proves the local part of the
audit:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}LOCAL}
```

in the following limited sense: the local/nonbulk/collar/interior/
counterterm/projective/RP-Cov rows are not live RPF atoms and may not be
charged again to RPF.

It does not prove `P23-RPF-ROWID-LAW`, `P23-RPF-ROWID-CE` unconditionally, or
`P23-RPF-ROWID-RES`.

Proof.

Paper 16 defines `T_HK^std` as a frozen pushed-forward clean heat-kernel row
with local counterterms absorbed and no nonlocal counterterm/scheme polymer
on the clean minimal branch.  Paper 20's strict reduced clean `SEL2` branch
closes nonbulk, collar, counterterm, projective/readout, and interior
Bianchi/off-sheet scalar ledgers when the exact clean conventions are used.
Paper 21 and Paper 23 keep `RPF` as a separate same-law exact-entry
factorization source, rather than merging it with RP/Cov, `CE`, or the local
ledgers.

These results show that the local rows are not live RPF rows.  They do not
identify the actual adaptive residual density of Definition 15.1 with the
Paper-16 clean residual density on `T_HK^std`, and they do not identify the
literal Möbius coefficients with Paper-16 \(K_i(Y)\). `square`

### Theorem 21.4: `ROWID` Current Verdict

The current papers do not prove `P23-RPF-ROWID`.  They prove only the local
no-double-charge part.  The remaining live identity is:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}LAW}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}CE}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}RES}.
}
```

On the exact `CE` branch, the middle clause is absorbed into the declared
central quotient, so the decisive unresolved clause becomes

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}RES}.
}
```

Equivalently, one must prove that finite Möbius inversion of the actual
adaptive residual density gives the same connected residual coefficients as
Paper 16's clean residual expansion.

Proof.

Definition 21.1 decomposes `ROWID`.  Lemma 21.3 proves only the local
component.  Section 15 constructs \(R_A^{N,j}\) from the actual pushed-forward
law, while Paper 16 defines \(K_i(Y)\) as the clean connected residual
coefficient on `T_HK^std`.  No theorem in Papers 16, 20, 21, or Sections
1--20 of this paper asserts equality of these coefficient tables on the
adaptive row.  Thus `ROWID` remains open exactly at the displayed residual
coefficient identity. `square`

### Corollary 21.5: Next Work After The `ROWID` Audit

The next proof attempt should not revisit local ledgers.  It should attack
`P23-RPF-ROWID-RES` directly by one of the following routes.

1. **Expansion uniqueness route.**  Show that Paper-16's clean residual
   coefficients are defined by the same finite Möbius inversion as Definition
   15.2 after the same central quotient.  This would give
   \(\lambda_{RPF}=0\).
2. **Dominated transform route.**  If Paper 16 uses a different connected
   polymer transform, prove a finite triangular transform from the literal
   atoms \(R_A^{N,j}\) to \(K_i(Y)\) with bounded inverse.  This gives a finite
   \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}\).
3. **Failure route.**  Exhibit a survivor atom whose label or coefficient is
   absent from the Paper-16 clean residual table.  Then the clean route fails,
   and RPF must be handled by a new actual-law KP theorem or carried as a
   finite/lower debit.

This is now the smallest honest target: prove equality or finite domination
of two explicit finite coefficient tables on the same pushed-forward scalar
law.

## 22. The Primitive Residual-Coefficient Source Verdict

Section 21 reduced the clean route to `P23-RPF-ROWID-RES`.  This section
checks whether Paper 16 already proves that primitive source theorem.  It
does not.  Paper 16 proves a same-row clean KP envelope and finite counting
theorem on `T_HK^std`; it does not print a coefficient-level equality between
the literal adaptive Möbius atoms of Definition 15.2 and the clean residual
coefficients \(K_i(Y)\).

This matters because a KP envelope can be true for many different coefficient
tables.  Equality of coefficient tables is extra structure.

### Definition 22.1: The Primitive Source Theorem

On the exact `CE` branch, define

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}RESCOEFF\text{-}SRC}
```

to be the assertion that there is a same-record finite map

```math
A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}
\longmapsto
(Y_A,\sigma_A)
```

such that, cofinally in the adaptive row,

```math
R_A^{N,j}
=
K_i(Y_A,\sigma_A)
```

as scalar residual coefficients after the same central quotient and centering
convention.  The finite-domination variant allows

```math
\|R_A^{N,j}\|_{\mathrm{osc}}
\le
e^{\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}}
\|K_i(Y_A,\sigma_A)\|_{\mathrm{ren}}
```

with finite \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}\), and with the same hull size counted by
`HK-FIN-COUNT`.

Thus, on the exact `CE` branch,

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}RES}
```

is exactly `P23-RPF-RESCOEFF-SRC` with \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}=0\), while the
finite-surcharge branch is the domination variant.

### Lemma 22.2: What Paper 16 Supplies

Paper 16 supplies the following inputs on the frozen row `T_HK^std`.

1. A common-row freeze: Definition 9J.11 and Corollary 9J.12 require all
   constants entering the analytic heat-kernel branch to live on one
   pushed-forward finite record row.
2. A residual envelope: Definition 9D.2 bounds the connected residual
   coefficients \(K_i(Y)\) after local counterterms have been removed.
3. A sharp KP scalar decision: Definition 9M.1 and Theorem 9M.1A decide the
   residual KP test from \(A_{res},\mu_{res},C_{KP},h_{KP},r_*\).
4. Finite counting: Definition 9M.1D and Corollary 9M.1F give
   \(C_{KP}=1\) and \(h_{KP}=\log(e\Delta_B L_{KP})\) when the finite
   same-row count `HK-FIN-COUNT(Delta_B,L_ent,L_KP)` is verified.

These are envelope and counting statements.  They do not define \(K_i(Y)\)
by the same Boolean-lattice Möbius inversion used in Definition 15.2, nor do
they map the adaptive survivor atoms \(A\) to Paper-16 labels
\((Y,\sigma)\).

Proof.

Definition 9J.11 fixes the heat-kernel row and Corollary 9J.12 forbids
mixing constants from different pushed-forward laws.  Definition 9D.2 then
uses \(K_i(Y)\) as the renormalized connected residual coefficient of the
whole-process record law after declared local counterterms are removed.
Definition 9M.1D counts finite labels, and Corollary 9M.1F exports
\(C_{KP},h_{KP}\).  None of these statements gives a literal formula

```math
K_i(Y)=
\sum_{B\subseteq A}(-1)^{|A|-|B|}
H(\omega_B,o_{A\setminus B},o_{V\setminus A})
```

for the adaptive residual density \(H_{N,j}\), and none gives a label map
from \({\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\) to the Paper-16 residual table.
`square`

### Lemma 22.3: Envelopes Cannot Force `RESCOEFF-SRC`

The Paper-16 envelope/counting package cannot by itself imply
`P23-RPF-RESCOEFF-SRC`.

Proof.

Work on any finite block graph with two possible residual coefficient
tables \(K\) and \(K'\) satisfying the same bound

```math
\sup_x\sum_{Y\ni x,\ \operatorname{diam}(Y)\ge r}
\|K(Y)\|_{\rm ren}
\le
A e^{-\mu r},
```

and the same bound for \(K'\), with the same finite label count
\(L_{KP}\).  Choose \(K'=0\) on one admissible connected polymer and adjust a
different admissible polymer by a smaller amount so the same envelope
remains true.  Both tables obey the same scalar KP input
\((A,\mu,C_{KP},h_{KP},r_*)\), but they are not coefficientwise equal.

Therefore an envelope plus a finite counting theorem does not determine the
coefficient table.  Since `RESCOEFF-SRC` is a coefficientwise identity or
finite domination statement for the actual adaptive Möbius atoms, it is not a
formal consequence of Paper-16 KP bounds alone. `square`

### Theorem 22.4: Primitive Source Current Verdict

The current corpus does not prove

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}RESCOEFF\text{-}SRC}.
```

Consequently, on the exact `CE` branch, adaptive Branch A remains parked at

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}RES}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LABEL\text{-}COVER}(0)
+
\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}<\infty
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTIVE\text{-}ROWDATA}.
}
```

This is sharper than the Section 20 package: the local ledgers and scalar KP
threshold are not the live issue.  The live issue is whether the actual
adaptive residual density has the same finite connected coefficient table as
the clean heat-kernel residual row, or at least a finite triangular
domination by it.

Proof.

Lemma 22.2 identifies exactly what Paper 16 supplies.  Lemma 22.3 shows that
those supplies do not force coefficient identity.  Section 21 shows that,
after local no-double-charge bookkeeping and exact central-entry division,
`ROWID` reduces to `ROWID-RES`.  Hence the displayed package is the remaining
primitive source package. `square`

### Corollary 22.5: Only Three Honest Continuations

After this audit, there are only three honest continuations for adaptive
Branch A.

1. **Print the coefficient formula.**  Add a new source theorem proving that
   Paper-16 \(K_i(Y)\) is generated by the same same-record Möbius transform
   as Definition 15.2 on the exact adaptive row.  This closes
   `ROWID-RES` with \(\lambda_{RPF}^{sharp}=0\).
2. **Print a finite triangular transform.**  Prove a rowwise finite
   transform from literal atoms \(R_A^{N,j}\) to clean coefficients \(K_i(Y)\)
   with bounded inverse.  This closes the finite-surcharge branch.
3. **Abandon the clean transfer.**  If no such equality or finite domination
   exists, do not keep importing the Paper-16 clean table.  Prove a fresh
   actual-law Dobrushin/KP theorem directly for the literal atoms of
   Definition 15.2, or carry/falsify the RPF debit.

Anything else would either reuse local ledgers already spent elsewhere or
silently replace the pushed-forward adaptive scalar law by a different
heat-kernel proof row.

## 23. Canonical Coefficient Gauge And The Closure Of `ROWID-RES`

Section 22 showed that Paper 16 does not itself print the coefficient identity
needed by `ROWID-RES`.  The way out is not to pretend that an envelope is an
identity.  The way out is to use the canonical finite coefficient gauge already
available on the actual adaptive law.

This section closes the coefficient identity obstruction in that canonical
gauge.  It does **not** close adaptive Branch A.  It changes the remaining
burden from coefficient identity to canonical finite-label entropy and active
row data.

### Definition 23.1: Canonical Anchored RPF Coefficient Row

On each exact `CE` adaptive row \((N,j)\), keep the same finite scalar law
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\), the same reference support, the same basepoint \(o\),
and the same finite over-refined cover \(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) as Definition 15.2.

For every survivor

```math
A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j},
```

define the canonical clean coefficient

```math
K_{can}^{N,j}(Y(A),\sigma_A^{can})
:=
R_A^{N,j},
```

where

```math
\sigma_A^{can}
:=
\bigl(
Y(A), A\subseteq Y(A),
\tau_{char}(A),\tau_{source}(A),\tau_{collar}(A),\tau_{cent}(A)
\bigr)
```

is a finite scalar label recording exactly the hull, the sub-support inside
the hull, and the already declared residual labels of Definition 20.2.  The
canonical row is the finite table

```math
{\mathcal K}_{RPF,can}^{N,j}
:=
\{K_{can}^{N,j}(Y(A),\sigma_A^{can}):
A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\}.
```

No new stochastic process is introduced.  This is only a coefficient gauge
for the same finite scalar Hamiltonian \(H_{N,j}^{RPF}\).

### Lemma 23.2: Uniqueness Of The Anchored Finite Interaction Expansion

Let \(V\) be a finite record cover, \(o\) a basepoint, and \(H\) a scalar
function on the finite pushed-forward record space.  Suppose a family
\(\{\Psi_A\}_{\emptyset\ne A\subseteq V}\) satisfies:

1. \(\Psi_A\) depends only on coordinates in \(A\);
2. \(\Psi_A(\omega_A)=0\) whenever at least one coordinate in \(A\) is set to
   its basepoint value and all smaller sub-support contributions have already
   been removed;
3. the exact reconstruction holds:

   ```math
   H(\omega)-H(o)=
   \sum_{\emptyset\ne A\subseteq V}\Psi_A(\omega_A).
   ```

Then \(\Psi_A\) is exactly the finite Möbius coefficient

```math
\Phi_A(\omega_A)
=
\sum_{B\subseteq A}
(-1)^{|A|-|B|}
H(\omega_B,o_{A\setminus B},o_{V\setminus A}).
```

Proof.

Evaluate the reconstruction at
\((\omega_B,o_{V\setminus B})\) for every \(B\subseteq V\).  This gives a
triangular linear system over the Boolean lattice of subsets of \(V\).  The
diagonal entries are \(1\), because each coefficient first appears on its own
support after all smaller supports have been removed.  Inverting that
triangular system is precisely the Möbius inversion formula displayed above.
Thus the anchored exact interaction expansion is unique. `square`

### Theorem 23.3: Canonical `ROWID-RES`

On the exact `CE` strict branch, the canonical coefficient row of Definition
23.1 proves

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}RES}_{can}.
```

More concretely, for every survivor
\(A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\),

```math
R_A^{N,j}
=
K_{can}^{N,j}(Y(A),\sigma_A^{can})
```

as scalar coefficients on the same adaptive pushed-forward law.  Hence the
coefficient surcharge is zero in the canonical gauge:

```math
\lambda_{RPF}^{can}=0.
```

Proof.

Definition 15.2 defines \(R_A^{N,j}\) by finite Möbius inversion of the
actual residual Hamiltonian \(H_{N,j}^{RPF}\), after exact central-entry
division and after the local/nonbulk/collar/interior/projective/RP-Cov rows
have been removed or carried outside RPF.  Lemma 15.3 gives exact
reconstruction.  Lemma 23.2 says the anchored coefficient system with these
properties is unique.  Definition 23.1 chooses the clean coefficient gauge to
be this unique anchored coefficient system.  The displayed equality follows
by definition and uniqueness, all inside the same scalar law. `square`

### Definition 23.4: Canonical Label Entropy

The price of using the canonical gauge is that the Paper-16 label count
\(L_{KP}\) is no longer automatically the right label count.  Define the
canonical label count at connected hull size \(n\) by

```math
L_{can}^{N,j}(n)
:=
\sup_{Y:\ |Y|=n}
\#\{\sigma_A^{can}:Y(A)=Y\}.
```

`P23-RPF-CAN-LABEL-ENT(h_can,C_can)` holds if cofinally

```math
L_{can}^{N,j}(n)\le C_{can}e^{h_{can}n}
```

for all \(n\).  Then the canonical KP entropy rate is

```math
h_{KP}^{can}
=
\log(e\Delta_B)+h_{can},
```

with \(C_{KP}^{can}=C_{can}\), up to harmless global finite prefactors.

If the stronger label-cover theorem

```math
\Sigma_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\subseteq\Sigma_{16,KP}^{N,j}
```

holds, then one may take \(C_{can}=1\) and
\(h_{can}=\log L_{KP}\), recovering Paper 16's clean count
\(h_{KP}=\log(e\Delta_B L_{KP})\).

### Theorem 23.5: Canonical Coefficient Domination

Assume `P23-RPF-CAN-LABEL-ENT(h_can,C_can)`.  Then the coefficient identity
side of the clean transfer is closed in the following precise sense:

```math
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
=
\|K_{can}^{N,j}(Y(A),\sigma_A^{can})\|_{\operatorname{osc}}
```

for every survivor \(A\), and the only change in the scalar KP test is the
replacement

```math
(C_{KP},h_{KP})
\quad\leadsto\quad
(C_{can},\log(e\Delta_B)+h_{can}).
```

Thus the canonical route proves `P23-RPF-CLEAN-ROWMAP(0)` relative to the
canonical finite row.  The remaining scalar decision is exactly Section 16's
row test with \(h_{KP}^{can}\) and \(C_{KP}^{can}\).

Proof.

The coefficient equality is Theorem 23.3.  The entropy replacement is the
same connected-set counting argument as Paper 16 Definition 9M.1D and
Corollary 9M.1F: connected hulls of size \(n\) containing a fixed block are
bounded by \((e\Delta_B)^n\), and each hull carries at most
\(C_{can}e^{h_{can}n}\) canonical residual labels.  Multiplication gives

```math
C_{can}\exp((\log(e\Delta_B)+h_{can})n).
```

No coefficient surcharge remains; only the label entropy changes. `square`

### Corollary 23.6: The Coefficient Obstruction Is Closed, Not The Branch

The obstruction

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ROWID\text{-}RES}
```

is closed in the canonical same-law coefficient gauge.  Adaptive Branch A is
therefore no longer blocked by coefficient identity/domination.  The live
tasks are now:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}LABEL\text{-}ENT}(h_{can},C_{can})
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTIVE\text{-}ROWDATA}_{can}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}KP\text{-}MARGIN}.
}
```

Here `P23-RPF-CAN-KP-MARGIN` is Section 16's scalar condition with

```math
C_{RPF}=C_{can},
\qquad
h_{RPF}=\log(e\Delta_B)+h_{can},
\qquad
\lambda_{RPF}=0.
```

If the canonical label entropy is no larger than Paper 16's clean
\(\log L_{KP}\), the previous clean scalar pass applies.  If it is larger,
the scalar table must be rerun with the enlarged entropy.  If
`P23-RPF-CAN-LABEL-ENT` fails, the canonical route fails and one must prove a
fresh actual-law KP theorem or carry/falsify the RPF debit.

This is a genuine shift of the frontier: the remaining problem is finite
entropy and active row data, not the equality of coefficient tables.

## 24. Canonical Label Entropy Worksheet And Scalar Survival Test

This section executes the six-step canonical entropy investigation promised
after Section 23.  The conclusion is deliberately two-sided:
