1. the current corpus proves a finite same-record canonical entropy bound by
   importing the Paper-21 over-refined carrier; but
2. that bound is much too coarse to certify the RPF scalar margin unless a
   later selector/automaton sharply reduces the canonical label count or the
   active row-data theorem sources an arbitrarily large finite residual
   margin on the same adaptive law.

### Definition 24.1: Canonical Local Vertex Multiplicity

For the adaptive RPF cover, define

```math
v_{RPF}^{can}
:=
\sup_{N,j}\sup_B
\#\{v\in V_{RPF}^{N,j}:v\text{ is rooted in block }B\}.
```

The Paper-21 Section-102 over-refined carrier gives a conservative finite
upper bound.  Let \(N_W^{99}\) be the reduced word count of Paper 21 Lemma
111.2:

```math
N_W^{99}
\le
6705705274431562880.
```

The active template list of Paper 21 Definition 102.3 obeys

```math
|\mathfrak T_{99}^{+}|
\le
24\left(1+3N_W^{99}+(3N_W^{99})^2\right),
```

and the remaining over-refined labels give

```math
|\overline V_{99}^{lit,+}|
\le
|\mathfrak T_{99}^{+}|\cdot
3\cdot 2^{80}\cdot133\cdot3\cdot16.
```

Define

```math
v_{99}^{+}
:=
|\mathfrak T_{99}^{+}|\cdot
3\cdot 2^{80}\cdot133\cdot3\cdot16.
```

Then the conservative same-record bound is

```math
v_{RPF}^{can}\le v_{99}^{+},
\qquad
\log v_{99}^{+}\le157.39.
```

Equivalently \(v_{99}^{+}\lesssim10^{68.36}\).  This is finite, but it is an
over-refined carrier bound, not a useful sharp constant.

Proof.

Paper 21 Definition 102.3 has four row classes, six template flags, and
degree \(0\le d\le2\), with three possible \(\lambda\)-labels and
\(N_W^{99}\) word choices per factor.  This gives the displayed
\(|\mathfrak T_{99}^{+}|\).  Paper 21 Definitions 102.4--102.6 add the
three \(\mu\)-labels, at most \(2^{80}\) rooted frontier labels, \(133\)
channel labels, three product-degree labels, and \(16\) symmetry/center
labels.  Multiplying gives \(v_{99}^{+}\).  The logarithmic numerical bound
is obtained by substituting Paper 21 Lemma 111.2's value of \(N_W^{99}\).
`square`

### Lemma 24.2: Crude Canonical Label Entropy

Using only the over-refined carrier and no physical selector, the canonical
label count satisfies

```math
L_{can}^{N,j}(n)
\le
2^{v_{99}^{+}n}.
```

Thus `P23-RPF-CAN-LABEL-ENT(h_can,C_can)` holds with

```math
C_{can}=1,
\qquad
h_{can}^{coarse}=v_{99}^{+}\log2.
```

Equivalently,

```math
\log h_{can}^{coarse}
\le
157.02.
```

Proof.

A connected hull of \(n\) blocks contains at most \(v_{99}^{+}n\) over-refined
RPF vertices in the conservative carrier.  A canonical support
\(A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) inside that hull is therefore one of at most
\(2^{v_{99}^{+}n}\) subsets.  In the canonical gauge, the auxiliary labels
\(\tau_{char},\tau_{source},\tau_{collar},\tau_{cent}\) are already encoded by
the selected over-refined vertices.  Hence no extra label alphabet is needed
for this coarse bound. `square`

### Definition 24.3: Selector/Automaton Sharpening Target

The crude \(2^{v_{99}^{+}n}\) count ignores the fact that most over-refined
subsets are not actual canonical RPF atoms.  A sharp canonical entropy proof
should print a finite automaton

```math
{\mathcal A}_{can}
```

whose accepted words are exactly the admissible survivor supports \(A\) in a
rooted connected hull.  Let \(\rho_{can}\) be the Perron root of its transfer
matrix and \(C_{can}^{aut}\) the corresponding finite prefactor.  Then the
desired sharpening is

```math
L_{can}^{N,j}(n)
\le
C_{can}^{aut}\rho_{can}^{n},
\qquad
h_{can}^{aut}:=\log\rho_{can}.
```

Current status: the corpus has not printed \({\mathcal A}_{can}\), so the
only unconditional entropy bound presently available is Lemma 24.2.

### Definition 24.4: Canonical Scalar KP Margin

For a proposed canonical row-data package define

```math
h_{RPF}^{can}:=\log(e\Delta_B)+h_{can},
\qquad
C_{RPF}^{can}:=C_{can},
\qquad
\Delta_{can}:=\mu_{res}^{can}-h_{RPF}^{can},
```

and

```math
B_{can}:=2A_{res}^{can}C_{can}.
```

The direct no-absorption canonical RPF route passes exactly when

```math
\Delta_{can}
>
\Delta_{crit}(B_{can})
=
\log\left(
{2+B_{can}+\sqrt{B_{can}^2+4B_{can}}\over2}
\right).
```

This is Theorem 16.2 with
\(\lambda_{RPF}=0\), \(h_{RPF}=h_{RPF}^{can}\), and
\(C_{RPF}=C_{can}\).

### Theorem 24.5: Coarse Entropy Does Not Certify Direct Survival

With the over-refined entropy bound of Lemma 24.2, direct canonical survival
requires at least

```math
\mu_{res}^{can}
>
\log(e\Delta_B)
+v_{99}^{+}\log2
+\Delta_{crit}(2A_{res}^{can})
```

when \(C_{can}=1\).  The present corpus does not source such a numerical
margin on the actual adaptive law.

Consequently the coarse over-refined entropy bound proves finiteness but does
not close `P23-RPF-CAN-KP-MARGIN`.

Proof.

Substitute \(h_{can}=v_{99}^{+}\log2\) and \(C_{can}=1\) from Lemma 24.2 into
Definition 24.4.  The displayed strict inequality is exactly the direct
threshold.  Paper 16 can tune finite margins on its clean worksheet after
the finite row data are verified, but the current Paper-23 adaptive row-data
package has not verified that the canonical row can be run with a margin of
order \(v_{99}^{+}\log2\) on the same adaptive law.  Therefore direct
survival is not certified. `square`

### Definition 24.6: Canonical Absorption Rescue

If \(\Delta_{can}>0\), define the exact minimal canonical absorption range

```math
R_{min}^{can}
:=
\min\left\{
R\ge1:
B_{can}
{e^{-\Delta_{can}R}
\bigl(R-(R-1)e^{-\Delta_{can}}\bigr)
\over
(1-e^{-\Delta_{can}})^2}
<1
\right\}.
```

This is finite whenever \(\Delta_{can}>0\).  The range-rescued route then
requires the same-law absorption theorem

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}ABSORB}(R)
```

for some \(R\ge R_{min}^{can}\), meaning all canonical atoms with hull size
\(<R\) are absorbed into the declared local block law, central entry factor,
finite normalization, or exact-entry battery without being recharged to any
other ledger.

### Theorem 24.7: Six-Step Canonical Entropy Verdict

The six-step investigation has the following current verdict.

1. **Local vertex multiplicity:** finite, with
   \(v_{RPF}^{can}\le v_{99}^{+}\) and \(\log v_{99}^{+}\le157.39\).
2. **Canonical label count:** finite, with
   \(L_{can}(n)\le2^{v_{99}^{+}n}\).
3. **Automaton sharpening:** not printed by the current corpus; this is now
   the main useful next finite-table task.
4. **Scalar insertion:** canonical entropy enters only through
   \(h_{RPF}^{can}=\log(e\Delta_B)+h_{can}\), with zero coefficient
   surcharge.
5. **Direct KP survival:** not certified by the coarse entropy bound; it
   would require the large displayed margin in Theorem 24.5.
6. **Range absorption:** formally available whenever \(\Delta_{can}>0\), via
   \(R_{min}^{can}\), but not certified because
   `P23-RPF-CAN-ABSORB(R)` has not been proved.

Thus adaptive Branch A is now parked at the sharper finite package

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}AUT}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTIVE\text{-}ROWDATA}_{can}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}KP\text{-}MARGIN}
}
```

where `P23-RPF-CAN-AUT` means either a selector/automaton entropy bound small
enough for Theorem 24.4, or a proof that the canonical entropy is too large
for every available same-law margin source.

This is a genuine improvement over Section 23: the coefficient identity is
closed, the finite entropy is bounded, and the remaining obstruction is now a
specific finite automaton/active-rowdata margin computation.

## 25. Canonical Selector Automaton

Section 24 showed that the crude over-refined carrier is finite but too large.
This section executes the selector/automaton construction up to the exact
point where the current corpus runs out of source data.  The distinction is
important: the structural automaton is finite and same-record, but sharpness
requires a finite value-locality table deciding when the actual Möbius
coefficient \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) is nonzero.

### Definition 25.1: Exact Canonical Selector Predicate

For a finite row \((N,j)\) and a finite nonempty support
\(A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}\), define

```math
{\bf 1}_{can}^{N,j}(A)=1
```

iff all of the following hold:

1. \(A\) has connected RPF hull \(Y(A)\);
2. the anchored Möbius coefficient is nonzero:

   ```math
   \Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0
   ```

   as a scalar function on the same adaptive pushed-forward row;
3. the literal classifier of Definition 18.1 satisfies

   ```math
   \mathfrak c_{RPF}(A)=\mathrm{CleanRPF};
   ```

4. exact `CE`, strict local ledger removal, clean collar/interior/counterterm
   conventions, and the RP/Cov diagonal selector are the same conventions used
   in Sections 18--24.

The exact canonical language is

```math
{\mathcal L}_{can}^{N,j}
:=
\{A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}:{\bf 1}_{can}^{N,j}(A)=1\}.
```

This is not an auxiliary model.  It is just the exact survivor predicate for
the already-defined finite scalar row.

### Definition 25.2: Component Tests

Write the selector as

```math
{\bf 1}_{can}
=
S_{conn}\,S_{val}\,S_{clean}\,S_{branch},
```

where:

1. \(S_{conn}(A)=1\) iff \(Y(A)\) is connected and rooted by the canonical
   hull convention;
2. \(S_{val}(A)=1\) iff \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0\);
3. \(S_{clean}(A)=1\) iff the classifier is `CleanRPF`, equivalently none of
   the closed classes

   ```math
   \mathrm{CElead},\mathrm{LocTime},\mathrm{Nonbulk},
   \mathrm{CollarBianchi},\mathrm{IntYM2},
   \mathrm{CtSch},\mathrm{ProjRead}
   ```

   applies;
4. \(S_{branch}(A)=1\) iff the exact strict branch conventions of Lemma 18.2
   are active.

The tests \(S_{conn},S_{clean},S_{branch}\) are structural finite-label tests
on the over-refined carrier.  The test \(S_{val}\) is a finite value-source
test for the actual adaptive pushed-forward law.  The current corpus has not
printed a local table for \(S_{val}\).

### Definition 25.3: Selector State Alphabet

Let \(\pi_{sel}\) be the coarsest quotient of the Paper-21 over-refined
vertex labels that preserves all structural tests in Definition 25.2.  A
selector state records only:

```math
s=
(
\tau_{shape}^{loc},
\tau_{char},
\tau_{source},
\tau_{collar},
\tau_{cent},
\tau_{closed},
\tau_{ports}
),
```

where:

1. \(\tau_{shape}^{loc}\) is the local attachment shape and root-port data;
2. \(\tau_{char}\), \(\tau_{source}\), \(\tau_{collar}\), and \(\tau_{cent}\)
   are the residual labels of Definition 20.2;
3. \(\tau_{closed}\) records whether a closed class of Definition 18.1 has
   already been triggered;
4. \(\tau_{ports}\) records the finite boundary ports needed to glue a
   connected hull through the block graph.

Define the finite state alphabet

```math
{\mathsf S}_{can}:=\pi_{sel}(\overline V_{99}^{lit,+}).
```

It is finite because \(\overline V_{99}^{lit,+}\) is finite by Paper 21
Theorem 102.7.  It satisfies

```math
|{\mathsf S}_{can}|\le v_{99}^{+},
```

but it may be much smaller because all labels irrelevant to the selector are
quotiented out.

### Definition 25.4: The Structural Selector Automaton

Let \(G_B\) be the block adjacency graph with maximum degree \(\Delta_B\).
For a rooted connected hull \(Y\), choose the canonical breadth-first spanning
tree \(T_Y\) using the fixed block ordering.  The structural selector
automaton

```math
{\mathcal A}_{can}^{str}
```

is the finite tree automaton with:

1. state set \({\mathsf S}_{can}\);
2. root-allowed states \({\mathsf S}_{root}\subseteq{\mathsf S}_{can}\);
3. child transition relation

   ```math
   M_{can}^{str}(s,t)\in\{0,1\},
   ```

   where \(M_{can}^{str}(s,t)=1\) iff a child block in state \(t\) can be
   attached to a parent block in state \(s\) without violating the local
   port, collar, central-entry, closed-class, or centering structural tests;
4. a bounded non-tree edge checker

   ```math
   E_{can}^{str}(s,t,e)\in\{0,1\}
   ```

   for extra edges \(e\) of \(Y\setminus T_Y\).

An assignment of states to blocks in \(Y\) is structurally accepted iff the
root state is root-allowed, every tree edge is \(M_{can}^{str}\)-allowed,
every non-tree edge is \(E_{can}^{str}\)-allowed, and no state triggers a
closed class.

This is an exact finite structural selector for
\(S_{conn}S_{clean}S_{branch}\).  It does not yet decide \(S_{val}\).

### Definition 25.5: Value-Locality Source Table

`P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL` is the assertion that the nonzero Möbius predicate
\(S_{val}\) is decided by a finite same-law value table on the selector
states.  Concretely, there must exist a finite set of value tags
\({\mathsf V}_{can}\), a map

```math
\upsilon_{can}: {\mathsf S}_{can}^{\le r_v}\longrightarrow{\mathsf V}_{can},
```

for some finite radius \(r_v\), and a subset
\({\mathsf V}_{nz}\subseteq{\mathsf V}_{can}\), such that for every survivor
candidate \(A\),

```math
S_{val}(A)=1
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\upsilon_{can}(\text{the radius-}r_v\text{ selector pattern of }A)
\in{\mathsf V}_{nz}.
```

All entries of \(\upsilon_{can}\) are evaluated from the actual
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) on the same pushed-forward scalar law.  Gauge-coordinate
proof variables are not allowed as hidden states.

The current corpus does not prove `P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL`.

### Theorem 25.6: Language Equivalence

Assume `P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL`.  Extend
\({\mathcal A}_{can}^{str}\) by the value tags of Definition 25.5 and call the
result

```math
{\mathcal A}_{can}.
```

Then, cofinally in \((N,j)\),

```math
A\text{ is accepted by }{\mathcal A}_{can}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
A\in{\mathcal L}_{can}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

The structural part of \({\mathcal A}_{can}\) is Definition 25.4, which is
constructed to be equivalent to \(S_{conn}S_{clean}S_{branch}=1\): the root
and port states enforce connected rooted hulls, and the closed-class flags
are exactly the negation of the seven non-`CleanRPF` classes in Definition
18.1 under the strict branch conventions of Lemma 18.2.  The value extension
is exactly Definition 25.5, which is equivalent to \(S_{val}=1\).  Multiplying
the four tests gives Definition 25.1. `square`

Without `P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL`, the structural automaton is an exact
structural over-selector but not a sharp canonical language selector.

### Definition 25.7: Transfer Matrix And Safe Entropy Bound

Let

```math
M_{can}(s,t)
```

be the transition matrix of the value-extended automaton when
`P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL` is available; otherwise use \(M_{can}^{str}\) and mark
the result as structural only.  Define

```math
d_{can}:=
\max_{s\in{\mathsf S}_{can}}
\#\{t\in{\mathsf S}_{can}:M_{can}(s,t)=1\}.
```

For arbitrary connected hulls of maximum degree \(\Delta_B\), a safe
same-record entropy certificate is

```math
L_{can}(n)
\le
|{\mathsf S}_{root}|\,
d_{can}^{\,n-1},
```

so one may take

```math
C_{can}^{aut}=|{\mathsf S}_{root}|,
\qquad
h_{can}^{aut}=\log d_{can}.
```

If a sharper graph-directed/tree partition-function calculation is printed,
it may replace \(d_{can}\) by the corresponding certified growth constant,
but the row-sum bound above is the currently safe matrix export for arbitrary
connected hulls.

### Theorem 25.8: Six-Step Automaton Verdict

Steps 1--6 of the sharp-selector program now have the following status.

1. **Exact selector predicate:** printed in Definition 25.1.
2. **Finite test split:** printed in Definition 25.2.
3. **Reduced state alphabet:** printed in Definition 25.3, with
   \(|{\mathsf S}_{can}|\le v_{99}^{+}\).
4. **Automaton:** the exact structural automaton is printed in Definition
   25.4.
5. **Language equivalence:** proved in Theorem 25.6 conditional on the finite
   same-law value table `P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL`; not proved unconditionally by
   the current corpus.
6. **Transfer matrix:** printed in Definition 25.7, with the safe entropy
   export \(h_{can}^{aut}=\log d_{can}\) once the value-extended transition
   table is supplied.

Therefore the next obstruction is no longer "build an automaton" in the
abstract.  It is the finite source theorem

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}VAL\text{-}LOCAL}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}TRANSITION\text{-}TABLE}
}
```

together with the scalar margin test of Section 24.  If the value-local table
is printed and \(d_{can}\) is small enough for Theorem 24.4, then
`P23-RPF-TRANS0` follows.  If no finite value-local table exists, the sharp
canonical automaton route fails and the branch must use a fresh actual-law KP
theorem or carry/falsify the RPF debit.

## 26. Same-Law Value Table For The Möbius Nonzero Predicate

Section 25 isolated the exact missing selector ingredient: decide, on the same
adaptive pushed-forward scalar law, whether the actual Möbius coefficient
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) is nonzero.  There are two different statements here.

The first is rowwise and finite: for a fixed adaptive row \((N,j)\), the
finite table exists because \(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) is finite and
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) is already a finite scalar function of the actual law.  The
second is cofinal and useful for the entropy margin: the decision must be
made by a bounded-radius canonical value automaton with finitely many states
independent of the row.  Section 26 closes the first statement and reduces
the second to a precise local residual-Hamiltonian source theorem.

### Definition 26.1: Exact Rowwise Value Table

For a fixed finite adaptive row \((N,j)\), define the exact same-law value
table

```math
{\mathcal T}_{val}^{N,j}
:=
\left\{
\left(A,\zeta_A^{N,j}\right):
\emptyset\ne A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}
\right\},
```

where

```math
\zeta_A^{N,j}
=
\begin{cases}
\mathrm{nz},&\Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0
\quad\text{on the row support of }\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2},\\
\mathrm{zero},&\Phi_A^{N,j}\equiv0
\quad\text{on the row support of }\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}.
\end{cases}
```

Equivalently, when Definition 15.1 uses essential boundary conventions, the
zero alternative is equality modulo \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\)-null row sets.
The table is a scalar-record table: its entries are evaluated from
\(H_{N,j}=\log{\mathcal R}_{N,j}\) and the Boolean-lattice formula of
Definition 15.2.  It contains no gauge-coordinate hidden state, continuum YM
measure, or auxiliary Markov kernel.

### Lemma 26.2: The Exact Rowwise Table Exists And Decides \(S_{val}\)

For every finite adaptive row \((N,j)\), \({\mathcal T}_{val}^{N,j}\) is a
finite same-law table and, for every candidate \(A\),

```math
S_{val}(A)=1
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\zeta_A^{N,j}=\mathrm{nz}.
```

Proof.

Definition 15.1 fixes the finite scalar record space \(\Omega_{N,j}\), the
actual pushed-forward law \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\), and the finite vertex cover
\(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\).  Hence the set of nonempty candidates
\(\emptyset\ne A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) is finite.

For each such \(A\), Definition 15.2 defines \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) by the finite
alternating sum

```math
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A)
=
\sum_{B\subseteq A}
(-1)^{|A|-|B|}
H_{N,j}(\omega_B,o_{A\setminus B},o_{V_{RPF}^{N,j}\setminus A}).
```

Thus the assertion \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\equiv0\) is an assertion about a finite
scalar function already built from the same pushed-forward row law.  Recording
the truth value of that assertion for each \(A\) gives
\({\mathcal T}_{val}^{N,j}\).  Definition 25.2 defines \(S_{val}\) by exactly
the same nonzero predicate, so the displayed equivalence follows. `square`

### Procedure 26.2A: Printing A Fixed-Row Value Table

For a concrete finite row \((N,j)\), the table is printed by the following
same-law finite procedure.

1. List the finite row vertex cover \(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\).
2. Enumerate nonempty candidate supports
   \(A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}\), optionally after first applying the structural
   filters \(S_{conn}\), \(S_{clean}\), and \(S_{branch}\).
3. For each surviving \(A\), evaluate the finite Boolean-lattice expression
   of Definition 15.2 from \(H_{N,j}=\log{\mathcal R}_{N,j}\) on the actual
   pushed-forward scalar law.
4. Mark the row entry as `zero` if that scalar record is identically zero on
   the selected row support, and `nz` otherwise.
5. Feed the resulting tag \(\zeta_A^{N,j}\) into the canonical selector of
   Definition 25.1.

The printed row has the schema

```math
\left(
A,\ \mathrm{can}(A),\
S_{conn}(A),\ S_{clean}(A),\ S_{branch}(A),\
\zeta_A^{N,j}
\right),
```

where \(\mathrm{can}(A)\) is the canonical anchored label of Section 23.  This
is the literal same-law finite table deciding the actual Möbius nonzero
predicate for that row.

### Corollary 26.3: Rowwise Sharp Selector Exists

For every fixed finite adaptive row \((N,j)\), the structural selector of
Definition 25.4 can be made exact by adjoining \({\mathcal T}_{val}^{N,j}\).
The resulting finite row selector accepts exactly the canonical clean RPF
survivor language

```math
{\mathcal L}_{can}^{N,j}.
```

This corollary does not yet give the entropy input required by Theorem 24.4.
The rowwise table may depend on the full row \((N,j)\), may have
\(2^{|V_{RPF}^{N,j}|}-1\) entries, and need not be generated by a bounded
canonical radius.  It closes finite-row decidability, not the cofinal
automaton margin.

### Definition 26.4: Local Residual-Hamiltonian Source

`P23-RPF-HLOC(r_H,{\mathfrak G}_H)` is the assertion that, cofinally on the
same adaptive `SEL2` scalar law, the residual Hamiltonian admits a finite
local generator decomposition

```math
H_{N,j}(\omega)-H_{N,j}(o)
=
\sum_{\gamma\in{\mathfrak G}_{H}^{N,j}}
h_{\theta(\gamma)}
\left(\omega_{\operatorname{supp}\gamma}\right),
```

where:

1. \(\theta(\gamma)\) belongs to a finite type set
   \(\Theta_H\), independent of \((N,j)\);
2. each \(h_\theta\) is a scalar-record function on the same pushed-forward
   row law;
3. \(\operatorname{diam}(\operatorname{supp}\gamma)\le r_H\);
4. the decomposition contains no term already removed into the local,
   central-entry, RP/Cov, readout, perimeter, cusp, or decoration ledgers.

For a generator \(\gamma\) and candidate \(A\), write

```math
\Delta_A h_\gamma
:=
\sum_{B\subseteq A}
(-1)^{|A|-|B|}
h_{\theta(\gamma)}
\left(\omega_{B\cap\operatorname{supp}\gamma},
      o_{\operatorname{supp}\gamma\setminus B}\right).
```

`P23-RPF-HVAL({\mathfrak G}_H)` is the finite value source stating that the
same-law local pattern of the finitely many generators intersecting a
radius-\(r_H\) canonical neighborhood decides whether

```math
\sum_{\gamma:A\subseteq\operatorname{supp}\gamma}
\Delta_A h_\gamma
```

is identically zero or nonzero.  This includes exact cancellation decisions
between generator contributions of the same local canonical pattern.

### Lemma 26.5: Local Generators Imply The Value-Local Table

Assume `P23-RPF-HLOC(r_H,{\mathfrak G}_H)` and
`P23-RPF-HVAL({\mathfrak G}_H)`.  Then
`P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL` holds with a finite value radius

```math
r_v\le r_H
```

after replacing \(r_H\) by the corresponding canonical adjacency radius if
the generator support metric and selector graph metric differ by the fixed
Paper-21 carrier constant.

Proof.

Apply the Boolean-lattice finite difference \(\Delta_A\) to the local
decomposition in Definition 26.4.  If
\(A\not\subseteq\operatorname{supp}\gamma\), the alternating sum in at least
one coordinate of \(A\setminus\operatorname{supp}\gamma\) cancels, so
\(\Delta_A h_\gamma=0\).  Therefore

```math
\Phi_A^{N,j}
=
\sum_{\gamma:A\subseteq\operatorname{supp}\gamma}
\Delta_A h_\gamma.
```

All generators contributing to the sum lie inside the radius-\(r_H\)
canonical neighborhood of \(A\).  The generator types, support shapes, and
scalar functions are finite by `P23-RPF-HLOC`; the zero/nonzero and exact
cancellation decisions for their local sums are finite by `P23-RPF-HVAL`.
Hence a finite map \(\upsilon_{can}\) of the form required in Definition
25.5 exists. `square`

### Theorem 26.6: Current Verdict For The Möbius Nonzero Table

The current corpus proves the exact finite row table
\({\mathcal T}_{val}^{N,j}\) of Definition 26.1 for every fixed row.  It does
not yet prove the uniform bounded-radius table
`P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL`.

More precisely, the remaining source theorem is

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HLOC}(r_H,{\mathfrak G}_H)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HVAL}({\mathfrak G}_H)
}
```

and, by Lemma 26.5, this theorem implies

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}VAL\text{-}LOCAL}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}TRANSITION\text{-}TABLE}.
```

Proof.

Lemma 26.2 proves the rowwise table directly from Definitions 15.1 and 15.2.
That proof uses the actual adaptive pushed-forward scalar law and is
therefore same-law.

The stronger uniform table is not printed in the existing source corpus.
Paper 23 Section 22 showed that Paper 16 supplies clean KP envelopes and
finite counting constants, not literal adaptive Möbius coefficient identities.
Paper 23 Section 25 printed the structural automaton but explicitly left
`P23-RPF-CAN-VAL-LOCAL` open.  The Paper-21 finite-table exports print
structural row maps and over-refined carriers while keeping literal source
values, zero/carry tags, and inverse/value slots as source-table data rather
than consequences of the structural carrier alone.  Thus the available
papers justify exact rowwise finite decidability, but not a cofinal
bounded-radius value automaton.  Lemma 26.5 identifies the missing primitive
source that would supply it. `square`

### Corollary 26.7: Updated Adaptive Branch-A Frontier

The Möbius nonzero predicate is no longer an undefined object:

```math
\forall (N,j)\quad
{\mathcal T}_{val}^{N,j}
\text{ exists and decides }
\Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0.
```

The live Branch-A obstruction is the sharp cofinal compression of that table:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HLOC}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HVAL}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTIVE\text{-}ROWDATA}_{can}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}KP\text{-}MARGIN}.
```

The next useful task is therefore to print the local residual-Hamiltonian
generator/value table, or prove that no bounded-radius same-law value table
can decide \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0\) on the adaptive `SEL2` branch.  Spending
the rowwise table directly is always finite for a fixed row, but it does not
yet preserve the scalar KP margin cofinally.

## 27. Five-Front Execution Of The HLOC Frontier

Section 26 sharpened the missing automaton source to

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HLOC}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HVAL}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTIVE\text{-}ROWDATA}_{can}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CAN\text{-}KP\text{-}MARGIN}.
```

This section executes the five steps in order.  The verdict is precise:
there is an exact finite row generator, but the current corpus does not prove
the cofinal bounded local generator alphabet required by `P23-RPF-HLOC`.
Everything after HLOC is finite and explicit once that source is supplied.

### Definition 27.1: The Exact Rowwise Möbius Generator

For each fixed finite adaptive row \((N,j)\), define

```math
{\mathfrak G}_{M}^{N,j}
:=
\{\,\gamma_A:A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}\,\},
```

with

```math
\operatorname{supp}\gamma_A=A,
\qquad
\theta(\gamma_A)=\operatorname{can}(A),
\qquad
h_{\gamma_A}:=\Phi_A^{N,j}.
```

The rowwise generator radius and rowwise generator size are

```math
r_M(N,j)
:=
\max_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}}
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A),
\qquad
s_M(N,j)
:=
\max_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF}^{N,j}}
\ell_{RPF}(A),
```

with value \(0\) if the row has no live atoms.

### Lemma 27.2: Rowwise HLOC Is Automatic

For every fixed finite adaptive row \((N,j)\),

```math
H_{N,j}(\omega)-H_{N,j}(o)
=
\sum_{\gamma_A\in{\mathfrak G}_{M}^{N,j}}
h_{\gamma_A}(\omega_A).
```

Thus exact finite-row localization holds with radius \(r_M(N,j)\) and size
\(s_M(N,j)\).

Proof.

This is Lemma 15.3 with the zero Möbius coefficients deleted from the sum.
Each \(h_{\gamma_A}\) is the same scalar record \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) defined by
Definition 15.2, and therefore depends only on the pushed-forward row
coordinates in \(A\).  No auxiliary law is introduced. `square`

### Definition 27.3: Cofinal Bounded HLOC Source

`P23-RPF-HLOC` is strictly stronger than Lemma 27.2.  It requires constants

```math
r_H<\infty,\qquad s_H<\infty,
```

a finite type alphabet \(\Theta_H\), and a cofinal selector such that the
rowwise Möbius generator can be replaced by a finite same-law local generator
family satisfying

```math
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(\operatorname{supp}\gamma)\le r_H,
\qquad
\ell_{RPF}(\operatorname{supp}\gamma)\le s_H,
\qquad
\theta(\gamma)\in\Theta_H,
```

with exact reconstruction of \(H_{N,j}-H_{N,j}(o)\) after all already-paid
local, central-entry, RP/Cov, readout, perimeter, cusp, and decoration ledgers
have been removed.

Equivalently, in terms of the literal Möbius atoms, a sufficient same-law
source is

```math
\Phi_A^{N,j}\equiv0
\quad\text{whenever}\quad
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)>r_H
\ \text{or}\
\ell_{RPF}(A)>s_H,
```

together with a finite canonical type table for the remaining nonzero atoms.
This is the exact bounded-support version of `P23-RPF-LITLOC` from Definition
15.4.

### Theorem 27.4: Current Verdict For `P23-RPF-HLOC`

The current corpus proves rowwise exact HLOC in the sense of Lemma 27.2, but
it does not prove cofinal bounded HLOC in the sense of Definition 27.3.

More sharply, the already closed source package cannot imply
`P23-RPF-HLOC` by itself.

Proof.

Lemma 27.2 proves the positive rowwise statement.  The stronger cofinal
statement would imply a uniform bound on the diameter and connected-hull size
of every nonzero literal Möbius coefficient on the selected adaptive branch,
up to a finite local type alphabet.

That bound is not supplied by the existing papers.  Definition 15.4
introduced `P23-RPF-LITLOC` and `P23-RPF-LITDECAY` as source gates, not as
proved consequences.  Section 21's finite-table exports print structural row
maps and over-refined carriers while explicitly leaving source values,
zero/carry tags, and inverse/value slots as source-table data.  Paper 16
supplies clean finite-row KP envelopes and counting constants, but Section 22
proved that those do not identify the actual adaptive Möbius atoms with a
bounded local generator table.

Finally, Section 13 proves independence of the closed non-RPF source package:
it permits both product residual completions and common-mode residual
completions.  A common-mode residual factor of the finite scalar form

```math
\exp\{\epsilon F(r_{x_1},\ldots,r_{x_m})\}
```

with \(m\) arbitrarily large changes only the RPF residual Hamiltonian while
preserving the already closed surface, RP/Cov, and readout bookkeeping.  Its
Boolean-lattice Möbius transform can have a nonzero coefficient on the full
set \(\{x_1,\ldots,x_m\}\).  Since \(m\) is arbitrary, no uniform bounded
HLOC radius or finite local type alphabet follows from the closed package
alone.

This does not falsify `P23-RPF-HLOC` for the actual adaptive law.  It proves
that HLOC is a real new same-law source theorem. `square`

### Definition 27.5: HVAL As A Finite Algebra After HLOC

Assume `P23-RPF-HLOC(r_H,{\mathfrak G}_H)`.  Let
\({\mathcal P}_{H}\) be the finite set of canonical local patterns consisting
of:

1. a rooted connected candidate \(A\) with
   \(\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)\le r_H\);
2. the finite list of generator types \(\theta(\gamma)\) whose supports
   contain \(A\);
3. the incidence data of those supports inside the radius-\(r_H\) canonical
   neighborhood.

For each pattern \(\pi\in{\mathcal P}_{H}\), define the same-law value
functional

```math
V_\pi
:=
\sum_{\gamma:A\subseteq\operatorname{supp}\gamma}
\Delta_A h_\gamma.
```

The HVAL table is

```math
{\mathcal T}_{HVAL}
:=
\{(\pi,\mathbf 1[V_\pi\not\equiv0]):\pi\in{\mathcal P}_{H}\}.
```

It is finite once the generator functions \(h_\theta\) are printed.

### Lemma 27.6: HLOC Reduces HVAL To Finite Same-Law Algebra

Under `P23-RPF-HLOC`, `P23-RPF-HVAL` is exactly the finite table
\({\mathcal T}_{HVAL}\).  There is no further infinite or continuum source in
HVAL.

Proof.

By HLOC, only finitely many generator types and support incidences can meet a
rooted candidate inside radius \(r_H\).  Lemma 26.5 shows that
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) is the finite sum of the corresponding finite differences
\(\Delta_A h_\gamma\).  Therefore deciding nonzero is exactly the finite
zero/cancellation table in Definition 27.5.  All entries are scalar functions
of the same pushed-forward row law. `square`

### Definition 27.7: Value-Extended Canonical Automaton Constants

When HLOC and HVAL hold, extend the structural automaton of Definition 25.4 by
the value tag of \({\mathcal T}_{HVAL}\).  Let \(M_{can}^{H}\) be its
transition matrix and set

```math
d_H
:=
\max_s\#\{t:M_{can}^{H}(s,t)=1\},
\qquad
C_H:=|{\mathsf S}_{root}^{H}|,
\qquad
h_H:=\log d_H.
```

Then the canonical residual label count obeys

```math
L_{can}^{N,j}(n)
\le
C_H e^{h_H n}.
```

The canonical KP entropy rate is therefore

```math
h_{KP}^{H}
=
\log(e\Delta_B)+h_H,
\qquad
C_{KP}^{H}=C_H.
```

### Lemma 27.8: The Automaton Step Is Conditional But Closed

`P23-RPF-HLOC + P23-RPF-HVAL` implies
`P23-RPF-CAN-LABEL-ENT(h_H,C_H)` and supplies the transition table required
by Section 25.

Proof.

Definition 25.7 gives the row-sum entropy bound for any value-extended
selector automaton.  Lemma 27.6 supplies the value tags.  Substituting
\(M_{can}^{H}\) into Definition 25.7 gives the displayed \(d_H,C_H,h_H\).
`square`

### Definition 27.9: Canonical Active Row Data After HLOC

Under the value-extended canonical table, define the active same-law row
constants by the smallest certified values satisfying, cofinally,

```math
\#\{A\ni x:\ell_{RPF}(A)=n,\ A\in{\mathcal L}_{can}^{N,j}\}
\le
C_H e^{h_H n},
```

and

```math
\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
\le
A_{res}^{H}e^{-\mu_{res}^{H}
(\ell_{RPF}(A)+\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A))}
```

for every active canonical survivor \(A\) not absorbed into the same-law local
ledger.  The starting range after legitimate local absorption is
\(R_H\).  This package is

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}ACTIVE\text{-}ROWDATA}_{can}^{H}
:=
(A_{res}^{H},\mu_{res}^{H},C_H,h_H,R_H).
```

If HLOC gives exact finite range, the exponential envelope may be replaced by
the direct finite activity norm

```math
\eta_H(a)
:=
\sup_x
\sum_{A\ni x,\ A\in{\mathcal L}_{can}^{N,j}}
2\,\operatorname{osc}(\Phi_A^{N,j})
e^{a\,\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)}
(\ell_{RPF}(A)-1),
```

again evaluated on the same pushed-forward scalar law.

### Theorem 27.10: Canonical KP Margin Test After HLOC

Assume `P23-RPF-HLOC + P23-RPF-HVAL` and the active row data of Definition
27.9.

The direct canonical KP route passes if

```math
\Delta_H
:=
\mu_{res}^{H}
-
\bigl(\log(e\Delta_B)+h_H\bigr)
>
\Delta_{crit}\left(2A_{res}^{H}C_H\right),
```

where

```math
\Delta_{crit}(B)
=
\log\left(
{2+B+\sqrt{B^2+4B}\over2}
\right).
```

The range-absorbed route passes if \(\Delta_H>0\) and

```math
2A_{res}^{H}C_H
{e^{-\Delta_H R_H}
\left(R_H-(R_H-1)e^{-\Delta_H}\right)
\over
(1-e^{-\Delta_H})^2}
<1.
```

Equivalently, in the exact finite-range form, the direct Dobrushin route
passes if \(\eta_H(a)<1\) for some \(a>0\).  Any of these pass conditions
implies `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

Proof.

The first inequality is Theorem 24.4 with \(h_{can}=h_H\) and \(C_{can}=C_H\),
equivalently Theorem 16.2 with
\(h_{RPF}=\log(e\Delta_B)+h_H\).  The range-absorbed inequality is Theorem
16.5 with the same replacement.  The finite-range activity norm is the
literal Dobrushin row bound of Lemma 15.6 restricted to the exact canonical
survivor table.  Once any of these bounds is \(<1\), Theorem 14.7 gives
`P23-RPF-TRANS0`. `square`

### Theorem 27.11: Five-Step Frontier Verdict

The requested five-step campaign has the following status.

1. **HLOC.**  Rowwise exact HLOC is proved by Möbius inversion, but cofinal
   bounded HLOC is not proved by the current corpus.  It is the first live
   source theorem.
2. **HVAL.**  HVAL is finite same-law algebra once HLOC is printed; it is not
   an independent analytic obstruction.
3. **Value automaton.**  The value-extended canonical automaton and entropy
   constants \((C_H,h_H)\) are finite once HLOC+HVAL are printed.
4. **Active row data.**  The needed row data reduce to the explicit constants
   in Definition 27.9.  They are not supplied by the current structural
   carrier alone.
5. **KP margin.**  The pass/fail inequality is exactly Theorem 27.10.  It
   cannot be tested numerically until HLOC/HVAL and active row data are
   sourced on the same adaptive law.

Therefore the new frontier is not four unrelated obstructions.  It is a
single primary source fork:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HLOC}
}
```

followed by finite algebra and the scalar row test.  If HLOC cannot be
proved, the honest alternative is to abandon bounded-local compression and
return to the more general same-law route of Sections 14--16:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LITDECAY}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOBRUSHIN\text{-}ACT}.
```

What is ruled out is treating the rowwise Möbius table as a cofinal local
automaton without proving a bounded generator alphabet or paying its entropy.

## 28. HLOC Decision Theorem: Exact Locality, Separator Law, Or Pivot

Section 27 showed that HLOC is the primary source fork.  This section closes
that fork as far as the present corpus can close it.  The point is simple but
important: exact cofinal HLOC is not a soft consequence of microscopic
locality or of finite rowwise Möbius inversion.  It is exactly a finite-range
vanishing theorem for the anchored Möbius coefficients of the **pushed-forward
residual law**.

### Definition 28.1: Finite-Range Möbius Support Gate

`P23-RPF-MOB-FR(r_H,s_H)` is the assertion that, cofinally on the exact `CE`
adaptive branch,

```math
\Phi_A^{N,j}\equiv0
```

whenever

```math
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)>r_H
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_{RPF}(A)>s_H.
```

The equality is equality as a scalar function on the same pushed-forward
row support used in Definition 15.1.  No off-record gauge process, continuum
Yang-Mills measure, or hidden Markov kernel may be used to certify it.

### Lemma 28.2: HLOC Is Equivalent To Finite-Range Möbius Support

On the exact `CE` strict branch, `P23-RPF-HLOC` is equivalent to
`P23-RPF-MOB-FR(r_H,s_H)` for some finite \(r_H,s_H\), together with the
finite canonical type table for the bounded local supports.

Proof.

Assume HLOC.  Then

```math
H_{N,j}(\omega)-H_{N,j}(o)
=
\sum_{\gamma}h_{\theta(\gamma)}
(\omega_{\operatorname{supp}\gamma})
```

with \(\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(\operatorname{supp}\gamma)\le r_H\) and
\(\ell_{RPF}(\operatorname{supp}\gamma)\le s_H\).  Apply the anchored
Boolean finite difference \(\Delta_A\).  If \(A\) is not contained in
\(\operatorname{supp}\gamma\), the alternating sum cancels in one coordinate
outside the support, so \(\Delta_A h_{\theta(\gamma)}=0\).  Hence the
Möbius coefficient \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) can be nonzero only when \(A\) is
contained in one local support.  This gives `P23-RPF-MOB-FR(r_H,s_H)`.

Conversely, assume `P23-RPF-MOB-FR(r_H,s_H)`.  Lemma 15.3 reconstructs
\(H_{N,j}-H_{N,j}(o)\) as the finite sum of all nonzero
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\).  The finite-range support gate deletes every support
outside \(r_H,s_H\), so the remaining \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) themselves are the
local generators.  For fixed \(r_H,s_H\), the Paper-21/Paper-23
over-refined local vertex alphabet has finitely many anchored canonical
patterns, giving the finite type table. `square`

### Definition 28.3: Separator HLOC Source

`P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC(r_{sep})` is the following same-law separator theorem.
There is a finite bounded separator enlargement

```math
\Omega_{N,j}\longrightarrow \Omega_{N,j}^{sep}
```

obtained by adjoining only scalar records of the same whole-process
`SEL2` law, such that:

1. the exact `CE` residual density is unchanged after pushing
   \(\Omega_{N,j}^{sep}\) back to \(\Omega_{N,j}\);
2. on \(\Omega_{N,j}^{sep}\), the residual log-density has a finite clique
   decomposition

   ```math
   H_{N,j}^{sep}-H_{N,j}^{sep}(o)
   =
   \sum_{\gamma\in{\mathfrak G}_{sep}^{N,j}}
   h_{\theta(\gamma)}(\omega_{\operatorname{supp}\gamma});
   ```

3. all supports have diameter at most \(r_{sep}\) in the separator graph;
4. no already-paid local, central-entry, RP/Cov, readout, perimeter, cusp,
   or decoration debit is reintroduced inside the separator factors.

This is a scalar-record theorem, not a microscopic Markov-process claim.  The
separator records must be printed as actual pushed-forward finite records.

### Lemma 28.4: Separator HLOC Implies HLOC On The Enlarged Battery

`P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC(r_{sep})` implies `P23-RPF-HLOC` for the enlarged finite
separator battery.  Consequently HVAL, the value-extended automaton, and the
KP tests of Section 27 apply on that enlarged battery with the corresponding
separator constants.

Proof.

The separator source already gives the finite local generator decomposition
required by Definition 26.4.  Since every separator variable is a declared
scalar record of the same pushed-forward law, the move is an operational
finite-battery enlargement.  Lemmas 26.5 and 27.6 then give HVAL, Lemma 27.8
gives the automaton entropy constants, and Theorem 27.10 gives the scalar KP
test. `square`

### Lemma 28.5: Marginal Pushforward Can Destroy Exact Locality

Exact locality of a larger scalar law does not imply exact HLOC after
projecting to a smaller residual battery.

Proof.

In finite probability, integrating out a separator variable produces an
effective log-density

```math
\log\sum_s
\exp\left(
h_L(\omega_L,s)+h_R(s,\omega_R)
\right),
```

which is generally not a sum of a left-local term and a right-local term.
Its anchored Boolean finite difference across \(L\cup R\) can be nonzero.
This is the ordinary finite marginalization effect, stated entirely inside a
finite pushed-forward scalar law.  Therefore microscopic or enlarged-battery
locality cannot be spent as HLOC on the projected RPF battery unless the
separator variables remain declared records or a separate cancellation theorem
is proved. `square`

### Theorem 28.6: Present-Corpus HLOC No-Go

The current corpus does not prove `P23-RPF-HLOC`; more strongly, the closed
source package of Sections 1--12 and the rowwise constructions of Sections
13--27 cannot imply it.

Proof.

By Lemma 28.2, HLOC would imply `P23-RPF-MOB-FR(r_H,s_H)` for finite
\(r_H,s_H\).  Section 15 introduced exact bounded support as `P23-RPF-LITLOC`
and exponential support decay as `P23-RPF-LITDECAY`; neither is proved by the
current papers.  Section 21's finite-table exports keep source values and
zero/carry decisions as explicit source data.  Section 22 proves that Paper
16's clean residual envelopes and counting constants do not identify the
actual adaptive Möbius coefficients.

The non-derivability is not merely missing bookkeeping.  Section 13 already
proves that the closed non-RPF source package is compatible with different
RPF residual completions.  For any \(m\), choose distinct residual block
records \(R_{x_1},\ldots,R_{x_m}\) and perturb only the RPF residual density
by a finite scalar factor

```math
\exp\{\epsilon\,R_{x_1}\cdots R_{x_m}\}.
```

The previously closed non-RPF gates see the same records as before.  But the
anchored Möbius coefficient on
\(A=\{x_1,\ldots,x_m\}\) is

```math
\epsilon
\prod_{i=1}^{m}(R_{x_i}-R_{x_i}(o)),
```

which is not identically zero for a nondegenerate residual row.  Since \(m\)
is arbitrary, no finite \(s_H\), and hence no finite HLOC source, follows
from the closed package.

This does not assert that the physical adaptive `SEL2` law lacks HLOC.  It
settles the logical status of the current corpus: HLOC is a new same-law
source theorem, not a consequence of what has already been proved. `square`

### Theorem 28.7: HLOC Issue Closed For Paper 23

The HLOC route has the following final status.

1. **Exact rowwise HLOC:** closed positively by Lemma 27.2, but rowwise only.
2. **Cofinal bounded HLOC from current sources:** closed negatively by
   Theorem 28.6.
3. **Positive exact HLOC route:** possible only by adding a new same-law
   separator/local-law source such as `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC`, after which Section
   27's HVAL/automaton/KP chain applies.
4. **No-smuggling rule:** locality may not be imported from microscopic
   gauge coordinates after projection; Lemma 28.5 shows why separator records
   must remain declared or be replaced by a proved cancellation theorem.
5. **Next viable route without new HLOC source:** abandon exact local
   compression and use the more general same-law estimates already prepared
   in Sections 14--16:

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LITDECAY}
   \quad\text{or}\quad
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOBRUSHIN\text{-}ACT}.
   ```

Thus HLOC is fully decided for the present paper: it is not an available
unconditional closure theorem.  It is either a newly declared separator
source, or the branch must proceed through decay/Dobrushin rather than exact
bounded local support.

## 29. Direct Finite-Range Vanishing: Final Decision

The remaining question is whether one can bypass the HLOC language and prove
finite-range vanishing of the literal anchored Möbius coefficients directly.
This section settles that direct route for the present corpus.

### Definition 29.1: Direct Finite-Range Vanishing

`P23-RPF-FR-VAN(r_0,s_0)` is the assertion that, cofinally on the exact
adaptive `SEL2` pushed-forward scalar law,

```math
\Phi_A^{N,j}\equiv0
```

whenever

```math
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)>r_0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_{RPF}(A)>s_0.
```

The equality is an equality of scalar records on the essential row support of
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  The statement uses the literal atoms of Definition
15.2 and no auxiliary gauge process, continuum Yang-Mills measure, area law,
or hidden Markov kernel.

### Lemma 29.2: Direct Vanishing Is Not A Separate Route

On the strict exact-entry branch,

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}FR\text{-}VAN}(r_0,s_0)
```

is the same support statement as `P23-RPF-MOB-FR(r_0,s_0)` and therefore is
equivalent to the support part of `P23-RPF-HLOC`.

Proof.

Definition 15.4 calls this exact bounded-collar literal localization
`P23-RPF-LITLOC`.  Definition 28.1 calls the same assertion
`P23-RPF-MOB-FR`.  Lemma 28.2 proves that bounded support of the literal
anchored Möbius atoms is exactly the support content needed for HLOC, with
the finite canonical type table supplied by the bounded Paper-21/Paper-23
local carrier.  Hence a direct proof of finite-range vanishing would not
bypass HLOC; it would be HLOC in literal Möbius form. `square`

### Lemma 29.3: Arbitrary-Order Same-Record Tail Completion

For every proposed finite pair \((r_0,s_0)\), the source package closed before
HLOC admits a finite scalar-record residual completion for which
`P23-RPF-FR-VAN(r_0,s_0)` fails while all already closed non-RPF ledgers are
unchanged.

Proof.

Choose \(m>s_0\) and choose residual vertices
\(x_1,\ldots,x_m\) with pairwise \(RPF\)-distance larger than \(r_0\), inside
a sufficiently large finite adaptive row.  Keep every already closed
coordinate, central factor, RP/Cov transport record, surface record, readout
record, counterterm convention, and whole-process scalar record exactly as in
the closed strict branch.  Adjoin only a residual scalar factor in the RPF
ledger.  On binary residual coordinates \(z_i\in\{0,1\}\), with base point
\(o_i=0\), replace the residual density by

```math
{\mathcal R}_{N,j}^{(\epsilon)}
=
Z_{\epsilon}^{-1}
{\mathcal R}_{N,j}^{(0)}
\exp\{\epsilon z_1z_2\cdots z_m\}
```

where \(Z_\epsilon\) is the harmless row normalization, or equivalently add
\(\epsilon z_1\cdots z_m\) to the residual Hamiltonian
\(H_{N,j}\).  For \(|\epsilon|\) small this is still a finite positive
same-record residual density on the declared RPF battery.

Every non-RPF source gate is unchanged, because the perturbation is a scalar
factor depending only on the residual RPF coordinates after the declared
central and local ledgers have been divided out.  It does not alter the
already printed surface activity, RP/Cov transport, central extraction,
readout, perimeter, cusp, or decoration records.

Now compute the anchored Boolean finite difference on
\(A=\{x_1,\ldots,x_m\}\).  All proper subproducts cancel and the contribution
of the added term is

```math
\Delta_A(\epsilon z_1\cdots z_m)
=
\epsilon z_1\cdots z_m,
```

which is not identically zero.  Thus
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0\), while
\(\ell_{RPF}(A)\ge m>s_0\) and
\(\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)>r_0\).  Since \((r_0,s_0)\) was arbitrary,
finite-range vanishing is not forced by the previously closed source
package. `square`

### Theorem 29.4: Direct Finite-Range Vanishing No-Go For The Present Corpus

The present corpus cannot prove direct finite-range vanishing of the actual
RPF anchored Möbius coefficients from the already closed source package.
Equivalently, there is no valid derivation in Papers 1--23 of

```math
\exists r_0,s_0<\infty\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}FR\text{-}VAN}(r_0,s_0)
```

unless a new same-law source theorem is added, such as a separator/local-law
identity `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC` or a printed literal row identity for the actual
adaptive `SEL2` residual Hamiltonian.

Proof.

If such a derivation existed, Lemma 29.2 would give the finite-range support
part of HLOC.  But Lemma 29.3 constructs, for every proposed finite range and
size, a finite same-record residual completion satisfying the already closed
non-RPF source package and violating that finite-range conclusion.  Therefore
the closed source package does not logically entail direct finite-range
vanishing.

This is the strongest no-go that is justified here.  It does **not** assert
that the physical adaptive `SEL2` law lacks an exact finite-range identity.
It says that such an identity is not contained in the current papers.  To use
it, one must print it as a new same-law theorem on
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\); otherwise the exact finite-range route is closed
negatively and the branch must use `P23-RPF-LITDECAY` or
`P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT`. `square`

### Corollary 29.5: Final Finite-Range Verdict

Finite-range vanishing is settled for Paper 23:

1. **Rowwise finite range:** true but useless cofinally, because each finite
   row has a finite full support by Lemma 27.2.
2. **Uniform cofinal finite range from the current corpus:** false as a
   derivable conclusion, by Theorem 29.4.
3. **Uniform cofinal finite range for the actual adaptive law:** still
   possible only as a new same-law source theorem, not as bookkeeping.
4. **Operational next step:** either prove the new separator/local-law source
   `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC`, or abandon exact finite range and prove a quantitative
   same-law tail estimate:

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LITDECAY}
   \quad\text{or}\quad
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOBRUSHIN\text{-}ACT}.
   ```

Thus the direct finite-range route is closed for good as a current-corpus
route.  The branch no longer spends time trying to extract exact bounded
support from rowwise Möbius inversion; that extraction is impossible without
a new physical scalar-record identity.

## 30. The Separator HLOC Source Identity

Section 29 closed direct finite-range vanishing as a current-corpus theorem.
The only exact-locality route left is therefore a genuine separator identity:
enlarge the finite scalar battery by declared same-law separator records and
prove that the residual Hamiltonian is local on that enlarged battery.  This
section makes that source theorem precise and rules out the cheap
"separator" constructions that would trivialize the problem.

### Definition 30.1: Admissible Separator Records

An admissible separator battery

```math
{\mathcal S}_{N,j}
=
\{S_\sigma^{N,j}\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma_{sep}^{N,j}}
```

for the adaptive exact-entry RPF row consists of scalar records of the same
whole-process `SEL2` law satisfying the following cofinal bounds.

1. **Same-law record condition.**  Each \(S_\sigma^{N,j}\) is a declared
   finite scalar record of the same pushed-forward law
   \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  It is not an independently sampled latent
   variable and not a gauge-coordinate proof variable outside the recorded
   battery.
2. **Bounded footprint.**  Each separator has a printed footprint
   \({\rm Foot}(\sigma)\subset V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) with

   ```math
   \operatorname{diam}_{RPF}{\rm Foot}(\sigma)\le r_F,
   \qquad
   |{\rm Hull}({\rm Foot}(\sigma))|\le s_F.
   ```

3. **No shortcut geometry.**  In the separator graph, two separator or RPF
   vertices may be adjacent only if their printed footprints intersect or lie
   within a fixed \(R_{adj}\)-collar in the original RPF graph.  A single
   row-global record may not make distant residual vertices adjacent.
4. **Finite type and value census.**  The separator type set and value-local
   table have row-independent finite bounds.  If a separator has a row-growing
   value set, the logarithm of that value count is an explicit entropy
   surcharge \(h_{sep}\), not a hidden zero-cost locality proof.
5. **No double charge.**  Separator factors may not reintroduce local,
   central-entry, RP/Cov, readout, perimeter, cusp, decoration, or already
   carried exact-entry debit rows.

Write

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SEP\text{-}ADM}
(r_F,s_F,R_{adj},h_{sep})
```

for the assertion that such an admissible separator battery has been printed.

### Definition 30.2: Admissible Separator HLOC

`P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC^adm(r_sep,r_F,s_F,R_adj,h_sep)` is the conjunction of
`P23-RPF-SEP-ADM(r_F,s_F,R_adj,h_sep)` with the following exact same-law
factorization.  There is an enlarged finite record law
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{sep}\) on

```math
\Omega_{N,j}^{sep}
=
\Omega_{N,j}\times{\mathcal S}_{N,j}
```

such that:

1. the projection to \(\Omega_{N,j}\) is exactly
   \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\);
2. after the same exact `CE` quotient, the enlarged residual Hamiltonian has
   a bounded local clique decomposition

   ```math
   H_{N,j}^{sep}-H_{N,j}^{sep}(o)
   =
   \sum_{\gamma\in{\mathfrak G}_{sep}^{N,j}}
   h_{\theta(\gamma)}
   \left(\omega_{\operatorname{supp}\gamma}\right);
   ```

3. every \(\operatorname{supp}\gamma\) has diameter at most \(r_{sep}\) in
   the admissible separator graph;
4. the type set \(\theta(\gamma)\in\Theta_{sep}\) is finite after paying
   \(h_{sep}\).

The original `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC` of Definition 28.3 is licensed only when this
admissibility package is present or when an equivalent finite entropy/footprint
ledger is printed.

### Lemma 30.3: Global-Code Separators Are Not Admissible

The construction that adjoins one record

```math
S_{glob}:=\omega_{V_{RPF}^{N,j}}
```

and writes the whole residual Hamiltonian as a one-site function of
\(S_{glob}\) does not prove `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC^adm`.

Proof.

The record \(S_{glob}\) is a same-law deterministic record, but its footprint
is the whole RPF row.  Hence

```math
\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}{\rm Foot}(S_{glob})
```

and the value count of the record grow with the row.  It violates the bounded
footprint clause and, if retained anyway, its state entropy must be paid as a
row-growing \(h_{sep}\).  With that entropy charged, the separator no longer
supplies the finite canonical selector/KP margin required by Section 27.

The same objection applies to prefix-product, parity, or cumulative separator
chains whose intermediate variables encode arbitrarily large regions while
appearing locally connected in an artificial graph.  Their printed footprints
grow with the row, or else they are not records of the same pushed-forward
law. `square`

### Lemma 30.4: Admissible SEP-HLOC Closes The Exact-Locality Branch

If `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC^adm(r_sep,r_F,s_F,R_adj,h_sep)` holds with finite
row-independent constants and the separator active row data obey the Section
27 scalar KP margin, then the exact-locality branch proves
`P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

Proof.

Definition 30.2 gives a bounded local generator decomposition on the enlarged
declared scalar battery.  Because the separator records are actual same-law
records, this is an operational battery enlargement rather than an auxiliary
process.  Lemma 28.4 gives HLOC on the enlarged battery.  Lemmas 26.5 and
27.6 reduce HVAL and the value table to finite same-law algebra; Lemma 27.8
prints the value-extended automaton; and Theorem 27.10 gives the scalar KP
pass/fail test with the separator entropy \(h_{sep}\) included.  If that test
passes, Theorem 27.10 yields `P23-RPF-TRANS0`. `square`

### Lemma 30.5: Paper-16 Local Coordinates Do Not Yet Supply SEP-HLOC

Paper 16 supplies a finite heat-kernel cutoff law and local proof-coordinate
action, but it does not by itself prove
`P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC^adm` for the adaptive high-\(\alpha\) `SEL2` exact-entry
RPF row.

Proof.

Paper 16 Definition 9A.1 defines the cutoff Yang-Mills law and its
pushed-forward finite record law.  Its Section 0A explicitly treats gauge
fields and plaquette variables as proof coordinates for facts about declared
records, not as unrecorded ontology.  Paper 16 Definition 9M.1D supplies
finite label-counting data on a frozen heat-kernel row when the common row
has already been fixed.

Paper 23 Sections 21 and 22 compare that frozen clean heat-kernel row with
the actual adaptive `SEL2` residual row.  They prove that Paper 16 gives
clean KP envelopes and finite counting constants, but not a literal
coefficient identity or a bounded triangular transform from the actual
adaptive Möbius atoms to Paper-16 clean coefficients.  Section 23 then closes
coefficient identity only by passing to the canonical finite coefficient
gauge; Sections 24--29 show that the remaining problem is the value-local
selector/locality source, not the existence of proof-coordinate local action.

Therefore Paper 16's local proof coordinates are not yet an admissible
separator HLOC source for Paper 23.  To become one, they must be reprinted as
declared finite scalar separator records on the same adaptive
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\) law, with bounded footprints, finite value census,
exact central quotient agreement, and no-double-charge ledger separation.
Those data are not currently printed. `square`

### Theorem 30.6: Current Verdict For `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC`

The present corpus does not prove `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC^adm`.  More precisely:

1. unrestricted separator HLOC is vacuous, because a global-code separator
   can localize any finite row while hiding row-scale entropy;
2. admissible separator HLOC is a genuine same-law source theorem with the
   finite footprint, value-census, no-shortcut, and no-double-charge clauses
   of Definition 30.1;
3. Papers 16, 20, 21, 22, and Sections 1--29 of this paper do not print the
   admissible separator battery or the exact enlarged local residual
   Hamiltonian identity for the adaptive `SEL2` law;
4. therefore the exact-locality route remains open only as the new source
   theorem

   ```math
   \boxed{
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SEP\text{-}HLOC}^{adm}
   +
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SEP\text{-}ROWDATA}
   +
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SEP\text{-}KP\text{-}MARGIN}.
   }
   ```

Without that package, the branch must use the non-HLOC route
`P23-RPF-LITDECAY` or `P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT`.

Proof.

Lemma 30.3 rules out the only purely formal construction that would make
separator HLOC automatic.  Lemma 30.5 checks the strongest available local
source, Paper 16, and shows that it has not been transferred as an admissible
same-law separator identity for the actual adaptive row.  The arbitrary-order
tail completion of Lemma 29.3 remains compatible with the already closed
non-RPF ledgers unless one adds exactly the new separator identity described
in Definition 30.2.  Hence the current corpus cannot derive admissible
separator HLOC. `square`

### Work Order After The Separator Audit

To make `P23-RPF-SEP-HLOC^adm` real rather than formal, the next paper would
have to print the following finite same-law data.

1. The separator record list \(S_\sigma^{N,j}\), with scalar readout map and
   pushed-forward law.
2. The footprint table \({\rm Foot}(\sigma)\), adjacency rule, and finite
   type/value census, including any entropy surcharge \(h_{sep}\).
3. The exact projection identity
   \((\pi_{\Omega})_*\Gamma_{N,j}^{sep}=\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).
4. The exact `CE`-quotiented local clique decomposition of
   \(H_{N,j}^{sep}\).
5. The no-double-charge audit against local, central-entry, RP/Cov, readout,
   perimeter, cusp, decoration, and carried exact-entry ledgers.
6. The separator active row constants and the Section-27 KP margin with
   \(h_{sep}\) included.

Until those six finite tables are printed, `SEP-HLOC` is not a proof.  It is
the name of the next possible exact-locality source theorem.

## 31. Terminal Investigation Of Both Remaining Options

After Section 30 there are only two honest ways to keep adaptive Branch A
alive:

```math
\text{(A) admissible separator HLOC}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\text{(B) literal decay/Dobrushin.}
```

This section investigates both to terminal current-corpus status.  The
standard is deliberately strict: an option is not counted as progress unless
it is a theorem on the same adaptive pushed-forward `SEL2` scalar law.

### Definition 31.1: The Two Terminal Route Packages

The exact-locality package is

```math
{\mathfrak S}_{sep}
:=
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SEP\text{-}HLOC}^{adm}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SEP\text{-}ROWDATA}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SEP\text{-}KP\text{-}MARGIN}.
```

The non-HLOC package is either of the following same-law alternatives:

```math
{\mathfrak S}_{dec}
:=
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}FINCOUNT}(C_{RPF},h_{RPF})
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LITDECAY}(A_0,\mu_0)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SCALAR\text{-}KP},
```

where `SCALAR-KP` is the Section-16 pass inequality, or directly

```math
{\mathfrak S}_{Dob}
:=
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOBRUSHIN\text{-}ACT}(q,a)
\quad(q<1).
```

All three packages are evaluated after the exact `CE` branch and the
no-double-charge local/RP-Cov/readout ledgers have been applied.

### Lemma 31.2: Separator Candidate Census

The admissible separator route has exactly the following candidate families.

1. **Global-code separators.**  Closed negatively by Lemma 30.3.  They are
   formal localizers with row-growing footprint or entropy.
2. **Gauge-coordinate separators.**  Link, plaquette, chart, and gauge-fixed
   variables may be proof coordinates, but they are not scalar records of the
   pushed-forward law unless explicitly read out.  They fail Definition 30.1.
3. **Finite scalar boundary separators.**  Boundary loop traces, block
   characters, spin-network scalars, or collar records are admissible
   candidates only if their footprints, value/type census, projection identity,
   and local clique decomposition are printed.
4. **Full nonabelian gluing data.**  A spin-network/intertwiner boundary
   battery could in principle encode exact nonabelian gluing as scalar data,
   but exactness requires a printed finite representation battery or a
   separately carried representation-tail debit.  Without that row, it is not
   `SEP-HLOC^adm`.

Proof.

The list follows from Definition 30.1.  Any separator must either be a
declared scalar record of the same pushed-forward law or it is inadmissible.
If it is declared but its footprint or value set grows with the row, its
entropy is not finite and the Section-27 KP margin cannot use it.  If it is a
finite scalar boundary/collar battery, it is a genuine candidate, but
Definition 30.2 still requires the exact projection and local clique
factorization.  Paper 16 supplies proof-coordinate locality and finite
counting on frozen rows, not this adaptive separator identity. `square`

### Theorem 31.3: Exact-Locality Option Fully Investigated

The exact-locality route is fully investigated for the current corpus.  Its
status is:

```math
{\mathfrak S}_{sep}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0},
```

but the current corpus does not prove \({\mathfrak S}_{sep}\).  There is no
remaining weaker separator shortcut.

Proof.

Lemma 30.4 proves the implication from admissible separator HLOC plus row data
and KP margin to `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.  Lemma 30.3 rules out global-code
localization; Lemma 30.5 rules out treating Paper-16 proof-coordinate locality
as an already printed adaptive separator source; and Lemma 31.2 exhausts the
remaining candidate classes.  Thus any positive proof must print exactly the
six finite tables listed after Theorem 30.6.  Until then, exact-locality is a
named new source theorem, not a live derivation from existing papers. `square`

### Lemma 31.4: Literal Decay And Dobrushin Are The Same Non-HLOC Problem

`P23-RPF-LITDECAY + P23-RPF-FINCOUNT` with the Section-16 scalar pass implies
`P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT(q,a)` for some \(q<1\).  Conversely,
`P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT(q,a)` is a direct finite influence-table route to
`P23-RPF-TRANS0` without first proving literal exponential decay of every
individual atom.

Proof.

The first implication is Theorem 15.8 plus the optimized scalar criteria of
Theorems 16.2 and 16.5.  The second implication is Theorems 14.5 and 14.3.
Both routes use the same declared literal atoms of Definition 15.2 and the
same finite pushed-forward law \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  Literal decay is a
convenient sufficient envelope for the influence row; Dobrushin is the
sharper direct row test. `square`

### Lemma 31.5: Current Corpus Does Not Imply Literal Decay Or Dobrushin

The source package closed before the RPF gate does not imply
`P23-RPF-LITDECAY` and does not imply `P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT(q,a)` for any
row-independent \(q<1,a>0\).

Proof.

For `LITDECAY`, use the arbitrary-order residual-tail completion of Lemma
29.3.  Fix any proposed constants \(A_0,\mu_0>0\).  Add to the residual
Hamiltonian a same-record term

```math
\epsilon z_1z_2\cdots z_m
```

on a connected or distant hull of size \(m\), with \(\epsilon>0\) fixed.
For sufficiently large \(m\),

```math
\epsilon>
A_0\exp\{-\mu_0(\ell_{RPF}(A)+\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A))\},
```

so literal decay fails while the already closed non-RPF ledgers remain
unchanged.

For Dobrushin, choose the same completion with \(m\) sites in a long chain or
with pairwise large distances.  A change in one coordinate changes the
conditional Hamiltonian of another coordinate through the \(m\)-body term by
an amount of order \(\epsilon\) on a positive row-support event.  The weighted
row sum contains at least

```math
c\,\epsilon\sum_{y\in A\setminus\{x\}}e^{a d_{RPF}(x,y)}
```

for some finite-state comparison constant \(c>0\).  By taking \(m\) or the
separations large, this exceeds any proposed \(q<1\).  Hence no uniform
Dobrushin certificate is a consequence of the closed non-RPF source package.

This is not a claim about the physical adaptive law.  It is a logical
non-derivability statement: the current hypotheses do not determine the RPF
tail or influence table. `square`

### Theorem 31.6: Non-HLOC Option Fully Investigated

The literal decay/Dobrushin route is fully investigated for the current
corpus.  Its status is:

```math
{\mathfrak S}_{dec}
\Longrightarrow
{\mathfrak S}_{Dob}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0},
```

and the scalar pass/fail inequalities are exactly those in Section 16.  The
current corpus does not prove \({\mathfrak S}_{dec}\) or \({\mathfrak S}_{Dob}\).

Proof.

The positive implication chain is Lemma 31.4.  The scalar thresholds are
Theorems 16.2 and 16.5:

```math
\mu_0-h_{RPF}
>
\Delta_{crit}(2A_0C_{RPF})
```

for direct passage, or the range-absorbed inequality \(Q_R(0)<1\) after a
same-law local absorption theorem.  Lemma 31.5 proves that the current
source package cannot supply those estimates automatically.  Thus the route
is neither vague nor closed: it is parked exactly at the finite oscillation
or influence row table on the actual adaptive law. `square`

### Theorem 31.7: Final Two-Option Verdict

Both remaining options have now been fully investigated.

1. **Exact separator route.**  It closes Branch A if and only if the
   admissible separator source package \({\mathfrak S}_{sep}\) is printed and
   passes its KP margin.  The current corpus does not prove it.
2. **Non-HLOC route.**  It closes Branch A if and only if the literal
   oscillation/influence table proves \({\mathfrak S}_{dec}\) or
   \({\mathfrak S}_{Dob}\) with strict margin.  The current corpus does not
   prove it.
3. **No third exact-locality shortcut.**  Direct finite range, unrestricted
   separator localization, and rowwise Möbius inversion are all closed
   negatively as current-corpus routes.
4. **Best next mathematical move.**  The sharper route is the non-HLOC
   Dobrushin table, because it asks for the actual influence norm directly and
   does not require an exact finite-range separator identity.

Consequently adaptive Branch A is not blocked by an undefined mystery.  It is
parked at a concrete finite same-law computation:

```math
\boxed{
\text{print and bound the actual RPF influence row }
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
\text{ on }\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}.
}
```

If the resulting limsup is \(<1\), Branch A closes.  If it is certified
\(\ge1\) with a lower floor large enough to reach the Paper-22 loss threshold,
Branch A fails.  If the row cannot be printed, the obstruction is a missing
same-law influence table, not a hidden locality principle.

## 32. Eight-Gate Execution Of The Separator Route

This section executes the separator route itself.  The question is not whether
one can name a separator source.  The question is whether the eight finite
same-law gates can be passed by the records and theorems currently available
in Papers 16, 20, 21, 22, and the preceding sections of this paper.

The answer is negative.  The separator route is falsified as an **available
Paper-23 route**.  It is not falsified as a possible future physical theorem:
a later paper may still print new scalar separator records and a new exact
local clique identity.

### Definition 32.1: The Eight Separator Gates

For a proposed separator package \({\mathcal S}_{N,j}\), define the eight
gates:

1. `SEP-G1-RECORD`: print the scalar separator record list
   \(S_\sigma^{N,j}\) on the same \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\) law.
2. `SEP-G2-FOOT`: print bounded footprints, adjacency, and no-shortcut
   geometry.
3. `SEP-G3-ENT`: print finite type/value counts or carry the entropy
   surcharge \(h_{sep}\).
4. `SEP-G4-PROJ`: prove exact projection
   \((\pi_\Omega)_*\Gamma_{N,j}^{sep}=\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).
5. `SEP-G5-CLIQUE`: prove the exact `CE`-quotiented local clique
   decomposition of \(H_{N,j}^{sep}\).
6. `SEP-G6-NDC`: pass the no-double-charge audit against local, central,
   RP/Cov, readout, perimeter, cusp, decoration, and carried exact-entry
   ledgers.
7. `SEP-G7-ROWDATA`: print the separator active row constants.
8. `SEP-G8-KP`: prove the separator scalar KP margin with \(h_{sep}\)
   included.

The route proves `P23-RPF-TRANS0` only if all eight gates pass cofinally.

### Table 32.2: Candidate Separator Families And Gate Status

| candidate family | G1 | G2 | G3 | G4 | G5 | G6 | G7 | G8 | verdict |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| global-code record \(S_{glob}=\omega_{V_{RPF}}\) | same-law deterministic | fails bounded footprint | row-scale entropy | yes | formal | not useful | no | no | rejected by Lemma 30.3 |
| gauge/link/plaquette proof coordinates | not scalar pushed-forward records unless read out | local as proof coordinates | finite at cutoff | no same-law record projection | local in gauge coordinates | mixes proof ledgers | no | no | inadmissible under Barandes ontology |
| finite boundary/collar scalar records already in the battery | yes where already declared | yes | finite | yes if deterministic readout | not proved | delicate: often already local/readout/collar ledgers | no | no | admissible candidates, but no clique identity |
| truncated spin-network/intertwiner boundary battery | yes if declared | yes | finite with cutoff | yes if declared | only truncated | representation-tail debit needed | no | no | not exact unless tail is carried |
| full exact nonabelian gluing battery | not finite without tail/limit data | local boundary footprint | unbounded representation entropy | not printed | possible only as new theorem | new no-double-charge audit | no | no | future source, not Paper 23 |

### Lemma 32.3: Gates 1--3 Do Not Produce Exact Locality

The current corpus can produce only structural candidates for Gates 1--3:
finite boundary/collar scalar records and truncated representation batteries.
These do not imply `SEP-G5-CLIQUE`.

Proof.

Paper 21 and this paper already contain finite collar, boundary-port,
character, and canonical label data.  Those records can satisfy the formal
record, footprint, and finite-counting requirements after truncation.  But
Sections 28--31 show that exact HLOC is not a consequence of finite rowwise
Möbius inversion, bounded labels, or local proof coordinates.  A finite list
of separator records becomes a proof only when the enlarged residual
Hamiltonian is actually written as a bounded local clique sum.  No such
identity is printed by the current corpus. `square`

### Lemma 32.4: Exact Projection Is Cheap Only For Deterministic Readouts

Gate `SEP-G4-PROJ` is automatic for deterministic scalar records already
declared as functions of the whole-process record law, but it is not automatic
for hidden separator variables or gauge proof coordinates.

Proof.

If \(S_\sigma^{N,j}=f_\sigma(\omega)\) is a declared scalar readout, the
enlarged law is the pushforward of \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\) by
\(\omega\mapsto(\omega,f(\omega))\), and projection is exact.  If instead
the separator is an auxiliary hidden variable chosen to make a factor graph
local, then projection exactness is a coupling assertion not supplied by the
original pushed-forward law.  If it is a gauge/link coordinate outside the
finite scalar battery, it is a proof coordinate rather than a record of
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  Both cases fail the same-law record condition until
a new scalar readout map and projection theorem are printed. `square`

### Lemma 32.5: Gate 5 Fails For All Current Separator Candidates

No current separator candidate proves the exact `CE`-quotiented local clique
decomposition required by `SEP-G5-CLIQUE`.

Proof.

Global-code separators are inadmissible by Lemma 30.3.  Gauge/link/plaquette
coordinates are not scalar separator records of the pushed-forward law unless
read out, and once read out the current corpus gives no exact clique identity
for the adaptive residual Hamiltonian.

Finite boundary/collar scalar records are genuine records, but Section 31
shows that they are only candidates.  They do not rule out the same-record
arbitrary-order residual-tail completion of Lemma 29.3: one may add an
\(m\)-body RPF residual factor supported far beyond any fixed collar while
leaving the already closed non-RPF ledgers unchanged.  Unless the separator
identity explicitly forbids that factor by printing the local clique
decomposition, the candidate records do not imply it.

Truncated spin-network/intertwiner batteries face the same obstruction plus a
representation-tail issue.  Truncation gives a finite scalar battery, but
exact nonabelian gluing then requires a declared tail bound or a carried
representation-tail debit.  If the tail is carried, the exact separator route
has not closed `RPF-TRANS0`; if it is ignored, the proof is not same-law
exact. `square`

### Lemma 32.6: Gates 6--8 Cannot Be Reached

Since Gate 5 fails for the current candidates, the no-double-charge audit,
separator row data, and separator KP margin cannot be executed as closure
gates.

Proof.

Gate 6 audits the factors in the local clique decomposition.  Without Gate 5
there are no separator factors to audit.  Gate 7 computes active constants
from the accepted factors, and Gate 8 tests the scalar KP inequality with
the accepted entropy.  Thus Gates 6--8 are downstream of the exact clique
identity.  They cannot be used to manufacture that identity. `square`

### Theorem 32.7: Separator Route Falsified As An Available Paper-23 Route

The separator route does not prove `P23-RPF-TRANS0` in the current paper.
More sharply, every separator package available from the current corpus fails
at least one of the eight gates, and all nontrivial admissible candidates fail
at Gate 5.

Proof.

Table 32.2 lists all separator families available from the present record
corpus.  Lemma 32.3 shows that the finite structural candidates pass at most
the first three gates.  Lemma 32.4 separates exact projection for declared
readouts from inadmissible hidden variables.  Lemma 32.5 proves that no
candidate supplies the exact enlarged local clique decomposition.  Lemma
32.6 then blocks the downstream no-double-charge, rowdata, and KP gates.

Therefore the eight-gate separator route is not merely unfinished; it is
falsified as a route available inside Paper 23.  A future proof must add a
new source theorem printing the exact separator records and clique identity.
Until that happens, the separator route is closed negatively and the only
productive Branch-A continuation is the non-HLOC influence-row route:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOBRUSHIN\text{-}ACT}(q,a),
\qquad q<1.
```

This theorem is a current-corpus falsification, not a physical impossibility
claim about all future scalar separator identities. `square`

### Corollary 32.8: Updated Work Order

Do not continue spending Paper-23 effort on `SEP-HLOC` unless a genuinely new
separator record/clique identity is supplied.  The next proof-producing task
is:

```math
\boxed{
\text{compute or bound }
\mathfrak D_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
\text{ for the actual adaptive row.}
}
```

The separator route is now a parked future-source branch.  The active branch
for this paper is Dobrushin/influence, not exact separator locality.

## 33. Direct Non-HLOC Influence Row Decision

Section 32 closed the separator route negatively for this paper.  We now run
the non-HLOC route without trying to smuggle exact locality back in.  The only
question is the actual same-law influence row of the pushed-forward adaptive
`SEL2` residual law.

This section tries the positive closure first.  It succeeds conditionally and
sharply: a strict cofinal Dobrushin row \(<1\) proves `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.  It
does not succeed unconditionally from the present corpus: the already closed
finite ledgers do not determine that row.

### Definition 33.1: Sharp Same-Law Influence Row

For a finite adaptive row \((N,j)\), let \(V_{RPF}^{N,j}\), \(d_{RPF}\), and
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\) be the residual vertex set, graph metric, and actual
pushed-forward scalar law of Definitions 14.4 and 15.1.

For \(x\ne y\), define the sharp finite conditional influence

```math
J_{xy}^{N,j}
:=
\sup_{\eta,\eta'}
\left\|
\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}
\bigl(\omega_x\in\cdot\mid \omega_{V\setminus\{x\}}=\eta\bigr)
-
\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}
\bigl(\omega_x\in\cdot\mid \omega_{V\setminus\{x\}}=\eta'\bigr)
\right\|_{TV},
```

where the supremum is over outside configurations \(\eta,\eta'\) that differ
only at \(y\), and conditionals are taken on the essential support.  Set
\(J_{xx}^{N,j}=0\).  For \(a>0\), define

```math
\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{N,j}(a)
:=
\sup_x\sum_y e^{a d_{RPF}(x,y)}J_{xy}^{N,j},
```

and the cofinal row value

```math
\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{cof}(a)
:=
\limsup_{N\to\infty}\limsup_{j\to\infty}
\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{N,j}(a).
```

The direct non-HLOC source theorem is

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOB\text{-}ROW}(q,a):
\qquad
\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{cof}(a)\le q<1.
```

This is stronger in form but weaker in assumptions than the separator route:
it asks only for the actual finite scalar conditional laws, not for a hidden
local factor graph.

### Lemma 33.2: Oscillation Row Dominates The Sharp Row

For every finite \((N,j)\) and every \(a>0\),

```math
\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{N,j}(a)
\le
\mathfrak D_{osc}^{N,j}(a),
```
