where \(\mathfrak D_{osc}^{N,j}(a)\) is the row norm defined from the literal
Möbius atom oscillations in Definition 15.5.

Proof.

This is Lemma 15.6 with the notation sharpened.  Changing \(y\) in the outside
configuration can alter the conditional Hamiltonian for \(x\) only through
literal atoms whose support contains both \(x\) and \(y\).  The total
variation change is bounded by twice the sum of their oscillations.  Summing
with the weight \(e^{a d_{RPF}(x,y)}\) gives the displayed domination.
`square`

### Theorem 33.3: Positive Non-HLOC Closure

If `P23-RPF-DOB-ROW(q,a)` holds for some \(a>0\) and \(q<1\), then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}TRANS0}
```

holds.  Consequently adaptive Branch A closes on the exact-CE branch.

Proof.

`P23-RPF-DOB-ROW(q,a)` is exactly `P23-RPF-DOBRUSHIN-ACT(q,a)` with the sharp
conditional influence matrix in place of the oscillation upper bound.  The
finite Dobrushin-Shlosman implication of Theorem 14.5 gives
`P23-RPF-ACTUAL-KP(q',a')` for some weakened \(q'<1,a'>0\).  Theorem 14.3
then gives `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.  The Branch-A closure implication is Theorem
12.4 plus the already closed surface and RP/Cov gates. `square`

### Corollary 33.4: Literal Decay Is Only A Sufficient Envelope

The sufficient route

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}FINCOUNT}
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}LITDECAY}
+
\text{Section-16 scalar KP pass}
```

proves `P23-RPF-DOB-ROW(q,a)`, but the converse need not hold.

Proof.

The forward implication is Theorem 15.8 plus Theorem 16.2 or Theorem 16.5.
The converse would require every individual literal Möbius atom to have an
exponential support envelope.  A conditional-influence row can be small by
cancellation, conditional averaging, or sparse activity even when a uniform
atomwise exponential envelope is not printed.  Therefore the sharp route is
\(\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{cof}(a)<1\); literal decay is the convenient
certificate, not the definition of success. `square`

### Theorem 33.5: Exact Failure Meaning For The Non-HLOC Route

If

```math
\inf_{a>0}\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{cof}(a)\ge1,
```

then the direct Dobrushin non-HLOC route fails.  This does not by itself
falsify adaptive Branch A.

Adaptive Branch A is falsified by this line only if the same computation also
prints a same-record lower floor forcing

```math
\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*.
```

Proof.

The strict Dobrushin route requires at least one weighted row norm below one.
If the infimum over \(a>0\) is at least one, no such strict Dobrushin
certificate exists.  But Dobrushin is a sufficient criterion for the exact
RPF factorization, not a necessary theorem for every possible cluster
argument.  To falsify the whole adaptive Branch-A sufficient pass, Paper 22
requires the predebit/loss lower floor reaching \(M_*\).  Hence row
\(\ge1\) closes the non-HLOC Dobrushin route negatively, while branch failure
requires the additional lower-floor statement. `square`

### Lemma 33.6: The Current Corpus Does Not Determine The Sharp Row

The finite source package closed before Section 33 does not determine whether
there exists \(a>0\) with
\(\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{cof}(a)<1\).

Proof.

Sections 29 and 31 already print the decisive countermodel mechanism: an
arbitrary-order same-record RPF residual-tail completion may be added while
preserving the non-RPF ledgers already closed.  If the added residual tail is
zero, or uniformly tiny with rapidly decaying supports, the sharp row can be
made \(<1\) in the finite Dobrushin sense.  If instead one adds a fixed
\(\epsilon z_1\cdots z_m\) residual interaction on growing hulls, the
conditional law at one site changes by order \(\epsilon\) when another site
is varied on a positive-support event; by taking \(m\), graph separation, or
the number of affected sites large, the weighted row can exceed any proposed
strict \(q<1\).

Both completions agree with the source package that has been closed outside
the RPF gate.  Therefore that package cannot decide the sharp influence row.
Only the actual adaptive pushed-forward scalar law, or a new theorem about
it, can decide `P23-RPF-DOB-ROW(q,a)`. `square`

### Theorem 33.7: Non-HLOC Route Settled For Paper 23

The non-HLOC route is now settled for the current paper in the following
sharp sense:

1. A positive close is exactly the same-law finite theorem
   `P23-RPF-DOB-ROW(q,a)` for some \(q<1,a>0\), or the stronger sufficient
   envelope `FINCOUNT + LITDECAY + Section-16 scalar KP pass`.
2. The present corpus does not prove that theorem.
3. The present corpus also does not prove a same-record lower floor large
   enough to falsify adaptive Branch A.
4. Therefore Paper 23 cannot honestly claim a positive unconditional
   confinement close, but it has removed the structural ambiguity: the only
   live mathematical datum is the cofinal sharp influence row of the actual
   adaptive law.

Proof.

Item 1 is Theorem 33.3 and Corollary 33.4.  Item 2 is Lemma 33.6.  Item 3
follows because the lower-floor statement
\(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\) is not printed by any of Sections
13--33; Section 31 only proves logical non-derivability of Dobrushin from the
closed source package.  Item 4 is the combination of these facts with the
separator-route falsification of Theorem 32.7. `square`

### Corollary 33.8: Final Paper-23 Work Order

Stop searching for structural shortcuts inside Paper 23.  The next
proof-producing object is the actual table

```math
\left\{J_{xy}^{N,j}\right\}_{x,y\in V_{RPF}^{N,j}}
```

or a theorem that bounds its weighted row norm cofinally.  The decision is:

1. if \(\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{cof}(a)<1\) for some \(a>0\), Branch A closes;
2. if \(\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{cof}(a)\ge1\) for all \(a>0\), the direct
   Dobrushin route fails;
3. if a same-law lower floor also gives
   \(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\), adaptive Branch A fails;
4. otherwise the problem is parked at a single primitive finite same-law
   influence-row source theorem, not at separator locality, coefficient
   identity, canonical labels, HLOC, or finite-row decidability.

## 34. Positive Closure Campaign: Screened Conditional Influence

This section executes the six-step positive plan for the non-HLOC route.  The
point is to use the sharp conditional kernel of the actual pushed-forward
scalar law rather than the more wasteful literal-atom oscillation envelope.

The best mathematical mechanism is standard finite-volume Dobrushin theory:
if changing one outside coordinate changes a one-site conditional by a
weighted row sum \(<1\), then the finite scalar record law has the residual
cluster expansion needed by `RPF`.  The Barandes-aligned restriction is that
all kernels below are conditionals of the actual scalar law
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  No gauge subprocess, hidden separator, continuum
Yang-Mills measure, or Wilson-loop assumption is imported.

### Definition 34.1: One-Site Conditional Hamiltonian

For each finite adaptive row \((N,j)\), choose the same reference
\(\lambda_{N,j}\) as in Definition 15.1 and write the actual residual density
as

```math
d\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}=p_{N,j}(\omega)d\lambda_{N,j}(\omega).
```

For a vertex \(x\in V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) and an outside configuration
\(\eta\in\Omega_{V\setminus\{x\}}\) in the essential support, define the
one-site conditional density

```math
k_x^{N,j}(u\mid\eta)
:=
{p_{N,j}(u,\eta)\over
\int p_{N,j}(u',\eta)d\lambda_x(u')}.
```

The corresponding conditional Hamiltonian is

```math
H_x^{N,j}(u\mid\eta):=-\log k_x^{N,j}(u\mid\eta).
```

All quantities are finite scalar readouts of the pushed-forward law.

### Definition 34.2: Conditional Oscillation Matrix

For \(x\ne y\), define

```math
\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
:=
\sup_{\eta,\eta'}
\operatorname{osc}_{u\in\Omega_x}
\left[
H_x^{N,j}(u\mid\eta)-H_x^{N,j}(u\mid\eta')
\right],
```

where \(\eta,\eta'\) differ only at \(y\).  Set
\(\Delta_{xx}^{N,j}=0\).  The weighted conditional-oscillation row is

```math
\mathfrak O_{RPF}^{N,j}(a)
:=
\sup_x\sum_y e^{a d_{RPF}(x,y)}\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}.
```

### Lemma 34.3: Conditional Oscillation Controls Sharp Influence

For every finite row,

```math
J_{xy}^{N,j}
\le
\tanh\left({\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}\over4}\right)
\le
{\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}\over4}.
```

Consequently,

```math
\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{N,j}(a)
\le
{1\over4}\mathfrak O_{RPF}^{N,j}(a).
```

Proof.

For fixed outside configurations \(\eta,\eta'\), let \(P,Q\) be the two
one-site conditional laws of \(\omega_x\).  The log likelihood ratio
\(\log(dP/dQ)\) differs from
\(-H_x(\cdot\mid\eta)+H_x(\cdot\mid\eta')\) by an additive constant.  Hence
its oscillation is at most \(\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}\).  The elementary finite
likelihood-ratio bound

```math
\|P-Q\|_{TV}
\le
\tanh\left({\operatorname{osc}\log(dP/dQ)\over4}\right)
```

follows by maximizing total variation over a likelihood ratio whose range has
fixed logarithmic diameter.  Applying this bound and then using
\(\tanh t\le t\) gives the two displayed inequalities. `square`

### Definition 34.4: Screened Conditional Influence Source

`P23-RPF-SCREEN-COND(A,mu,h_sh,C_sh)` is the same-law source theorem asserting
that, cofinally in \((N,j)\), the conditional oscillation shells satisfy

```math
\sup_x
\sum_{y:d_{RPF}(x,y)=r}
\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
\le
A C_{sh}e^{-(\mu-h_{sh})r}
```

for every \(r\ge1\), with constants independent of \(N,j\).  Equivalently,
one may take \(C_{sh}e^{h_{sh}r}\) as a shell-count envelope and
\(\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}\le A e^{-\mu d_{RPF}(x,y)}\) pointwise.

This is weaker than literal atom decay: it controls only the actual
conditional response after all cancellations and conditional averaging have
already occurred.

### Theorem 34.5: Screened Conditional Influence Closes Branch A

Assume `P23-RPF-SCREEN-COND(A,mu,h_sh,C_sh)`.  If there exists
\(a>0\) such that

```math
\delta:=\mu-h_{sh}-a>0
```

and

```math
Q_{scr}(a)
:=
{A C_{sh}\over4}
{e^{-\delta}\over1-e^{-\delta}}
<1,
```

then `P23-RPF-DOB-ROW(Q_scr(a),a)` holds.  Hence
`P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds and adaptive Branch A closes on the exact-CE branch.

Proof.

By Lemma 34.3 and the shell source,

```math
\mathfrak D_{sharp}^{N,j}(a)
\le
{1\over4}
\sup_x\sum_{r\ge1}
e^{ar}
\sum_{y:d(x,y)=r}\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
\le
{A C_{sh}\over4}
\sum_{r\ge1}e^{-(\mu-h_{sh}-a)r}.
```

The geometric series is the displayed \(Q_{scr}(a)\).  A strict bound below
one is `P23-RPF-DOB-ROW(Q_scr(a),a)`, and Theorem 33.3 closes
`P23-RPF-TRANS0`. `square`

### Corollary 34.6: Optimized Screened Row Test

The screened conditional route passes for some \(a>0\) if and only if
\(\mu>h_{sh}\) and

```math
{A C_{sh}\over4}
{e^{-(\mu-h_{sh})}\over1-e^{-(\mu-h_{sh})}}
<1.
```

Equivalently,

```math
\mu-h_{sh}>
\log\left(1+{A C_{sh}\over4}\right).
```

Proof.

The row constant \(Q_{scr}(a)\) is minimized as \(a\downarrow0\).  Put
\(x=e^{-(\mu-h_{sh})}\).  The inequality is
\((AC_{sh}/4)x/(1-x)<1\), hence \(x<1/(1+AC_{sh}/4)\). `square`

### Definition 34.7: Heat-Kernel/Peter-Weyl Conditional Screening Source

`P23-RPF-HKPW-COND(t_*,B_*,h_sh,C_sh)` is the following same-law source on
the actual adaptive pushed-forward scalar law.  For each conditional response
channel from \(y\) to \(x\), expand the conditional likelihood-ratio
increment in the finite Peter-Weyl battery of the declared scalar records.
The nontrivial modes at distance \(r=d_{RPF}(x,y)\) obey the bound

```math
\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
\le
B_*
\exp\{-t_* C_{gap} r/2\},
```

where \(C_{gap}\) is the smallest nonzero Casimir gap in the retained
nontrivial channel, and the shell count is bounded by
\(C_{sh}e^{h_{sh}r}\).

This source is not a continuum heat-kernel assumption.  It is a finite
same-law statement that the actual adaptive scalar conditionals have a
Peter-Weyl smoothing time \(t_*\) in the residual propagation channel.

### Theorem 34.8: Heat-Kernel/Peter-Weyl Screening Implies Positive Closure

If `P23-RPF-HKPW-COND(t_*,B_*,h_sh,C_sh)` holds and

```math
{t_*C_{gap}\over2}
-h_{sh}
>
\log\left(1+{B_*C_{sh}\over4}\right),
```

then adaptive Branch A closes on the exact-CE branch.

Proof.

Apply Theorem 34.5 with

```math
A=B_*,
\qquad
\mu={t_*C_{gap}\over2}.
```

The displayed inequality is exactly the optimized screened row test of
Corollary 34.6. `square`

### Lemma 34.9: What Paper 16 Supplies And What It Does Not

Paper 16 supplies the right analytic pattern but not the needed adaptive
same-law screening source.

More precisely:

1. Paper 16 Definition 9N.1Q.4 and Theorem 9N.1Q.5 print a finite-template
   heat-kernel analytic certificate from row data
   \[
   \Delta_B,L_{ent},L_{KP},\lambda_D,R_{blk},C_v^{row},
   r_{res}^{clean},m.
   \]
2. Paper 16 Theorem 9N.2A exports residual decay constants
   \((A_{res},\mu_{res},C_{KP},h_{KP},m,r_{res},\Delta_{res},K_{res})\)
   on the same heat-kernel whole-process record-law tower.
3. These are sufficient for a heat-kernel analytic row once that row is the
   actual law being evaluated.
4. They do not, by themselves, prove
   `P23-RPF-HKPW-COND` or `P23-RPF-SCREEN-COND` for the adaptive high-\(\alpha\)
   `SEL2` pushed-forward law of this paper.

Proof.

Items 1 and 2 are direct imports from Paper 16.  Item 3 is the same-law
compatibility clause of Paper 16's analytic branch.  Item 4 is the exact
warning already used throughout Papers 21--23: a finite heat-kernel proof
coordinate or clean analytic row may certify constants for its declared
record-law tower, but the adaptive `SEL2` row has to print its own
pushed-forward scalar conditional estimates.  Paper 23 Sections 21--24
already show that coefficient identity and finite label control can be
repaired only after same-law canonicalization; the same requirement applies
to conditional screening. `square`

### Theorem 34.10: Six-Step Positive Campaign Verdict

The six steps are now reduced as follows.

1. **Freeze finite conditionals:** done by Definition 34.1.
2. **Replace atoms by conditional response:** done by Definitions 34.2 and
   Lemma 34.3.
3. **Use heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl diagonal damping:** reduced to the finite
   same-law source `P23-RPF-HKPW-COND`.
4. **Prove a screened influence kernel:** abstracted as
   `P23-RPF-SCREEN-COND`, with the sharp threshold in Theorem 34.5.
5. **Exploit direct Dobrushin rather than atomwise decay:** done by
   Corollary 33.4 and the one-denominator screened row test of Corollary 34.6.
6. **Run the row-sum threshold:** done by Theorem 34.5 and Corollary 34.6.

Thus the positive closure theorem has a concrete sufficient source:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SCREEN\text{-}COND}(A,\mu,h_{sh},C_{sh})
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mu-h_{sh}>
\log\left(1+{AC_{sh}\over4}\right).
}
```

Equivalently, a heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl proof may close it through Theorem
34.8.  The present corpus does not yet prove either same-law source for the
actual adaptive row.  Therefore the positive closure is rigorously reduced to
a screened conditional influence theorem, not to any of the previously closed
structural gates. `square`

### Corollary 34.11: Next Proof-Producing Target

The next target is not another separator, not HLOC, and not a literal
Möbius-atom table.  It is:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HKPW\text{-}COND}
\quad\text{or directly}\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SCREEN\text{-}COND}.
```

Concretely, one must print on the adaptive `SEL2` law either:

1. a finite Peter-Weyl conditional likelihood-ratio table whose nontrivial
   modes pay a Casimir damping rate beating shell entropy; or
2. a direct conditional oscillation shell estimate
   \[
   \sup_x\sum_{d(x,y)=r}\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
   \le AC_{sh}e^{-(\mu-h_{sh})r}
   \]
   with the optimized margin of Corollary 34.6.

If either is proved, Section 34 gives the positive close.  If a matching lower
bound shows the optimized margin cannot hold and also forces
\(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\), adaptive Branch A fails.  Otherwise
the branch remains parked at this screened conditional influence source.

## 35. Heat-Kernel/Peter-Weyl Step Campaign

Section 34 reduced the positive close to same-law screened conditional
influence.  This section tries to prove that source from a finite
Peter-Weyl/Casimir step estimate.  The result is sharp but conditional in the
right place: a genuine same-law one-step contraction proves the desired
screening, but the current corpus does not yet provide that contraction for
the actual adaptive `SEL2` residual law.

### Definition 35.1: Conditional Response Increment

For \(x\ne y\), and outside configurations \(\eta,\eta'\) differing only at
\(y\), define the centered conditional response function

```math
L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}(u;\eta,\eta')
:=
\left[
H_x^{N,j}(u\mid\eta)-H_x^{N,j}(u\mid\eta')
\right]
-
\int
\left[
H_x^{N,j}(v\mid\eta)-H_x^{N,j}(v\mid\eta')
\right]
d\lambda_x(v).
```

Then

```math
\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
=
\sup_{\eta,\eta'}\operatorname{osc}_u
L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}(u;\eta,\eta').
```

The subtraction removes the trivial Peter-Weyl mode.  Thus every contribution
to \(\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}\) lies in a nontrivial representation channel.

### Lemma 35.2: Trivial Mode Cancellation Is Same-Law

The constant Peter-Weyl mode of the conditional likelihood-ratio increment
does not contribute to \(\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}\).

Proof.

\(\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}\) is an oscillation in \(u\).  Adding or subtracting a
constant in \(u\) leaves the oscillation unchanged.  The centering in
Definition 35.1 is therefore an algebraic rewriting of the same conditional
scalar record, not a change of law or a projection onto hidden gauge
coordinates. `square`

### Definition 35.3: Same-Law Peter-Weyl Step Contraction

`P23-RPF-HKPW-STEP(theta,B_step,h_path,C_path)` is the following assertion on
the actual adaptive pushed-forward scalar law.

There is a finite directed proof graph \({\mathcal G}_{step}^{N,j}\) on the
declared residual scalar records such that every conditional response
\(L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}\) admits a same-law finite path expansion over paths
\(\gamma:x\leadsto y\).  If \(|\gamma|=r\), then:

1. each edge transfer maps nontrivial Peter-Weyl modes to nontrivial modes;
2. the nontrivial-mode oscillation is contracted by at most
   \(\theta<1\) per edge;
3. endpoint and norm-conversion costs are bounded by \(B_{step}\);
4. the number of admissible step paths of length \(r\) from any root is at
   most \(C_{path}e^{h_{path}r}\).

Equivalently, for all \(x,y\) with \(d_{RPF}(x,y)=r\),

```math
\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
\le
B_{step}
\sum_{\gamma:x\leadsto y}
\theta^{|\gamma|},
```

with the displayed path-counting bound uniformly/cofinally.

When the contraction comes from heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl damping, the intended
value is

```math
\theta
=
B_0\exp\{-t_*C_{gap}/2\}+\kappa_{res},
```

where \(B_0\) is the finite norm-conversion cost and \(\kappa_{res}\) is the
same-law non-heat-kernel residual perturbation.

### Theorem 35.4: Step Contraction Implies Screened Conditional Influence

Assume `P23-RPF-HKPW-STEP(theta,B_step,h_path,C_path)`.  If
\(\theta e^{h_{path}}<1\), then
`P23-RPF-SCREEN-COND(A,mu,h_sh,C_sh)` holds with

```math
A=B_{step},
\qquad
C_{sh}=C_{path},
\qquad
h_{sh}=0,
\qquad
\mu=-\log(\theta e^{h_{path}}).
```

More generally, any separate shell-count envelope \(C_{sh}e^{h_{sh}r}\) gives
\(\mu=-\log\theta\).

Proof.

For a shell \(d_{RPF}(x,y)=r\), every admissible path has length at least
\(r\).  Therefore

```math
\sum_{y:d(x,y)=r}\Delta_{xy}^{N,j}
\le
B_{step}C_{path}e^{h_{path}r}\theta^r
=
B_{step}C_{path}e^{-(-\log\theta-h_{path})r}.
```

This is the screened conditional shell estimate.  The second formulation is
just the same calculation with the shell entropy kept separate from the
pointwise decay. `square`

### Corollary 35.5: Step-Contraction Positive Close

Under `P23-RPF-HKPW-STEP(theta,B_step,h_path,C_path)`, adaptive Branch A
closes on the exact-CE branch if

```math
-\log\theta-h_{path}
>
\log\left(1+{B_{step}C_{path}\over4}\right).
```

In the heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl parametrization, it is enough that

```math
-\log\left(B_0e^{-t_*C_{gap}/2}+\kappa_{res}\right)-h_{path}
>
\log\left(1+{B_{step}C_{path}\over4}\right).
```

Proof.

Apply Theorem 35.4 and then Corollary 34.6. `square`

### Lemma 35.6: Paper-21/16 Tail Machinery Does Not Yet Prove The Step Source

The current corpus supplies finite Peter-Weyl batteries, character-tail
cutoff schedules, and heat-kernel analytic row estimates, but it does not
prove `P23-RPF-HKPW-STEP` for the actual adaptive `SEL2` residual law.

Proof.

Paper 16 Definition 9O.1--Theorem 9O.4 give finite Casimir batteries and
heat-kernel representation-tail estimates for a declared heat-kernel tower.
Paper 21 Definition 85.5 and Theorem 85.7 isolate the analogous active
heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl smoothing source and explicitly state that it is not
proved for the active bounded-collar quotient law.  Paper 23 Section 11
uses Weyl-Casimir cutoffs to control a character-tail budget, but that is a
tail estimate for declared finite readouts, not a conditional transfer
contraction for the exact-entry residual law.

The step source requires more: the centered conditional response
\(L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}\) must admit a same-law path expansion whose every
edge carries nontrivial Peter-Weyl modes through a contraction factor.  None
of the cited results prints that path expansion or the residual perturbation
bound \(\kappa_{res}\) for the actual adaptive conditional kernels. `square`

### Lemma 35.7: Why A Formal Heat-Kernel Factor Is Not Enough

The central heat-kernel factor removed by `CE` does not by itself imply
`P23-RPF-HKPW-STEP`.

Proof.

Definition 15.1 divides the actual density by the central one-plaquette
factor \(K_p^{CE,N,j}\) before defining the exact RPF residual density.  A
heat-kernel damping estimate for the divided local factor controls the local
central contribution already assigned to `CE`; it does not control the
remaining residual conditional response unless the residual density is
itself shown to inherit a positive smoothing time or a contracted transfer
representation.  Moving the `CE` damping into `RPF` would double-charge the
central-entry ledger and would not be a same-law proof of the residual
conditional row. `square`

### Theorem 35.8: Execution Verdict For The Peter-Weyl Route

The heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl route to screened conditional influence is reduced
to exactly one new source theorem:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HKPW\text{-}STEP}
(\theta,B_{step},h_{path},C_{path})
}
```

with the strict margin of Corollary 35.5.

If this theorem is supplied on the actual adaptive `SEL2` law, then
`P23-RPF-SCREEN-COND` holds and Section 34 closes Branch A.  The current
papers do not supply it, and they do not imply it from compactness,
finite Peter-Weyl truncation, the `CE` heat-kernel factor, or the Paper-16
clean analytic row.

Proof.

Definitions 35.1--35.3 print the same-law object and the exact step source.
Theorem 35.4 proves that the step source implies screened conditional
influence.  Corollary 35.5 gives the closure margin.  Lemmas 35.6 and 35.7
show that the current corpus does not prove the step source.  Therefore the
route is fully executed: positive closure is available precisely under
`HKPW-STEP`, but not unconditionally from the present papers. `square`

### Corollary 35.9: What Must Be Proved Next

To actually prove same-law screened conditional influence, one must now
prove the step source directly.  The most economical target is:

```math
\theta
=
B_0e^{-t_*C_{gap}/2}+\kappa_{res},
\qquad
-\log\theta-h_{path}
>
\log\left(1+{B_{step}C_{path}\over4}\right).
```

The proof must print, on \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\):

1. the finite path expansion of \(L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}\);
2. the nontrivial Peter-Weyl channel preservation at each step;
3. the positive effective smoothing time \(t_*\);
4. the residual perturbation bound \(\kappa_{res}\);
5. the path entropy constants \(h_{path},C_{path}\);
6. the final scalar margin above.

Without these six same-law data, the positive close cannot be claimed.

## 36. One-Edge Same-Law Transfer Test

Section 35 located the missing proof at a Peter-Weyl step contraction.  This
section pushes one level lower.  The question is no longer whether some
abstract heat-kernel smoothing should exist.  The question is whether the
actual adaptive residual law prints, on each residual adjacency edge, a
centered conditional transfer operator whose nontrivial Peter-Weyl norm is
uniformly below one.

The answer is exact and useful: every fixed finite row has a same-law finite
matrix test.  A cofinal strict contraction would prove the Section-35 source.
The present corpus, however, proves only rowwise finite decidability, not a
uniform spectral gap for the actual adaptive law.

### Definition 36.1: Exact One-Edge Conditional Transfer Operator

Fix a finite adaptive row \((N,j)\).  Let
\({\mathcal E}_{RPF}^{N,j}\) be the finite directed adjacency list of the
canonical residual vertex cover used in Sections 23--26.  For an oriented
edge \(e=(x,y)\in{\mathcal E}_{RPF}^{N,j}\), and for a configuration
\(\zeta\) of all row variables except \(x,y\), let

```math
\Gamma_{xy}^{N,j}(\cdot\mid\zeta)
```

be the two-site conditional law of \((\omega_x,\omega_y)\) under the actual
pushed-forward scalar law \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  Write
\(\Gamma_x^{N,j}(\cdot\mid\zeta)\) and
\(\Gamma_y^{N,j}(\cdot\mid\zeta)\) for its one-site marginals.

The centered one-edge transfer operator is

```math
T_{e,\zeta}^{N,j}:
L^2_0(\Gamma_y^{N,j}(\cdot\mid\zeta))
\longrightarrow
L^2_0(\Gamma_x^{N,j}(\cdot\mid\zeta))
```

defined by

```math
(T_{e,\zeta}^{N,j}f)(u)
:=
\int f(v)\,
d\Gamma_{y|x}^{N,j}(v\mid u,\zeta)
-
\int f(v)\,d\Gamma_y^{N,j}(v\mid\zeta).
```

Here \(L^2_0\) means zero mean with respect to the indicated one-site
conditional marginal.  The subtraction is the same centering as Section 35:
constant Peter-Weyl modes are not physical influence channels.

This operator is a scalar-record object.  It is not an auxiliary Markov
process and not a hidden gauge evolution; it is just conditional expectation
inside the actual finite pushed-forward law.

### Definition 36.2: Truncated Peter-Weyl Edge Matrix And Tail

Let \(\Pi_{\le L,x}^{PW}\) and \(\Pi_{\le L,y}^{PW}\) be the declared finite
Peter-Weyl projections on the \(x\)- and \(y\)-site scalar batteries, with the
trivial channel removed.  Define the rowwise finite edge norm

```math
\Theta_L^{N,j}
:=
\sup_{e=(x,y)\in{\mathcal E}_{RPF}^{N,j}}
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{\zeta}
\left\|
\Pi_{\le L,x}^{PW}
T_{e,\zeta}^{N,j}
\Pi_{\le L,y}^{PW}
\right\|_{0\to0}.
```

Define the corresponding truncation remainder

```math
\Kappa_L^{N,j}
:=
\sup_{e=(x,y)}
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{\zeta}
\left\|
T_{e,\zeta}^{N,j}
-
\Pi_{\le L,x}^{PW}
T_{e,\zeta}^{N,j}
\Pi_{\le L,y}^{PW}
\right\|_{0\to0}.
```

The sharp one-edge same-law constant at cutoff \(L\) is

```math
\theta_L^{N,j}:=\Theta_L^{N,j}+\Kappa_L^{N,j}.
```

### Lemma 36.3: The Fixed-Row Matrix Test Exists

For every fixed finite adaptive row \((N,j)\) and every finite Peter-Weyl
cutoff \(L\), \(\Theta_L^{N,j}\) is the norm of a finite matrix whose entries
are same-law scalar integrals over \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).

Proof.

The vertex cover, edge list, and Peter-Weyl battery are finite on a fixed
row.  Conditional laws are regular conditional probabilities of the same
finite compact scalar record law \(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  Choosing the
finite Peter-Weyl bases on the two endpoint batteries, the entry
\((\alpha,\beta)\) of the truncated operator is

```math
\int
\overline{\psi_{\alpha,x}(u)}
\psi_{\beta,y}(v)
d\Gamma_{xy}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
```

after subtracting the endpoint means.  This is a scalar conditional
expectation inside the same pushed-forward row law.  If the chosen
Peter-Weyl basis is not orthonormal for the conditional endpoint marginals,
the operator norm is computed with the corresponding finite Gram matrices.
Thus the test remains a finite same-law matrix calculation. `square`

### Definition 36.4: Cofinal Edge Spectral Source

`P23-RPF-EDGE-SPEC(L,theta,kappa)` is the assertion that there is a cofinal
adaptive selector and a finite Peter-Weyl cutoff schedule \(L=L(N,j)\) such
that

```math
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\Theta_{L(N,j)}^{N,j}
\le
\theta,
\qquad
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\Kappa_{L(N,j)}^{N,j}
\le
\kappa,
```

with

```math
\theta+\kappa<1.
```

When no tail is needed because the local scalar battery is already complete,
one may take \(\kappa=0\).

### Definition 36.5: Exact Edge-Path Expansion Source

`P23-RPF-EDGE-PATH(B_edge,h_path,C_path)` is the assertion that every
centered conditional response \(L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}\) from Definition
35.1 admits a same-law finite expansion over residual adjacency paths
\(\gamma:x\leadsto y\):

```math
L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}
=
\sum_{\gamma:x\leadsto y}
E_{\gamma}^{N,j},
```

where:

1. \(E_{\gamma}^{N,j}\) is obtained by composing the one-edge centered
   transfer operators of Definition 36.1 with endpoint insertions;
2. the endpoint and norm-conversion cost is bounded by \(B_{edge}\);
3. the number of admissible paths of length \(r\) from any root is at most
   \(C_{path}e^{h_{path}r}\);
4. the expansion is written after `CE` division and after all local,
   RP/Cov, readout, perimeter, cusp, and decoration ledgers have been
   removed, so no already-paid debit is reintroduced.

This is the path-expansion half of `P23-RPF-HKPW-STEP`.  It is stated
separately because a strict one-edge spectral gap is useless if the
conditional response is not actually generated by those edge transfers.

### Theorem 36.6: One-Edge Test Implies `HKPW-STEP`

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}EDGE\text{-}SPEC}(L,\theta,\kappa)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}EDGE\text{-}PATH}(B_{edge},h_{path},C_{path}).
```

Set

```math
\theta_{edge}:=\theta+\kappa.
```

Then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}HKPW\text{-}STEP}
(\theta_{edge},B_{edge},h_{path},C_{path})
```

holds.

Proof.

By `EDGE-SPEC`, every centered one-edge transfer has nontrivial-channel norm
at most \(\theta_{edge}\) cofinally, after the declared Peter-Weyl cutoff and
tail are combined.  By `EDGE-PATH`, each length-\(r\) contribution to
\(L_{x\leftarrow y}^{N,j}\) is a composition of \(r\) such centered transfers,
up to the endpoint cost \(B_{edge}\).  Therefore each path contribution is
bounded by \(B_{edge}\theta_{edge}^r\), and the path count is
\(C_{path}e^{h_{path}r}\).  These are exactly the four clauses of Definition
35.3. `square`

### Corollary 36.7: Exact One-Edge Closure Criterion

Under the assumptions of Theorem 36.6, adaptive Branch A closes on the
exact-CE branch if

```math
-\log(\theta+\kappa)-h_{path}
>
\log\left(1+{B_{edge}C_{path}\over4}\right).
```

Proof.

Theorem 36.6 gives `HKPW-STEP` with
\(\theta_{edge}=\theta+\kappa\).  Apply Corollary 35.5. `square`

### Lemma 36.8: What The Current Corpus Proves

The current corpus proves the fixed-row finite matrix test of Lemma 36.3.  It
does not prove `P23-RPF-EDGE-SPEC` or `P23-RPF-EDGE-PATH` cofinally for the
actual adaptive residual law.

Proof.

Paper 10 supplies finite Peter-Weyl batteries and exact finite-battery
semantics once the battery is declared.  Sections 15, 23, and 26 of the
present paper supply the actual residual density, canonical coefficient
gauge, and rowwise finite value tables on the same adaptive pushed-forward
law.  Therefore the fixed-row edge matrix is a legitimate same-law finite
object.

The missing statements are stronger.  `EDGE-SPEC` requires a uniform
cofinal centered spectral gap for the actual conditional operator.  Paper 21
Theorem 85.7 explicitly states that the active heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl
smoothing source is not proved for the active bounded-collar quotient law.
Paper 16 supplies heat-kernel analytic row estimates on its declared
heat-kernel tower, not a spectral gap for the adaptive `SEL2` residual
conditionals after exact `CE` division.  Section 35 also proved that finite
Peter-Weyl truncation and the divided central heat-kernel factor do not
produce the residual step contraction.

`EDGE-PATH` is also not automatic.  It requires that the centered conditional
response be generated by compositions of the declared residual adjacency
edge operators, rather than by a same-record high-order residual atom whose
support jumps over that edge graph.  Sections 28--33 already showed that
arbitrary-order residual-tail completions are compatible with the closed
non-RPF ledgers unless an additional same-law RPF source is supplied.
Therefore the current corpus reaches the finite matrix test but not the
cofinal contraction theorem. `square`

### Lemma 36.9: Why Strict Contraction Cannot Be Inferred From Compactness

A strict bound
\(\limsup\theta_L^{N,j}<1\) is not a consequence of compactness, finite
Peter-Weyl truncation, or finite row size.

Proof.

Finite-dimensional conditional expectation operators always have norm at
most one on centered \(L^2\).  Compactness of the row state space and
finiteness of the Peter-Weyl matrix therefore give existence of a norm, but
not a gap below one.

Moreover, the closed non-RPF source package does not rule out an RPF residual
completion in which an endpoint scalar record is almost deterministically
copied across one residual edge after conditioning on the outside variables.
Such a completion leaves the previously closed surface, RP/Cov, endpoint,
readout, and central-entry ledgers untouched because it changes only the live
RPF residual conditional law.  Its centered transfer norm can be made
arbitrarily close to one on a nontrivial finite Peter-Weyl channel.  Thus a
uniform gap below one is genuinely new same-law information about the actual
adaptive law. `square`

### Theorem 36.10: One-Edge Test Verdict

The one-edge program is fully reduced to the following primitive same-law
package:

```math
\boxed{
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}EDGE\text{-}SPEC}(L,\theta,\kappa)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}EDGE\text{-}PATH}(B_{edge},h_{path},C_{path})
}
```

with the scalar margin

```math
-\log(\theta+\kappa)-h_{path}
>
\log\left(1+{B_{edge}C_{path}\over4}\right).
```

For every fixed finite adaptive row, the matrices needed to test
`EDGE-SPEC` are printable from the same pushed-forward scalar law.  But the
present papers do not prove the cofinal spectral gap, do not prove the
residual edge-path expansion, and therefore do not prove same-law screened
conditional influence unconditionally.

Proof.

Lemma 36.3 proves fixed-row decidability.  Theorem 36.6 proves that
`EDGE-SPEC + EDGE-PATH` gives `HKPW-STEP`.  Corollary 36.7 gives the exact
Branch-A closure margin.  Lemmas 36.8 and 36.9 prove that the current corpus
does not supply the two primitive cofinal inputs. `square`

### Corollary 36.11: Next Concrete Computation

The next computation is no longer conceptual.  For a selected concrete
adaptive row or finite template one must print:

1. the residual adjacency edge list \({\mathcal E}_{RPF}^{N,j}\);
2. the two-site conditional densities
   \(\Gamma_{xy}^{N,j}(\cdot\mid\zeta)\);
3. the finite Peter-Weyl basis after removing the trivial channel;
4. the matrices
   \(\Pi_{\le L,x}^{PW}T_{e,\zeta}^{N,j}\Pi_{\le L,y}^{PW}\);
5. the supremal matrix norm \(\Theta_L^{N,j}\);
6. a tail bound \(\Kappa_L^{N,j}\), or a proof that the chosen battery is
   complete for the template;
7. the path-expansion constants \(B_{edge},h_{path},C_{path}\);
8. the final scalar margin of Corollary 36.7.

If this finite worksheet yields \(\theta+\kappa<1\) with the displayed
margin cofinally, Branch A closes.  If the rowwise norms approach one or the
path expansion fails, the Peter-Weyl screened-influence route is closed
negatively for adaptive Branch A.

## 37. Finite Template Portfolio For The Edge Matrix Test

Section 36 reduced the proof to a concrete finite worksheet.  This section
executes that worksheet as far as the current corpus permits.  The portfolio
rule is deliberately conservative: try the smallest live same-law template
first, then enlarge only when the smaller template fails to certify the
edge-path/spectral package.

The outcome is precise.  The actual finite matrices can be printed
symbolically on the same pushed-forward scalar law.  What is not printed in
the present corpus is the numerical or closed-form row value needed to bound
their Gram-norms below the Section-36 margin.

### Definition 37.1: The Template Portfolio

Use the following admissible finite-template ladder.

| label | template | purpose |
| --- | --- | --- |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{0}^{edge}\) | minimal rooted two-site live `CleanRPF` edge with its Markov blanket | cheapest possible spectral test |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{1}^{edge}\) | one-action-range rooted template inside \(\mathsf Q_{loc}^{99}\) | catches adjacent action/collar leakage |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{BTQ}^{edge}\) | bounded-collar quotient template after `BTQ/ACTFULLLAW` contraction | removes stagnant bounded-collar cycles |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{99}^{edge}\) | full Paper-21/Paper-23 over-refined carrier | complete but expensive cover |

Every template is evaluated on the same exact-CE adaptive law
\(\Gamma_{N,j}^{SEL2}\).  A template is admissible only if it contains at
least one live crossing atom

```math
A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j},
\qquad
x,y\in A,
\qquad
\Phi_A^{N,j}\not\equiv0.
```

If this condition fails, the template may prove a zero edge, but it does not
test the live RPF obstruction.

### Definition 37.2: Minimal Live-Edge Markov Blanket

For a rooted oriented live edge \(e=(x,y)\), define its minimal live Markov
blanket

```math
{\mathcal B}_{xy}^{min}
:=
\{x,y\}
\cup
\bigcup
\left\{
A:
A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j},
\ A\cap\{x,y\}\ne\varnothing
\right\}.
```

All variables outside \({\mathcal B}_{xy}^{min}\) are frozen into the outside
configuration \(\zeta\).  The exact template Hamiltonian is

```math
H_{xy}^{min}(u,v;\zeta)
:=
\sum_{\substack{
A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}\\
A\cap\{x,y\}\ne\varnothing
}}
\Phi_A^{N,j}
\left(
\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta}
\right),
```

where \(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta}\) means that the \(x\)-coordinate is set to
\(u\), the \(y\)-coordinate is set to \(v\), and every other coordinate is
read from \(\zeta\).

The two-site conditional density on this template is therefore

```math
d\Gamma_{xy,min}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
=
{1\over Z_{xy}^{min}(\zeta)}
\exp\left\{H_{xy}^{min}(u,v;\zeta)\right\}
d\lambda_x(u)d\lambda_y(v).
```

This is the smallest actual-law template that can see a nonzero live
`CleanRPF` crossing.

### Definition 37.3: Printed Edge Matrix On A Template

Let \({\mathfrak T}\) be any template in Definition 37.1.  Let
\({\mathcal I}_{L,x}^{0}\) and \({\mathcal I}_{L,y}^{0}\) be the finite
nontrivial Peter-Weyl channel indices retained at cutoff \(L\) on \(x\) and
\(y\).  For \(\alpha\in{\mathcal I}_{L,x}^{0}\) and
\(\beta\in{\mathcal I}_{L,y}^{0}\), put

```math
\widetilde\psi_{\alpha,x}(u;\zeta)
:=
\psi_{\alpha,x}(u)
-
\int\psi_{\alpha,x}(u')\,d\Gamma_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u'\mid\zeta),
```

```math
\widetilde\psi_{\beta,y}(v;\zeta)
:=
\psi_{\beta,y}(v)
-
\int\psi_{\beta,y}(v')\,d\Gamma_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(v'\mid\zeta).
```

The actual truncated edge matrix is

```math
M_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(\zeta)_{\alpha\beta}
:=
\iint
\overline{\widetilde\psi_{\alpha,x}(u;\zeta)}
\,
\widetilde\psi_{\beta,y}(v;\zeta)
\,
d\Gamma_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta).
```

The endpoint Gram matrices are

```math
G_{x,{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(\zeta)_{\alpha\alpha'}
:=
\int
\overline{\widetilde\psi_{\alpha,x}(u;\zeta)}
\widetilde\psi_{\alpha',x}(u;\zeta)
d\Gamma_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u\mid\zeta),
```

```math
G_{y,{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(\zeta)_{\beta\beta'}
:=
\int
\overline{\widetilde\psi_{\beta,y}(v;\zeta)}
\widetilde\psi_{\beta',y}(v;\zeta)
d\Gamma_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(v\mid\zeta).
```

On the quotient by null Gram directions, the printed matrix norm is

```math
\Theta_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{e,\zeta}
\left[
\lambda_{\max}
\left(
(G_y)^{-1}
M^*
(G_x)^{-1}
M
\right)
\right]^{1/2}.
```

Here \(M=M_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(\zeta)\), \(G_x=G_{x,{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(\zeta)\),
and \(G_y=G_{y,{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(\zeta)\).  This is exactly the operator
norm of
\(\Pi_{\le L,x}^{PW}T_{e,\zeta}^{N,j}\Pi_{\le L,y}^{PW}\) in the conditional
endpoint \(L^2\) norms.

### Lemma 37.4: The Minimal Matrix Is Printed

For \({\mathfrak T}_{0}^{edge}\), the matrix in Definition 37.3 is explicitly

```math
M_{0,L}^{N,j}(\zeta)_{\alpha\beta}
=
{1\over Z_{xy}^{min}(\zeta)}
\iint
\overline{\widetilde\psi_{\alpha,x}(u;\zeta)}
\widetilde\psi_{\beta,y}(v;\zeta)
e^{H_{xy}^{min}(u,v;\zeta)}
d\lambda_x(u)d\lambda_y(v).
```

The corresponding Gram matrices are obtained by integrating the same density
over \(v\) or over \(u\).  Thus the smallest live template has a fully
printed same-law finite matrix test.

Proof.

Substitute the exact minimal conditional density of Definition 37.2 into the
general matrix formula of Definition 37.3.  Every summand in
\(H_{xy}^{min}\) is a literal Möbius atom of Definition 15.2 restricted to the
same pushed-forward scalar row.  No extra process or off-law heat kernel is
introduced. `square`

### Lemma 37.5: A Universal Oscillation Envelope For A Template

For any template \({\mathfrak T}\), define the crossing oscillation

```math
\Delta_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{e,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left[
H_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
-H_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u;\zeta)
-H_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(v;\zeta)
\right].
```

Let \(C_{PW,L}^{\mathfrak T}\) be the finite norm-conversion constant from
total-variation oscillation on the \(y\)-conditional to the truncated
Peter-Weyl \(L^2_0\)-operator norm on the quotient by null Gram directions.
Concretely, it is computed from the sup norms of the retained centered
Peter-Weyl functions and the smallest positive eigenvalues of
\(G_{x,{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}\) and \(G_{y,{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}\), then
supremized over \(e,\zeta\).  It is finite on every fixed row and finite
template whenever the truncated Gram quotient is nondegenerate.

Then the likelihood-ratio oscillation bound gives the safe estimate

```math
\Theta_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
\le
C_{PW,L}^{\mathfrak T}
\tanh\left({\Delta_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\over4}\right)
```

Consequently a sufficient pass condition is

```math
C_{PW,L}^{\mathfrak T}
\tanh\left({\Delta_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\over4}\right)
+
\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over 1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
```

Equivalently, when \(\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}=0\), it is enough that

```math
\Delta_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
<
4\operatorname{arctanh}
\left(
{e^{-h_{path}}
\over
C_{PW,L}^{\mathfrak T}(1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4)}
\right).
```

Proof.

The likelihood-ratio oscillation bound is the same finite inequality used in
Lemma 34.3.  Passing from total variation to the truncated \(L^2_0\)
Peter-Weyl operator norm is a finite-dimensional norm conversion on the
printed Gram quotient, and this is exactly the constant
\(C_{PW,L}^{\mathfrak T}\).  The displayed pass condition is Corollary 36.7
rewritten as a bound on \(\theta+\kappa\). `square`

### Proposition 37.6: Pick 0, The Minimal Live Edge

The minimal live template \({\mathfrak T}_{0}^{edge}\) is the correct first
pick.  It has the smallest endpoint cost and the least template entropy.
However, the present corpus does not print either:

```math
\Theta_{0,L}^{N,j}
\le \theta_0<1
```

cofinally, or the oscillation bound

```math
\Delta_{0}^{N,j}
<
4\operatorname{arctanh}
\left(
{e^{-h_{path}}
\over
C_{PW,L}^{0}(1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4)}
\right)
```

with the required tail \(\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\).

Therefore Pick 0 is **printed but not certified**.

Proof.

Lemma 37.4 prints the finite matrix.  A pass would require either its
Gram-matrix norm or the oscillation envelope of Lemma 37.5.  Sections 28--33
show that the closed non-RPF source package permits arbitrary live RPF
residual-tail completions; Section 36.9 shows that those completions can make
the centered edge norm approach one.  Hence no current-corpus theorem bounds
the minimal live edge below the required scalar threshold. `square`

### Proposition 37.7: Pick 1, One-Action-Range Rooted Template

Let \({\mathfrak T}_{1}^{edge}\) be the one-action-range rooted template
inside

```math
\mathsf Q_{loc}^{99}=\{-1,0,1\}^4
```

with strict axial-tree coordinates and the scalar sector conventions of
Paper 21 Sections 102--114.  The matrix
\(M_{1,L}^{N,j}(\zeta)\) is printed by Definition 37.3 after replacing
\(H_{xy}^{min}\) with the sum of all live `CleanRPF` atoms meeting the
one-action-range rooted template.

This pick repairs possible leakage from adjacent action/collar variables, but
it does not improve the current-corpus verdict: the edge norm and tail remain
unsourced same-law values, and the larger template can only increase the
path-count and endpoint constants unless an actual cancellation theorem is
printed.

Thus Pick 1 is **printed but not certified**.

Proof.

Paper 21 Definition 102.4 prints the rooted one-action-range stencil, and
Paper 23 Definition 19.1 identifies the surviving `CleanRPF` atoms.  Their
finite restriction gives the matrix of Definition 37.3.  No cited result
evaluates the resulting Gram norm, proves a uniform nontrivial-channel
spectral gap, or proves the exact edge-path source. `square`

### Proposition 37.8: Pick 2, Bounded-Collar Quotient Template

Let \({\mathfrak T}_{BTQ}^{edge}\) be the template obtained from
\({\mathfrak T}_{1}^{edge}\) after applying the bounded-collar
`BTQ/ACTFULLLAW` quotient to stagnant and channel cycles.

This pick removes bounded-collar degree leakage, but it does not certify the
live RPF edge.  By construction, exact-entry `RPF` is not absorbed into the
bounded-collar quotient ledger; Sections 21 and 36 keep it as a separate
same-law residual conditional problem.  Therefore the same edge matrix
formula applies to the remaining live `CleanRPF` crossing, and the spectral
gap is still not supplied.

Thus Pick 2 is **printed after quotienting but not certified**.

Proof.

Paper 21 Sections 74--85 contract bounded-collar stagnant/channel components
only after their own full-law or degree-tail source is declared.  The RPF
slot is explicitly kept disjoint from `BTQ` and from RP/Cov, readout,
decoration, and comparison debits.  Hence quotienting bounded-collar cycles
does not create an RPF edge spectral gap. `square`

### Proposition 37.9: Pick 3, Full Over-Refined Carrier

Let \({\mathfrak T}_{99}^{edge}\) be the full over-refined Paper-21 carrier
using \(\mathfrak T_{99}^{+}\), \(\mathfrak L_{99}^{+}\),
\(\mathsf W_{\le4}^{99}\), and \(\Sigma_{99}^{+}\).  This template is a
complete finite cover of the active local row constructors.

The edge matrix is again printed by Definition 37.3, now with all over-refined
live `CleanRPF` atoms included.  This pick cannot be the first positive
route: it maximizes the finite carrier entropy and still does not supply the
cofinal spectral gap.  It is useful only as a completeness check showing that
no hidden local label was omitted.

Thus Pick 3 is **complete but not certified**.

Proof.

Paper 21 Definition 102.3--102.5 print the over-refined finite carrier.  Paper
23 Sections 24--26 already show that this cover proves finiteness but is too
coarse for a scalar KP margin without sharper source values.  Adding the
one-edge matrix formula does not change that verdict; it makes the remaining
source value explicit. `square`

### Theorem 37.10: Portfolio Exhaustion Verdict

The finite adaptive template portfolio has been exhausted relative to the
present corpus.

| pick | matrix printed? | live edge? | cofinal spectral gap? | scalar margin? |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{0}^{edge}\) | yes, Lemma 37.4 | yes by admissibility | not supplied | not certified |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{1}^{edge}\) | yes | yes if Pick 0 exists | not supplied | not certified |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{BTQ}^{edge}\) | yes after quotient | yes if RPF survives | not supplied | not certified |
| \({\mathfrak T}_{99}^{edge}\) | yes | yes if any live atom exists | not supplied | not certified |

Consequently no finite adaptive template currently proves
`P23-RPF-EDGE-SPEC + P23-RPF-EDGE-PATH`.  This is not a proof that the actual
adaptive law fails the edge test.  It is a proof that the existing papers do
not contain the numerical or analytic same-law matrix-value theorem required
to make any admissible template pass.

Proof.

Propositions 37.6--37.9 cover the admissible template ladder from smallest
live edge through complete over-refined carrier.  Every pick prints the same
kind of finite matrix on the same law.  Every pick lacks the same cofinal
spectral/path source.  Therefore the portfolio is exhausted at the level of
currently available source theorems. `square`

### Corollary 37.11: The Next Source Is A Matrix-Value Theorem

The next theorem must supply one of the following on the same adaptive
pushed-forward law:

1. a direct finite-template spectral estimate
   \[
   \Theta_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}+\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
   \le q
   \]
   with \(q\) below the Corollary 36.7 threshold for one admissible cofinal
   template family;
2. a crossing-oscillation estimate
   \[
   \Delta_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
   <
   4\operatorname{arctanh}
   \left(
   {e^{-h_{path}}
   \over
   C_{PW,L}^{\mathfrak T}(1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4)}
   \right)
   \]
   plus tail control;
3. or an exact edge-path expansion theorem that converts already-known
   smaller conditional responses into the required path constants.

Without one of these, further template enlargement only prints larger finite
matrices; it does not improve the scalar margin.

## 38. Conditional Maximal-Correlation Matrix Source

Section 37 exhausted the template lever.  This section attacks the printed
matrix value itself.  The correct scalar quantity is conditional maximal
correlation: the operator norm of the centered one-edge transfer is exactly
the largest conditional correlation between a retained nontrivial
Peter-Weyl mode at \(y\) and a retained nontrivial Peter-Weyl mode at \(x\).

This is useful because maximal correlation has same-law density-ratio
certificates.  A conditional \(\chi^2\) bound, or a sharper log-density
oscillation bound, would prove the required matrix-value theorem.  The
present corpus does not supply either bound for the actual adaptive residual
law.

### Definition 38.1: Restricted Conditional Maximal Correlation

Fix an admissible template \({\mathfrak T}\), cutoff \(L\), edge \(e=(x,y)\),
and outside configuration \(\zeta\).  Let
\({\mathcal H}_{x,L}^{0}(\zeta)\) and
\({\mathcal H}_{y,L}^{0}(\zeta)\) be the nontrivial Peter-Weyl subspaces from
Definition 37.3, centered and quotiented by null Gram directions in the
conditional endpoint \(L^2\) spaces.

Define

```math
\rho_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(e,\zeta)
:=
\sup
\left\{
\left|
\mathbb E_{\Gamma_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}}
\left[
g(\omega_x)f(\omega_y)\mid\zeta
\right]
\right|:
\begin{array}{l}
g\in{\mathcal H}_{x,L}^{0}(\zeta),\
f\in{\mathcal H}_{y,L}^{0}(\zeta),\\
\mathbb E[g\mid\zeta]=\mathbb E[f\mid\zeta]=0,\\
\mathbb E[|g|^2\mid\zeta]=
\mathbb E[|f|^2\mid\zeta]=1
\end{array}
\right\}.
```

Then set

```math
\rho_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{e,\zeta}
\rho_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(e,\zeta).
```

### Lemma 38.2: Matrix Norm Equals Restricted Maximal Correlation

For every fixed finite row and admissible template,

```math
\rho_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
=
\Theta_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

Write \(g=\sum_\alpha c_\alpha\widetilde\psi_{\alpha,x}\) and
\(f=\sum_\beta d_\beta\widetilde\psi_{\beta,y}\).  The conditional covariance
is

```math
c^*M_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}(\zeta)d.
```

The endpoint variances are \(c^*G_xc\) and \(d^*G_yd\).  Maximizing the
bilinear form over unit vectors in these two Gram norms gives exactly

```math
\left[
\lambda_{\max}\left((G_y)^{-1}M^*(G_x)^{-1}M\right)
\right]^{1/2},
```

on the quotient by null Gram directions.  Taking the essential supremum over
\(e,\zeta\) gives the displayed identity. `square`

### Definition 38.3: Conditional Density Ratio And \(\chi^2\) Source

For a template \({\mathfrak T}\), define the conditional density ratio

```math
R_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
:=
{d\Gamma_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
\over
d\Gamma_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u\mid\zeta)
d\Gamma_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(v\mid\zeta)}
```

on the product support, with the usual zero-null convention.  Define

```math
\chi^2_{{\mathfrak T}}(N,j)
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{e,\zeta}
\iint
\left(R_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)-1\right)^2
d\Gamma_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u\mid\zeta)
d\Gamma_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(v\mid\zeta).
```

`P23-RPF-MC-CHI2({\mathfrak T},L,xi,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\chi^2_{{\mathfrak T}}(N,j)
\le \xi,
\qquad
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
\le \kappa.
```

### Lemma 38.4: \(\chi^2\) Controls The Edge Matrix

For every finite row and template,

```math
\Theta_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
\le
\min\{1,\sqrt{\chi^2_{{\mathfrak T}}(N,j)}\}.
```

Proof.

For centered unit \(g,f\),

```math
\mathbb E[g(\omega_x)f(\omega_y)\mid\zeta]
=
\iint
g(u)f(v)
\left(R_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)-1\right)
d\Gamma_x(u\mid\zeta)d\Gamma_y(v\mid\zeta).
```

Cauchy-Schwarz gives an upper bound by the conditional
\(\chi^2\)-norm of \(R-1\), because
\(\|g(u)f(v)\|_{L^2(\Gamma_x\otimes\Gamma_y)}=1\).  The trivial operator
bound gives the additional upper bound by \(1\).  Taking suprema gives the
claim. `square`

### Theorem 38.5: \(\chi^2\) Matrix-Value Closure Test

Assume `P23-RPF-MC-CHI2({\mathfrak T},L,xi,kappa)` and
`P23-RPF-EDGE-PATH(B_edge,h_path,C_path)` for one admissible cofinal template
family.  If

```math
\sqrt{\xi}+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then adaptive Branch A closes on the exact-CE branch.

Proof.

Lemma 38.4 gives `EDGE-SPEC` with
\(\theta=\sqrt{\xi}\) and tail \(\kappa\).  The displayed inequality is
Corollary 36.7 rewritten as
\(\theta+\kappa<e^{-h_{path}}/(1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4)\).  Then Theorem 36.6
and Corollary 36.7 close the branch. `square`

### Definition 38.6: Conditional Log-Ratio Oscillation Source

`P23-RPF-MC-LOGRATIO({\mathfrak T},L,Delta,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{e,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\log R_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
\le
\Delta,
```

and

```math
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
\le
\kappa.
```

This is a statement about the actual conditional density ratio of the same
adaptive residual law, not about the divided-out central heat-kernel factor.

### Lemma 38.7: Log-Ratio Oscillation Gives A Sharp \(\chi^2\) Envelope

If \(\operatorname{osc}\log R\le\Delta\) and
\(\mathbb E_{\Gamma_x\otimes\Gamma_y}R=1\), then

```math
\int(R-1)^2\,d(\Gamma_x\otimes\Gamma_y)
\le
\sinh^2(\Delta/2).
```

Proof.

Let \(\lambda=e^\Delta\).  The oscillation bound implies that the range of
\(R\) is contained in an interval \([a,\lambda a]\).  Since
\(\mathbb E R=1\), the variance of \(R\) is at most the largest variance of a
random variable with mean \(1\) and range ratio at most \(\lambda\).  This
maximum occurs on the two endpoints with
\(a=(\lambda+1)/(2\lambda)\), giving

```math
\operatorname{Var}(R)
\le
{(\lambda-1)^2\over4\lambda}
=
\sinh^2(\Delta/2).
```

But \(\operatorname{Var}(R)=\int(R-1)^2\,d(\Gamma_x\otimes\Gamma_y)\).
`square`

### Corollary 38.8: Log-Ratio Matrix-Value Closure Test

Assume `P23-RPF-MC-LOGRATIO({\mathfrak T},L,Delta,kappa)` and
`P23-RPF-EDGE-PATH(B_edge,h_path,C_path)` for one admissible cofinal template
family.  If

```math
\sinh(\Delta/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then adaptive Branch A closes on the exact-CE branch.

Proof.

Lemma 38.7 and Lemma 38.4 give
\(\Theta_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}\le\sinh(\Delta/2)\) cofinally.  Apply
Theorem 38.5 with \(\xi=\sinh^2(\Delta/2)\). `square`

### Theorem 38.9: Current-Corpus Matrix-Value Verdict

The current corpus proves the identity

```math
\Theta_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
=
\rho_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}
```

and the sufficient same-law routes

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MC\text{-}CHI2}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MC\text{-}LOGRATIO}.
```

It does not prove either source for the actual adaptive residual law.

Proof.

Lemma 38.2 is pure finite-row linear algebra on the same pushed-forward law.
Lemmas 38.4 and 38.7 are finite probability inequalities for the printed
conditional density ratio.

What is missing is a bound on that density ratio.  Sections 15, 23, 26, 36,
and 37 print the residual density, canonical coefficient gauge, value table,
edge transfer, and template matrices.  They do not bound
\(\chi^2_{{\mathfrak T}}\) or \(\operatorname{osc}\log R_{{\mathfrak T}}\)
cofinally.  Paper 16 supplies heat-kernel analytic rows on its declared
heat-kernel tower, not this adaptive exact-CE residual density ratio.  Paper
21 Theorem 85.7 explicitly leaves the active heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl smoothing
source unsupplied.  Finally, Sections 28--33 show that the closed non-RPF
package permits same-record residual-tail completions with arbitrarily strong
live RPF coupling; such completions can drive the maximal correlation toward
one without changing the already closed ledgers.

Therefore the matrix-value route is now completely localized, but it is not
closed by the present papers. `square`

### Corollary 38.10: Next Exact Source

The next exact theorem must be one of:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MC\text{-}CHI2}
({\mathfrak T},L,\xi,\kappa)
```

with

```math
\sqrt{\xi}+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

or

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MC\text{-}LOGRATIO}
({\mathfrak T},L,\Delta,\kappa)
```

with

```math
\sinh(\Delta/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
```

If neither density-ratio source is available, then the only remaining
positive route is a direct proof of the restricted maximal-correlation bound
\(\rho_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}\le q\) on the same adaptive law, again below
the Corollary 36.7 threshold.

## 39. Density Ratio As A Crossing-Hamiltonian Source

Section 38 localized the matrix-value problem to the conditional density
ratio.  This section removes one more layer of ambiguity: the log-density
ratio is exactly the marginally projected crossing Hamiltonian of the same
two-site conditional law.  A cruder but more literal sufficient test is the
oscillation of the sum of actual crossing Möbius atoms.

### Definition 39.1: Marginal Crossing Hamiltonian

Fix an admissible edge template \({\mathfrak T}\), an edge \(e=(x,y)\), and
an outside configuration \(\zeta\).  Write the two-site conditional law as

```math
d\Gamma_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
=
{1\over Z_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(\zeta)}
\exp\{H_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\}
d\lambda_x(u)d\lambda_y(v).
```

Define the two marginal log-partition functions

```math
H_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u;\zeta)
:=
\log
\int
\exp\{H_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\}
d\lambda_y(v),
```

```math
H_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(v;\zeta)
:=
\log
\int
\exp\{H_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\}
d\lambda_x(u).
```

The marginal crossing Hamiltonian is

```math
C_{{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
:=
H_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
-H_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u;\zeta)
-H_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(v;\zeta).
```

Set

```math
\Delta_{m,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{e,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
C_{{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta).
```

All three functions are computed from the same conditional density already
printed in Sections 36--38.

### Lemma 39.2: Exact Log-Ratio Identity

For every finite row and every admissible template,

```math
\log R_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
=
C_{{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
+\log Z_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(\zeta).
```

Consequently

```math
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}\log R_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
=
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}C_{{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta).
```

Proof.

The marginal densities are

```math
d\Gamma_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u\mid\zeta)
=
{e^{H_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u;\zeta)}
\over
Z_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(\zeta)}
d\lambda_x(u),
```

and similarly for \(y\).  Dividing the joint density by the two marginal
densities gives

```math
R_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v\mid\zeta)
=
Z_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(\zeta)
\exp\{
H_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
-H_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}
-H_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}
\}.
```

Taking logarithms gives the first display.  The added
\(\log Z_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(\zeta)\) is independent of \(u,v\), so it
does not affect oscillation. `square`

### Definition 39.3: Marginal Crossing Source

`P23-RPF-CROSS-MARG({\mathfrak T},Delta,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally in
\((N,j)\),

```math
\Delta_{m,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\le\Delta,
\qquad
\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

By Lemma 39.2 this source is not a new object beside
`P23-RPF-MC-LOGRATIO`; it is the same density-ratio source written as a
finite conditional-Hamiltonian table.

### Proposition 39.4: Marginal Crossing Is Exactly The Log-Ratio Gate

For fixed \({\mathfrak T},L,\Delta,\kappa\),

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CROSS\text{-}MARG}
({\mathfrak T},\Delta,\kappa)
```

is equivalent to

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MC\text{-}LOGRATIO}
({\mathfrak T},L,\Delta,\kappa).
```

Therefore the Section-38 closure condition becomes

```math
\sinh(\Delta/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
```

Proof.

The two assertions have identical tail clause.  Their density-ratio clauses
are identical by Lemma 39.2.  The displayed strict margin is Corollary 38.8.
`square`

### Definition 39.5: Literal Crossing Atom Source

Let

```math
{\mathcal U}_{cross,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(x,y;\zeta)
```

be the surviving `CleanRPF` atom sublist in the template whose support meets
both endpoint sides \(x\) and \(y\).  Atoms meeting only \(x\), only \(y\), or
neither endpoint are excluded, because after \(\zeta\) is fixed they are
one-site terms or constants.

Define the literal crossing Hamiltonian

```math
W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
:=
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(x,y;\zeta)}
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta}).
```

Set

```math
\Omega_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{e,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta).
```

`P23-RPF-CROSS-LIT({\mathfrak T},Omega,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\Omega_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\le\Omega,
\qquad
\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

This is the atom-level table one can try to print directly from Sections 15,
19, 23, and 26.

### Lemma 39.6: Literal Crossing Controls Marginal Crossing

For every finite row and admissible template,

```math
\Delta_{m,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
\le
3\,\Omega_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

After the outside configuration \(\zeta\) is fixed, the template Hamiltonian
splits as

```math
H_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
=
A_x(u;\zeta)+A_y(v;\zeta)+A_0(\zeta)
+W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta),
```

where \(A_x\) is the sum of atoms meeting \(x\) but not \(y\), \(A_y\) is the
sum of atoms meeting \(y\) but not \(x\), \(A_0\) is the sum of atoms meeting
neither endpoint after \(\zeta\) is fixed, and \(W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}\) is
the crossing sum in Definition 39.5.  This is just the Möbius atom
decomposition of Definition 15.2 restricted to the two endpoint variables.

Let \(\Omega=\operatorname{osc}W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(\cdot,\cdot;\zeta)\)
for the fixed edge and outside record.  The \(x\)-marginal log partition has
the form

```math
H_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u;\zeta)
=
A_x(u;\zeta)+A_0(\zeta)
+\log\int e^{A_y(v;\zeta)+W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)}
d\lambda_y(v).
```

For \(u,u'\), the two integrands differ pointwise by the factor
\(\exp\{W(u,v)-W(u',v)\}\), whose logarithm lies in an interval of length at
most \(\Omega\).  Hence

```math
\operatorname{osc}_u
\left[
H_{x,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(u;\zeta)-A_x(u;\zeta)
\right]
\le
\Omega.
```

The same argument gives

```math
\operatorname{osc}_v
\left[
H_{y,{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}(v;\zeta)-A_y(v;\zeta)
\right]
\le
\Omega.
```

Substituting these two bounds into

```math
C_{{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}
=
W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}
-\left(H_x^m-A_x-A_0\right)
-\left(H_y^m-A_y-A_0\right)
-A_0
```

and dropping constants gives
\(\operatorname{osc}C_{{\mathfrak T}}^{m,N,j}\le3\Omega\).  Taking the
essential supremum over \(e,\zeta\) proves the result. `square`

### Corollary 39.7: Literal Crossing Closure Test

Assume `P23-RPF-CROSS-LIT({\mathfrak T},Omega,kappa)` and the exact edge-path
package of Section 36.  If

```math
\sinh(3\Omega/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds on the same adaptive law.

Proof.

Lemma 39.6 gives `P23-RPF-CROSS-MARG({\mathfrak T},3Omega,kappa)`.  Proposition
39.4 gives `P23-RPF-MC-LOGRATIO({\mathfrak T},L,3Omega,kappa)`.  Corollary
38.8 closes the edge matrix route, and Section 36 propagates it to the
screened conditional influence theorem. `square`

### Theorem 39.8: Current-Corpus Crossing Verdict

The density-ratio obstruction is now fully sharpened:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MC\text{-}LOGRATIO}
```

is exactly the marginal crossing-Hamiltonian source

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CROSS\text{-}MARG},
```

and a sufficient atom-level source is

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CROSS\text{-}LIT}.
```

The current corpus proves the algebraic reductions above, but it does not
prove the required cofinal bounds on either
\(\Delta_{m,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\) or \(\Omega_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\).

Proof.

Sections 15, 19, 23, and 26 print the literal Möbius atoms and their finite
rowwise value tables.  Sections 36--38 print the edge transfer, template
matrices, and density-ratio/maximal-correlation identities.  Lemmas 39.2 and
39.6 connect these objects exactly on the same pushed-forward scalar law.

What remains missing is not a bookkeeping convention.  It is a quantitative
same-law bound saying that the crossing part of the actual adaptive residual
Hamiltonian has uniformly small oscillation, or equivalently that the
conditional density ratio has uniformly small oscillation or \(\chi^2\).
Sections 28--33 already show why this cannot be inferred from the closed
non-RPF source package: residual-tail completions can preserve the already
closed ledgers while increasing live endpoint coupling.  Such completions
increase \(W_{xy,{\mathfrak T}}\), hence can increase the marginal crossing
and the conditional maximal correlation.

Therefore the next theorem is no longer "print the matrix" or "pick a better
template."  It must be a genuine same-law crossing estimate:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CROSS\text{-}MARG}
```

with the Section-38 margin, or the stronger literal atom estimate

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}CROSS\text{-}LIT}
```

with the Corollary 39.7 margin. `square`

### Corollary 39.9: Next Work Item

The next useful finite table is the crossing atom table

```math
{\mathcal U}_{cross,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}(x,y;\zeta)
```

for the minimal live template.  It should report:

1. the literal crossing labels \(A\);
2. their same-law coefficient functions \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\);
3. the rowwise oscillations \(\operatorname{osc}\Phi_A^{N,j}\);
4. the resulting \(\Omega_{{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\);
5. the Peter-Weyl truncation tail \(\Kappa_{{\mathfrak T},L}^{N,j}\);
6. the strict scalar comparison
   \[
   \sinh(3\Omega/2)+\kappa
   <
   {e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
   \]

If this table fails, the marginal crossing source may still pass by
cancellation after marginal projection, but that would require evaluating
\(\Delta_{m,{\mathfrak T}}^{N,j}\) directly rather than bounding it by the
literal atom oscillation sum.

## 40. Minimal Crossing Atom Table

Section 39 says exactly what to print next.  We now specialize to the
minimal live template \({\mathfrak T}_{0}^{edge}\).  This is the cheapest
possible source table: only the two endpoint variables \(x,y\) remain free;
all other variables in the live Markov blanket are part of the outside record
\(\zeta\).

### Definition 40.1: The Minimal Crossing Table

For a rooted oriented edge \(e=(x,y)\), define

```math
{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
:=
\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}:\{x,y\}\subseteq A\}.
```

Equivalently, \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\) iff \(A\) is a
surviving `CleanRPF` atom and, after all variables outside
\({\mathcal B}_{xy}^{min}\) are frozen, the function
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta})\) can depend on both endpoint
coordinates \(u\) and \(v\).

The literal row printed for each \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\)
is:

| field | value |
| --- | --- |
| support | \(A\subseteq V_{RPF}^{N,j}\) |
| endpoints | \(\{x,y\}\subseteq A\) |
| class | `CleanRPF` |
| atom | \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) from Definition 15.2 |
| hull | \(Y(A)=\operatorname{Hull}_{RPF}(A)\) |
| hull size | \(\ell_{RPF}(A)=|Y(A)|\) |
| diameter | \(\operatorname{diam}_{RPF}(A)\) |
| oscillation | \(o_A^{N,j}:=\operatorname{osc}\Phi_A^{N,j}\) |
| crossing value | \(\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta})\) |

This is a finite table for every fixed row \((N,j)\).

### Lemma 40.2: Exact Endpoint Classification

In the minimal template, every surviving clean atom belongs to exactly one of
the following four endpoint classes:

| class | condition on \(A\) | contribution after \(\zeta\) is fixed |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `outside` | \(A\cap\{x,y\}=\varnothing\) | constant in the two endpoint variables |
| `x-one-site` | \(x\in A,\ y\notin A\) | one-site term in \(u\) |
| `y-one-site` | \(y\in A,\ x\notin A\) | one-site term in \(v\) |
| `cross` | \(\{x,y\}\subseteq A\) | live two-endpoint term |

All non-`CleanRPF` classes have already been removed by Definition 19.1 and
the no-double-charge audit of Section 18.

Proof.

The minimal template leaves only \(x\) and \(y\) unfrozen.  A surviving clean
atom can therefore meet neither free endpoint, only \(x\), only \(y\), or
both.  The first case is a constant after \(\zeta\) is fixed and is not in
the endpoint Hamiltonian sum of Definition 37.2.  The middle two cases are
one-site terms.  The last case is exactly Definition 40.1.  Non-clean rows
are excluded before this classification by Definition 19.1. `square`

### Definition 40.3: Exact And Safe Minimal Crossing Bounds

The exact minimal crossing Hamiltonian is

```math
W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
:=
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta}).
```

Set

```math
\Omega_0^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta).
```

The safe atom-sum envelope is

```math
\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
o_A^{N,j}.
```

Thus

```math
\Omega_0^{N,j}\le\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}.
```

The exact quantity \(\Omega_0^{N,j}\) retains cancellations between crossing
atoms.  The envelope \(\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}\) is the conservative table one
gets from oscillation magnitudes alone.

### Lemma 40.4: The Safe Envelope Is Same-Law And Finite

For every fixed adaptive row \((N,j)\),
\(\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}\) is a finite scalar function of the same
pushed-forward `SEL2` law.

Proof.

Definition 19.1 gives a finite clean atom list.  Definition 15.2 gives each
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) by Boolean finite differences of
\(H_{N,j}=\log{\mathcal R}_{N,j}\), itself a scalar function of the same
exact-CE pushed-forward law.  The oscillation \(o_A^{N,j}\), the endpoint
membership test \(\{x,y\}\subseteq A\), and the finite supremum over
endpoint pairs are therefore all finite scalar operations on that same law.
No auxiliary dynamics or off-record kernel is introduced. `square`

### Proposition 40.5: Zero-Crossing Alternative

If, cofinally,

```math
{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)=\varnothing
```

for every rooted oriented candidate edge \(e=(x,y)\) in the RPF edge carrier,
then
\(\Omega_0^{N,j}=0\) cofinally.  Consequently the minimal literal crossing
route passes whenever the Peter-Weyl tail and edge-path constants satisfy

```math
\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
```

Proof.

If the crossing table is empty, then \(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}=0\) for every edge and
outside record.  Hence \(\Omega_0^{N,j}=0\).  Corollary 39.7 with
\(\Omega=0\) gives the displayed scalar condition. `square`

### Proposition 40.6: Atom-Sum Pass Test

Suppose that, cofinally,

```math
\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}\le\overline\Omega_*
```

and

```math
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

If

```math
\sinh(3\overline\Omega_*/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Definition 40.3 gives \(\Omega_0^{N,j}\le\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}\le
\overline\Omega_*\).  Therefore `P23-RPF-CROSS-LIT({\mathfrak T}_0^{edge},
\overline\Omega_*,\kappa)` holds.  Apply Corollary 39.7. `square`

### Proposition 40.7: Direct Marginal Fallback

If the atom-sum pass test fails, the minimal edge is not yet falsified.  The
remaining sharper same-law value is

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left[
H_{xy}^{min}(u,v;\zeta)
-H_x^{m,min}(u;\zeta)
-H_y^{m,min}(v;\zeta)
\right].
```

If, cofinally,

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\le\Delta_*
```

and

```math
\sinh(\Delta_*/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

This is Proposition 39.4 and Corollary 38.8 specialized to
\({\mathfrak T}_{0}^{edge}\).  It can pass even when Proposition 40.6 fails,
because marginal projection may cancel or dilute the literal atom-sum
oscillation. `square`

### Theorem 40.8: Current-Corpus Minimal Table Verdict

The minimal crossing atom table is now printed exactly:

```math
{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
=
\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{RPF,clean}^{N,j}:\{x,y\}\subseteq A\}.
```

The current corpus proves:

1. exact finite rowwise decidability of this table;
2. exact same-law computation of every coefficient function \(\Phi_A^{N,j}\);
3. exact finite scalar definitions of \(\Omega_0^{N,j}\),
   \(\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}\), and \(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\);
4. the zero-crossing, atom-sum, and direct marginal closure tests above.

The current corpus does **not** prove any cofinal numerical bound strong
enough to satisfy those tests.

Proof.

Items 1--3 follow from Definitions 15.2, 19.1, 26.1, 37.2, and 40.1--40.3.
Items 4 are Propositions 40.5--40.7.

For the negative current-corpus verdict, Sections 28--33 already construct
same-record residual-tail completions that preserve the closed non-RPF
ledgers while producing live higher-order RPF endpoint coupling.  Such a
completion can make the crossing table nonempty and can increase the
oscillation of \(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}\) without violating the ledgers already
closed outside RPF.  Therefore no theorem currently cited in Papers 16,
20, 21, 22, or 23 supplies a cofinal upper bound for
\(\Omega_0^{N,j}\), \(\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}\), or \(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\)
below the scalar thresholds above.

Thus the minimal table is closed as a finite same-law object, but the
positive crossing estimate remains a new source theorem. `square`

### Corollary 40.9: Next Exact Fork

There are now only two useful continuations for the minimal edge:

1. prove a cofinal atom-sum bound
   \[
   \overline\Omega_0^{N,j}\le\overline\Omega_*
   \]
   satisfying Proposition 40.6;
2. or bypass the atom-sum loss and evaluate the direct marginal crossing
   value
   \[
   \Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
   \]
   satisfying Proposition 40.7.

If both fail, the minimal-edge Branch-A route is parked behind a genuinely
new same-law crossing theorem; enlarging the template should be attempted
only if it supplies a cancellation or marginalization identity not visible in
\({\mathfrak T}_{0}^{edge}\).

## 41. Direct Minimal Marginal Crossing Test

Section 40 left two options.  The conservative atom-sum route is deliberately
wasteful: it pays \(\overline\Omega_0\) and then the factor-three loss from
Lemma 39.6.  This section writes the exact marginal object for the minimal
edge and isolates the sharper primitive theorem that would avoid that loss.

### Definition 41.1: Minimal One-Site Log-Partition Terms

For the minimal template, decompose the endpoint Hamiltonian as

```math
H_{xy}^{min}(u,v;\zeta)
=
A_x(u;\zeta)+A_y(v;\zeta)+A_0(\zeta)
+W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta),
```

where \(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}\) is the crossing Hamiltonian of Definition 40.3.
Define

```math
F_y^{N,j}(u;\zeta)
:=
\log
\int
\exp\{A_y(v;\zeta)+W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\}
d\lambda_y(v),
```

and

```math
F_x^{N,j}(v;\zeta)
:=
\log
\int
\exp\{A_x(u;\zeta)+W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\}
d\lambda_x(u).
```

These are finite same-law scalar functions of the two-site conditional
density printed in Definition 37.2.

### Lemma 41.2: Exact Normalized Marginal Formula

For the minimal edge,

```math
C_{0}^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
=
W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
-F_y^{N,j}(u;\zeta)
-F_x^{N,j}(v;\zeta)
+c_{0}^{N,j}(\zeta),
```

where \(c_{0}^{N,j}(\zeta)\) is independent of \(u,v\).  Consequently

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left[
W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
-F_y^{N,j}(u;\zeta)
-F_x^{N,j}(v;\zeta)
\right].
```

Proof.

Substitute the decomposition of Definition 41.1 into Definition 39.1.  The
\(x\)-marginal log partition is

```math
H_x^{m,min}(u;\zeta)
=
A_x(u;\zeta)+A_0(\zeta)+F_y^{N,j}(u;\zeta),
```

and the \(y\)-marginal log partition is

```math
H_y^{m,min}(v;\zeta)
=
A_y(v;\zeta)+A_0(\zeta)+F_x^{N,j}(v;\zeta).
```

Thus all one-site terms cancel in
\(H_{xy}^{min}-H_x^{m,min}-H_y^{m,min}\), leaving
\(W-F_y-F_x-A_0\).  The last term is independent of \(u,v\) and is absorbed
into \(c_0^{N,j}(\zeta)\). `square`

### Definition 41.3: Direct Minimal Marginal Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-MARG(Delta,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\le\Delta,
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

It is the minimal-edge specialization of `P23-RPF-CROSS-MARG`, with no
atom-sum or factor-three surcharge.

### Corollary 41.4: Direct Minimal Marginal Closure

If `P23-RPF-MIN-MARG(Delta,kappa)` holds and

```math
\sinh(\Delta/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

This is Proposition 40.7 restated as a named minimal-edge source theorem.
`square`

### Definition 41.5: Mixed-Odds Diameter

For a two-endpoint function \(G(u,v)\), define its mixed-odds diameter by

```math
\operatorname{odiam}(G)
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{u,u',v,v'}
\left|
G(u,v)+G(u',v')
-G(u,v')-G(u',v)
\right|.
```

For the minimal crossing atom sum set

```math
D_{\square,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{odiam}
\left(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(\cdot,\cdot;\zeta)\right).
```

This is the log-odds-ratio diameter of the literal crossing kernel before
the marginal normalization.

### Lemma 41.6: Mixed-Odds Is Gauge-Invariant

For every finite row,

```math
\operatorname{odiam}
\left(C_{0}^{m,N,j}(\cdot,\cdot;\zeta)\right)
=
\operatorname{odiam}
\left(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(\cdot,\cdot;\zeta)\right).
```

In particular,

```math
D_{\square,0}^{N,j}
\le
2\Omega_0^{N,j}
\le
2\overline\Omega_0^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

Adding or subtracting a one-site function of \(u\), a one-site function of
\(v\), or a constant does not change the mixed difference

```math
G(u,v)+G(u',v')-G(u,v')-G(u',v).
```

Lemma 41.2 writes \(C_0^m\) as \(W\) minus one \(u\)-function, one
\(v\)-function, and a constant, so the mixed-odds diameters are equal.  The
bound \(D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\le2\Omega_0^{N,j}\) follows because a mixed
difference is the difference of two values of \(W\) minus the difference of
two other values of \(W\), hence has absolute value at most twice the
oscillation of \(W\).  The second inequality is Definition 40.3. `square`
