### Proposition 41.7: What The Mixed-Odds Test Does And Does Not Prove

The mixed-odds table is a useful diagnostic but is not, by itself, the
minimal marginal source.

What it proves is exact gauge invariance: all one-site endpoint terms and all
normalization choices have been removed.  What it does not prove from the
current corpus is a bound

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\le \Psi(D_{\square,0}^{N,j})
```

strong enough for Corollary 41.4.

Proof.

The first statement is Lemma 41.6.  For the second, note that
\(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\) is the full oscillation of the normalized log-density
ratio \(C_0^m=\log R+\) constant.  The mixed-odds diameter controls only
four-point differences, not the absolute range after marginal normalization,
unless an additional same-law normalization or positivity theorem is supplied.
The current papers provide the rowwise finite table but not such a cofinal
normalization theorem. `square`

### Theorem 41.8: Current-Corpus Direct Marginal Verdict

The direct minimal marginal test is now fully specified:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}MARG}(\Delta,\kappa)
```

with the strict scalar condition of Corollary 41.4.

The current corpus proves the exact formula for \(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\) and
the gauge-invariant mixed-odds diagnostic \(D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\), but it
does not prove the required cofinal upper bound on \(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\).

Proof.

Definitions 41.1, 41.3, and 41.5 print the relevant finite scalar tables.
Lemma 41.2 removes the one-site pieces exactly, and Lemma 41.6 identifies the
mixed-odds invariant.  Corollary 41.4 gives the closure theorem.

The missing assertion is quantitative: the actual adaptive minimal edge must
have small enough normalized marginal crossing.  No result in Papers 16, 20,
21, 22, or the earlier sections of Paper 23 bounds the functions
\(F_x,F_y\) or the normalized range of \(W-F_y-F_x\) cofinally below the
displayed scalar threshold.  Sections 28--33 also show that this cannot be
derived from the already closed non-RPF ledgers alone.

Therefore the factor-three atom-sum loss has been bypassed formally, but not
closed numerically.  The new primitive source is the direct marginal theorem
`P23-RPF-MIN-MARG(Delta,kappa)`. `square`

### Corollary 41.9: Next Work Item

The next useful table is not another atom list.  It is the normalized
minimal-edge marginal table:

1. \(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\);
2. \(F_y^{N,j}(u;\zeta)\);
3. \(F_x^{N,j}(v;\zeta)\);
4. \(C_0^{m,N,j}=W-F_y-F_x+c_0\);
5. \(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\);
6. \(\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\);
7. the strict comparison
   \[
   \sinh(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}/2)+\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}
   <
   {e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
   \]

If this direct table fails, then the minimal-edge route is parked behind a
new same-law marginal crossing estimate, not merely behind missing notation.

## 42. Normalized Minimal-Edge Marginal Table

Section 41 named the primitive source.  This section prints the actual table
that would decide it.  The table is a same-law finite conditional-density
table; the only missing ingredient is a cofinal numerical range bound.

### Definition 42.1: The Normalized Minimal Table

For each finite adaptive row, each rooted candidate edge \(e=(x,y)\), and
each outside record \(\zeta\), define the row

| field | value |
| --- | --- |
| crossing kernel | \(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\) |
| \(y\)-marginal log partition | \(F_y^{N,j}(u;\zeta)\) |
| \(x\)-marginal log partition | \(F_x^{N,j}(v;\zeta)\) |
| normalized log ratio | \(C_0^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)=W-F_y-F_x+c_0\) |
| range | \(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}(x,y;\zeta)=\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}C_0^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)\) |
| mixed odds | \(D_{\square,0}^{N,j}(x,y;\zeta)=\operatorname{odiam}W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(\cdot,\cdot;\zeta)\) |
| Peter-Weyl tail | \(\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}(x,y;\zeta)\) |

The cofinal quantities are the essential suprema over \(x,y,\zeta\).

### Lemma 42.2: Exact Rowwise Extremal Problem

For every fixed row,

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\left(
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{u,v} C_0^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
-
\operatorname*{ess\,inf}_{u,v} C_0^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
\right).
```

If the row density is represented by a continuous positive density on a
compact finite group battery, the essential suprema and infima may be
replaced by ordinary maxima and minima on the compact endpoint space.

Proof.

The first display is only the definition of oscillation applied to the
exact normalized formula of Lemma 41.2.  In the continuous positive compact
case, \(W,F_x,F_y\) and hence \(C_0^m\) are continuous finite scalar
functions on compact endpoint spaces, so extrema exist and agree with the
essential extrema. `square`

### Definition 42.3: Peter-Weyl Range Certificate

Let \(\Pi_{\le L}^{xy}\) denote the finite Peter-Weyl projection on the two
endpoint scalar battery.  Define the truncated normalized range

```math
\Delta_{m,0,L}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left(\Pi_{\le L}^{xy} C_0^{m,N,j}\right)(u,v;\zeta).
```

`P23-RPF-MIN-MARG-PW(L,delta_tail,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\left\|
C_0^{m,N,j}
-
\Pi_{\le L}^{xy}C_0^{m,N,j}
\right\|_{\infty}
\le
\delta_{tail},
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

Then

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
\le
\Delta_{m,0,L}^{N,j}+2\delta_{tail}.
```

Proof.

The oscillation of \(f\) differs from the oscillation of \(g\) by at most
\(2\|f-g\|_\infty\).  Apply this to
\(f=C_0^{m,N,j}\) and \(g=\Pi_{\le L}^{xy}C_0^{m,N,j}\). `square`

### Corollary 42.4: Finite Truncated Pass Test

Assume `P23-RPF-MIN-MARG-PW(L,delta_tail,kappa)` and suppose that, cofinally,

```math
\Delta_{m,0,L}^{N,j}\le\Delta_L.
```

If

```math
\sinh((\Delta_L+2\delta_{tail})/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Definition 42.3 gives
\(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\le\Delta_L+2\delta_{tail}\).  Corollary 41.4 then
closes. `square`

### Definition 42.5: Sinkhorn-Range Source

The normalized formula

```math
C_0^m=W-F_y-F_x+c_0
```

is the continuous finite-record analogue of Sinkhorn scaling of the positive
kernel \(e^W\) to its two one-site marginals.  Define
`P23-RPF-MIN-SINK(Theta)` to assert that, cofinally,

```math
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left[
W_{xy,0}^{N,j}
-F_y^{N,j}
-F_x^{N,j}
\right]
\le
\Theta
```

uniformly in \(x,y,\zeta\).  This is exactly
`P23-RPF-MIN-MARG(Theta,kappa)` without the Peter-Weyl tail clause.

### Proposition 42.6: No Free Mixed-Odds Closure

The mixed-odds invariant \(D_{\square,0}\) is not, by itself, the source
needed for Branch A.  The required source is a range statement for the
Sinkhorn-normalized kernel \(W-F_y-F_x\).

Proof.

Lemma 41.6 proves that mixed odds is unchanged by one-site gauge
renormalization.  But Corollary 41.4 needs the full range of \(C_0^m\), not
only its four-point mixed differences.  A bound on \(D_{\square,0}\) can be
useful only after a same-law normalization theorem converts mixed-odds
control into range control for the actual adaptive endpoint marginals.  The
current corpus contains no such theorem.  Therefore replacing
`P23-RPF-MIN-MARG` by a bare mixed-odds bound would be an unlicensed
shortcut. `square`

### Theorem 42.7: Current-Corpus Normalized Table Verdict

The normalized minimal-edge table is fully printed by Definition 42.1.  The
current corpus proves the exact finite extremal problem of Lemma 42.2 and the
conditional finite Peter-Weyl certificate of Definition 42.3.  It does not
prove:

1. a cofinal bound on \(\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}\);
2. a cofinal finite Peter-Weyl sup-norm tail for \(C_0^m\);
3. a Sinkhorn-range theorem converting mixed-odds control into the required
   normalized range bound.

Proof.

Definitions 41.1--41.5 and 42.1 print the exact row values.  Lemma 42.2 is
finite compact extremal algebra, and Definition 42.3 is the standard finite
projection/tail route already used elsewhere in the paper, now applied to the
normalized log ratio itself.

The missing items are exactly the quantitative assertions listed above.
Papers 16 and 20 provide heat-kernel and Peter-Weyl tail estimates only for
their declared heat-kernel or scalar-readout ledgers; Section 35 already
proved that those estimates do not imply a conditional transfer contraction
for the actual adaptive residual law.  Sections 28--33 show that the closed
non-RPF ledgers permit residual completions with live endpoint coupling.
Thus the normalized table exists, but no current theorem bounds its cofinal
range below the Corollary 41.4 threshold. `square`

### Corollary 42.8: Next Exact Source

The next theorem must be one of:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SINK}(\Theta)
```

with

```math
\sinh(\Theta/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

or the finite Peter-Weyl version

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}MARG\text{-}PW}
(L,\delta_{tail},\kappa)
```

plus a truncated range bound \(\Delta_{m,0,L}^{N,j}\le\Delta_L\) satisfying

```math
\sinh((\Delta_L+2\delta_{tail})/2)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
```

Without one of these normalized-range sources, the minimal-edge route remains
parked at the same-law marginal crossing obstruction.

## 43. Small-Coupling Sinkhorn Range Reduction

Section 42 parked the proof at a normalized range source.  This section gives
the useful finite-probability reduction: the Sinkhorn-normalized range is the
doubly centered crossing interaction plus a quadratic log-Laplace remainder.

### Definition 43.1: Endpoint Base Measures

For a fixed minimal edge and outside record, absorb constants into the
one-site endpoint measures

```math
d\nu_x^{N,j}(u\mid\zeta)
:=
{e^{A_x(u;\zeta)}d\lambda_x(u)
\over
\int e^{A_x(u';\zeta)}d\lambda_x(u')},
```

```math
d\nu_y^{N,j}(v\mid\zeta)
:=
{e^{A_y(v;\zeta)}d\lambda_y(v)
\over
\int e^{A_y(v';\zeta)}d\lambda_y(v')}.
```

For \(W=W_{xy,0}^{N,j}(\cdot,\cdot;\zeta)\), define

```math
\bar W_y(u):=\int W(u,v)d\nu_y(v\mid\zeta),
\qquad
\bar W_x(v):=\int W(u,v)d\nu_x(u\mid\zeta),
```

and

```math
\bar W:=\iint W(u,v)d\nu_x(u\mid\zeta)d\nu_y(v\mid\zeta).
```

The doubly centered crossing part is

```math
W^{dc}(u,v)
:=
W(u,v)-\bar W_y(u)-\bar W_x(v)+\bar W.
```

Set

```math
\Theta_{dc,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v} W^{dc}(u,v).
```

Also define the one-line coupling width

```math
\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\max\left\{
\sup_u\operatorname{osc}_v W(u,v),
\sup_v\operatorname{osc}_u W(u,v)
\right\}.
```

All expectations are conditional expectations under the same minimal-edge
endpoint records; no reference law is introduced.

### Lemma 43.2: Finite Log-Laplace Remainder

Let \(Z\) be any bounded scalar record under any probability law.  If
\(\operatorname{osc} Z\le\omega\), then

```math
0\le \log\mathbb E e^Z-\mathbb E Z\le{\omega^2\over8}.
```

Proof.

The lower bound is Jensen.  The upper bound is Hoeffding's finite
log-Laplace lemma after shifting \(Z\) to an interval of length \(\omega\).
Equivalently, among variables supported in an interval of length \(\omega\)
with fixed mean, the exponential moment is maximized by a two-endpoint law,
and the resulting centered log moment is at most \(\omega^2/8\). `square`

### Lemma 43.3: Exact Doubly Centered Expansion

For the minimal edge,

```math
C_0^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
=
W^{dc}(u,v)-r_y(u)-r_x(v)+c_{dc}(\zeta),
```

where

```math
r_y(u)
:=
\log\int e^{W(u,v)}d\nu_y(v\mid\zeta)-\bar W_y(u),
```

```math
r_x(v)
:=
\log\int e^{W(u,v)}d\nu_x(u\mid\zeta)-\bar W_x(v),
```

and \(c_{dc}(\zeta)\) is independent of \(u,v\).

Proof.

Rewrite \(F_y\) and \(F_x\) from Definition 41.1 using the normalized
measures \(\nu_y\) and \(\nu_x\).  Their one-site normalizing constants are
absorbed into \(c_{dc}(\zeta)\).  Then

```math
F_y(u)=\log\int e^{W(u,v)}d\nu_y(v\mid\zeta)+\mathrm{const},
```

and similarly for \(F_x\).  Substitute these two identities into
\(C_0^m=W-F_y-F_x+c_0\), add and subtract
\(\bar W_y(u)\), \(\bar W_x(v)\), and \(\bar W\), and absorb constants into
\(c_{dc}\). `square`

### Proposition 43.4: Small-Coupling Sinkhorn Range Bound

For every finite row,

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
\le
\Theta_{dc,0}^{N,j}
+
{(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j})^2\over4}.
```

Proof.

By Lemma 43.2, for each fixed \(u\),

```math
0\le r_y(u)\le {(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j})^2\over8},
```

and for each fixed \(v\),

```math
0\le r_x(v)\le {(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j})^2\over8}.
```

Therefore
\(\operatorname{osc} r_y\le(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j})^2/8\) and
\(\operatorname{osc} r_x\le(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j})^2/8\).  Lemma 43.3
then gives

```math
\operatorname{osc} C_0^m
\le
\operatorname{osc}W^{dc}
+\operatorname{osc}r_y
+\operatorname{osc}r_x
\le
\operatorname{osc}W^{dc}
+{(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j})^2\over4}.
```

Taking the essential supremum over \(x,y,\zeta\) proves the claim. `square`

### Definition 43.5: Doubly Centered Minimal Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-DCENTER(Theta,omega,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\Theta_{dc,0}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}\le\omega,
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

This is a purely finite same-law source: it controls the true mixed part of
the crossing kernel and the one-line coupling width.

### Corollary 43.6: Doubly Centered Closure Test

Assume `P23-RPF-MIN-DCENTER(Theta,omega,kappa)`.  If

```math
\sinh\left({\Theta+\omega^2/4\over2}\right)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Proposition 43.4 gives `P23-RPF-MIN-SINK(Theta+omega^2/4)`.  Apply
Corollary 42.8. `square`

### Theorem 43.7: Current-Corpus Small-Coupling Verdict

The small-coupling Sinkhorn reduction is proved as finite same-law
probability algebra:

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
\le
\Theta_{dc,0}^{N,j}
+
{(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j})^2\over4}.
```

The current corpus does not prove the cofinal source
`P23-RPF-MIN-DCENTER(Theta,omega,kappa)` with constants satisfying the
Corollary 43.6 margin.

Proof.

Definitions 43.1 and 43.5 are finite conditional expectations under the
same minimal-edge endpoint law.  Lemmas 43.2 and 43.3 prove the only new
probability input, and Proposition 43.4 gives the reduction.

What remains missing is source data for the actual adaptive residual law:
a bound on the doubly centered crossing oscillation
\(\Theta_{dc,0}^{N,j}\), a bound on the one-line coupling width
\(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}\), and the already declared Peter-Weyl tail
\(\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\).  The previous papers provide finite row
decidability and several unrelated heat-kernel/Peter-Weyl tail ledgers, but
not this adaptive residual endpoint source.  Sections 28--33 show that it is
not implied by the closed non-RPF ledgers. `square`

### Corollary 43.8: Next Exact Source

The next theorem should be attempted in the following strict order:

1. prove `P23-RPF-MIN-DCENTER(Theta,omega,kappa)` with
   \[
   \sinh\left((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2\right)+\kappa
   <
   {e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4};
   \]
2. if that fails, prove `P23-RPF-MIN-SINK(Theta')` directly;
3. if both fail, return to the finite Peter-Weyl route
   `P23-RPF-MIN-MARG-PW`.

This is the first place where a genuinely small coupling theorem could close
the minimal-edge Branch-A route without paying the atom-sum factor-three loss.

## 44. One-Line And Mixed-Difference Source Audit

Section 43 reduced the normalized marginal source to three quantities:
\(\Theta_{dc,0}\), \(\omega_{\parallel,0}\), and \(\Kappa_{0,L}\).  This
section prints the finite atom tables that control the first two.  The result
is conservative but exact: one-line widths control
\(\omega_{\parallel,0}\), and mixed finite differences control
\(\Theta_{dc,0}\) with a safe factor two.

### Definition 44.1: One-Line Atom Width Table

For each crossing atom
\(A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\), define

```math
\omega_{\parallel}(A;x,y)
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{\zeta}
\max\left\{
\sup_u\operatorname{osc}_v
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta}),
\sup_v\operatorname{osc}_u
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta})
\right\}.
```

The safe one-line table is

```math
\overline\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\omega_{\parallel}(A;x,y).
```

This table is finite for every fixed row.

### Lemma 44.2: One-Line Atom Width Controls Endpoint Width

For every finite row,

```math
\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}
\le
\overline\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

The crossing kernel is the finite sum

```math
W_{xy,0}^{N,j}
=
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta}).
```

Taking a one-line oscillation of a finite sum is bounded by the sum of the
one-line oscillations.  Supremizing over \(u\)-lines, \(v\)-lines, outside
records, and endpoint pairs gives the claim. `square`

### Definition 44.3: Mixed Finite-Difference Atom Table

For each crossing atom \(A\), define its endpoint mixed finite-difference
diameter

```math
\delta_{\square}(A;x,y)
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{u,u',v,v',\zeta}
\left|
\Phi_A(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta})
+\Phi_A(\omega_A^{u',v',\zeta})
-\Phi_A(\omega_A^{u,v',\zeta})
-\Phi_A(\omega_A^{u',v,\zeta})
\right|.
```

The safe mixed-difference table is

```math
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\delta_{\square}(A;x,y).
```

### Lemma 44.4: Atom Mixed Differences Control Kernel Mixed Odds

For every finite row,

```math
D_{\square,0}^{N,j}
\le
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

The mixed difference of \(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}\) is the sum of the mixed
differences of the atoms in
\({\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\).  Taking absolute values and applying
the triangle inequality gives the bound for each \(x,y,\zeta\).  Supremizing
gives the displayed inequality. `square`

### Lemma 44.5: Mixed Differences Control Double-Centered Oscillation

For every finite row,

```math
\Theta_{dc,0}^{N,j}
\le
2D_{\square,0}^{N,j}
\le
2\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

For fixed \(x,y,\zeta\), write \(W=W_{xy,0}^{N,j}\).  By Definition 43.1,

```math
W^{dc}(u,v)
=
\iint
\left[
W(u,v)+W(u',v')
-W(u,v')-W(u',v)
\right]
d\nu_x(u')d\nu_y(v').
```

The integrand is a mixed finite difference of \(W\), hence has absolute
value at most \(D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\).  Therefore
\(|W^{dc}(u,v)|\le D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\) for every \(u,v\), and
\(\operatorname{osc}W^{dc}\le2D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\).  Taking the essential
supremum over \(x,y,\zeta\) gives the first inequality.  The second is Lemma
44.4. `square`

### Definition 44.6: Mixed-Line Minimal Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-MIXLINE(D,omega,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\le D,
\qquad
\overline\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}\le\omega,
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

This is the atom-level finite source behind
`P23-RPF-MIN-DCENTER`.

### Corollary 44.7: Mixed-Line Closure Test

Assume `P23-RPF-MIN-MIXLINE(D,omega,kappa)`.  If

```math
\sinh\left({2D+\omega^2/4\over2}\right)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Lemmas 44.2 and 44.5 give

```math
\Theta_{dc,0}^{N,j}\le2D,
\qquad
\omega_{\parallel,0}^{N,j}\le\omega.
```

Thus `P23-RPF-MIN-DCENTER(2D,omega,kappa)` holds.  Apply Corollary 43.6.
`square`

### Proposition 44.8: Current-Corpus Mixed-Line Verdict

The current corpus proves that the one-line and mixed-difference tables are
finite same-law row tables.  It does not prove cofinal constants
\((D,\omega,\kappa)\) satisfying the Corollary 44.7 margin.

Proof.

Definitions 44.1 and 44.3 use only the already printed atom functions
\(\Phi_A^{N,j}\) on the same pushed-forward scalar law.  Lemmas 44.2--44.5
are finite algebra and triangle inequalities.

What is not supplied by Papers 16, 20, 21, 22, or the earlier sections of
Paper 23 is a cofinal estimate on the one-line atom widths
\(\omega_{\parallel}(A;x,y)\), the mixed finite differences
\(\delta_{\square}(A;x,y)\), or the Peter-Weyl tail \(\Kappa_{0,L}\) in this
actual adaptive residual endpoint law.  Sections 28--33 again show why these
bounds are not consequences of the closed non-RPF ledgers alone: residual
tail completions can create live endpoint mixed variation while preserving
those ledgers. `square`

### Corollary 44.9: Next Exact Source

The next source should be attempted as

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}MIXLINE}(D,\omega,\kappa)
```

with the Corollary 44.7 margin.  If the factor two in Lemma 44.5 is too
expensive, a sharper future theorem must prove a signed/range improvement
from mixed finite differences to \(\Theta_{dc,0}\); it cannot be assumed from
mixed odds alone.

## 45. Anchored Endpoint-Gauge Mixed Source

Section 44 charged one-line widths and mixed finite differences separately.
That is safe, but it pays endpoint-additive variation that the normalized
marginal \(C_0^m\) never sees.  This section removes that surcharge by
choosing a deterministic endpoint gauge.  The key point is that, after
anchoring, the mixed finite-difference table controls both the doubly
centered oscillation and the one-line Hoeffding width.

### Definition 45.1: Endpoint Anchor Gauge

For every finite row, endpoint pair \(x,y\), and outside record \(\zeta\),
choose deterministic reference endpoints

```math
u_\star=u_\star(x,\zeta),
\qquad
v_\star=v_\star(y,\zeta).
```

In a compact group battery one may take the identity element; in a finite
enumerated battery one may take the first element in the declared scalar
ordering.  The choice is made before evaluating the law and introduces no
new random record.

For each crossing atom
\(A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\), write

```math
G_A(u,v;\zeta):=\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta}).
```

Define the anchored mixed representative

```math
G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}(u,v;\zeta)
:=
G_A(u,v;\zeta)
-G_A(u,v_\star;\zeta)
-G_A(u_\star,v;\zeta)
+G_A(u_\star,v_\star;\zeta).
```

Thus

```math
G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}(u,v_\star;\zeta)=0,
\qquad
G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}(u_\star,v;\zeta)=0.
```

The anchored minimal crossing kernel is

```math
W_{xy,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
:=
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}(u,v;\zeta).
```

### Lemma 45.2: Endpoint Gauge Does Not Change The Two-Site Law

Replacing \(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}\) by
\(W_{xy,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}\) and absorbing the removed endpoint terms into
\(A_x\) and \(A_y\) leaves the two-site conditional law and the normalized
marginal \(C_0^m\) unchanged.

Proof.

For each atom,

```math
G_A(u,v)
=
G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}(u,v)
+G_A(u,v_\star)
+G_A(u_\star,v)
-G_A(u_\star,v_\star).
```

The second term is a function only of \(u\), the third only of \(v\), and the
last is independent of \(u,v\).  Summing over \(A\) therefore rewrites the
same endpoint Hamiltonian as

```math
H_{xy}^{min}
=
A_x^{\mathrm{anc}}(u;\zeta)
+A_y^{\mathrm{anc}}(v;\zeta)
+A_0^{\mathrm{anc}}(\zeta)
+W_{xy,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}(u,v;\zeta).
```

The total Hamiltonian is identical pointwise.  Hence the two-site
conditional density is identical.  Lemma 41.2 is invariant under one-site
endpoint additions, so \(C_0^m\) is also unchanged. `square`

### Lemma 45.3: Anchoring Kills Exactly Endpoint-Additive Atoms

For a fixed atom and fixed outside record, the following pointwise
conditions are equivalent:

1. \(G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}\equiv0\);
2. \(G_A(u,v)=a(u)+b(v)+c\) for some endpoint functions \(a,b\) and scalar
   \(c\);
3. every endpoint mixed finite difference of \(G_A(\cdot,\cdot;\zeta)\)
   vanishes.

Consequently the table value \(\delta_\square(A;x,y)\) is zero exactly when
these equivalent conditions hold for almost every outside record in the
essential supremum defining \(\delta_\square\).

Proof.

If \(G_A=a(u)+b(v)+c\), the anchored four-term expression cancels
identically.  Conversely, if \(G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}\equiv0\), then

```math
G_A(u,v)
=
G_A(u,v_\star)+G_A(u_\star,v)-G_A(u_\star,v_\star),
```

which is endpoint-additive.  The equivalence with vanishing mixed finite
differences is the same four-point identity with arbitrary
\((u,u',v,v')\); choosing \((u',v')=(u_\star,v_\star)\) gives the anchored
form, while endpoint-additive functions have all mixed finite differences
zero.  Taking the essential supremum over outside records gives the final
statement about \(\delta_\square(A;x,y)\). `square`

### Definition 45.4: Anchored Mixed Census

For every finite row, define the same-law mixed census

```math
{\mathcal C}_{mix,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
:=
\left\{
\left(A,\delta_\square(A;x,y),G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}\right):
A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
\right\}.
```

Classify an atom as:

| class | condition | charged role |
| --- | --- | --- |
| endpoint-additive | \(\delta_\square(A;x,y)=0\) | absorbed into \(A_x,A_y,A_0\) |
| genuinely mixed | \(\delta_\square(A;x,y)>0\) | charged through \(G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}\) |

The safe anchored mixed table is the same mixed table from Section 44:

```math
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\delta_{\square}(A;x,y).
```

### Lemma 45.5: Mixed Differences Control Anchored One-Line Width

For every finite row,

```math
\omega_{\parallel,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}
\le
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j},
```

where \(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}\) is the one-line coupling
width of \(W_{xy,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}\).

Proof.

For each atom and fixed \(u\),

```math
G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}(u,v)-G_A^{\mathrm{anc}}(u,v')
=
G_A(u,v)-G_A(u,v')-G_A(u_\star,v)+G_A(u_\star,v'),
```

which is a mixed finite difference of \(G_A\).  Hence its absolute value is
at most \(\delta_\square(A;x,y)\).  Supremizing over \(v,v'\) gives the
one-line \(v\)-oscillation bound.  The \(u\)-line bound is identical.  Sum
over atoms and take the essential supremum over \(x,y,\zeta\). `square`

### Lemma 45.6: Mixed Differences Control Anchored Double Centering

For every finite row,

```math
\Theta_{dc,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}
\le
2\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

Endpoint anchoring subtracts one-site functions and constants from
\(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}\), so the mixed finite-difference diameter of
\(W_{xy,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}\) is the same as that of
\(W_{xy,0}^{N,j}\).  Lemma 44.5 applied in the anchored gauge gives the
claim. `square`

### Definition 45.7: Anchored Mixed Minimal Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-ANCHMIX(D,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\le D,
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

It is a sharper source than `P23-RPF-MIN-MIXLINE`: the one-line width is no
longer an independent input, because Lemma 45.5 supplies
\(\omega\le D\) in the anchored gauge.

### Corollary 45.8: Anchored Mixed Closure Test

Assume `P23-RPF-MIN-ANCHMIX(D,kappa)`.  If

```math
\sinh\left({2D+D^2/4\over2}\right)+\kappa
<
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

By Lemmas 45.5 and 45.6,

```math
\Theta_{dc,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}\le2D,
\qquad
\omega_{\parallel,0}^{\mathrm{anc},N,j}\le D.
```

Lemma 45.2 leaves the normalized marginal \(C_0^m\) unchanged, so
Proposition 43.4 may be applied in the anchored gauge.  The Peter-Weyl tail
\(\Kappa_{0,L}\) is attached to the unchanged normalized marginal table, so
its bound is not altered by the endpoint gauge.  Therefore the hypotheses of
Corollary 43.6 are satisfied with \((\Theta,\omega,\kappa)=(2D,D,\kappa)\),
and the result follows. `square`

### Proposition 45.9: Current-Corpus Anchored Mixed Verdict

The endpoint-additive surcharge is now closed: it does not need to be paid in
the minimal-edge source.  The current corpus still does not prove the cofinal
anchored mixed source `P23-RPF-MIN-ANCHMIX(D,kappa)` with constants satisfying
Corollary 45.8.

Proof.

Definitions 45.1 and 45.4 are finite same-law constructions.  Lemma 45.2 is
exact Hamiltonian bookkeeping on the same conditional law, not a change of
process.  Lemma 45.3 proves that all endpoint-additive crossing atoms are
absorbed into one-site weights.  Lemmas 45.5 and 45.6 show that the only
remaining finite table to bound is the mixed finite-difference table
\(\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\), together with the existing Peter-Weyl tail
\(\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\).

What remains missing is quantitative: Papers 16, 20, 21, 22, and the earlier
sections of Paper 23 do not provide a cofinal bound
\(\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\le D\) small enough for Corollary 45.8, nor
do they provide the corresponding \(\Kappa_{0,L}\) tail bound in this actual
adaptive minimal-edge residual law.  The residual-tail countermodels of
Sections 28--33 still apply after anchoring: they can carry genuinely mixed
four-point variation rather than endpoint-additive variation. `square`

### Corollary 45.10: Next Exact Source

The next source is now the two-constant theorem

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}ANCHMIX}(D,\kappa),
```

with the Corollary 45.8 scalar margin.  If this fails because the factor
\(2D\) in Lemma 45.6 is too expensive, the only sharper continuation is a
signed/range theorem for
\(\Theta_{dc,0}^{\mathrm{anc}}\) itself, not another endpoint-additive
quotient.

## 46. Anchored Budget And Tail Split

Section 45 leaves a two-constant source:

```math
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\le D,
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\le\kappa.
```

This section turns the scalar margin into an explicit budget.  The point is
to know, before doing more finite-table work, how much mixed four-point
variation can actually be spent.

### Definition 46.1: Anchored Edge Budget

Set

```math
B_*^{edge}
:=
{e^{-h_{path}}\over1+B_{edge}C_{path}/4}.
```

This is the right side of the Section-45 anchored closure inequality.  It is
already a same-law edge-path constant from Definition 36.5; no new process or
continuum input is introduced.

For \(0\le\kappa<B_*^{edge}\), define

```math
D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa)
:=
-4+
\sqrt{
16+8\,\operatorname{arsinh}(B_*^{edge}-\kappa)
}.
```

If \(\kappa\ge B_*^{edge}\), set \(D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa):=0\) and mark
the anchored mixed route as scalar-budget blocked.

### Lemma 46.2: Exact Anchored Scalar Budget

For \(D\ge0\) and \(\kappa\ge0\), the Section-45 scalar condition

```math
\sinh\left({2D+D^2/4\over2}\right)+\kappa
<
B_*^{edge}
```

holds if and only if

```math
0\le\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
0\le D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa).
```

Proof.

The function

```math
D\longmapsto {2D+D^2/4\over2}
=D+{D^2\over8}
```

is strictly increasing on \(D\ge0\), and \(\sinh\) is strictly increasing.
Thus the inequality is equivalent to

```math
D+{D^2\over8}
<
\operatorname{arsinh}(B_*^{edge}-\kappa),
```

which already requires \(\kappa<B_*^{edge}\).  Multiplying by \(8\) and
solving the quadratic inequality

```math
D^2+8D
<
8\,\operatorname{arsinh}(B_*^{edge}-\kappa)
```

gives the positive root displayed in Definition 46.1. `square`

### Definition 46.3: Minimal Tail Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)` asserts that there is a cofinal Peter-Weyl cutoff
schedule \(L=L(N,j)\) such that

```math
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\Kappa_{0,L(N,j)}^{N,j}
\le
\kappa.
```

This is the minimal-edge normalized-tail source from Sections 41--45,
separated from the mixed four-point table.

### Definition 46.4: Anchored Mixed Diameter Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-DMIX(D)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\le D.
```

With this notation,

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}ANCHMIX}(D,\kappa)
```

is exactly

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}DMIX}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

### Corollary 46.5: Budget-Split Closure Criterion

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}DMIX}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

If

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa),
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Definitions 46.3 and 46.4 give
`P23-RPF-MIN-ANCHMIX(D,kappa)`.  Lemma 46.2 is exactly the scalar condition
in Corollary 45.8. `square`

### Proposition 46.6: Current-Corpus Budget Verdict

The scalar part of the anchored mixed route is now fully explicit.  The
current corpus does not prove either live quantitative subsource:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}DMIX}(D),
\qquad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa),
```

with \(D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa)\).

Proof.

Lemma 46.2 is pure scalar algebra.  Definitions 46.3 and 46.4 are the two
finite same-law quantities already isolated in Sections 42--45.  No previous
paper supplies a cofinal bound on the actual minimal-edge Peter-Weyl tail
\(\Kappa_{0,L}\) for this normalized residual law, and no previous paper
supplies a cofinal small bound on the anchored mixed finite-difference sum
\(\overline D_{\square,0}\).  The residual-tail countermodels of Sections
28--33 still permit arbitrary genuinely mixed endpoint variation unless a
new same-law source rules it out. `square`

### Corollary 46.7: Next Work Item

The next finite table is not another scalar inequality.  It is the anchored
mixed census deciding and bounding

```math
\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}
=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_A \delta_\square(A;x,y).
```

The Peter-Weyl tail may be attacked in parallel, but without a
`MIN-DMIX` bound below \(D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa)\), no tail improvement can
close the anchored minimal-edge route.

## 47. Anchored Mixed Census Table

Section 46 splits the problem into a tail source and a mixed-diameter source.
This section prints the exact finite row table for the mixed-diameter side.
It decides which actual Möbius crossing atoms contribute nonzero anchored
mixed variation.

### Definition 47.1: Exact Anchored Mixed Row Table

For each finite adaptive row, each rooted candidate edge \(e=(x,y)\), and
each outside record \(\zeta\), define the row table

| field | value |
| --- | --- |
| atom | \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\) |
| raw atom function | \(G_A(u,v;\zeta)=\Phi_A^{N,j}(\omega_A^{u,v,\zeta})\) |
| anchored representative | \(G_A^{anc}(u,v;\zeta)\) |
| mixed diameter | \(\delta_\square(A;x,y)\) |
| zero flag | \(z_A=1_{\{\delta_\square(A;x,y)=0\}}\) |
| active mixed flag | \(m_A=1_{\{\delta_\square(A;x,y)>0\}}\) |

The active anchored mixed set is

```math
{\mathcal U}_{mix,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
:=
\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y):
\delta_\square(A;x,y)>0\}.
```

The exact row value is

```math
D_{mix,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{mix,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\delta_\square(A;x,y).
```

By construction \(D_{mix,0}^{N,j}=\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\), but the
new notation emphasizes that only active mixed atoms are charged.

### Lemma 47.2: Same-Law Finite Decidability

For every fixed finite adaptive row, the table in Definition 47.1 is a
same-law finite row table.  In particular, the predicate

```math
\delta_\square(A;x,y)>0
```

is decidable on the same pushed-forward scalar law.

Proof.

The atom list \({\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\) is finite by Section 40.
Each \(G_A\) is the scalar Möbius coefficient function already printed in
Sections 15 and 40, evaluated on the same exact-CE pushed-forward law.  The
anchor operation of Definition 45.1 uses deterministic endpoint choices and
finite arithmetic.  The mixed diameter is a finite supremum in a finite
battery, or a compact essential supremum in the compact finite-battery
presentation already allowed in Lemma 42.2.  Hence the zero and active flags
are finite scalar decisions on the same row. `square`

### Lemma 47.3: Zero Rows Carry No Debit

Atoms with \(z_A=1\) do not contribute to \(C_0^m\), to
\(\Theta_{dc,0}^{anc}\), or to \(\omega_{\parallel,0}^{anc}\) except through
endpoint one-site weights already absorbed in Lemma 45.2.

Proof.

If \(z_A=1\), Lemma 45.3 gives
\(G_A^{anc}\equiv0\) almost surely in the outside record.  Thus the anchored
representative contributes nothing to \(W_{xy,0}^{anc}\).  The removed part is
endpoint-additive and has already been absorbed into \(A_x,A_y,A_0\), which
does not change \(C_0^m\) by Lemma 45.2. `square`

### Definition 47.4: Mixed Census Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-MIXCENSUS(D)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
D_{mix,0}^{N,j}\le D.
```

Equivalently, since \(D_{mix,0}^{N,j}=\overline D_{\square,0}^{N,j}\), this
is `P23-RPF-MIN-DMIX(D)` with the active mixed atoms explicitly printed.

### Corollary 47.5: Census Closure Test

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}MIXCENSUS}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

If

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa),
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Definition 47.4 is Definition 46.4 with zero rows removed.  Apply Corollary
46.5. `square`

### Proposition 47.6: Current-Corpus Mixed Census Verdict

The current corpus proves finite row decidability of the anchored mixed
census.  It does not prove the cofinal numerical bound

```math
D_{mix,0}^{N,j}<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa).
```

Proof.

Lemma 47.2 closes the finite-table and nonzero-decision part.  Lemma 47.3
closes the no-debit status of endpoint-additive rows.  What remains is not
logical decidability but quantitative smallness of the active mixed row sum.
The earlier residual-tail countermodels can place small or large genuinely
mixed four-point variation into active atoms while preserving the already
closed non-RPF ledgers.  Therefore the table is printed, but the pass/fail
value of its cofinal supremum is still a source theorem:
`P23-RPF-MIN-MIXCENSUS(D)`. `square`

### Corollary 47.7: Next Exact Source

The live anchored minimal-edge route is now:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}MIXCENSUS}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
```

with

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa).
```

If the census bound fails only because the triangle sum over active mixed
atoms is too expensive, the next route must bound the signed anchored sum
\(W_{xy,0}^{anc}\) or \(\Theta_{dc,0}^{anc}\) directly.  Another zero-row
census cannot improve the already exact endpoint-additive quotient.

## 48. Minimal Peter-Weyl Tail Audit

Section 47 left two live quantities:

```math
D_{mix,0}^{N,j},
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}.
```

This section audits the cheaper one first.  The tail can be set to zero only
when the minimal endpoint scalar battery is complete at a finite Peter-Weyl
cutoff, or when the normalized minimal-edge table is actually bandlimited on
the same pushed-forward law.  Otherwise \(\kappa\) is a genuine source, not a
notation problem.

### Definition 48.1: Minimal Tail-Zero Certificate

`P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL0(L0)` asserts that, cofinally, the two-endpoint
Peter-Weyl cutoff \(\Pi_{\le L_0}^{xy}\) is exact for the normalized
minimal-edge endpoint table:

```math
\Pi_{\le L_0}^{xy}C_0^{m,N,j}
=
C_0^{m,N,j},
\qquad
\Kappa_{0,L_0}^{N,j}=0.
```

This includes the truly finite-complete endpoint battery case, where
\(\Pi_{\le L_0}^{xy}\) is the identity on the declared scalar endpoint
battery.  It also includes a nontrivial bandlimited row, but only if that
bandlimit is proved on the actual adaptive pushed-forward law.

### Lemma 48.2: Tail-Zero Certificate Closes `KTAIL(0)`

If `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL0(L0)` holds, then

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(0)
```

holds.

Proof.

Take the cofinal cutoff schedule \(L(N,j)=L_0\).  The second clause of
Definition 48.1 gives \(\Kappa_{0,L_0}^{N,j}=0\) cofinally, hence the
limsup in Definition 46.3 is zero. `square`

### Definition 48.3: Minimal Quantitative Tail Certificate

For \(\kappa\ge0\), `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL-BD(kappa)` asserts that there is a
cofinal cutoff schedule \(L=L(N,j)\) such that

```math
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\Kappa_{0,L(N,j)}^{N,j}
\le
\kappa.
```

This is the same assertion as `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)`, but the `BD`
notation will be used when the source is supplied by an explicit finite
Peter-Weyl tail estimate rather than by exact finite completeness.

### Lemma 48.4: Rowwise Decidability Is Not Cofinal Tail Control

For every fixed finite adaptive row, the value of
\(\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\) at any declared finite cutoff \(L\) is a same-law
finite row quantity.  This does not, by itself, prove
`P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)` for any useful \(\kappa\).

Proof.

The tail \(\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}\) is part of the normalized minimal table of
Section 42 and is evaluated on the same pushed-forward scalar row.  Thus it
is rowwise finite once the row and cutoff are fixed.

The cofinal source, however, asks for a cutoff schedule with a limsup bound
along the adaptive branch.  A collection of rowwise finite values gives no
uniform/cofinal tail estimate unless one also proves finite completeness,
bandlimiting, or a quantitative decay theorem for the actual adaptive
normalized residual law. `square`

### Proposition 48.5: Current-Corpus Tail Verdict

The current corpus does not justify setting \(\kappa=0\) for the minimal
endpoint route, except conditionally under `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL0(L0)`.
Nor does it supply a nonzero quantitative bound
`P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL-BD(kappa)` small enough for the Section-46 budget.

Proof.

Papers 16, 20, 21, 22, and the earlier sections of Paper 23 contain several
finite-battery and Peter-Weyl bookkeeping tools, but the normalized minimal
edge \(C_0^m\) here is the actual adaptive residual endpoint law after
exact-CE division and after the endpoint gauge.  The already printed sources
do not prove that this table is finite-complete at a fixed cutoff, and they
do not print a cofinal decay estimate for \(\Kappa_{0,L}\) in this table.

Thus the cheap tail audit is closed: \(\kappa=0\) is available only under the
explicit certificate of Definition 48.1; otherwise `MIN-KTAIL(kappa)` remains
a live same-law source. `square`

### Corollary 48.6: Tail-First Reduction

If `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL0(L0)` is later supplied, the anchored census route
reduces to the single inequality

```math
D_{mix,0}^{N,j}
<
D_{\mathrm{crit}}(0)
```

cofinally.  Without that certificate, every census bound must be paired with
the tail budget

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa).
```

## 49. True-Bridge Mixed Census

Section 47 printed the exact active mixed census.  This section refines the
row labels so the table distinguishes support/topology zeros from true
bridges.  The goal is not to prove smallness yet; it is to ensure that the
only rows charged in \(D_{mix,0}\) are genuinely two-endpoint rows.

### Definition 49.1: Endpoint Visibility And True-Bridge Flags

For an anchored atom \(G_A^{anc}\), define the endpoint visibility flags

```math
\nu_x(A;x,y)
:=
1_{\{\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{v,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_u G_A^{anc}(u,v;\zeta)>0\}},
```

```math
\nu_y(A;x,y)
:=
1_{\{\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{u,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_v G_A^{anc}(u,v;\zeta)>0\}}.
```

Define the true-bridge flag

```math
\beta_A(x,y)
:=
1_{\{\delta_\square(A;x,y)>0\}}.
```

The corresponding row classes are:

| class | condition |
| --- | --- |
| endpoint-blind | \(\nu_x=0\) or \(\nu_y=0\) |
| endpoint-additive | \(\nu_x=\nu_y=1\) but \(\delta_\square=0\) |
| true bridge | \(\beta_A=1\) |

The true-bridge set is

```math
{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
:=
\{A\in{\mathcal U}_{cross,0}^{N,j}(x,y):\beta_A(x,y)=1\}.
```

### Lemma 49.2: Endpoint-Blind And Endpoint-Additive Rows Are Zero

If \(A\) is endpoint-blind or endpoint-additive, then

```math
\delta_\square(A;x,y)=0.
```

Proof.

If \(A\) is endpoint-blind, then \(G_A^{anc}\) is independent of one of the
two endpoint variables.  Every mixed finite difference in \(u,u',v,v'\)
therefore cancels.  If \(A\) is endpoint-additive, Lemma 45.3 gives the same
conclusion. `square`

### Lemma 49.3: True Bridges Are Exactly Active Mixed Rows

For every finite adaptive row,

```math
{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
=
{\mathcal U}_{mix,0}^{N,j}(x,y).
```

Consequently

```math
D_{br,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\delta_\square(A;x,y)
=
D_{mix,0}^{N,j}.
```

Proof.

Both sets are defined by the same condition
\(\delta_\square(A;x,y)>0\).  Lemma 49.2 explains why the complementary
finite-table labels carry no mixed debit. `square`

### Definition 49.4: True-Bridge Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE(D)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
D_{br,0}^{N,j}\le D.
```

By Lemma 49.3 this is equivalent to `P23-RPF-MIN-MIXCENSUS(D)`, but the
bridge notation will be used when the proof proceeds by support/topology
classification rather than by direct numeric evaluation of every atom.

### Corollary 49.5: True-Bridge Closure Test

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGE}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

If

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa),
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Lemma 49.3 identifies `MIN-BRIDGE(D)` with `MIN-MIXCENSUS(D)`.  Apply
Corollary 47.5. `square`

### Proposition 49.6: Current-Corpus True-Bridge Verdict

The current corpus proves that the true-bridge table is finite and that
endpoint-blind or endpoint-additive rows carry no debit.  It does not prove a
cofinal bridge-amplitude bound small enough for the Section-46 budget.

Proof.

Definitions 49.1 and 49.4 are finite same-law row definitions.  Lemmas 49.2
and 49.3 close the structural zero tests.  What remains is the size of the
true-bridge amplitudes
\(\delta_\square(A;x,y)\) on the actual adaptive residual law.  The
residual-tail countermodels of Sections 28--33 can carry genuinely mixed
four-point variation on true bridges while preserving the closed non-RPF
ledgers.  Hence bridge classification is closed, but bridge smallness is a
new source:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGE}(D).
```

`square`

### Corollary 49.7: Next Exact Source

The live minimal-edge source package is now

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGE}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
```

with

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa).
```

If this bridge triangle sum is too large, the next meaningful route is not a
finer zero classification.  It is the signed anchored range source

```math
\Theta_{dc,0}^{anc}\le\Theta
```

for the full sum \(W_{xy,0}^{anc}\), paired with the same `MIN-KTAIL`
source.

## 50. True-Bridge Amplitude Source Audit

Section 49 identifies the exact rows that still matter.  This section asks
whether their amplitudes can be sourced directly, rather than merely counted.
The rule remains the same-law rule: every quantity below is evaluated under
the actual adaptive `SEL2` pushed-forward scalar law, after the deterministic
anchor gauge of Section 45 and before any off-record replacement by a cleaner
law.

### Definition 50.1: Bridge Amplitude Table

For \(A\in{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\), define the printed bridge
amplitude

```math
d_A^{br}(x,y):=\delta_\square(A;x,y).
```

The rowwise bridge-amplitude table is

```math
{\mathcal T}_{br}^{N,j}
:=
\left\{
\left(A,x,y,d_A^{br}(x,y)\right):
A\in{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
\right\}.
```

For any finite row this table is a finite same-law object: the entries are
obtained by taking the same four-point mixed oscillation of the literal
anchored interaction \(G_A^{anc}\) that defines the true-bridge flag.

### Definition 50.2: Bridge-Amplitude Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGEAMP(D)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
d_A^{br}(x,y)
\le D.
```

Thus `BRIDGEAMP(D)` is the amplitude-evaluation form of
`MIN-BRIDGE(D)`.  The point of the new name is proof discipline: a future
argument must either print the amplitudes or dominate them on the same law,
not merely relabel the active rows.

### Lemma 50.3: Bridge-Amplitude Equivalence

For every \(D\ge0\),

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGEAMP}(D)
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGE}(D).
```

Proof.

Definitions 49.4 and 50.2 use the same bridge set and the same summand
\(\delta_\square(A;x,y)\). `square`

### Definition 50.4: Same-Law Bridge Damping Certificate

A bridge damping certificate consists of a finite type map

```math
\tau:{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\to{\mathcal B}
```

and constants \(a_b,m_b\ge0\) such that, cofinally and uniformly in
\((x,y)\),

```math
d_A^{br}(x,y)
\le
a_{\tau(A)}\,\exp(-m_{\tau(A)}\,\ell(A)),
```

where \(\ell(A)\) is a same-law printed bridge length/separation statistic.
Let

```math
D_{\mathrm{damp}}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
a_{\tau(A)}\,\exp(-m_{\tau(A)}\,\ell(A)).
```

`P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGEDAMP(D)` asserts the existence of such a certificate with
\(D_{\mathrm{damp}}\le D\).

### Proposition 50.5: Positive Bridge-Damping Closure

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGEDAMP}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

If

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa),
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

`BRIDGEDAMP(D)` implies `BRIDGEAMP(D)` by Definition 50.4, hence
`MIN-BRIDGE(D)` by Lemma 50.3.  Corollary 49.5 then applies. `square`

### Lemma 50.6: Why Counting Alone Cannot Prove Bridge Damping

The finite cardinality of the bridge table, even with the canonical selector
entropy from Sections 23--25, does not imply `BRIDGEDAMP(D)` for any useful
strict \(D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa)\).

Proof.

Cardinality controls how many rows are charged.  It does not control the
same-law mixed oscillation of a nonzero row.  The residual-tail completions
of Sections 28--33 can preserve the same closed non-RPF ledgers and the same
finite row labels while assigning an \(O(1)\) mixed four-point amplitude to a
surviving bridge row.  Therefore a damping statement requires new numerical
information about the actual pushed-forward scalar law, such as a conditional
spectral gap, a literal decay theorem, or a signed cancellation theorem.  It
cannot be inferred from finite labeling alone. `square`

### Proposition 50.7: Current-Corpus Bridge-Amplitude Verdict

The current corpus proves the finite bridge-amplitude table row by row, but it
does not prove `P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGEDAMP(D)` with constants in the closing
range.

Proof.

Definitions 50.1 and 50.2 are finite algebra on a fixed adaptive row, so the
table exists and is decidable rowwise.  Proposition 50.5 gives the positive
same-law theorem that would close the branch.  Lemma 50.6 shows why the
existing finite entropy and selector results are insufficient: they do not
bound actual mixed amplitudes.  The previous papers supply no uniform
same-law conditional spectral gap, no same-law literal bridge-decay theorem,
and no signed bridge cancellation theorem for the actual adaptive residual
law. `square`

### Corollary 50.8: Sharp Positive Bridge Frontier

The strongest positive triangle-sum bridge route now has the form

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGEDAMP}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa),
```

with

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa).
```

If this is too expensive, the next route must use cancellation in the full
anchored sum, not another unsigned bridge census.

## 51. Signed Anchored Range Source

The bridge-amplitude route is deliberately brutal: it pays the absolute
mixed diameter of every true bridge.  The exact marginal, however, uses the
signed anchored sum.  This section records the cancellation route without
leaving the actual adaptive scalar law.

### Definition 51.1: Signed Bridge Sum

Let

```math
W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
:=
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)}
G_A^{anc}(u,v;\zeta).
```

Its doubly centered signed range is

```math
\Theta_{br,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left[
\left(W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}\right)^{dc}(u,v;\zeta)
\right],
```

and its signed one-line width is

```math
\omega_{br,0}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\max\left\{
\sup_u\operatorname{osc}_v W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}(u,v;\zeta),
\sup_v\operatorname{osc}_u W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
\right\}.
```

Both quantities are taken after summing the true bridge rows with their
actual signs.

### Lemma 51.2: Bridge Sum Equals The Mixed Part Of The Minimal Marginal

After the deterministic anchor gauge, endpoint-blind and endpoint-additive
rows contribute nothing to the doubly centered part of \(C_0^m\).  Therefore

```math
\left(C_0^m\right)^{dc}
=
\left(W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}\right)^{dc}
```

up to the Peter-Weyl tail already charged to `MIN-KTAIL`.

Proof.

Section 45 absorbs endpoint-additive pieces into the one-site and constant
terms without changing \(C_0^m\).  Lemma 49.2 shows that endpoint-blind and
endpoint-additive rows have zero mixed debit.  The remaining atoms are exactly
the true bridges by Lemma 49.3.  Projection error is precisely the tail term
isolated in Section 48. `square`

### Definition 51.3: Signed Minimal-Bridge Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED(Theta,omega,kappa)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\Theta_{br,0}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\omega_{br,0}^{N,j}\le\omega,
\qquad
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

This source is sharper than `MIN-BRIDGE(D)` when the actual bridge rows
cancel in the anchored sum.  It is not a new law: it is the same
double-centered minimal marginal calculation, evaluated before absolute-value
triangle losses.

### Proposition 51.4: Signed Closure Theorem

Assume `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED(Theta,omega,kappa)`.  If

```math
\sinh\left({\Theta+\omega^2/4\over2}\right)+\kappa
<
B_*^{edge},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

By Lemma 51.2, the finite part of the minimal marginal has doubly centered
range at most \(\Theta\) and one-line width at most \(\omega\).  The
small-coupling Sinkhorn reduction of Proposition 43.4 gives the normalized
minimal marginal range bound

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
\le
\Theta+\omega^2/4.
```

Adding the Peter-Weyl tail \(\kappa\), the edge contraction budget is exactly
the Section-46 condition

```math
\sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)+\kappa<B_*^{edge}.
```

Thus the minimal-edge spectral route closes, and hence `P23-RPF-TRANS0`
holds. `square`

### Definition 51.5: Signed Cancellation Certificate

`P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE-CANCEL(Theta,omega)` asserts the existence of a finite
same-law pairing or signed partition of the true bridge table such that the
sum of each block has doubly centered range and one-line width whose total
is bounded by \((\Theta,\omega)\).

Concretely, it consists of a finite partition
\({\mathcal P}_{br}^{N,j}(x,y)\) of \({\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\) and
block sums

```math
H_P(u,v;\zeta)
:=
\sum_{A\in P}G_A^{anc}(u,v;\zeta),
```

such that cofinally

```math
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\sum_{P\in{\mathcal P}_{br}^{N,j}(x,y)}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}(H_P^{dc})
\le\Theta,
```

and similarly the sum of the block one-line widths is at most \(\omega\).

### Corollary 51.6: Cancellation Implies Signed Source

If `P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE-CANCEL(Theta,omega)` and
`P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)` hold, then
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED(Theta,omega,kappa)` holds.  Therefore the scalar
condition of Proposition 51.4 closes `P23-RPF-TRANS0`.

Proof.

Summing the block bounds controls the signed bridge sum by the triangle
inequality at block level.  The partition is on the same bridge table and
does not change the pushed-forward law. `square`

### Proposition 51.7: Current-Corpus Signed-Source Verdict

The signed route is the sharpest remaining positive route inside adaptive
Branch A, but the current corpus does not yet prove the required signed
source.

Proof.

Sections 41--45 already prove that the exact normalized minimal marginal is
the correct object.  Section 51 removes the remaining unnecessary unsigned
atom loss by summing the true bridges with signs before taking the
doubly centered range.  This is strictly stronger than another bridge census
and remains Barandes-aligned: the only stochastic object is the actual
adaptive pushed-forward scalar law, and all conditionals are record
conditionals of that law.

However, no previous paper prints a cofinal signed bridge partition, a
same-law involution pairing bridge atoms to cancel, or a direct uniform bound
on \(\Theta_{br,0}^{N,j}\) and \(\omega_{br,0}^{N,j}\).  Thus the route is
positive and exact, but not yet unconditional. `square`

### Corollary 51.8: Terminal Paper-23 Positive Frontier

The adaptive Branch-A proof now has two exact same-law positive frontiers:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGEDAMP}(D)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
```

with

```math
\kappa<B_*^{edge},
\qquad
D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa),
```

or the sharper signed route

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED}(\Theta,\omega,\kappa)
```

with

```math
\sinh\left({\Theta+\omega^2/4\over2}\right)+\kappa
<
B_*^{edge}.
```

The first route asks for actual bridge damping.  The second asks for actual
signed cancellation or direct signed range control.  The present corpus
supplies neither numerical source, so Paper 23 has pushed adaptive Branch A
to the exact positive proof-producing theorem rather than closing it
unconditionally.

## 52. Signed-Cancellation Gate Audit

This section executes the first three signed-route tasks:

1. freeze the scalar gate;
2. print the admissible cancellation-block table;
3. test the natural same-law symmetries as candidates for
   `P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE-CANCEL(Theta,omega)`.

The conclusion is sharp: the current corpus proves the rowwise finite
cancellation extremal problem, but the obvious geometric/representation
symmetries are quotient or equality symmetries, not anti-symmetries.  They do
not prove a nontrivial signed cancellation source without an additional
same-law anti-row identity.

### Definition 52.1: Frozen Signed Gate

For \(0\le\kappa<B_*^{edge}\), set

```math
M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)
:=
2\,\operatorname{arsinh}(B_*^{edge}-\kappa).
```

The signed route closes exactly when

```math
\Theta+\omega^2/4<M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa).
```

Equivalently, for a fixed one-line width \(\omega\), the allowed signed
doubly centered range is

```math
\Theta
<
\Theta_{\max}(\omega,\kappa)
:=
M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)-{\omega^2\over4}.
```

If \(\Theta_{\max}(\omega,\kappa)\le0\), no nonnegative \(\Theta\) can close
the signed gate at that \((\omega,\kappa)\).

### Lemma 52.2: Scalar Gate Equivalence

`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED(Theta,omega,kappa)` closes `P23-RPF-TRANS0` if and only if
the frozen gate of Definition 52.1 holds.

Proof.

Proposition 51.4 gives

```math
\sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)+\kappa<B_*^{edge}.
```

Since \(\sinh\) is strictly increasing, this is equivalent to
\(\Theta+\omega^2/4<2\operatorname{arsinh}(B_*^{edge}-\kappa)\). `square`

### Definition 52.3: Admissible Cancellation Block

An admissible signed cancellation block is a finite subset
\(P\subset{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\) together with a same-law identity
for its anchored block sum

```math
H_P(u,v;\zeta)
:=
\sum_{A\in P}G_A^{anc}(u,v;\zeta).
```

The block is admissible only if all identities used to form it are identities
of scalar records under the same adaptive pushed-forward law.  A geometric
similarity, a formal representation duality, or an OS/RP inequality is not an
admissible cancellation identity unless the relevant scalar equality is
declared and proved on the active finite battery.

The block pays

```math
\Theta(P):=\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}(H_P^{dc}),
```

and

```math
\omega(P):=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\max\left\{
\sup_u\operatorname{osc}_v H_P,
\sup_v\operatorname{osc}_u H_P
\right\}.
```

### Table 52.4: Natural Cancellation Candidates

The following table is the same-law cancellation audit.

| candidate block generator | same-law status | what it proves | cancellation verdict |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| endpoint exchange \(x\leftrightarrow y\) | admissible only when the two-site conditional law and active records are exchange-invariant | equality of exchanged rows | not anti-equality; no cancellation unless an extra sign law is supplied |
| orientation reversal/conjugation | Paper-21 physical quotient allows pairing only for declared real/paired scalar records | equality or complex conjugacy of scalar records | no negative sign in real scalar battery; no cancellation |
| representation dual \(\rho\leftrightarrow\rho^*\) | admissible for central characters under declared dual/paired convention | equality/conjugacy of character records | not a signed pairing |
| OS reflection | same finite battery supplies positivity/reflection inequality | inequality or reflected paired row | not an equation unless saturation is proved |
| covariance/hypercubic orbit | declared template covariance quotient | orbit equality | quotient only; it may reduce counting but not amplitude |
| CE division/retraction partner | already used to separate endpoint-additive/local pieces | no-double-charge ledger identity | true bridges are the residual mixed rows, so no remaining local partner cancels them |
| Möbius sibling/inclusion-exclusion row | same formal Möbius sign pattern exists rowwise | alternating signs in the expansion | magnitudes are actual conditional coefficients; equality of magnitudes is a new source |
| Paper-16 clean polymer partner | same-row KP envelope after clean-row import | domination envelope | not a literal anti-row identity |

### Lemma 52.5: Declared Symmetries Are Not Cancellation Sources

The declared physical symmetries from the Paper-21 quotient rules do not, by
themselves, prove a nonzero cancellation block with
\(\Theta(P)\) or \(\omega(P)\) smaller than the corresponding unsigned
triangle bound.

Proof.

Paper 21's physical quotient rules identify records only when they are equal
scalar records on the same pushed-forward law or when the active battery
declares a paired real convention.  Equality and conjugacy reduce the number
of labels; they do not introduce a minus sign.  Reflection positivity is an
inequality unless a saturation or extremality statement is separately proved.
CE/retraction identities have already been spent to remove endpoint-additive
and local pieces in Sections 45 and 49; applying them again to true bridges
would double-charge the local ledger.  Möbius signs are formal signs in the
coefficient expansion, but cancellation requires same-law equality or
controlled domination of the actual conditional coefficient magnitudes.  That
is exactly the missing signed source, not a consequence of the quotient
rules. `square`

### Definition 52.6: Rowwise Signed Extremal Table

For each finite row, define

```math
{\mathfrak C}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)
:=
\inf_{{\mathcal P}}
\left(
\sum_{P\in{\mathcal P}}\Theta(P),
\sum_{P\in{\mathcal P}}\omega(P)
\right),
```

where the infimum is over all admissible finite partitions of
\({\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}(x,y)\), ordered componentwise.  Equivalently one
may enumerate all partitions because the bridge table is finite on each
adaptive row.  Let

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{can}}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\inf_{\mathcal P}\sum_{P\in{\mathcal P}}\Theta(P),
\qquad
\omega_{\mathrm{can}}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y}
\inf_{\mathcal P}\sum_{P\in{\mathcal P}}\omega(P),
```

with the infima restricted to admissible same-law identities.

### Proposition 52.7: Rowwise Decidability Of Signed Cancellation

For every fixed finite adaptive row, the signed cancellation extremal table
\({\mathfrak C}_{br,0}^{N,j}\) is finite and decidable on the same law.

Proof.

Sections 47--51 prove that the bridge table is finite rowwise and that each
anchored row \(G_A^{anc}\) is a same-law scalar function.  A finite set has
only finitely many partitions.  For each partition, the block sums \(H_P\),
their doubly centered ranges, and their one-line widths are finite extremal
problems over the same finite endpoint records.  Thus the rowwise table is
finite and decidable. `square`

### Proposition 52.8: Current-Corpus Cancellation Verdict

The current corpus does not prove
`P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE-CANCEL(Theta,omega)` in the closing range of
Definition 52.1.

Proof.

Proposition 52.7 proves rowwise decidability, so there is no undefined
finite-table obstruction.  Lemma 52.5 proves that the natural candidates
available in Papers 16, 21, and 23 are not cancellation identities: they are
record equalities, quotient rules, inequalities, local ledger identities, or
domination envelopes.  None supplies a same-law anti-row identity of the form

```math
G_A^{anc}+G_{A'}^{anc}
\quad\hbox{has small doubly centered range and one-line width}
```

uniformly on the adaptive cofinal branch.  Therefore the signed cancellation
route remains positive and exact, but its proof requires a new same-law
source controlling the rowwise signed extremal table:

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{can}}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\omega_{\mathrm{can}}^{N,j}\le\omega,
```

with \(\Theta+\omega^2/4<M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)\). `square`

### Corollary 52.9: What A Positive Cancellation Proof Must Supply

To prove `P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE-CANCEL(Theta,omega)` positively, it is necessary
and sufficient, within the Section-52 framework, to supply a cofinal
same-law bound on the rowwise signed extremal table:

```math
\limsup_j\Theta_{\mathrm{can}}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\limsup_j\omega_{\mathrm{can}}^{N,j}\le\omega.
```

Together with `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(kappa)`, the signed branch closes exactly
when

```math
\Theta+\omega^2/4
<
M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa).
```

The useful next theorem is therefore not another symmetry quotient.  It is a
same-law signed extremal estimate, or an explicit anti-row identity whose
block sums realize such an estimate.

## 53. Direct Signed Extremal Object

Section 52 shows that the natural pairings do not supply cancellation for
free.  The next honest move is therefore to stop partitioning the bridge
table and evaluate the actual signed object itself:

```math
W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}
=
\sum_{A\in{\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}}G_A^{anc}.
```

This is the most Barandes-aligned form of the problem: one pushed-forward
scalar law, one declared conditional Hamiltonian, and no hidden subprocess
decomposition.

### Definition 53.1: One-Block Signed Extremal Source

Define the direct signed one-block values

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}
:=
\Theta_{br,0}^{N,j},
\qquad
\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}
:=
\omega_{br,0}^{N,j}.
```

`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-EXT(Theta,omega)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\le\omega.
```

Thus

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}EXT}
(\Theta,\omega)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
```

is exactly `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED(Theta,omega,kappa)`.

### Lemma 53.2: The One-Block Route Dominates Partition Cancellation

If `P23-RPF-MIN-BRIDGE-CANCEL(Theta,omega)` holds, then
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-EXT(Theta,omega)` holds.

Proof.

The one-block signed sum is the sum of the admissible partition block sums.
The triangle inequality at block level gives the bounds in Definition 51.5,
which are precisely the direct values of Definition 53.1. `square`

Therefore the direct one-block route is never worse than a proved partition
certificate.  It may be strictly better because it keeps cancellations across
all bridge rows until the final range is taken.

### Definition 53.3: Compact Same-Law Extremal Problem

For a fixed adaptive row and fixed adjacent minimal edge \((x,y)\), let
\({\mathsf K}_{xy}^{N,j}\) be the compact finite-record domain consisting of
the endpoint scalar records \(u,v\) and the conditioned environment
\(\zeta\) under the actual adaptive pushed-forward scalar law.  The direct
signed range is the finite compact optimization

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}(x,y)
=
\sup_{\zeta\in{\mathsf K}_{xy}^{N,j}}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left[
\left(W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}\right)^{dc}(u,v;\zeta)
\right],
```

and

```math
\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}(x,y)
=
\sup_{\zeta\in{\mathsf K}_{xy}^{N,j}}
\max\left\{
\sup_u\operatorname{osc}_v W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j},
\sup_v\operatorname{osc}_u W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}
\right\}.
```

The global values are the essential suprema over \((x,y)\).  Since
\({\mathcal U}_{br,0}^{N,j}\) is finite rowwise and all \(G_A^{anc}\) are
finite scalar record functions, this is an ordinary finite compact extremal
problem on the same law.

### Proposition 53.4: Direct Signed Closure

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}EXT}
(\Theta,\omega)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

If

```math
\Theta+\omega^2/4<M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa),
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Definition 53.1 identifies `SIGNED-EXT + KTAIL` with
`MIN-SIGNED(Theta,omega,kappa)`.  Apply Lemma 52.2. `square`

### Definition 53.5: Finite Dual Certificate

Let \({\mathcal Q}_{closed}^{N,j}\) be the finite list of scalar constraints
already proved by the closed Paper-23 ledgers on the adaptive row: exact
normalization, central-entry identities that were explicitly retained,
declared covariance/quotient equalities, no-double-charge local removals, and
the closed surface/RP-Cov ledgers.  Let \({\mathcal M}_{closed}^{N,j}\) be
the compact convex set of pushed-forward scalar laws satisfying these
constraints.

A finite dual certificate for `SIGNED-EXT(Theta,omega)` is a finite list of
nonnegative multipliers and equality multipliers proving, over
\({\mathcal M}_{closed}^{N,j}\),

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\le\omega.
```

Equivalently, after replacing the two oscillation bounds by finite-dimensional
universal inequalities on the printed endpoint records, this is a finite
convex, semialgebraic, or analytic dual certificate on the actual finite
scalar record body.  No discreteness of the endpoint record values is
assumed.

### Lemma 53.6: Dual Certificates Are Same-Law Valid

Any finite dual certificate of Definition 53.5 proves
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-EXT(Theta,omega)`.

Proof.

The certificate is an inequality over the same compact set of pushed-forward
scalar laws satisfying the already proved row constraints.  No auxiliary law,
unconditioned continuum measure, or hidden Markov decomposition is inserted.
Therefore the bound holds for the actual adaptive law whenever that law lies
in \({\mathcal M}_{closed}^{N,j}\). `square`

### Table 53.7: Available Routes For The Direct Signed Object

| route | same-law status | possible output | current-corpus verdict |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| exact evaluation of \(W_{br,0}^{anc}\) | fully admissible | exact \((\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}},\omega_{\mathrm{dir}})\) | rowwise finite, but no cofinal numerical table is printed |
| finite dual certificate over \({\mathcal M}_{closed}\) | fully admissible | rigorous uniform upper bound | no certificate currently supplied |
| Peter-Weyl truncation plus tail | admissible if `MIN-KTAIL(kappa)` is supplied | finite spectral computation plus \(\kappa\) | tail remains live and finite spectral values are not printed |
| RP/positivity inequalities | admissible inequalities | possible convex constraints | no saturation or sign-control strong enough for the signed gate |
| covariance/conjugation quotient | admissible equality quotient | reduced variable count | quotient only; no negative sign or amplitude decay |
| Paper-16 clean KP envelope | admissible as domination after same-row import | unsigned decay envelope | does not bound the direct signed range without a row-value theorem |
| residual-tail countermodel audit | admissible falsification test | non-derivability from closed ledgers | shows the current closed ledgers do not imply the signed gate |

### Proposition 53.8: Positivity And Quotients Do Not Decide The Direct Range

The currently available RP, positivity, covariance, conjugation, and quotient
relations do not imply a closing bound for
\((\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j},\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j})\).

Proof.

Covariance and conjugation reduce labels, but preserve the value of the
scalar row rather than bounding its signed oscillation.  RP and positivity
give inequalities on quadratic or reflected finite-battery expectations.
They can constrain a moment body, but without a saturation or a dual
certificate they do not bound the pointwise conditional Hamiltonian range.
The Paper-16 clean KP envelope is an unsigned domination theorem after the
same-row import; it is not a value identity for the actual signed bridge sum.
Thus these tools are useful components of a future finite dual certificate,
but none is itself the missing direct signed estimate. `square`

### Proposition 53.9: Current-Corpus Direct Signed Verdict

The current corpus proves that the direct signed extremal problem is finite
and rowwise decidable, and it proves the exact scalar condition under which
the resulting bound would close adaptive Branch A.  It does not prove the
cofinal numerical bound required by `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-EXT`.

Proof.

Definitions 53.1 and 53.3 give the exact finite compact same-law extremal
problem.  Proposition 53.4 gives the positive closure theorem.  Lemma 53.6
shows the strongest admissible proof format: a finite dual certificate on
the closed scalar record body.  Table 53.7 exhausts the available current
routes.  Exact rowwise evaluation is finite but not cofinal; Peter-Weyl
truncation still needs `MIN-KTAIL`; positivity and quotient relations lack a
closing dual certificate; and Paper-16 gives unsigned clean envelopes rather
than actual signed bridge values.

Finally, the residual-tail countermodels used in Sections 28--33 and
47--50 remain compatible with the closed non-RPF ledgers while changing a
surviving true-bridge mixed mode.  Such completions can change
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\) and \(\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\) without
violating the already closed surface, RP/Cov, local, or endpoint-additive
bookkeeping.  Therefore the direct signed value is not determined by the
current source package. `square`

### Corollary 53.10: Final Same-Law Direct-Signed Frontier

The direct signed route is now fully reduced to the following primitive
source package:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}EXT}
(\Theta,\omega)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
```

with

```math
\Theta+\omega^2/4
<
M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa).
```

Equivalently, one may supply a same-law finite dual certificate proving the
two direct extremal inequalities.  Without such a certificate, the signed
route remains a precise positive theorem but not an unconditional confinement
proof.

## 54. Finite Dual Certificate Campaign

Section 53 identifies the cleanest possible proof format: a finite same-law
dual certificate for the direct signed extremal inequalities.  This section
executes that campaign.  The outcome is decisive for the current corpus: such
a certificate would close the signed route, but it is not derivable from the
closed ledgers already present in Papers 1--23.

### Definition 54.1: Closed Scalar Record Body

For a fixed adaptive row, let \({\mathcal M}_{54}^{N,j}\) be the compact set
of finite pushed-forward scalar laws satisfying exactly the constraints
already closed before the live RPF signed-range source:

1. normalization and positivity of the finite scalar law;
2. declared centrality, covariance, conjugation, and quotient equalities;
3. the exact central-entry identities that were retained rather than carried;
4. the no-double-charge local/endpoint-additive removals from Sections
   18, 45, and 49;
5. the closed surface/activity side and fixed-template geometry side;
6. the RP/Cov diagonal-shell transport ledger already assigned outside the
   RPF signed source;
7. all finite row definitions of \(W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}\), but no bound on its
   signed range and no Peter-Weyl tail zero unless separately supplied.

Thus \({\mathcal M}_{54}^{N,j}\) is deliberately the largest same-law scalar
body licensed by the current closed corpus.  A certificate over this body is
not allowed to import continuum Yang-Mills area laws, off-law heat kernels, or
hidden Markov subprocesses.

### Definition 54.2: Universal Signed Inequality Family

Let \(F=W_{br,0}^{anc,N,j}\).  A proposed pair \((\Theta,\omega)\) defines
the following universal inequalities on \({\mathcal M}_{54}^{N,j}\):

```math
-\Theta
\le
F^{dc}(u,v;\zeta)-F^{dc}(u',v';\zeta)
\le
\Theta,
```

for all endpoint records \(u,u',v,v'\) and environments \(\zeta\), and

```math
-\omega
\le
F(u,v;\zeta)-F(u,v';\zeta)
\le
\omega,
```

```math
-\omega
\le
F(u,v;\zeta)-F(u',v;\zeta)
\le
\omega.
```

These inequalities are exactly equivalent to

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\le\omega.
```

### Definition 54.3: `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-DUAL(Theta,omega)`

`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-DUAL(Theta,omega)` asserts that, cofinally, every
inequality in Definition 54.2 has a finite same-law certificate over
\({\mathcal M}_{54}^{N,j}\).  The certificate may use:

1. equality multipliers for the closed scalar equalities;
2. nonnegative multipliers for positivity/RP/covariance inequalities;
3. finite semialgebraic, convex, or analytic dual terms valid on the compact
   finite record body;
4. no target RPF signed-range inequality as an input.

### Lemma 54.4: Dual Certificate Closes The Direct Signed Source

If `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-DUAL(Theta,omega)` holds, then
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-EXT(Theta,omega)` holds.

Proof.

The dual certificate proves every universal signed inequality of Definition
54.2 on the same compact scalar record body that contains the actual
adaptive pushed-forward law.  Definition 54.2 is equivalent to the direct
signed extremal bounds. `square`

### Corollary 54.5: Dual-Ktail Closure

Assume

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}DUAL}
(\Theta,\omega)
+
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

If

```math
\Theta+\omega^2/4<M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa),
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Apply Lemma 54.4 and then Proposition 53.4. `square`

### Table 54.6: Closed Constraints Versus The Signed Inequalities

| closed constraint family | can enter a dual certificate? | obstruction to closing by itself |
|---|---:|---:|
| normalization/positivity | yes | constrains probabilities, not pointwise mixed Hamiltonian range |
| RP/reflection positivity | yes | inequality only; no saturation or extremal certificate is printed |
| covariance/conjugation quotient | yes | reduces variables but gives equality, not smallness |
| central-entry identities | yes | already spent to define the exact same-law branch; no signed range bound |
| local/endpoint-additive removals | yes | removes zero mixed rows; true bridges remain |
| Paper-16 clean KP envelope | only after same-row import | unsigned domination, not direct signed value |
| Peter-Weyl truncation | yes if paired with tail source | tail and finite spectral values remain unsourced |
| residual-tail freedom | yes as obstruction | varies true-bridge mixed modes while preserving closed ledgers |

### Proposition 54.7: Equality-Only Duals Cannot Close

No certificate using only normalization, covariance/conjugation quotient
equalities, central-entry equalities, and local/endpoint-additive removals can
prove `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-DUAL(Theta,omega)` in a nontrivial closing range.

Proof.

Those constraints identify or delete rows.  They do not bound the magnitude
of a surviving true-bridge row.  After Sections 49 and 52, the surviving
object is exactly the signed true-bridge Hamiltonian.  Equality-only
constraints can rewrite this object but cannot force its oscillation below a
strict positive scalar gate unless the rewrite deletes all true bridges or
creates an anti-row identity.  Sections 49 and 52 prove that neither is
available from the declared equalities. `square`
