### Proposition 54.8: RP/Positivity Without A Dual Certificate Is Insufficient

The currently printed RP and positivity inequalities do not by themselves
prove `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-DUAL(Theta,omega)`.

Proof.

RP and positivity constrain finite expectation and moment matrices.  The
target inequalities in Definition 54.2 are uniform conditional Hamiltonian
range inequalities.  Passing from the former to the latter is precisely a
dual certificate or an extremal theorem over \({\mathcal M}_{54}^{N,j}\).
No such multiplier certificate, saturation theorem, or extremal separation
argument is printed in Papers 1--23.  Hence RP/positivity may be part of a
future certificate, but does not currently constitute one. `square`

### Proposition 54.9: Current-Corpus Dual No-Go

The current closed corpus does not prove
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-DUAL(Theta,omega)` for constants satisfying the signed
gate.

Proof.

If such a dual certificate were derivable from the closed corpus, then every
law in \({\mathcal M}_{54}^{N,j}\) would satisfy the universal signed
inequalities of Definition 54.2.  But the residual-tail countermodel family
used in Sections 28--33 and 47--53 is built precisely inside the slack left
by the closed non-RPF ledgers: it preserves the normalization, declared
quotients, RP/Cov carries, local removals, and endpoint-additive bookkeeping,
while changing a surviving true-bridge mixed mode of the actual RPF residual.

Varying that mode changes \(F^{dc}\), and hence changes
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\) and \(\omega_{\mathrm{dir}}^{N,j}\), without
violating the constraints listed in Definition 54.1.  Therefore the closed
constraint body contains admissible same-record completions whose signed
range is not bounded by the desired closing constants.  A dual certificate
from only those constraints cannot exist. `square`

### Corollary 54.10: Exhausted Same-Law Dual Frontier

The finite dual route has the following exact status.

1. A cofinal finite certificate
   `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-DUAL(Theta,omega)` plus `MIN-KTAIL(kappa)` closes
   adaptive Branch A whenever

   ```math
   \Theta+\omega^2/4<M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa).
   ```

2. The current closed ledgers do not imply such a certificate.
3. A positive proof now requires at least one genuinely new same-law input:
   a printed dual certificate, a sharp direct signed evaluation, a same-law
   spectral/tail theorem, or an actual bridge damping theorem.

Thus Section 54 does not merely rename the obstruction.  It proves that the
existing equality/positivity/RP/covariance/local ledgers are too weak to
certify the direct signed range.  The remaining route is a new numerical
same-law source theorem.

## 55. Minimal Peter-Weyl Tail Source Campaign

Both surviving positive routes carry the same tail debit:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa).
```

This section attacks that common bottleneck.  The target is not an abstract
Peter-Weyl fact about compact groups.  It is a same-law statement about the
actual normalized minimal-edge Hamiltonian after `BC/CE`, anchoring, and the
adaptive `SEL2` push-forward.

### Definition 55.1: Minimal Tail Profile

For the normalized minimal-edge Hamiltonian \(C_0^{m,N,j}\), define the
tail profile

```math
\kappa_{PW}^{N,j}(L)
:=
\Kappa_{0,L}^{N,j}
=
\left\|(I-\Pi_{\le L}^{xy})C_0^{m,N,j}\right\|_{\mathrm{edge}},
```

where the norm is the same edge-contraction norm used in Sections 42, 46,
and 48.  The live source is

```math
\limsup_{(N,j)}
\kappa_{PW}^{N,j}(L(N,j))
\le\kappa
```

for some cofinal cutoff schedule \(L=L(N,j)\).

### Definition 55.2: Exact Finite-Band Source

`P23-RPF-MIN-PWBAND(L0)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
(I-\Pi_{\le L_0}^{xy})C_0^{m,N,j}=0.
```

This is the same as `P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL0(L0)`, but the `PWBAND` name records
the proof mechanism: the actual normalized minimal-edge Hamiltonian is a
finite Peter-Weyl polynomial on the same pushed-forward law.

### Lemma 55.3: Finite-Band Source Gives Zero Tail

If `P23-RPF-MIN-PWBAND(L0)` holds, then
`P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(0)` holds.

Proof.

This is Lemma 48.2 with the source mechanism made explicit. `square`

### Proposition 55.4: Finite Record Does Not Imply Finite Band

The fact that the adaptive row uses a finite list of scalar records does not
imply `P23-RPF-MIN-PWBAND(L0)` for any fixed \(L_0\).

Proof.

The finite row records are finitely many scalar functions and conditional
probability weights.  The minimal-edge Hamiltonian \(C_0^m\) is obtained
after conditioning, central-entry division, logarithmic/normalizing
operations, and endpoint anchoring.  A logarithm or conditional ratio of
finite Peter-Weyl polynomials need not be a finite Peter-Weyl polynomial.
Therefore finite record dimension gives rowwise decidability of a truncated
table, but not exact spectral support. `square`

### Definition 55.5: Uniform Peter-Weyl Decay Source

Let \(\lambda_{L+1}^{xy}\) be the smallest nonzero two-endpoint Casimir level
outside the cutoff \(\Pi_{\le L}^{xy}\).  For constants \(A,t>0\),
`P23-RPF-MIN-PWDECAY(A,t)` asserts that, cofinally and for all sufficiently
large \(L\),

```math
\kappa_{PW}^{N,j}(L)
\le
A\exp(-t\lambda_{L+1}^{xy}).
```

More generally, a summable profile \(r_L\downarrow0\) may replace the
exponential profile; the exponential form is the heat-kernel/Casimir ideal.

### Lemma 55.6: Uniform Tail Decay Gives Arbitrarily Small Ktail

If `P23-RPF-MIN-PWDECAY(A,t)` holds, then
`P23-RPF-MIN-KTAIL(0)` holds.  More generally, if
\(\kappa_{PW}^{N,j}(L)\le r_L\) cofinally with \(r_L\to0\), then
`MIN-KTAIL(0)` holds.

Proof.

Choose a cofinal cutoff schedule \(L(N,j)\to\infty\).  The uniform bound gives
\(\limsup\kappa_{PW}^{N,j}(L(N,j))=0\). `square`

### Table 55.7: Candidate Tail Sources

| candidate source | would imply | current-corpus verdict |
|---|---:|---:|
| finite-complete endpoint scalar battery | `PWBAND(L0)` | not the active compact-group endpoint law |
| exact finite Peter-Weyl Hamiltonian after `BC/CE` | `PWBAND(L0)` | not printed; finite records do not imply it |
| heat-kernel/Casimir smoothing on the residual channel | `PWDECAY(A,t)` | Paper-16/Paper-19 supply this on declared heat-kernel rows, not on the actual adaptive residual law |
| Paper-20 actual heat-kernel coefficient estimates | possible local coefficient decay | controls selected heat-kernel coefficients, not the divided residual minimal-edge Hamiltonian tail |
| Paper-21 bounded-collar/degree-tail tables | finite row/collar bookkeeping | degree or support tails, not Peter-Weyl spectral decay of \(C_0^m\) |
| compact-group SD/Casimir self rows | possible analytic identity after a source theorem | same-support identities; no smoothing/tail estimate by themselves |
| Paper-16 clean KP envelope | unsigned clean-polymer decay | not a Peter-Weyl tail bound unless a same-row signed value transfer is supplied |
| rowwise truncation computation | finite value for fixed row and \(L\) | no cofinal decay schedule |

### Proposition 55.8: Current-Corpus Finite-Band Verdict

The current corpus does not prove `P23-RPF-MIN-PWBAND(L0)`.

Proof.

The only route to `PWBAND(L0)` is an exact statement that
\(C_0^{m,N,j}\) belongs to a fixed finite Peter-Weyl span on the actual
adaptive pushed-forward law.  Papers 10 and 21 provide finite declared
Peter-Weyl batteries and finite row tables.  Papers 16, 19, and 20 provide
heat-kernel coefficient and tail information on declared heat-kernel or
clean analytic rows.  None proves that the normalized, central-entry-divided,
anchored minimal-edge residual Hamiltonian is itself bandlimited.  By
Proposition 55.4, finite row data alone is insufficient. `square`

### Proposition 55.9: Current-Corpus Quantitative Tail Verdict

The current corpus does not prove `P23-RPF-MIN-PWDECAY(A,t)` or any explicit
profile \(r_L\to0\) for the actual adaptive minimal-edge residual
Hamiltonian.

Proof.

The heat-kernel/Casimir estimates in the earlier papers are real analytic
tools, but their declared object is the heat-kernel or clean analytic row.
The exact-entry RPF object in Paper 23 is the residual Hamiltonian after
`BC/CE` and anchoring on the adaptive `SEL2` law.  Sections 21--23 and
35--37 already enforce the no-smuggling rule: a clean heat-kernel proof
coordinate does not become a same-law residual spectral-gap or tail theorem
without a literal row-value transfer.  No such transfer is printed.

Likewise, the Paper-21 degree-tail and bounded-collar tables are finite
combinatorial controls.  They do not imply Peter-Weyl coefficient decay for
the conditional logarithmic residual.  The residual-tail countermodels used
throughout Sections 28--54 can place surviving true-bridge mixed variation
in high Peter-Weyl modes while preserving the already closed non-RPF ledgers.
Therefore no cofinal quantitative tail profile is derived from the current
corpus. `square`

### Corollary 55.10: Ktail Frontier

The common tail bottleneck is now fully explicit:

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
```

must be supplied by one of the following genuinely new same-law inputs:

1. exact finite-band support `P23-RPF-MIN-PWBAND(L0)`;
2. uniform Peter-Weyl decay `P23-RPF-MIN-PWDECAY(A,t)`;
3. an explicit cofinal numerical table for
   \(\kappa_{PW}^{N,j}(L(N,j))\);
4. a direct signed/bridge theorem whose proof avoids Peter-Weyl truncation
   entirely and pays no \(\kappa\).

At present none is available.  Thus the shared tail source is not closed; it
is a genuine numerical same-law theorem still needed by both the direct
signed route and the bridge-damping route.

## 56. Full-Object Signed No-Tail Route

Section 55 shows that Peter-Weyl tail control is a genuine same-law source,
not bookkeeping.  The remaining way to avoid paying that source is to stop
truncating.  This section tests the full normalized minimal-edge Hamiltonian
directly.

The target object is the exact same-law conditional Hamiltonian
\(C_0^{m,N,j}\) from Sections 41--45, after `BC/CE`, deterministic endpoint
anchoring, and the adaptive `SEL2` push-forward.  No projection
\(\Pi_{\le L}^{xy}\) is applied.

### Definition 56.1: Full-Object Signed Extremal Values

Define

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{full}}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\operatorname{osc}_{u,v}
\left[(C_0^{m,N,j})^{dc}(u,v;\zeta)\right],
```

and

```math
\omega_{\mathrm{full}}^{N,j}
:=
\operatorname*{ess\,sup}_{x,y,\zeta}
\max\left\{
\sup_u\operatorname{osc}_v C_0^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta),
\sup_v\operatorname{osc}_u C_0^{m,N,j}(u,v;\zeta)
\right\}.
```

`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL(Theta,omega)` asserts that, cofinally,

```math
\Theta_{\mathrm{full}}^{N,j}\le\Theta,
\qquad
\omega_{\mathrm{full}}^{N,j}\le\omega.
```

This is not the Section-53 bridge-sum source and it is not paired with
`MIN-KTAIL`.  It bounds the complete two-endpoint conditional Hamiltonian.

### Proposition 56.2: Full-Object No-Tail Closure

Assume `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL(Theta,omega)`.  If

```math
\sinh\left({\Theta+\omega^2/4\over2}\right)
<
B_*^{edge},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

The Sinkhorn range reduction used in Proposition 43.4 is a statement about
the normalized minimal-edge conditional Hamiltonian itself.  With no
Peter-Weyl projection, there is no spectral tail term.  The full-object
source gives the doubly centered range and one-line width bounds for
\(C_0^{m,N,j}\), hence

```math
\Delta_{m,0}^{N,j}
\le
\Theta+\omega^2/4.
```

The Section-46 edge-contraction gate is therefore

```math
\sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)<B_*^{edge},
```

which is exactly the displayed assumption.  Thus the minimal-edge spectral
route closes and `P23-RPF-TRANS0` follows. `square`

### Definition 56.3: Full-Object Finite Dual Certificate

Let \({\mathcal M}_{56}^{N,j}\) be the compact finite scalar record body
obtained from \({\mathcal M}_{54}^{N,j}\) by replacing the truncated/direct
bridge target with the exact full row definition of \(C_0^{m,N,j}\).  The
closed constraints are still only:

1. normalization and positivity;
2. declared centrality, covariance, conjugation, quotient, and reflection
   equalities;
3. exact `BC/CE` and central-entry identities retained in the branch;
4. local, endpoint-blind, and endpoint-additive removals already proved;
5. surface/activity and RP/Cov ledgers already assigned outside the live RPF
   signed source;
6. the exact finite row formula for \(C_0^{m,N,j}\), with no Peter-Weyl
   truncation and no tail source.

`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL-DUAL(Theta,omega)` asserts that, cofinally, the
universal inequalities

```math
-\Theta
\le
(C_0^m)^{dc}(u,v;\zeta)-(C_0^m)^{dc}(u',v';\zeta)
\le
\Theta,
```

and the two one-line inequalities bounded by \(\omega\), have finite
same-law certificates over \({\mathcal M}_{56}^{N,j}\).

### Lemma 56.4: Full Dual Certificate Closes Full Source

If `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL-DUAL(Theta,omega)` holds, then
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL(Theta,omega)` holds.

Proof.

The dual certificate proves the displayed universal inequalities on the
same compact scalar record body containing the actual adaptive pushed-forward
law.  These inequalities are exactly the definitions of
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{full}}\le\Theta\) and
\(\omega_{\mathrm{full}}\le\omega\). `square`

### Corollary 56.5: Full-Dual No-Tail Closure

If

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}FULL\text{-}DUAL}
(\Theta,\omega)
```

and

```math
\sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)<B_*^{edge},
```

then `P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.

Proof.

Apply Lemma 56.4 and Proposition 56.2. `square`

### Table 56.6: Full-Object Routes

| route | would close? | current-corpus status |
|---|---:|---:|
| exact cofinal evaluation of \((\Theta_{\mathrm{full}},\omega_{\mathrm{full}})\) | yes | finite for each fixed row, no cofinal bound printed |
| finite dual certificate over \({\mathcal M}_{56}\) | yes | valid proof format, no certificate printed |
| equality/quotient/covariance only | no | rewrites labels but does not bound surviving mixed range |
| RP/positivity only | no | moment constraints, not pointwise conditional Hamiltonian bounds |
| bridge signed route plus `MIN-KTAIL` | yes | reintroduces the tail source; not the no-tail route |
| `PWBAND/PWDECAY` | yes for tail route | Section 55 proves these are unsourced |
| screened conditional influence or Dobrushin row | yes upstream | Sections 33--39 reduce to new same-law row values |
| residual-tail countermodel family | obstruction | varies high spectral full-object range while preserving closed ledgers |

### Proposition 56.7: Current-Corpus Full-Object No-Go

The current corpus does not prove
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL(Theta,omega)` or
`P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL-DUAL(Theta,omega)` in the closing range of
Proposition 56.2.

Proof.

The full-object route deliberately includes all Peter-Weyl modes of
\(C_0^{m,N,j}\).  This removes the need for a tail debit, but it also means
that any uncontrolled residual-tail completion contributes directly to
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{full}}\) and \(\omega_{\mathrm{full}}\).

The residual-tail countermodel family used in Sections 28--33, 47--55
preserves the closed scalar constraints: normalization, declared quotient and
covariance equalities, local and endpoint-additive removals, RP/Cov carries,
and the already closed surface/activity ledgers.  It can nevertheless place
surviving true-bridge mixed variation in modes not fixed by those ledgers.
For the truncated route this appears as `MIN-KTAIL`; for the full-object
route it appears directly as unbounded or undetermined full signed range.

Therefore the closed constraint body \({\mathcal M}_{56}^{N,j}\) still
contains same-record completions with different values of
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{full}}\) and \(\omega_{\mathrm{full}}\).  A universal
closing inequality over that body cannot be derived from the current corpus.
The positive theorem is real, but its numerical source is not present in
Papers 1--23. `square`

### Corollary 56.8: Final No-Tail Verdict

The direct no-tail route has now been settled to the same standard as the
tail route.

1. A cofinal proof of `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL(Theta,omega)` closes adaptive
   Branch A whenever

   ```math
   \sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)<B_*^{edge}.
   ```

2. A finite same-law dual certificate
   `P23-RPF-MIN-SIGNED-FULL-DUAL(Theta,omega)` is a sufficient proof format.
3. The current corpus does not supply either source.
4. The remaining positive routes are exactly:
   - full-object signed range control with no tail debit;
   - bridge/signed control plus a separately sourced `MIN-KTAIL`;
   - an upstream screened conditional influence/Dobrushin theorem strong
     enough to imply the full range control.

Thus Section 56 removes the last ambiguity about whether the Peter-Weyl tail
can be dodged by phrasing.  It can be dodged only by proving a stronger
full-object signed theorem on the same adaptive pushed-forward scalar law.
That theorem is a genuine new same-law numerical source.

## 57. Terminal Source Theorem And Paper-24 Export

Papers 21--23 have now exhausted the adaptive Branch-A bookkeeping route.
This section freezes the export.  The point is not that adaptive Branch A is
proved.  It is that its remaining positive content is no longer hidden in
surface accounting, RP/Cov transport, exact-entry normalization, canonical
labels, or Peter-Weyl phrasing.

### Definition 57.1: Terminal Adaptive Branch-A Source Alternatives

The terminal alternatives are the following same-law source packages.

1. **Full-object no-tail signed route**

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}FULL}
   (\Theta,\omega)
   ```

   with

   ```math
   \sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)<B_*^{edge}.
   ```

2. **Full-object finite dual certificate**

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}FULL\text{-}DUAL}
   (\Theta,\omega)
   ```

   with the same scalar gate.

3. **Signed/truncated route**

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}EXT}
   (\Theta,\omega)
   +
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
   ```

   or the finite-dual version, with

   ```math
   \sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)+\kappa<B_*^{edge}.
   ```

4. **Unsigned bridge-damping route**

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}BRIDGEDAMP}(D)
   +
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
   ```

   with

   ```math
   \kappa<B_*^{edge},
   \qquad
   D<D_{\mathrm{crit}}(\kappa).
   ```

5. **Upstream Dobrushin/screening route**

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}SCREEN\text{-}COND}
   ```

   satisfying the Section-34 threshold, or directly

   ```math
   \mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}DOB\text{-}ROW}(q,a),
   \qquad q<1.
   ```

These alternatives are all evaluated on the same adaptive pushed-forward
finite scalar law.

### Theorem 57.2: Terminal Positive Closure Theorem

If any alternative in Definition 57.1 holds with its stated scalar gate, then
`P23-RPF-TRANS0` holds.  Consequently the adaptive Branch-A RPF predebit is
zero on the declared large-\(N\), high-\(\alpha\), `SEL2` scalar law.

Proof.

Alternative 1 is Proposition 56.2.  Alternative 2 is Corollary 56.5.
Alternative 3 is Proposition 53.4 or Corollary 54.5.  Alternative 4 is
Corollary 50.5, together with the Section-46 scalar budget.  Alternative 5
is Theorem 34.5 or Theorem 33.3.  Each theorem is a same-law theorem and uses
only finite scalar records of the adaptive branch. `square`

### Proposition 57.3: No Further Current-Corpus Bookkeeping Source

The current corpus does not imply any terminal alternative in Definition
57.1 by further use of:

1. endpoint/corner surface geometry;
2. activity-tree counting;
3. RP/Cov transport;
4. local, collar, endpoint-blind, or endpoint-additive removals;
5. central-entry division or exact `BC/CE` bookkeeping;
6. covariance, conjugation, reflection, or quotient equalities;
7. finite label counting or finite row decidability;
8. Paper-16 clean KP envelopes without a same-law value certificate;
9. Peter-Weyl truncation without `MIN-KTAIL`;
10. heat-kernel/Casimir estimates not transferred to the actual adaptive
    residual Hamiltonian.

Proof.

Items 1--3 are closed outside the live RPF source by Sections 1--12.  Items
4--6 remove or identify rows but do not bound surviving true-bridge mixed
range, by Sections 18, 45, 49, 52, and 54.  Item 7 gives finiteness and
rowwise decidability, not a cofinal scalar margin, by Sections 24--27 and
47.  Item 8 is exactly the Paper-16 import obstruction of Sections 20--23.
Item 9 is the tail obstruction of Sections 48 and 55.  Item 10 is ruled out
by the no-smuggling audits in Sections 35--39 and 55.

The same residual-tail completion argument used in Sections 28--33 and
47--56 preserves the closed non-RPF ledgers while changing the remaining
RPF mixed/full-object values.  Therefore the missing theorem is not another
bookkeeping identity.  It is a genuinely new same-law numerical or dual
certificate. `square`

### Definition 57.4: Paper-24 Primary Export

Paper 24 receives the following primary problem:

```math
\mathrm{P24\text{-}RPF\text{-}FULL\text{-}DUAL\text{-}CERT}
(\Theta,\omega)
```

meaning a cofinal finite same-law certificate for

```math
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}FULL\text{-}DUAL}
(\Theta,\omega)
```

over the closed scalar body \({\mathcal M}_{56}^{N,j}\), with

```math
\sinh((\Theta+\omega^2/4)/2)<B_*^{edge}.
```

The negative alternative is a same-law witness family

```math
\mathrm{P24\text{-}RPF\text{-}FULL\text{-}DUAL\text{-}WIT}
```

inside \({\mathcal M}_{56}^{N,j}\) showing that no such closing constants can
be certified from the closed constraints.

### Corollary 57.5: Paper-23 Freeze

Paper 23 is frozen as an adaptive Branch-A source reduction and
current-corpus falsification ledger.  It does not prove continuum Yang-Mills
confinement.  It proves that, after all closed finite-table work is spent,
the adaptive Branch-A route requires a new same-law certificate or witness.
The next paper should therefore be a certificate campaign, not another
bookkeeping audit.
